Chronicles of the land of England

Here begy^neth the table of this book / that men kalled Chronicles of the lord
of England
FIrst in the prologue is contained. how Albyne wit her sustres e^trid into
this I Will. and named it Albion The begynny^g of the book co^teyneth how brute
was engendered of them of Troy. and how he slew his fadre and modre Cap. j How
Brute was driven out of his land: and how he held him in greece / and
delivered the Troyans there out of bondage Ca. ij How Coryn becam brutes man
and how king Goffar was disco^fited and of the foundacyon of Tours in Torayne
capit. iij / How brute arrived at Tottenesse in the I Will of Albyo^. and of the
bataill bitwen^ Coryn and Gogmagog / capitu. iiij How Brute made London: and
named this lord britaigne. and scotland albanye: and Walys Cambre. and of the
deuysio^ of the lord to his thresones Capit. v. How king Madan reigned in pees.
and of the death of his sons / and how that one slow that other / and how after
the wulfes slew him that had slain his brother. ca. vj How king Ebrak
conquered france: and begat xx sons and xxiij daughters Capitulo / vij Of
king brute Grenesheld the first sone of king Ebrack capi. viij Of king Leyl
brute grenesheldis sone Capitulo ix Of king Lud ludibras that was king Leyles
sone Capit x Of king Bladud that was sone of king Lud ludibras capit. xi Of
king Leir and of his iij. daughters: and how the yo^gest was married to the king
of France cap. xij How king Leir was dryue^ out of his lord by his folly and
how cordeill his yo^gest daughter helped him in his need Capit. xiij How Morga^
and Codenage which were nevews to cordeyll werryd on her and had her in pryso^
Ca. xiiij. How Reynold that was Conedages sone reigned after his fadre And in
his time it Rayned blood three days Capit. xv How Gorbodia^ reigned after
reinold his fadre Capi / xvi How the two sons of gorbodia^ fought for ye
heritage: and how they both were slain capit / xvij How iiij ky^ges held all
Britaigne: And what their names were capitulo xviiij Of king Doneba^t that was
cleteus sone: and how he wa^ ye land ca. xix. How Donebant was the first king
that ever wered crown of gold in britaigne cap. xx How Brenne and Belyn
departed bitwene he^ the lord after the death of Doneba^t her fadre. and of
their werre capitulo xxi / How belyn drofe out of this la^d Guthlagh of
De^marke and samye cap. xxij How accord was made bitwen^ Bre^ne and Bely^ by ye

How the land of England was first named Albion / and by what encheson it was
so named
There was in the noble land of Surre a noble myghti king and a man of great
renome that men called Dioclisian: that well and worthily him governed and
ruled through his noble chivalry. So that he conquered all the lands about
him: so that almost all the kings of the world to him were ente^dant Hit
befell thus that this Dyoclesian spoused a gentill damysell that was wonder
fair. and was his Emes daughter. and men called her labana. And she loved hy^
as reso^ would. so that he gate upon her.xxxiij. doughtres / of the which the
eldest men called Albine. and thees damiselles wha^ they come^ unto age: they
bicomen so fair / that it was wonder: Wherefore that this Dyoclisian anon^ let
make a somaunce / and commanded by his lre^s that all the kings that helden
of hy^ should come at a certay^ day as in her lre^s were contained to make a
ryall feste / At which day thider they come^ and brought wit hem amyrallis
princes and dukes and noble chyualrye. The fest was rially arrayed / and there
they lived en joy and myrthe enough that it was wonder to wit. And it befell
thus that this Dyoclisian thought to marie his doughtres among all the kings
that tho were at that sole^pnite and so they spaken and ded that albyne his
eldest daughter and all her sustres richely were married unto.xxxiij. kings
that were lords of great honor and of power at this sole^pnite And when the
solempnyte was done: every king took his wife and lad he^ in to her own contre
and there made he^ queen's. And it befell thus afterward that this dame albyne
bycome so stout and so stern that she told little prys of her lord. and of
him had scorn and despit and would not done his will but she would have her
own will in diverse matters. and all her other sustres euerichone bear he^ so
euel against her lords that it was wonder to wit / and for asmoch^ as he^
thought that her husbondes were naught of so hye perage comen: as her fadre But
the kings that were her lords would have castised him with fair speech and
behestes / and also by yeftes / and warned hem in fair manner upon all love and
friendship that they should amend her lyther condycyons / but all was for
naught. for they dydden her own will in all thing that hem lyked and had of
power / Wherefore the xxxiij. kings upon a time and often times beten her wifes
for they we^d that they would have amended her tacches and her wikked thewes /
but of such conditions they were. that for fair spech^ and warnyng they dydden
all the wers / and for betynges eftsoon mochel wers / Wherefore the king yt
had wedded albyne wrote the tacches and conditions of his wife albyne. and sent
the letter to dioclisian her fadre / And wha^ the other kings herd that
albynes lord had sent a letter to Dyoclisia^. anon they sent lettres ensealed
with her seals the condycyons and the tacches of her wyfes also. When the
noble king dyoclisian saw and herd so many complayntes of his doughtres: he was
sore ashamed and became wonder angrye and wroth toward his doughtres. and
thought both night and day how that he might amend it that they so mysded. And
anon sent he his lre^s unto ye xxxiij ky^ges that they should come to hy^ and
bring with hem her wifes euerichone at certay^ day. for he would there castyse
them of their wikkednesse / if he might in any manner or wise: So that the
kings camen all at that day and time that tho was set between hy^ / and the
king Dioclisian vnderfeng hem all with much honor and made a solemn feast
to all that were under his lordship / And the thridde day after that
solempnite the noble king Dioclisian sent after his.xxxiij. doughtres that they
should come and speak with him in his chamber / and when they were come to her
fadre. he spoke unto hem of her wikkednesse and of her cruelty. and
dispytously hem reproved and vndernam and to hem he said that if they would not
be chastysed they should his love lose for evermore And when the ladies herde^
all this / they became^ moch^ abashed and greatly ashamyd and to her fadre they
said / that they would make all ame^des and so they departed out from her
fadres chamber: And dame albyne that was the eldest suster lad hem all to her
chamber and to made void all that were thery^ne so that no live was among
he^. but she and her sustres. Tho said this albine. my fair sustres well we
known that the king our fadre us has reproved shamed and despised for
encheso^ to make us obedient unto our housbo^des: but certes that shall j never
whiles yt j live. sith that I am come of a more hyer kings blood tha^ my^
husbo^de is / and wha^ she had thus said: all her sustre^ said ye same / and
tho said albyne. j wot well fair sustres yt our husbo^des have playned unto
our fadre upon us / wherefore he has us thus foul reproved and despised.
wherefore sustres my counseyll is that this night when our husbondes ben^ a
bed all we with own assent cutte^ her throtes: and than we may been in pees
of hem. and better we mow do this thing under our fadres power than else
where. And anon all the ladies consented and granted to this counseyll / And
when night was come^ the lords and ladies went to bed / and anon as her
lords were a sleep: they cut all her husbo^des throtes. and so they slowen
hem all. Whenne that Dioclisian the king her fadre herd of this thy^g / he
become hugely wroth against his doughtres and anon^ would hem all have brent^ But
all the barons and lords of Surre counceylled not so for to do such
sternesse to his ownes doughtres. but only should void the la^d of hem for
evermore: so that they never should come ayen^. and so he did. And Dioclisia^
that was her fadre anoue commanded hem to gone in to a ship / and delivered to
hem vytailles for half a year. And when this was done all the sustren went in
to the ship and sailed forth in the sea. and bytoke all her fre^des to appolyn
that was her god. And so long they saylled in the sea till at the last they
came and arrived in an isle that was all wilderness And when dame albyne was
come to that land and all her sustres: this albyne went forth out of the ship
and said to her othyr sustres For asmoche said she as I am the oldest suster of
all this company and first this land have taken. and for as moch^ as my name
is albyne: I will that this lord be called albion after my^ own name / and
anon^ her sustre^ granted it to her wit a good will. Tho went all the sustres
out of the ship and toke^ the land Albyo^ as her suster called it. And there
they went up and down and fond nether man ne woman ne child but wild bestes
of diverse ky^des. And when^ her vytailles were dispended and hem faylled: they
fed hem wit herbs and fruits in seson of the year / and so they leued as
they best might. and after that they token flessh^ of dyuerses bestes and
bicame wonder fat and so they desired mannys company and mannys kind that hem
failled: and for hete they woxen wonder coragious of kind: so that they
desired more mannis company than any other solace or mirthe^ When the deuel
that perceived he went by diverse co^treyes and nomme body of the eyr and
likynge natures shad of men / and come in to the land of Albion. and lay by
the wymen and shad the natures upon hem and they conceived: and after they
brought forth Geants / of the whych^ men kalled Gogmagog and an other
la^gherigan. and so they were ne^pned by diverse names: and in this manner they
came forth: and were borne horrible geants in Albyo^. and they dwelled in caves
and in hulles at her will. and had the lord of Albion as hem lyked / unto the
time that Brute arrived and came to Totnesse that was i^ the isle of albion. And
there this brute conquered and sconfyted the geants above said

Here ends the prolog of Albion: that tho was an I Will: and herkene now how
brute was gotten. and how he slow first his mother / and afterward his fader And
how he conquered Albion that after he ne^pned Bretaygne after his own name /
that now is kalled England after the name of Engist of Saxony
Capitulo primo
There was in the noble cite of great Troy a noble king and a man of great
power that was kalled Eneas / and when the cite of Troy was lost and destroyed
through heem of greece. this Eneas wit all his meyne fled the^s and come in to
lumbardie / there that tho was lord and governor of that lord a king that
was called Latyne. And an other king there was that was kalled Turocelyne. that
strongely werred upon this king Latyne. that often times did him moch^ harm:
And when this king herd that Eneas was come^. he vnderfeng hy^ with mochel
honor / and him with held for as moch^ as he had herd of hy^: and wist well
that he was a noble kinght and a worthy of his body and of his deeds This Eneas
help king Latyne in his werre. and shortly for to tell / so well and worthily
he did: that he slow Turocelyne and discomfyted hy^ and all his people. And
when all this was done: king latyne yaf all that land that was Turocelynis to
Eneas in marriage with Lauyne his daughter. the most fair creature that any
man wist: and so they lived to gedre in joy and myrthe all her lyfes time. And
after he wedded a wife / and upon her begat a sone that was called Silueyne:
and this Sylueyne wha^ he could some reason of man. vnwytyng his fadre and
against his will. acqueynted with a damisell that was cosy^ to leuine that was
king Latynes daughter the queen that was Eneas wife: and brought the damisell
with child. and when Ascamus his fadre it wist anon let enquere of the wysest
maistres and of the gretest clerks what child ye damisell should bring forth /
and they answered and said that she should bring forth a sone that should quelle
both fadre and mother. and so he did For his mother deyed in bery^g of hy^. Ad
wha^ this child was borne his fadre let call hy^ Brute. And the maistres said
that he should do much harm and sorwe in many diverse places / and after he
should come to great honor and worship This king Ascamus deyde wha^ god would
and silueyne his sone received ye land and made hy^ wonderlich^ well beloved
among his people. And when brute yt was silueynus sone was xv. year old. he
went upon a day wit his fadre for to pley and solace: and as this brute should
shete unto an heart / his arwe myshapped and glaced: and so there brute quelled
his fadre.

How Brute was driven out of the land / and how he held hy^ in greece Capitulo
secundo
ANd when this myschance befalle was: the people of the land made sorwe enough
And were sore an a^gred / and for encheson thereof they driven Brute out of the
land and would not suffer him among he^ and he saugh that he must not abide.
and went fro thens in to greece and there fond he vij.M. men that were of the
lygnage and kynryd of Troy that were come^ of great blood as the story
tells. as of men and wymen and children which were all holden in throldome
and bondage of the king Pa^dras of greece / for the death of Achylles. that was
bitraied and slain at troy / This brute was a wonder fair man and a strong
and hughe of his age and of glad chere and se^blant / and also worthy of body /
and was well beloved among his people. This king Pa^dras herd speak of his
goodness and his co^dicyons: and anon made hy^ dwell with him. so that Brute
bicome wonder pryue and moch^ beloved with the king: so that long time brute
dwelled with the king. So at ye last they of Troy and Brute spaken to gydre of
kynred and of lygnage and of acqueyntau^ce. and there pleyned hem unto Brute of
her sorwe and of her boundage / and of many other shames that the king Pandras
had hem done: and to Brute they saide^ upon a time Ye be a lord of owr lygnage
and a strong man and a mighty: be ye our capiteyn and lord / and we will
bycome yowr men and your co^mau^dements done. in all manner things: and bring
ye us out of this wrecchednesse and bondage. and fight we with the king: for
through the grace of the great god we shall hy^ overcome and we shall make you
king of the land and to you done homage / and of you we shull hold evermore.
Brut had tho great pite of her bondage that they were brought in. and preuely
he went hy^ from the kings court. and all tho that were of Troy went and put
he^ in to the wodes and in to mo^taignes. and hem held and sent unto the king
Pandras that he should give he^ leave sauelych^ for to went out of the land:
for they would no le^ger dwell in his bondage. The king Pa^dras wax tho sore
annoied: and swore that he would slay he^ euerichone: and ordained a great power
and went toward hem all for to fyght^ But brute and his men ma^ly hem
defended and fiersly foughten and quelled all ye ky^ges me^ that none of he^
escaped. and toke^ the king and hy^ held in pryso^ / and ordained cou^seyl
bitwene he^ what they might done Sum said that he should be put to death. and
sum said. that he should be exiled out of the land. and sum said that he
should be brent. And tho spoke a wise knight that was called Me^prys: and said
to Brute and to all the of Troy / if king Pandras would yield him and have his
life. I counsel that he give unto brute that is our duke and our souerayngne
his daughter Gennoge^ to his wife and in marriage with her an ho^derd ships
well arrayed: and all his tresour of gold and silver / of corn and wine: and as
moch^ as needs to have of o thing and other / and than go owte of his land and
ordeyne we us land else / were fore we ne none of owr kynred that comen after
us shall never have pees in this la^d among he^ of Greece / for we have slain
many of her knights and of her other fre^des / that ever more werre and
co^take should ben^ among us. Brute tho and all his folk consented well to
that co^seyll. and this thing they tolden to king Pandras: and therefore to have
his life he granted as much as they axed. and anon yaf unto Brute Gennoge^
his daughter to wife / and the.C ships wit as much as he^ needs of all
vytailles. as before was ordained. Brute tho took his wife and all his men that
forsook the la^d of greece / and wente^ hem unto the (...) / and hadde^ wind
and weder at will / and came^ the thridde day in to an I Will that was called
Lorgers / Brute anon^ sent of his men a land for to aspie the manner of the
co^tre. and they fonde^ an old Cite all vasted and forlet / and was therinne
nether man ne woman ne no thing dwelly^g and in the middel of this cite they
fonde^ an old temple of a fair lady that was called Dyane ye goddess And
they camen ayen^ unto brute and told him what they had seyn and fonde^ / and
counceilled hy^ to gone and to done sacrefice unto dame Dyane / For she was
wont to give answer of what thing that ever man prayed her / and namely unto
them that her honored with sacrefice. Brute went to that jmage and said. Dyane
noble goddess lady / that all thing have in might and in thy power: wyndes /
waters. wodes / feldes / and all things of ye world. and all manner of bestes
that there in ben^: To you I make my prayer that ye me counceylle and tell
where and in what place that I shall may have and find a couenable dwelling
for me and for for my people. and when I shall have fonden this by your
cou^ceill: there shall I make in the honor of you a well fair temple and a
noble. whery^ne that ye shall evermore ben honowred: When he had done his
prayer: the goddess Dyane answerde to hy^ in this manner. Brute said she. go
even forth thy wey over ye see i^to france toward the west / and there ye shall
fy^de an I Will that is kalled Albyo^ / and that isle is bycompasset all wit the sea and no man may come there in but it ben^ by ships: And in that land were
wont to be gea^ts / but nowo it is not so: but all wilderness and that
forsayde land is destynyed and ordained for you and for your people

How that the vaillau^t knight Coryn became Brutes men. and how that the king
Goffars was discomfyted Capitulo iij
When Brute herd this a^swere of Diane the goddess. anon let he the ancres
wind up and sailed in to the hygh^ see / and when he and his men had
saylled.xx. days and moo: they fonden fast beside a cost of the sea a thousand
men of the lygnage and kynred of Troy / and her sovereign and her maistre of
all was kalled Coryn. And when Brute wiste whennes they were / he tho vnderfeng
hem with moch^ joye. in to his ships. and lad he^ forth with him / This Coryn
tho become Brutes men^ / and to him he did feaulte and homage. And so so long
they saylled forth in the sea till they camen in to Gasconye^ and anon they
arrived in the haue^ of Lyrgers. and there they dwelled.viij. days he^ for to
reste^ and her saylles for to amend there that it was need.. These tydy^ges
sone camen to the king Goffar that was lord of that land / how that mochel
folk of strange land weren arrived in his land. in the haven of Lirgers:
Wherefore he was sore angered and anoyed / that they camen and arrived in his
land without leave: and anon he ordained hy^ a great power for to driven
owte. and to destroy brute with his people / But king Goffar was discomfyted
and all his folk. and him self fled in to france to seek help and socour.
And in that time reigned in France.xij / kings: and the.xj. kings assembled a
great power for to help Goffar for to fight against brute: Goffar dwelled with
hem of France half a year and more / And brute in the mean time and his
company destroyed all the la^d of gasconie and let take all the tresour that
the Goffar has: and let bring it in to his ships: And this brute fond in
that land a fair place and much couenable. and there made he a fair and a
strong castle.

When all this thing was dou^. King goffar came fro France and xj. kings
with him. and broughte^ xx.M / men for to fight against Brut and his company /
and brute had but vij.M / and / ccc / men: nevertheless when the two hosts
mete^ to gedre / brutes folk through help of him self and of Turyn his cosyn /
and of Coryn that well and manly him deffended and foughte^ so that i^ little
time they had quelled of the frenshme^ two thousand and moo / and the other
that tho were a live fled a way / And in this bataill Tury^ that was brutes
cosyn was slain / and Brut let burye him worthily wha^ he had space and leyser
in the castle that he had made / and tho let he call the castle Tours for ye
name of Turyne that there was buried / and yet in to this day there is a noble
cite that is called Tours:

When king Goffar wyste that Turyn was deed: he came again with his men: and
after yaf a strong bataill unto Brute: but brute and his men were so weary of
fyghtyng that they might no longer endure: but ma^gre him and all hise. Brute
went into his castle with all his men / and made the yates fast for to save
him self. and for to take counseyll among hem what were best for to do /
Brute and Coryn took counceill and ordained that Coryn preueli should go owte
and hyde him in a wode that there by was: till a morn / So that in the morning
when king Brute should fight wit his enemies Coryn should come with his folk in
that own side. and slay and do all the harm that he might: And on the
morning in the dawenyng Brute went owte of the castle and faught vaylliauntly
with his enemies: and they fiersly defended hem. But wythyn a little time Brute
and his folk slew viij.C of king goffars men: tho came Coryn fro the
busshement and smote to ground he and his company all that would stand or
abide. so that the King goffart and his folk were discomfited / and begone
fast to flee. and Brute and Coryn with her company fersely hem pursued and
quelyd mo of them in their fleddyng than they dyden in the bataille.

And in that manner the vaillau^t king Brute had the victory of his enemies /
But nevertheless he made moch^ sorrow for his cosyn Thury^ that there was slayn^
and for the other also of his men that he had lost in the bataille / and there
were slain of his men vij c. and xv / the which he let nobely burye in ye
castle of Tours / there that he had buried Turyn his cosyn

How king Brute arrived at Tottenesse in the I Will of Albion. and of the bataille
that was between Coryn and Gogmagog Capitulo quarto
WHen all this thing was done Brute would no longer there dwell for to fight
/ ne moo lose of his people For kynghts Goffarus people might every day encresse
moo and moo And brutes people lassen: and therefore he took all his men and went
unto the sea. and had wynd and weder at will / And the fyfthe day afterward
they arrived i^ an haven at Tottenesse: and camen in to the jle of Albion. And
there fo^de they nethir man nethir woman / as the storye tells / but ye Gea^ts
and they that were there dwelled in hills and in caves. Brute saw that the
lord was fair and at his lyking / and good also for him and for his folk. as
the goddess Dyane had him behyght. Tho was king Brute wonder glad and right
well content / and he let assemble upon a day all his folcke for to make a
solemn sacrefyce and a great fest in honowr and reverence of Dyane ye
goddess: through whose counseyll that he was comen in to that good and fair
la^d. And when they had her solempnyte made: upon a day as they sat at mete /
there camen upon hem suddenly xxx. geants. and quelled of Brutes men xxx. Brute
and his men anon sturte^ up and foughten with the geants and quelled he^
euerycho^: But one geant that was the maistre of all the other and was called
Gogmagog. He was stronger and hyer than any of the other gea^ts. and Brute kept
him and saved his life / for encheson that he should wrestell wit Coryn. for
Coryn was greter and hyer than any of brutes men. from the gerdelstede upward.
Gogmagog and Cory^ undertook for to wrastlyn ynfere* and so to gedre they
wrastled long time. But at the last Gogmagog the geant held Coryn so fast
that he brack two rybbes of his side. Wherefore the vaylliau^t knight Coryn was
sore angry: and took tho Gogmagog the geant between his arms and kast him
down upon a roche so that gogmagog brak all to pieces and so deyed he an evil
death: and therefore ye place is called yet unto this day the saulte of gogmagog
/ and tho yaf Brute all that contre to Coryn: and Coryn it kalled after his
name Cornewaille: and his men he kalled Cornewailles: and so shull the men of
that co^tre ben^ called for evermore: And in that contre dwelled Coryn and all
his men / and made there towns and howses. and inhabyted the land at her will.

How that Brute made london: and kalled this land bretaigne / and scotland
Albyne and walys Cambir. Capitulo quinto
BRute and his men wente^ forth: and sawen about i^ diverse places where they
might find a good place and couenable: that they might make a cite for him and
for his folk: So at ye last they camen by a fair River that is kalled the
Thamys. and there brute began to make a fair cite / and let call it new
Troy. in mind and remembrance of ye great Troy from which place all her
lygnage was come^ And this brute let fall a down wodes / and let cry and sow
lands / and done mow mede for sustenau^ce of him and of his people and he
departed the la^d to hem. so that euerychon of them had a certay^ place for to
dwell upon. and brute let call all this land Bretaigne after his own name.
and his folk he let call Bretons. And this brute had gotten on his wife
Geunogen three soens / that were worthy of deeds / The first was kalled Lotry^.
the second Albanak / and the thread Ca^ber. And brute bare corone in ye cite of
new Troy xx. year / after the time that the cite was made. and there he made
the laws that the Breto^s holde^ / And this noble king brute was wonderly well
beloved among all men and people. and Brutes sons also loved wonderly well to
gedre. And when this king brute had sought all ye land in le^gthe and in
bread / he fond a land that joined to Bretaign^ in the north / and that land
yaf Brute to Albanack his sone: and let kalle it Albanye after his name: that
now is kalled Scotland. And brute fond an othre contree toward the west. and
that he yaf to Camber his other sone. and he let call it Camber after his
name: and now it is kalled wales*

And wha^ Brute had reigned.xx. year as before is said: he deyed in the cite of
new Troy and there his sone him entryd wit mochel honor. And Lotryn brutes
sone was crownyd king wit mochel solempnite of all the land of Bretaigne. And
after wha^ he was crownyd: albanack and Camber his two brethren went again in
to her own contre. and lived with mykel honor. And lotryn her brother reigned
and was king and governed the land well and wisely / for he was a good man and
wonder well beloved of all his land.

And it befell so that Albanack Lotryns brother dwelled in his own land wit
mochel honor and worship and governed his la^d wisely / and then came the
king Humbar of hunla^d wit a great power and arrived i^ Albayne and would have
conquered the land: and began to werre upon Albanack. and hy^ quelled in
bataille / Wha^ albanak was slain: the folck of ye land fled unto Lotryn and
told him for he was king of Bretaigne how that his brother was slain and
prayed hy^ of help. for to avenge his brothers death. Lotrine anon^ let
assemble all the breto^s of ke^t of dover in to derewent of north folk and
southfolck of keftefen and of lyndessey / and when they were assembled they
sped fast to ward their ennemies for to give he^ bataille: Lotryne had sent to
Ca^ber his brother that he should come al so to hy^ with all the power that he
might make ^ hy^ for to help. and so he did with good will: And so they come^
all to gedres and to took her wey preuelich for to sech^ Hu^bar where they might
him find And so it betell that this Hu^bar was besides a water that was a
great river wit his folk hy^ for to dispotre. And tho came Lotryne and Ca^ber
his brother with all her folk suddenly er that any of that other wist / And when
hu^bar saw hy^ come he was sore adrad. for as much as his men wist it not. and
also they were unarmed. and anon Hu^bar for dread lept in to the water and
dre^ched hy^ self and so died he / and his men were all slain so that none
of them escaped^ and therefore is that water called Hu^bar / and evermore shall
it be called thus. for encheson that king Humbar was therinne dre^ched And
after that Lotryne went to his ships and took there all their goold and
silver / as much as he fand unto him self: and all that other pilfre he yaf
unto other folk of the host. and they founden in one of the ships a fair
damysell that was king Humbars daughter. and was kalled Estilde. And when king
Lotryne saw her / he took her with hy^ for her fayrnesse. and for her he was
overtaken wit love and would have wedded her / This tydy^ges came to Coryn. and
anon he thought to avenge him upon Lotrin / for as moch^ as lotryne had made
covenant for to spouse Corines daughter that was kalled Gue^tolen / and Coryn
in haste went to him unto the new Troy / and thus said he to the king
lotryne. Now certes said he ye reward me full evil for all the pains that
I suffered and have had many times for King Brute your fadre: and therefore I
will now avenge me upon you. and drew out his swerd an high and would have
slain the king Lotryne. but the damisell went bytwe^ne hem and made hem
accorded in this manner that king Lotryne should spouse Guentolen. which that
was Corynes daughter / and so Lotryne did: And nevertheless that he had spoused
Guentolen Corines doughtyr. preuelych^ he came to Estrilde and brought her with
child / and gate on her a fair daughter which was called Abra^. Hit befell
anon after that Corine deyed: and anon as he was ded / king lotryne forsake
Guentolen his own wife / and made Estrilde queen of his royaulme And gue^tolen
went the^s all in to Cornewaille and seysed a^le the land in her hands for
as moch^ as she was her faders heir. and vnderfong feaultres and homages of all
the men of the land. and after assembled a great host and a great power for to
ben upon lotryne avenged that was her lord. and came to him and yaf him a
strong bataylle / And there was Lotryn slain and his men discomfited / the xv.
year of his regne. Guentolen let take Estrild and Abra^ her daughter and let
bind both hands and fete and cast hem in to a water. and so they were
drenched: where fore that water was evermore called after Abram^ after the name
of ye damisel that was Estrildis daughter / And the Englisshmen calls that
water seuerne / and walshmen call it abram in to this day / And when this was
don: Gwentelon let crown her queen of that land. and governed the land full
well and wisely unto the time that Madan her sone that lotryne had beget upon
her was of.xx. winter age that he might be king. so that the queen regnyd xv.
year: and tho let she her sone crown And he reigned and governed the land well
and honorabely / and she went into Cornuwaille: and there she dwelled all her
lyfes time

Of king Madan how he reigned in pees all his lyfes tyme^ and of Menpris and of
Maulyn his sons. and how Menpris slew maulyn his brother: and how the wulfes
drow him all to pieces / Capitulo sexto
When the vaylliaunt king Madan had reigned.xxx. yere^ he deyed / And lies in
the new Cite of Troy and he had two sons / of which the own was called
Menprys and that other men kalled Maulyn / And these two brethren after her
fadres death stryuen fast for the land And Me^prys for encheson that he was the
eldest sone would gladli have had all that land but Maulyn would not grant
ne suffer him / so that they token a a day of love and accord: And at this day
Me^pris let quelle his brother through treson. and him self afterward held the
land and anon let crown him king and reigned / and after bicame so lither a
man that he destroyed in a while all the men of his land And at the last he
became so wikked and so lecherous that he forsook his own wife. and used the
sin of sodom Wherefore almighty god was wroth and upon hy^ took vengeance.
For on a day as he went in a wode an hountyng / he lost his folk: and went
allone up and down crieng after his men. and there came wulfes and all to drowe
him in to pieces / when he had reigned xxiiij. year: And wha^ his people wist that
he was deed they made joy enough: And anon made Ebrac his son king / and he
reigned with much honor.

Of King Ebrack how he conquered france and bygate xx. sons and xxiij.
doughtres: Cap. vij
THis Ebrac reigned lx. year: and he was a strong man and a mighty. And this
Ebrac through his might and the great help of his brytons conquered all France
/ and wan there so much gold and silver: that wha^ he came again in to his land
He made a noble cite / and after his name let call it ebrac / that is called
every wik / And this king made ye castle of maidenes that now is called
Edinburgh: This king had xx. sons and.xxiij. doughtres by diverse wymen gotten:
and the sons were called as ye shall here Brute grenesheld / Marga^t Seysel
Morgh with Flenghan Bladud Iaky^ Ky^bar Rocelm Spadogh Gother Kaier and
Assaruth / And the daughters hyghten as ye shall here after Elegyne ymofen
Oghdas Chel Medhan. mailour Omdur Cambredan Raga^ Re^thely Neest Chega^
Skalduld Gladus Heberhym Abalaghe and Blandan / and thees were the xxiij
daughters: and the brethere^ bycame good knights and worthy in many contrees

Of the king brute grenesheld the first sone of Ebrack the king / Capitulo
octauo
AFter the death of king Ebrac reigned Brute grenesheld his sone xxx. year: that
was Ebrakes first sone which that well and nobely reigned And when time came: he
deyed and lies at york:

Of king Leyl Capitulo ix
And wha^ Brute grenesheld was deed reigned his sone leyl xx / year: and he made
a fair town and let kalle it karlyle after his name / and was a worthy man /
and much beloved of his people. And when he had reigned xxij. year: he deyed and
lies at Carlille. And in this time reigned king Solomon in Iherusalem: and made
the noble temple / and to him came Sybelle queen of Saba / for to here and see
if it were soth that men spoke of the great and noble wit and wysedom of king
Solomon: and she fond it soth that men had her told

Of king Lud ludibras that was king Leyles sone Capitulo x.
ANd after this king leyl reigned his sone Lud Ludybras: that made the Cite of
Canterbury and of wyncestre And he reigned xiij. year: and deyed and lies at
wynchestre

Of king Bladud that was Ludibras sone How that he reigned and was a good man /
and a nygromancer Capitulo xi.
ANd after this Lud Ludibras reigned Bladud his sone: and he was a great
nygromancer / and through his craft of nygromancye: he made the meruaillous
hothe bathes as the gest tellyth^ / and he reigned xxi year and he lies at the
new troy.

Of king Leyr and of the answer of his io^gest daughter that gracyously was
married to the king of France Capitulo xij
AFter this king Bladud reigned Leir his sone / and this Leyr made the town of
lycestre. and let call the Town after his name and he governed the town well
and nobely / This king leyr had.iij. doughteres / The first was called
Gonorill. the second Rygan: and the thridde daughter was called Cordeill. and
the iongest daughter was fairest and best of condicyo^s. The king her fadre
became to an old man and would that his doughtres were married er that he deyde:
but first he thought to assaye which of hem loved him most and best: for she
which that loved hy^ best should best ben^ married. And he axed of the first
how much she him loved / and she answered and said. better tha^ her own life.
Now certes said the fadre that is a great love Tho axed he of the second
daughter / how much that she him loved. and she said. more and passy^g all
creatures of ye world / by my troth said ye fadre: I may no more axe And tho
axed he of ye thridde daughter how much she him loved / Certes fadre said she
/ my susters have told you glosing words / but forsothe I shall tell troth
/ for j love you as moch^ as j ought to love my fadre / and for to bring you
more in certain how I love you: I shall you tell / as ye been worth ye be
loved. The king her fadre wend that she had scorned him and become wonder
wroth and swore by heaven and earth she should never have good of him. but his
daughters that loved hy^ so moch^: should ben^ well auau^ced and married And ye
first daughter he married to Managles king of scotland And the second he married
to hanemos earl of cornualle. and so they ordained and spoke bitwene he^ that
they should depart the reaulme between hem two after the death of king Leyr her
fadre / so that cordeyl his youngest daughter should no thing have of his land^
But this Cordeyll was wonder fair and of so good condicyo^s and manners that
the king of France Aga^pe herd of her speak / and sent to the king Leir her
fadre for to have her unto his wife and prayed hy^ thereof And king Leir her
fadre sent hy^ word that he had departed the lord unto his ij. doughtres and
said he had no more land wherwyth her to marie And when aga^pe herd this
answer: he sent anon^ to Leir and said / that he axed nothy^g with her: but
only her clothyng and her. And anon king leir sent her over the sea to the
king of France. and he received her with much worship. and wit moch^
solempnite spoused he her / and made her queen of France

How the king Leir was driven owte of his land through his folly / and how
Cordeill his yo^gest daughter help him in his need Capitulo.xiij.
THus it fell afterward that the two eldelst doughtres would not abide till leir
her fadre was deed: but werred upon him whiles that he lived / and much sorwe
and shame hy^d did. wherefore they beno^men hy^ holy the royaulme / and bitwene
hem had ordained that one of he^ should have king Leir to soiorne all his life
time / with.xl. knights and squyers that he might worshuply go and ride
whidder that he would / in to what co^tre that he^ lyked to pley and. to
solace: So that Managles king of Scotland had king Leir with him in the manner
as is above said / and or other half year were passed / corneil that was his
eldelst daughter and queen of Scotland was so anuoyet of hy^ and of his people.
that anon she and her lord spoke to gedre. wherefore his knights half and his
squyers from hy^ were gone. and no mo left but only xxx / And wha^ this was
done Leir began for to make much sorwe for encheson that his estate was
empeired And me^ had of hy^ more scorn and despyte / than ever they had before.
wherefore he wist not what for to do: and at ye last he thought that he would go
in to Cornewaille to Rygan his other daughter. And when he was comen the earl
and his wife that was Leires daughter welcomed him and with much joy dwelled
he there wit xxx. knights and squiers And he had not dwelled there scarsely xij
months but that his daughter of hy^ was weary and of his company. and her
lord and she of hy^ had scorn and despite: so that from xxx^ knights they
broughte^ unto x / and afterward v. and so there left with him no moo: Tho made
he sorrow enough and said sore weeping. Allas that he ever cam^ into that land.
and said yet had been better to have dwelled with my first daughter: And anon^ he
went the^nes to his first daughter: but anon as she him saw come: she swore by
all the gods and by as moch^ as she might / yt he should have no mo with hi^
but one knyght^ if he would there abide / Tho began Leir ayen^ to weep and made
moch^ sorrow / and said tho / alas now have I to longelyued that this sorwe and
this meschyef to me now is fall. For now am I pour / that some time was rich
/ but now have I no friend ne kyn yt me woll do any good: But wha^ I was rich
all men me honored and worshipped: and now every man has of me scorn and
despyte. And now I wot well that Cordeil my yongeste daughter said to me troth
when she said as much as j had so much should I ben^ beloved. and all the
while that j had good tho was I beloved and honored for my richesse / but my
two daughters glosed me tho / and now of me they set little prys / and soth
told me Cordeill: but I would not believe it ne understand / and therefore j let
her go fro me as a thing that I set little prys of / And now j wot never
what for to do sith yt my two daughters me thus have disceyued that j somoch^
loved And now must I needs sech^ her that is in an other la^d that lightly I
let gone fro me wytoute any reward or yeftes: and she said that she loved me
as moch^ as she ought to love her fadre by all manner of reason. and tho I
should have axed of her no more / and so by the fair beheftes and through the false speech of my ij. eldest daughters I am disceyued. In this manner Leir long
time began to make his moan. and at the last he shope hy^ to the sea and passed
over into france / and asked and aspied where the queen might be fonde^ / and
me^ told hy^ where she was. and wha^ he cam^ to the cite there she was in /
preuely he sent his squire unto ye queen for to tell her that her fader was
comen to her for great needs And wha^ the squire came to the quen^ he told her
every dele of her susters from the beghy^nyng unto ye end / Cordeill the queen
anon^ took gold and silver plente and took it to ye squire in cou^seille that
he should gon^ and bear it unto her fadre and that he should go in a certay^ Cite
and him array and wasshe / and tha^ come ayen^ to her and bring with hy^ an
honest company of knights x^ / at lest with her meyne / and then^ he should
send to her lord the king and say yt he were comen for to speak with his
doughtir and him for to seen. and so he did. And when the king and ye queen
herd that they camen: with mochel honor they him received. and the king of
France tho let send through all his royaume and conmau^ded that all men
should to hy^ be entendaund to king Leir the queen's fadre in all manner of
thing as if it were to him self. Wha^ king Leyr had dwelled there a month and
more. he told to the king and to ye queen his doughtyr / how his.ij. eldest
doughtres had him served / Aga^pe anon let ordeyne a great host and send in
to Bretaygne with Leir the queen's fader for to conquer his land ayen^ and his
ky^gdo^. And Cordeyll also came wit her fadre into bretaigne for to have ye
royaume after her fadres death: and they went to ship and passed the sea and
came in to bretaigne and foughte^ with the felons and he^ sco^fyted and quelled
/ And tho had he his land ayen^ / and after lived three year / and held his
Royaume in pees. and afterward he deyed: and Cordeill his daughter hy^ let
e^burye with mikel honor at lycestre.

How Morgan and Conedage that were neveus to cordeyl werred upon her and put
her in to pryso^ Cap / xiiij
When that king Leir was dede^ cordeil his yo^gest daughter held and had the
land v / year. and in the mean time deyed her lord Agampe that was king of
France / and after his death she left vydue And tho came Morga^ and Conedage
that were cordeyl sustre sons and to her had enymite for as much as there
aunte should have the land. So that between he^ they ordained a great power
and upon her werred greatly: and never they rest till they had her taken and put
her un to death* And tho Morga^ and conedage seysed all the land and departed
it between hem And they helden it xij year. and wha^ ye xij year were gon^ there
began bitwene him a great debate: so yt they werred stro^gli togedre: and eueri
of hy^ did other much disese. For Morgan would have had all that land fro
beyond hu^bar that Conedage held: but he came against hy^ wit a strong power
so yt Morga^ durst not abide but fled away into wales and conedage pursued hi^
and took hi^ and queld him: Tho came Conedage again and seysed all the land in
to his hand and held it: and reigned after xxxiij year / and tho deyed he and
lies at new Troy

How Reygnold that was Conedages sone reigned aftir his fadre / and in his time
it rayned blood. three days. in tokenyng of great death Capitulo xv
ANd after this Conedage reigned Reygnold his sone a wise knight and an herdy
and curtois that well and nobeli governed the la^d. and wonder well made him
beloved of all manner of folcke: and i^ his time it rayned blood that lasted
three days as god would / and sone after there came great death of people / for it
deyde without no^bre. wherefore no man might skape till that almighty god thereof
took mercy and pite / and tho began it cese and this reignold reigned xxij year.
and dyed and lies at york

How Gorbodyan reigned in pees that was reygnoldes sone: Capitulo xvi
After this reygnold reigned Gorbodia^ his sone / xv / year: and after he dyed
and lies at york

How Gorbodyan had.ij. sons: and how that one slow that other. for to have
the heritage: and how ydoine her mother quelled that other / wherefore his la^d
was destroyed Cap. xvij
WHen this Gorbodya^ was deed. his ij. sons that he had becamen stout and
proud* and ever warred to gedre for ye la^d. the one was called Far and that
other Porres: And this ferres would have all the la^d / but that other would not
suffer hy^ / Ferres had a felo^s heart: and thought through treson to slay his
brother / But preuely he went in to france. and there abode he with the king
Syward: till upon a time when he came ayen^ and fought wit his brother ferres.
but it happed to hy^ euell^ for he was slain first / Wha^ ydome her mother wist
that porres was deed she made a great sorrow for encheson that she loved hy^
more tha^ that other. and thought hy^ for to quelle preuely. and preuely she
came to her sone upon a night wit two knyues and there with cut she his
throat. and the body also i^ to small pieces: who herd ever of such^ a kursed
mother that quelled wit her own hands her own sone / and long time after came
the reprove and shame to the mother that for encheson that own sone murdrid
that othir^ so she lost he^ both

How iiij. kings courtoisly held all Bretaigne and what ben^ her names Cap /
xviij
When the two brethren were so deed they left behynd he^ nethir sone ne
daughter ne none other of the kynred that might have the heritage / and for as
moch^ as the stre^gest men dryue^ and sco^fyted ye feblest and toke^ all her
lands: so that in every country they had great werre and strife under thay^.
but among all other things there were among he^ in the co^tre that overcame
all the other / and through stre^gth^ and might they token all the lands. and
every of thay^ took a certay^ contre. and in his contre let kalle hy^ king: and
one of he^ was called Scater / and he was king of scotland. and that other was
called Dawailliere. and he was king of loegers and of all the la^d that was
lotrinus that was brutes sone. The thridde was called rudac and he was king of
walys: And yt iiij was called Cloten and he was king of cornewaille / But this
clote^ should have had all the land by reso^. for there was no man that wist
non^ so rightful heyr as he was / But they that were stre^ghest set little by
he^ that were of less estate: and therefore this clote^ had no more la^d among
he^ than cornewaylle

Of king Doneba^t that was clotes sone: and how he had wo^ne the la^d: Capitulo
xix
THis clote^ had a sone that was called Doneba^t that after the death of his
fadre became an herdy man and a fair and curtois. so that he passed all ye
ky^ges of britaigne of france in ma^hede and worthynesse And anon^ as he was a
knight he wist well wha^ that his fader lived he was most rightful heyr of all
the la^d. and should have had it by reason / but other kings yt were of more
stre^gth^ than he was / beno^me hy^ his la^d. And afterward this Donebant
ordained him power / and first conquered he all ye land of Loegiers and after
he would have conquered all Scotland and walys: and Scater cam^ with his men
and yaf hy^ bataill. and Rudac cam^ aye^ with his walshmen for to help him.
but it befell so that Rudak was queled and scater also in play^ bataill. and so
donebant had the victory and conquered all the land: and well maintened it in
pees and in quiet / that never before it was so well maintened.

How Donebant was first king that ever wered crown of gold in Bretaigne
Capitulo xx
This donebant let make hy^ a croune of gold and wered ye crown upon his head
as never king did before: and he ordained a statut / that had a man done never
so moch^ harm if he might come in to yt temple no man should hy^ misdo / but
gon^ therein sauf and in pees / and after go in to what country hy^ lyked / and
if any man set any ho^de upon hy^ / he tha^ should lose his life And this
Donebant made the town of Malmesbury and the town of ye vyse: and wha^ he had
reigned well and wortheli xl. year he deyed and lies at new Troy

How Brenne and Bely^ departed bitwene thay^ ye la^d after the death of doneba^t
her fadre and of the werre Capitulo xxi
ANd after that this Doneband was deed / his sons that he had departed the
land bitwene he^ as her fader had ordained. so that Bely^ his eldest sone had
all the land on this half humbar. and his brother Bre^ne had all the la^d from
humbar unto scotland / but for as moch^ that belyn had the best part / Bre^ne
therefore was wroth and would had more of the la^d: and Belyn his brother would
grant hi^ no more. wherefore co^tak and werre arose between he^.ij. but Bre^ne
the younger brother had no might ne strength aye^s bely^ / and therefore bre^ne
through co^seyl of his folck went fro the^s in to norwey to ye king Olsinges and
prayed hy^ of help and socour for to conquer all ye la^d upon Belyn his
brother upon that covenant that he would have his daughter to wife / and the
king Olsinges him granted. Belyn anon as his brother was to norwey: he seized
in to his hand all ye land of Northumberland / and took all the castelles /
and let hem array and keep the costs of the sea that brenne should not arryue
in no side but that he were take The king Olsinges let assemble a great host
and delyuerd his doughtyr to bre^ne and all that to hy^ was necessary. and
this damisell Samye had long time loved a king that was called gutlagh^ and to
hy^ she told all her counsel / how that bre^ne should have her: and her led
with hy^ for evermore: and so he should lose her wtoute she might forsake and be
delivered from Bre^ne. and wha^ gutlagh had herd this tidy^g he lay for to
aspye bre^ne with as many ships as he might have: so that ye ij. fletes mette^
to gedre and fougte^ long time / so that Bre^ne and his ships turned ayen^
and were disco^fyted / and king gutlagh took samie and put her i^ to his
ship: and Bre^ne shamefulli fled then^s as a man disco^fyted / And gutlagh
would have gone i^to his own co^tre: but there came upon hy^ a great tempest
that v. days lastyd. so that through that tempest he was driven into Bretaigne
wit iv / ships and no mo / and tho that kept the costs of ye see token
Gutlagh and famye and all his folk. and he^ presented to belyn. and belyn put
he^ in to prison

How belyn drofe out of his land king Gutlagh of De^marke and Samye Ca / xxij
HIt was not long after ye Bre^ne came ayen^ with a great nauye and se^te to
his brother Bely^ / that he should yield ayen^ his land. his wife. his folk. and
his castelles. or else he would destroy his land / Bely^ drade no thing his
menace and would no thing don after that his desire. Wherefore bre^ne came with
his folk and fought with belyn / Brenne was disco^fyted and his folk slain:
and hy^ self fled with xij / men into france And this Belyn that was Brennes
brother went to york and took cou^seyl what he might don with king Gutlagh.
For king gutlagh profred to become his man and to hold his land of hy^
yeldy^g by year a thousand pound of silver for ever more / and for sikernesse
of this couenaunts to behold Gutlagh should bry^g him good hostages and to him
should done homage and all his folk / and yet he should swear upon a book yt
these couena^ts should never ben^ broke ne falsed / Belyn tho by counseyl of his
lords and of his folk granted hy^ his axyng / And so Gutlagh became his man
/ and belyn vnderfeng of hy^ his homage by oath and by writing the same
couena^ts. And upon these couena^ts king Gutlagh no^me samye and his folk. and
went the^s and turned again to denmarck / Evermore after. were the covenants
holden and the truage paid till the time that Honelos was king of Denmark /
and also of this land through his wife Gildeburgh that he had spoused^ for she
was the right heir of this land This Bely^ dwelled in pees and worshipfully
him held among his barons. and he made iiij real weyes one from the Est in to
the west: and that was kalled watlyngstrete: and an other / from the north unto
the south. that was called jkelmestrete / and ij. other weyes he made i^
bossy^ge through out the land. that on is called toss / and that other
fossedike. and he mai^tened well ye good laws that Donebant his fadre had made
and ordained i^ his time. as before is said

How accord was made bitwene Bre^ne and Bely^ through Cornewen her mother Ca /
xxiij
BRe^ne that was Belynus brother had long time dwelled in trau^ce: and there had
he conquered a great lordship through marriage / For he was duke of Bourgoyn^ /
through the daughter of the duke Fewy^ that he had spoused. that was right heyr
of the land And this Bre^ne ordained a great power of his folk / and also of
france. And he came in to this land for to fight with king Bely^ his brother:
and Belyn came also against him with a great power of bretons / and would have
yeuen hy^ battle / but their mother Cornewenne that tho lived had herd yt one
brother would have destroyed that other: and went between her sons and hem
made accorded with much pain. so that at the last ye two brethren with
michell blys went to gedre in to great Troy / that now is called London / and
there they dwelled a year. and after they took their cou^seil for to gone
conquer all france / and so they dyde^: and brent towns and destroyed the
land both in length^ and bread. and the king of france yaf hy^ battle with
his power. but he was over comen: and yaf truage unto Belyn and to his brother.
And after that: they wenten forth to Rome and conquered Rome and all Lu^bardye
/ and Germanye / and took homage and feaulte of Earls Barons and of all other.
And after they camen in to this land of Bretaigne and dwelled with Bretons
here in joy and rest: And tho made Bre^ne ye town of Bristowe / and sith he
went over to his own Lordship and there dwelled he all his life. and Belyn
dwelled at new Troy / and there he made a fair gate that is kalled
belyngesgate after his own name. And when this Belyn had reigned nobely xj.
year he dyed and lies at new Troy

How king Cormbatrus quelled the king of De^marc for encheso^ that he would not
pay hi^ his truage Capitulo xxiiij
And after this bely^ reigned his sone Cormbatrus a good man and worthy. and ye
king o^ de^marke would not pay hy^ his truage: that is to say M. pound as he
had sworn by oath for to pay it ^ and also by writing recorded to bely^ his
fadre ^ Wherefore he was evil paid For this king Cormbatrus assembled a great
host of Brytons and went in to De^marke and slow the king gut^ath and brought
the la^d in subiectyo^ all new. and took of the folk feaultes and homages.
and after he went ayen^ in to his la^d. and as he came forth by Orkeney: he
fo^de xxx. ships full of men and women besides the kost of the sea. and ye
king axed what they were / An earl that was maistyr of hem all courtoysly
a^swerd unto ye king and said that they were exiled out of spaigne and so that
they had trauailled half a year and more in the sea. for to wyte^ if they might
find any king in any lord that of he^ would have pity or mercy to give he^
any land in any contre / where in they might dwell and have rest and become
his liege men and to hy^ would done homage and feaulte whiles that he lived and
to his heirs after hy^ / and of hy^ and his heirs holden that land / and
when the king this herd. he had pity of he^ and yafe he^ an I Will al wilderness
there yt noma^ was dwelling saufe only wild bestes / and the earl thanked
moch^ the king. and became his man. and did hi^ homage and feaulte: and took
all his folk and went in to the same jle. and the earl was called Irlamall^ and
therefore he let call that land jrla^de after his own name: The king Cormbatrus
came ayen^ in to his la^d / and reigned xxv. year / and after he deyd and lies
at new Troy

How king Morwith deyed a myschevous death through a best for his wilderness Ca
xxviij
AFter this Howa^ reigned morwith / and became wicked and so stern: till at the
last great vengeance came to hy^ For as he went upon a time by the sea side:
he mete a great best yt was black and horrible and hydous / and he we^d that it
had ben^ a whale of the sea / and bent an alabastre and would have slain that
best wit a quarrel. but he might not smite hy^ And when he had shot all his
quarelles the best anon^ came to hy^ in a great have and hy^ devoured a life /
and so he deyed for his wikkednesse through ve^gau^ce* of god / after that he

Of Gra^dobodia^ that was morwiths sone that made the town of Cambrigge:

Of Artogaill that was Grandobodianus sone / how he was made king: and sith put
a down for his wikkednesse Capitulo xxx
AFter Grandobodian reigned his sone Arthogaille v / year. and he became so

How Lud was made king after the death of Ely his fadre Capitulo xxxiiij
AFter the death of Ely reigned Lud his sone and governed well the land. and
much honored good folk and tempred and amendet wicked folk: This lud loved
more to dwell at troy tha^ in any other place of ye la^d wherefore ye name of
new Troy was left and tho was the cite kalled ludstone But the name is
changed through variance of lre^s and now is kalled London And this king made
in the cyce a fair gate and kalled it ludgate after his name / and ye folk of
the cite hete it Londres: and wha^ he had reigned xj year. he deide and lies at
London And he had two young sons Andraghe^ and Tormace / but they could nether
speak ne go for yonthe. and therefore ye breto^s crowned a stro^gh knight that
was called Lud: and was Cassibalamus brother and made hy^ king of Bretaigne

How the bretons granted to cassibalam that was Ludes brother the land In whose
time Julius caesar came twyes for to conquer the land Capitulo xxxv
AFter the death of king Lud reigned his brother cassybalam and bicame a good man
and much beloved of his bretons. so that for his goodness and curtosie they
granted hy^ the royaulme for evermore to him and to his heirs And the king of
his goodness let norisshe worthelych^ both^ sons that were lud his brothers
sons And after made he ye eldest sone Earl of Cornewaille. and that other earl
of London / And while the king Cassibalay^ reigned: came julyus caesar that was
emperor of Rome in to this land with a power of Romans / and would have had
this la^d through strength / but Cassybalay^ overcame him in bataill through
help of the Bretons and drofe him owte of this land. and he went ayen^ to rome
and assembled a great power an other time: and come ayen^ in this land for to
give bataille to Cassibalan. but he was discomfyted through strength^ of the
breto^s. and through help of the earl of Cornewaille and the earl of london his
brother. and through help of Gudyan king of Scotland / and corband king of
northwalys. and of Brytail king of southwalys: and in this battle was slain
oon that was cassibalans brother / wherefore he made much sorwe. and so went
Julius caesar out of this la^d with a few of romans that were left a live /
and tho went cassibala^ ayen^ to London and made a fest unto all his folk yt
tho had hy^ help. And wha^ that feste was done: each man went into his own
contre

Of the debate that was bitwene Cassybala^ and the earl of London / and of the
truage that was paid to Rome Cap / xxxvi
ANd after it befell thus upon a day that the gentil men of ye ky^ges household
and ge^till men of the Earls household of london after mete went together for to
play. and through debate that arose among he^ Euelyn that was the earls cosyn
of London queld jrenglas that was the kings cosyn. wherefore the king swore that
Euelyn should be hanged: but the Earl of London that was Euelinus lord would not
suffer it / wherefore the king was wroth toward the Earl and thought hy^ to
destroy. And preuel^ the Earl sent ^re^s to Julius caesar. that he should come
in to his land for to help hy^: and hy^ avenge upon the king: and he would
help hy^ with. all his might. And when the emperor herd this tydy^g: he was
full glad and ordained a strong power and came ayen^ the thridde time in to
this la^d. and the Earl of London halp him wit.vij.M. men. And at the thridde
time was cassibala^ ouercome^ and disco^fyted and made pees to the Emperor /
for three thousand pound of silver: yeldy^g by year for truage for this land
for evermore: And half a year passed the Emperor went to Rome: and the Earl of
london with him: for he durst not abide in this land. And after cassybalam
reigned xvij year in pees: and tho deyed he the / xvij. year of his regne: and
lies at york

Of kymbalay^ that was Andragenes sone a good man. and well governed the land.
Capitulo xxxviij
AFter the death of Andrage^ reigned ky^balaym his sone that was a good man and

Of king Gynder that was kymbalaynus sone that would not pay the truage to Rome
for the land that Cassybala^ had granted. and how he was slain of ye
romay^s Capitulo xxxix
ANd aftyr the death of this kymbalay^ reigned Gy^der his sone a good man and a
worthy: and he was of so hygh^ heart that he would not pay to Rome that truage
that king Cassibalay^ had granted unto Julius Caesar / wherefore the Emperor
that tho was that was called Claudius caesar / was sore annoyed and ordained a
great power of romans. and camen in to this land for to co^quere the truage
through stre^gthe and have it of the king / but the king Gynder and Armager his
brother gadred a great host to gydre of bretons and yafe the bataylle to the
Emperor Claudius. and quelled of the Romans great plente: The emperor had a
knight that was kalled Hamo^ / that saw that his people were fast slayn^ /
preuelich^ he kast a way his own arms. and took the arms of a deed breton
and armed him wit his armure: and came in to the bataill to the king and said
in this manner / Sir be ye of good heart for goddis love: for the romay^s that
ben^ your enemies anon shall be slain and disco^fyted euerychon And ye king
yaf no keep ne reward to his spech^ for encheson of the arms that he had upon
him and wend it had been a breton But the traitor ever held him next the
king. and preuely under ye shuldres of his arms he smote ye king that he was
deed and fell dou^ to the earth. Wha^ armager saw his brother deed he cast
away his arms and took to him his brothers arms and came i^ to ye bataill
among the Bretons / and bad hem hertely for to fight. and fastely a down the
romans: and for the arms they wende^ it had been the king Gynder that erst was
slayn^ that they wist not. Then^ gone the Bretons hertely fight and quelled ye
romans / so that at the last ye emperor forsake the field and fled as fast
as he might with his folk in to the cite of Wynchestre. and the false traitor
hamo^ that had queld the king began anon^ fast for to fle with all the have
that he might / And Armager the ky^ges brother pursued him full ferseiy with a
ferse heart* and drofe hy^ unto a water: and there he took him. and anon smote
of both^ hands head and feet and hew the bodi all to pieces and cast hy^ in to
the water / wherefore the water was called hamonus haue^. and afterward there was
made a fair town that yet stands and is kalled soupthanpto^. and afterward
Armager went to wy^chestre for to seek Claudius caesar the Emperor. and there
Armager him took. and Claudius ye Emperor through counsel of his romans
that with hy^ were left a live made pees wit Armager / in this manner as ye shall
here. that is to say / how that Claudius the Emperor should give to Armager
Gennen his fair daughter for to have to wife: so that this la^d fro that time
afterward should be in the emperors power of rome: upon such covenant yt
never afterward none Emperor of rome should take non^ other truage of this la^d
but only feaulte and so they were accorded. And upon this covenant Claudius
caesar sent to rome for his daughter Gennen / and wha^ she was comen claudius
caesar yaf her to Armager for to be his wife And armager spoused her at london
with much solempnite and mirthe / and tho was armager crouned and made king of
Bretaigne

Of king Armager in whose time saint petre preched in Anthiochie with the other
apostoles in diverse contreyes Ca. xl
And this king Armager reigned well and worthily and the land governed And
claudius caesar in remembrance of this accord and for the reverence and honor
of his daughter made in this land a fair town and a fair castle. and let
call the town after his name claucestren that now is kalled Gloucestre: And
when this was all done: the emperowr took his leave / and he went ayen^ to rome.
And armager was tho king and governed the land well and nobely all his lyfes
time / and this Armager got a sone on his wife / that was kalled westmer / And
whiles that this king Armager reigned / saint petre preched in Anthyoche. and
there he made a noble chyrch^ / in which he sat first and there he dwelled
vij. year / and after he went to rome / and was made pope till that Nero the
emperor let him martre: and tho preched openly all the apostles in diverse
lands the right faith. And wha^ Armager had reigned xxiiij year / he deyed and
lies at london

How the king Westmer yaf to Berynger an Island forlet / and there this Berynger
made the town of Berewyke Capitulo xli.
ANd after this Armager reigned his sone westmer a good man and worthly. and
well governed the land Hit befell so that tydynge came to him on a day. that
the king Rodryck of Gasconye was come^ in to his land wit a great no^bre of
people. and was dwelyng in stainesmore / and when king westmer herd these
tidings: he let assemble an great host of Breto^s. and came to the king
rodryck and yaf hy^ bataill / and king westmer queld rodryck wit his own
hands in plain bataill And when king rodrykes men saw that her lord was
deed. they yolden him all unto ye king westmer. and bicame^ his men for
evermore. and he yaf hy^ a contre that was forlete^ / wheryn they might dwell:
And thydder they went and dwelled there all her lyfes time / and ixC / men
there were of hem / and no mo left at that bataille Her gouerneur and prince
was kalled Berynger: and anon^ he began a town to make: that they might
thery^ne dwell and have restorte and let kalle the town Berewik upon twede:
and there they dwelled and bycame rich. but they had no women among hem: and
the Breto^s would not give her doughtres to the strangers. wherefore they went
over the sea in to the Irland and brought with hy^ women and spoused thay^. but
the men koude not understand that la^gages ne the speech of the women: and
therefore they spaken to gedre as scotts: and afterward through changyng of her
langages in all france they were called the scotts / and so shulle^ that
folk of that contre ben^ kalled for evermore

How king Westmer let arere a stone in the entryng of westmerland / there that
he had slain king Roderyck^ and there he began first howsing Capitulo xlij
ANd after this bataill that is above said when roderyk was deed / king westmer

and yet hit stant and evermore shall it stand. and let grave in the stone
lre^s that thus said. The king westmer of Bretaigne quelde in this place
Roderyk his enemy. And this Wastmer was the first man that made towns and
house in england. and at that stone begy^neth westmerla^d that westmer let call
aft his own name And wha^ westmer had so done: he dwelled all his lyfes time
in that contre of westmerla^d For he beloved that contre more than any other

Of king Coil that was westmers sone that held his land in pees al his lyfes

After this king westmer reigned his sone coyl a good man and a worthy and of

How king lucie reigned after coill his fadre that was a good man and after he
becam christian Ca xliiij
After king coil reigned lucye his sone yt was a good man to god and to all ye
people: He sent to rome to that apostle Eule^tre that tho was pope and said / he
would become a cryste^ man and receive baptism in ye name of god and torn to
the right believe: Eule^tre sent two legatys that were called Pagan and elybayne
in to this land and baptized the king and all his main. and after went they
fro town to town and baptized the people till all the land was baptized: and
this was in the Clvj year after ye incarnacion of our lord ^hu^ crist. and this
king made tho. ij erche bisshoppes / on at ca^terburye an other at york / and

his land and reigned with mochel honor xij year: and after dyed and lies at
