How this la^d was long without a king and how ye breto^s chose^ a king C. xlv
THis king Lucie had none heir of his bodi bygote^ yt was atterward great harm
and sorrow to ye la^d For after this king Lucies death none of the great of the
la^d would suffer an other to be king / but lived in werre and in debate among
hem l. year without king But it befell afterward that a great prince came fro rome
into this land that men called seuerie. naught for to werre: but for to save ye
right of rome / but natheles he had not dwelled half a year i^ this la^d yt ye
breto^s ne quelled he^. wha^ they of rome wist that Seuerye was so slain. they
sent an other great lord into this land that me^ kalled Allec that was a strong
man and a mighty of body^ and dwelled in this land long time / and did moch^
sorwe to the Breto^s. so that aftyr for pure malice they chosen hem a king
among hem that men kalled astlepades. and assembled a great host of bretons
and went to London to sech^ allec: there they fo^den him and queld him and all
his felaws: and one that me^ kalled walon defended hy^ fersely and fought long
with the bretons: But at the last he was discomfyted and the bretons nomme hi^
and bounde^ hands and feet and kast hy^ into a water. wherefore that water was
called afterward walbroke / Tho reigned Astlepades in quyete till one of his
Earls that men kalled Coill. made a fair town ayens ye kings will and let
kalle the town Colchestre after his name / wherefore the king was full wroth and
thought to destroy the Earl / and began to werre upon him. and brought great
power and yaf batail to the earl: and the earl defended hy^ fersely with his
power and slow the king him self in that bataille and tho was Coill crowned
and made king of this land: This Coil reigned and governed the royaulme well and
nobely: for he was a noble man and well beloved among the Breto^s: Wha^ they of
Rome herden that Astlepades was slain: they were wonder glad. and sent an
other great prince of Romans / which was kalled Constau^ce. and he came to
the king Coyll for to challenge ye truage that was wont to be paid to rome. And
the king a^swerde well and wisely: and said that he would pay to rome all that
reason would with good will: And so they accorded and without any contak both
they dwelled to gedre in love / The king Coill yaf his daughter Eleyne to
Consta^ce for to have her to his spouse. which that was both fair wise and
good and well lettred. And this Consta^ce spoused her there with moch^ honor.
and it befell sone afterward that this King coyll deyed in the year of his
regne xiij / and lies at Colchestre entiered

Of king Constance that was an Romay^: which was chosen king after the death of
Coyll. for as much yt he had spoused Eleyn which that was king Coyles
daughter Capitulo xlvi
AFter this king Coyl Co^stance was made king. and crowned for as much as that
he had spoused king Coyles daughter which was heir of the land. The which
Consta^ce reigned well and wortheli governed the land. and he begat on his wife
Eleyn a sone that was called Co^stantyne. and this king bare true faith and
truly did to hem of Rome all his life / And when he had reigned xv. year: he
dyed and lies at york.

How Constantyne that was king Constances sone and the sone of saint Eleyn /
governed and ruled the land. and was an Emperor of Rome Capitulo xlvij /
AFter king Co^sta^ce reigned Constantine his sone and the sone of seint Eleyne
yt fond the holy cross in the holy land / and how Constantyne became
Emperor of Rome / Hit befell so in that time There was an emperor at Rome a
sarazyne a Tyrant that was called Maxencyus / which that put to death all that
believed in god and destroyed the holy chirch^ by all his power: and slew all
the christian men that he might fy^de. And among all other he let martre saint
Kateryne / and many other christian people that for dread of death they fledde^ and
camen in to this land to the king Constantine and told him of the sorwe that
Maxence did to cristie^te Wherefore Consta^tyne had great pity and made moch^
sorrow. and assembled a great host and a great power / and went over to rome
and took ye cite and quelled all that there in were of mysbeleue that he might
find. and tho was he made Emperor: and was a good man. and governed hy^ so
well that all lands to him were atte^dau^t for to ben under his gouernaill /
And this deuel Tyrant Maxence that time was in ye land of Greece and herd this
tydynge / then^ he became wode. and suddenly he dyed / and so he ended his life:
When Constantine went fro this land to Rome he took with him his mother Eleyne.
for the mochel wisdom that she could. and other great lords yt he most
loued^ that one was called Hoell. and the other was called taberne. and the
thridde Morhin. and took all his land to keep unto the earl of Cornewaille
that was called Octauia^: and anon^ as this octauyan wist that his lord was
dwelly^g at rome. he seized all the land in to his hand. and therewith did all
his will. among high^ and low. and they held him for king. When this tydinge
came to Consta^tyne the emperor: he was wonder wroth toward ye earl Octauyan /
and sent Taberne with xij.M. men for to destroy the earl for his falsenesse.
and he arrived at Portesmouth / And when Octauyan wiste that: he assembled a
great power of Bretons and disco^fyted Taberne / and Taberne fled thens in to
Scotland / and ordained there a great power. and came ayen^ in to this land an
other time for to give bataille to Octauia^ / When Octauya^ herd tell that.
he assembled a great power and cam^ toward Taberne as much as he might: so
that the two hosts mette^ upon steinesmore and stro^geli smoten to gydre. And
tho was Octauyan disco^fited and fled thens in to Norwey. and Taberne seysed
all the land in to his hands. towns castelles asmoch^ as they there had And
since this Octauia^ came ayen^ fro Norwey wit a great power and seysed ayen^ all
the land in to his hand. and drofe out all the Romans. and was tho made king
and reigned

How Marunia^ that was ye emperors Cosyn of rome spoused Octauians daughter
and was made king. Capitulo xlviij
THis king Octauyan governed the land well and nobely: but he had non^ heir sauf
a doughtyr that was a yo^ge child that he loved asmoch^ as his life / and for
as much that he was seek and was in point of death and might no longer regne:
he would have made one of his neveus to have ben^ king / the which was a noble
knight and a strong man which was called Conan meriedok. and he should have
kept the kings doughtyr and have married her wha^ time had ben^. But the lords
of the land would not suffer it: but yaf her cou^seill to be married to so^me
hygh^ man of honor. and tha^ might she have all her lust and take cou^seil of
ye emperor Constantine her lord. And at this cou^seill they accorded and chose
tho Cador of Cornewaill for to went to ye emperor for to do this message. and
he took the wey and went to Rome and told to ye emperor this tyding well and
wisely / and the Emperor sent into this land with hi^ his own cosyn that was
his uncles sone a noble knight and a strong that was called Maxymian: and he
spoused Octauianus doughtyr / and was crowned king of this land

How Maximian that was the emperors cosyn conquered Almorican. and yaf it to
Cona^meriedok. Cap. xlix
THis king Maxymia^ bicame so ryall that he thought to co^quere the land of
Amorycan for great richesse that he herd tell yt there was in that land: so
that he ne left man that was of worthiness knight squier ne none other man /
that he ne took wit him to great damage of all the land For he left at home
behynd hi^ no man for to keep the land / but he took hem with him fro this
land.xxx. thousand knights that were doubthy mennys bodies: and went over in
the land of Amorican: and there slew he the king the which was called Imball:
and conquered all the land And wha^ he had so done he kalled Cona^ and said^
for as moch^ as king Octauyan have made you king of Bretaigne and through me ye
were let and destrobled that ye were not king I give you all this land of
Amorican / and make you thereof king And for as much as ye ben a breton and
your men also and become fro bretaigne I will that this la^d have the same name
and no more be kalled Amorica^ / but it shall be called lyttel Bretaigne: and the
la^d fro whe^s ye ben comen shall be called mochel bretaigne: and so shall me^
know that one Bretaign^ fro that other / Conan moriedok thanked hi^ frendeli.
and so was he made king of littel bretaigne. And wha^ all this was don Maximian
went the^s to rome / and was tho made Emperor after Constantyne / Conan
meriedok dwelled in littel bretaigne with mochel honor and let ordeyne ij.M.
plougme^ of the land: for to erye the land to harwe it and saw / and fessed
he^ richely after that they were: and for as much as king Conan ne none of his
knights or of his people would no take wifes of the nacyon of france. he sent
tho in to great Bretaigne to ye earl of Cornewaille that men called Dyonothe.
that he should chese through out all the land xj.M / of maidens that is to
say. viij / M / for the mean people and three thousand for the gretest lords
that should hem spouse: And when Dionothe vnderfounge this commandment he let
seche through all ye great bretaygne as many as the nombre came to: for no man
durst withstonde his commau^dements for as much as all the la^d was taken to
hymward and to keep to done all thing that hem good lyked And when all the
mayde^s were assembled he let hem come before him to london: and let ordeyne
for he^ ships hastily asmoch^ as he^ needs to ye vyage and took his own
doughtere that was called Vrsula: that was the fairest creature that any man
wist / and would have sent her to king Conan that should have spoused her and
made her queen of the land / but she anon made preuely to god a vow of
chastity that her fadre wiste not ne no man else that was living upon the
earth.

How vrsula and xi.m. maide^s that were in his company went toward little
Bretaigne: and were all martred at Coleyne Cap. l.
THis Vrsula chese on her company xi m. maide^s. that of all other she was
lady and maistresse: and all they went into the ship at one time. in ye
water yt was called the Tamyse and conmau^ded her kyn and all her friends to
almighty god: and sailled toward little Bretaigne. But when they were come^
into ye hygh^ see / a strong te^peste arose as it was goddis will. And vrsula
wit her ships and her conpanye were dryue^ toward hundla^d through tempest and
arrived in the haue^ of the cite of Coleyne. The king of ye la^d that was
called Gowan was tho in ye Cite / and wha^ he wist the tyding that so many fair
maide^s were there arrived. he took Elga his brother and other of his household
with him: and went to the ships to see^ that fair company / and when he saw
hem so fair: he and his company would have over feign he^ and betake fro hem
her mayde^hode. But vrsula that good maid cou^seilled / prayed / warned and
thought hem that were her felawes that they should defend he^ with all her
might. and rather suffer the death than suffer her body to be defowled / so that
all the maidens became so steadfast in god that they he^ defended through his
grace so that none of hem had power to done he^ any shame wherefore the king
Gowan was sore anoyed: that he for wroth let slay hem euerychone. and so were
all the maydenes martred for the love of god / and lain at Coleyne

How king Gowan came for to destroy this la^d. And how a man of great power
that was kalled Gracyan deffended this land Capitulo lj.
WHa^ all this was don. king Gowa^ that was a sarezy^ called his brother Elga.
and said to hy^ that he should go to co^quere ye la^d that all the fair mayde^s
were in borne. And he ordained tho a great power of pechitet / of Denmark. of
orkoney / and of norwey / And they came into this land and bre^t towns and
slew folck and cast a down chyrches and houses and religion / and robbed the
la^d in le^ght and bread / and put to death all the that would not forsake the
right believe and criste^dome: and for as moch^ as there was no sovereign that
might he^ help. For the king Maxymian had taken wit hy^ all ye worthy men:
and was goon to co^quere littel bretaign^^ and in the same time that ye here
now tell. was saint Albone martred through ye wode tyrant Dyoclisia^ in the
same place where is now an abbye made of seint Albone whiles yt he was a
paynyme. but he converted hi^ to god through the predicacyon of a clerk and a
wise man that was called Antybell / that was herburghed a night in his house.
and this was after the incarnacyon of jesu crist / cc.xxvi. year. And me^ shall
understand that saint Albone suffered his martyrdom before that saint Edmond
was martred. and therefore is sey^t Albone called the first Martyr of England /
This Gowannes brother and his folk that were sarasynes went through out the
land: and destroyed all thing that they fonden. and no thing they ne spared.
When this tydy^g cam^ to rome. how that king Gowan had bigonne for to destroy
this land / the Emperor of Rome sent a strong man and of great power that was
called Gracia^ wit xxiiij M. men well fyghtyng for to cast out Sarasenes out of
this land And all they arrived at ports mouth / Maximian might not come him
self for as moch^ as he was chosen Emperor after the death of Consta^tinus
that was saint Elynes sone / When this gracya^ was arrived with his host / he
let aspie preuely where the king Gowa^ might be fonde^: and he came upon hem
suddenly as they lay in her beds and discomfited him and slew hem in her
beds every cho^ that non^ of hem escaped sauf Gowan that fled with much
sorrow into his contre / Sone aftir this Maximian was slain at Rome through
treson. And when Gracyan wist that tydyng he let crown hy^ self king of this
land.

How Gracyan made him self king when Maximia^ was slay^ And afterward ye
Bretons queld him for his wikkednesse. C. lij /
THis Gracya^ wha^ he began to regne / he became so wikked and stern / and so
moch^ did he to ye breto^s that they slow hy^ among he^. Tho ye king Gowan
had understood that Gracya^ was slain and down to death he assembled a great
power and came ayen^ into this la^d. and if he had ers^don^ harm: tho did he
moch^ more. for tho destroyed he all this land and the criste^ people that was
in much Bretaign^ / so that no man was so herdie for to nempne god and he that
so did anon^ he was put to strong death: But the bishop of london that was tho
that was called Gosseley^ / escaped and went the^s to the^ of Rome to seche
socour to help to destroy the sarrazenes yt had destroyed this land. And the
romay^s sayde^ that they had be so often anoyed for her sending after folk in
to bretaigne all for to help ye breto^s and they would not more so done. And
so ye bishop Gosseleyne went the^s without any socour or help: And tho went
he to the king of little bretaigne that was kalled Aldroye / and this was the
thridde king after Gowa^ meriedoke as before is said / The bishop prayed this
king Aldroye of help and socour: The king had great pity in his heart when he
had herd how the Bishop fled: and how the Christian men weren slain in great
Bretaigne through paynyms and sarazenes / He granted him Constantyne his
brother for to help hy^ wit power of folk: and him did array horse armure and
ships and all thing that hem needs to that vyage: And when all thing was
ready he called the bishop and to hy^ said I take you here to help and socour
Co^sta^tyn^ my brother upon this covenant that if god give him grace the
paynymes and the sarazenes to shende and to disco^fyte that than ye make hy^
king. And the bishop granted it hy^ with a good will. Constantyne and the
bishop took leave of the king Aldroye / and betok hem to god / and delyuerd
thaym xij M men / and went to her ships and sailled toward great bretaigne /
and arrived at Totenesse. Wha^ the bretons herd the tidings that to he^ came
socour / they were stro^gely helped and ordained he^ an hughe nombre of people.
and cam^ to he^ with moch^ honor. Gowa^ anon^ as he wist of his tidings he
assembled all the sarazenes and came against hem and yafe hem bataille. and
Constantyne slow him with his own hands. And all the other sarazenes were
discomfyted and slain that non^ escaped but they that were converted unto god

How Co^stantyne that was the kings brother of little Bretaign^ was crowned
king of mochel bretaigne for his worthynesse Capitulo liij
ANnone after the bataylle they went to london and crouned there Consta^tyne /
and made hy^ king of this land: and the bishop Gosselyne set the croune on
his head and anoyted him as falls to a king for to ben^ / and tho began
criste^dome: This king Co^sta^tine when he was crowned anon after he spoused
his wife through ye counseyll of the Bretons. and he begat three sons on her:
The first was called Constance^ that other Aurelambros / and the thridde Vter
/ Consta^ce the eldest brother wha^ he came to age he made hi^ a monk at
Wyncestre. Consta^tyne her fadre was slain through treson: for it befell on a
time that Pehite came to hy^ upon a day in message as it were and said that he
would speak preuely with the king in counseyl. The king let void his chamber
of ye men yt were wythy^ne / and there abode no mo but the king and the Pehyte.
and mad^ a co^tenau^ce as though he would have spoke with the king in his ere.
and there he queld hy^ with a long knyfe. and after went he secretly out of
the chamber in to an other chamber so at the last no man wist where he was
become. wha^ ye kings meyne wist that her lord was so ded they made so much
sorwe yt they wist not what to do: for his two sons Anrila^bros and Vter
were^ so yo^ge yt none of he^ might be ky^g^ and ye thridde brother was monk
at wi^cestre / as is said. But Vortyger that was Earl of westsexe thought
preuely in his heart through queyntyse to be king and went to winchestre / there
that Constance was monk and to him said Co^sta^ce your fader is deed. and yowr
two brethren that ben^ wit Gosseleyne the bishop of London for to norysshe
ben so young that none of hem may be king: wherefore ^j counsel you that ye
forsake your habyt and come with me / and I shall don so with the Bretons that
ye shall be made king

Of Constance that was king Co^stantynus sone that was mo^k at Wynchestre / and
how he was made king after his faders death through counseyll of Vortyger yt was
Earl of Westsexe / for as much as Aurylambros and Vter his two brethren were
but young of age / And Vortyger let slay hy^ for to be king him self Ca / liiij
This Vortyger cou^ceylled this Consta^ce so much till he forsook his habyte
and went with hy^: And anon afterward he was crowned and made king by assent
of the breto^s. This king Constau^ce when he was crowned and made king he wist
not ne knew but little of ye world ne cowde no thy^g that aparteigned to a king
/ but he made Vortyger his chief maistre and counseillier / and yaf him all
his power for to ordeyne and to do asmoche as to the royaulme aparteigned So
that him self no thing entermedled / but only bare the name of King. When
Vortyger saw that he had all ye land in his ward and gouernaille at his own
will he thought a pryue treson and to slay Constaunce the king that he might him
self ben^ crowned and made king and regne. And let send after an C / knights
of Pehites the worthiest of all the land. and held thaym for to dwell wit
hy^: as to be kepars of his bodi. as he would went through the la^d to ordeyne
things that aparteigned to a king. And this Vortyger honored so much the
ho^dred knights / and so much yafe thaym of gold and silver and so rich
iewelles robes horse and of other things ple^te / wherefore they held him moch^
more lord than they dyde^ the king And Vortyger told he^ if he might be king ^
ye: as it were through treson: he would make him the richest of all the land.
So at ye last through great yeftes that he had give largely / they cried through
ye contre that Vortiger were better worthy to be king than Co^stau^ce: Wherefore
vortyger made semblau^t as he had ben^ wroth: and departed thens fro the court:
and said he must gon^ else whidder for things that he had to done: and so the
traitor said for encheson yt they should slay him that is to say Constance /
When this vortiger was gone it befell sone after that ye ho^dred knights of
Pehites broken the doors of the kings chamber and there they him slowe^ and
smoten of his heed and bare it to vortiger there that he dwelled And when
vortiger saw that heed he wept full te^derly with his eye / and notheles he was
full glad of his death And anon let take the hundred knights of Pehites and
bind her hands behind him and led him to london and there they were dampened
to the death as falls traitors And anon after all the Bretons of ye land by
common assent crouned vortiger and made hy^ king of the land

How that the wardeyns that had the two children to keep that were Co^sta^tynes
sons ladde hem to little Bretaygne for the treson and falsenesse of vortyger.
Capitulo lv /
THis king vortyger wha^ he was crouned they that had the two children in
keeping Auryla^bros and vter / through ordinance of Gosseleyne that was bishop
of london. at his death durst not dwell in the land with ye children: but lad
he^ to the king of litell Bretaigne. for asmoche as he tho wist ye treson of
vortiger that tho was made king / through who^ co^stance her brother was slay^.
wherefore the hundred knights of Pehytes were put to death. and bare all ye
blame as that vortyger had not wist thereof: ne nothir there to consented. And so
the kepars of the two children dred lest vortiger would put he^ to death through
his treson and falsenesse as he had don her brother beforne / and therefore they
were lad over in to littel bretaigne / and the king thaym received with mochel
honor and let hem to norysshe. and there they dwelled till they becamen fair
knights and strong and fers: and thought to be avenged upon the death of
Co^sta^ce her brother wha^ they saw her time: and so they did as ye shall here
tell afterward Hit was not long after that the tydinges ne came over see to
the kynred of the hundred knights of Pehites that were dampened and put to death
through vortiger in this land. therefore they were wo^derly wroth and swore^
that they would ben^ aue^ged of her kynnes death. and camen in this land wit a
great power. and robbed in many places and queld and did all the sorwe that
they might. Wha^ vortyger it wist: he made much sorwe and was sore anoyed And
in an other place tidings came to him that Aurila^bros and vter his brother
ordained and assembled a great host for to come in to mochel bretaign^. that is
to say in to this land for to ben^ avenged upon Constance her brothers death
So that in one half and in that other he was brought i^ to so moch^ sorwe that
he ne wist whidder to gon^

How Engist and xj thousand men came in to this land / to who^ vortyger yafe a
place that kalled is thong castle Capitulo lvi
ANd sone after this sorwe tydynge came to vortiger that a great nauye of
stra^giers were arrived in the contre of ke^t But he wist not whe^s they were.
ne wherefore they were come^ into this la^d / The king sent anon a messagier
thidder / that so^me of he^ should come and speak wit hy^: for to wit what
folk they were: and what they axed and into what contre they would gone There
were two brethere^ maistres and princes of that strong company / that one was
kalled Engist and that othyr horsse^ Engist went to the king and told him the
encheson: wherefore that they were arrived in his la^d And said: Sir we been of
contre that called is Saxony that is the land of Ermanie: where in is so much
sorwe that the people be so much that the land may not he^ sustain The
maistres and princes that have the land to govern and rule. maken to comen
before hem men and women: that bold ben among hem for to fight. and that best
may trauaille in to diverse lands. and so they shall hem give horse and harnaye
Armure and all thing that hem needs and after they shall say to hem that
they go in to an other co^tre / where that they mow live as her auncestres did
beforne he^: And therefore Sire king if ye have ought to do with our company.
we be come into your land and with good well: will we you serve and your land
help keep and defend from your enemies: if ye ^aue need / Wha^ vortiger herd
this tydinge he said he would glad^y hem withold upon covenant (...) they might
delyuere his land of his enemies / he would give hem reasonable lo^des where they
sho^d dwell for evermore: Engist thanked him goodly. and in this manner he and
his company xj.M. should dwell with the king vortiger. and so much they did
through his boldness that they delyured the land clean of his enemies / Tho
prayed Engyst the king of so much la^d that he might make to him a cite. for
him and for his meyne. The king answerde / that it was not to done without the
counsel of his Breto^s / Then Engyst prayed him estsones for as much land
or place as he might compose with a thonge of a skin. and wervpon he might
make hi^ a manner for to dwell on / And the king granted it him freely. Tho
nomme engyst a bullys skin and cut it as small as he might all in to a
thwo^ge all a round. and there with compased he as much land as that he made
upon a fair castle And when this castle was made. he let kalle it ye
Thwoncastell / For as much as the place was marked with the thonge

Of Romewen that was Engistes doughtyr. and how the king Vortyger spoused her
for her beauty Capitulo lvij
WHa^ this castle was mad and full well arrayed Engyst sent by letter in to the
co^tre that he came of / after an hundred ships filled with strong man. that
were bold for to fyghtyng in all batailles. and that they should bring with hem
Romewe^ his daughter that was ye fairest creature that a man might see: and
when the people was comen that he had sent after. he took hem in to the castle
with much joy. and him self upon a day went unto the king and prayed him
there worthily that he would come and se his new manner that he had made i^ the
place that he had compassed with a thonge of the skin The king anon granted
it him freely and with him went thydder / and was well a paid with the castle
and with the fair work. and to gedre there they eten and dronken wit mochel
joy. And when night came that the king Vortyger should gon^ in to his chamber
for to take there his nyghtes rest Romewe^ that was Engistes daughter came with a
coupe of gold in her hands and kneled before the king and said to hi^
waissaille. and ye king wist not what it was to mean: ne what he should a^swere.
For as much as him self ne none of his Bretons yet could none Englysh speke^
ne understand it ^ but spoken tho the same langages that bretons yet done
Nevertheless a latiner told ye king the fulle understanding there of waissaille
and that other should a^swere dry^ke haille: And that was the first time that
wassaille and drinkhaille came up in this land. and from that time unto this
time it is well used in this land / The king Vortyger saw the fairness of
romewen and his arms laid about her neck / and swetely kyssed her: And anon
right he was anamered upon her that he desired to have her to wife / and asked
of Engist her fadre: And Engyst granted him upon this covenant that the king
should give him all the contre of kent that he might dwell theryn and his
people. The king him granted preuely and wit good will / and anon after he
spoused the damysell. which that was much confusion to him self And therefore
all the bretons became so wroth for encheso^ that he had spoused a woman of
mysheleue. wherefore they went all from him and no thing to him took keep ne
help him in thing that he had to done

How vortymer that was vortigers sone was made king and Engist dryue^ owte and
how Vortimer was slain Cap / lviij
THis Engist went into ke^t and seized all the la^d i^ to his hand for him and
for his men and bicame in a little whill of so great poer and so moch^ people
had yt men wist not in lyttel time which were the kings men and which were
Engist men / wherefore all bretaigne had of him dread and said among he^ that if
they ne took other counseill between he^. all the land should be betrayed through
Engyst and his people / Vortiger ye king had bigote^ on his first wife iij
sons: the first was called vortimer / ye ij. catagre^ and the thridde passe^t.
The bretons all by one assent chosen vortimer to be her lord and sovereign and
her cou^cellier in every bataille and crowned hy^ and made hy^ king / and would
suffer vortiger no longer to regne. for encheson of the alia^ce bitwene Engist
and hy^ / The bretons ordained a great host to drive out Engist and his
company of the land. and yafe him three batailles / that first was in kent
there he was lord / The second was at tetforde / and the thridde was in a shire
and is kalled Nycoll in a more and in this bataille hem met Catagre^ and Horse
engistes brother so that each of hem slew that other. but for as much as the
contre was yeue^ long before to horn through vortyger tho he had spoused his
cousin there he had made a fair castle that men called horn castle: after his
own name. And vortimer was so anoyed for his brothers death Catagre^ that he
was deed in such a manner: wherefore anon he let fell ye castle to grou^^de.
and after that he ne lest night ne day till he had dryue^ out engist and all
his people of the land and when Engist was driven away Romewen his doughtyr
made sorwe ynowe: and queyntely spoke to he^ that were next the king vortymer
and pryuyest with him / and so much she yaf him of yestes that he was
enpoisened and deyed at london: the iiij. year of his regne. and there he lies

How the bretons chose^ an other time vortiger to be their king / and engyst
came ayen^ in to this land / and they foughten to gedre Capitulo lix.
AFter Vortemers death the Bretons by her conmune assent estsones made vortiger
her king. upon this covenant yt he should never after suffer Engist ne none of
his estsones to comen in to this land / And wha^ all this was done / Romewen ye
queen preuely se^te by letter to Engist that she had e^poisened vortymer and
that vortyger her lord ayen^ bare the crown and reigned. and that he should come
into this land well arrayed with much people for to avenge him upon the bretons
and to win this la^d ayene: And wha^ Engist herd this tidinge he made great
joy: and apparailled him hastily with xv. thousand men yt were doubgthy in
every battle and came into this land: And wha^ Vortiger herd tell that Engyst
ayen^ was come^ with a great power into this land: he assembled his Bretons and
went against Engist for to have yeuen him bataill and his folk. But Engist
drad hy^ sore of the bretons / For they had disco^fyted him beforne. and had
driven him owte with strength / wherefore Engist prayed a love day / and said he
was not comen into this land for to fight: but for to have his land ayen^ if
he might accord with the Bretons and of hem have grace. The king Vortiger
through cou^ceyll of his breto^s granted a love day: and thus it was ordained
through the Bretons that the same love day should ben^ hold fast beside
Salysbury upon an hill. And Engist should come thidder wit iiij.C / knights
without moo. and the king with as many of ye wysest of his land And at that
day the king came with his counsel as it was ordained But engist had warned
his knights preuely and hem commanded that every of hem should put a long
knyf in his hose. And when he said. fair syres now is time to speak of love
and pees / every man anon^ should drew out his knyfe and slay a breto^ and so
they quelled a thousand and lxi. of knights / and with much sorrow many of
hem escaped. and ye king vortiger him self tho was taken and lad to
Thongcastell and put into prison. And so^me of engystes men would that the king
had been brent all quyke. and Vortiger for to have his life granted hem asmoche
as they would axe and yaue up all the lands towns castelles Cytees and
burghes to engyst and to his folk. and all the Brytons fled thens into
wales and there they held him stille And engyst went through the land and
seized all in to his hand wit frau^chises and in every place let kast a down
chyrches and howses of Relygyone: and destroyed criste^dome through the land:
and let change the name of the land / that noman of his were so hardy after y^
time to call this land Bretaign^ but call it Engistesland. and he departed
all that land to his men: and made there vij. ky^ges for to stre^ghte the land:
that the breto^s should never come after thery^ / The first kingdom was ke^t
there that Engist him self reigned and was lord and maistre over all the other.
And other king had southsexe. that now is called Chichesstre / The.iij. king
had westsex / The iiij / king had Eestsexe / The v. king had Esta^gyll that
now is called nortfolk Southfok Merchemerich^ yt is to say the Erldome of
Nychol: The vj / had leicestreshire Northm^ptonshire Hertford and hunty^gdone.
The vij / had Oxu^ford Gloustre Winchestre Warrewyk and Derbyshyre /

How Vortiger went into wales: and began there a castle that would not stand
wytout mortier te^pred with blood C lx
WHa^ Engist had departed all the land in this manner bitwene his men. he
delivered Vortiger out of prison / and suffered him freely to gone whidder that
he would. and he no^me his wey and went in to wales there that his bretons
dwelled: for as much as that la^d was strong and wykked to win: And Engist
never came there ne knew it never before that land. Vortiger held hy^ there
with his bretons and ared cou^ceyl what him was best all for to done / And they
yaf him cou^ceyll to make a strong castle that he might him self therynne
keep and defend if it were need: the werkmen anon begannen to work that
castle upon ye hylle of breigh but certes thus it befell all ye work that the
masons made a day: it fell down on the night and wist not what it might ben^:
and thereof the king was sore anoyed of that chance. and wist not what to done
wherefore he sent after the wylest clerks and also for all learned men that
were through out wales that might be fonde^ For they should tell wherefore the
foundament so failled under the work: And they should him tell what thing
that was best for to done And when thiese clerks and wise maistres long time
had studied. they sayden to the king that he should done seek a child borne of
a woman that never had with man to done and that child he should slay and
tempre with his blood the mortier of the work. and so should the work ever
endure without end

How the king let seche merly^ through all wales for to speak wit him
Capitulo lxi
When the king herd this: he commanded his messagiers anon to went through
out all wales to seek ye child if they might him find: and that they should
bring him forth with he^ unto him^ and in recorded and witness of this
thing. he delivered he^ his lre^s that they ne were destroubled of no man ne
let / and tho the messagiers went the^s and spedde so fast that they came in
to a town yt was kalled Karmardyne: and as they passed forth her way / they
fonden two children of xiiij year age. chydy^g to gydre with hasty words and one
of hem said to that other / Done bat said he. ye done all wrong to chydde or
strife with me For ye have ne wit ne reason as I have / Certes Merly^ said ye
other child: of your wit ne of yowr reason I make no force. for men tell
co^muneli^ that ye have no thing of god almighty / sith ye had never fadre. but
every man knows well who is your mother. The messagyers of the king Vortyger
wha^ they herde^ the strife between ye two children. they axed of hem that
sto^de^ besides hem. whe^s this Merlyn was borne and also who him norisshed:
And the folk he^ told that a great gentle woman him bare in Karmardyne that
was called Adhan: But never man might wite who that might be the chyldes fadre.
When the kings messagiers herde^ this tydi^g they we^ten anon to him that was
wardeyne of the town and told hy^ the kings wyll^ and his lre^ showed hy^
wherefore they were come^ thydder Merlyn and his mother anon^ were sent to fore ye
wardeyne of the town: and he commanded hem that they should gon^ to the king
as it was ordained by his messagiers. Merlyn and his mother went thens and
camen to fore the king And there they were vnderfonge wit mochel honor. And
the king axed of that lady if ye child were her sone: and who him begat / The
lady answerde full te^derli wepy^g and said. she had never company of man
wordely. But sire king quod she. as I was a yo^ge maiden in my fadres chamber
and other of great lygnage were i^ my company that often times were wo^t to
play and to solace. I beleft allone in my chamber and would not gone owte for
brennyng of the son: and upon a time there came a fair bacheler and entered in
to my chamber there that I was allone / but how he came in to me and where I
wiste it never / ne yet wot j it not. for the doors were fast barred and wit
me he did game of love. for I ne had might ne power him to deffende fro me. and
often he came to me in that forsaid manner / so that he begat this child. but
never might I wit what he was

Of the answer of Merly^ where for the king axed why his work might not stand
that he had begone ner prove Cap / lxij
WHa^ Merly^ had herd all that his mother had said / he spak to the king in
this manner. Sire how I was begote^ axe ye no more / for it fallyth naught to
you ne to non^ other to wit. but tell me the encheso^ wherefore I am to you
brought: and wherefore ye have sent after me. Certes said the king. My wise
counceilliers have done me to understood that ye mortier of the work that j
have bego^ne / behooved to be tempred with your blood / or the fou^dament shall
faill evermore: Sir said Merlyn will ye slay me for my blood for to tempre
therewith your mortier / Ye said the king: or else never shall my castle
stade: as my counceilliers done me to understood Tho a^swerde merlyn to the
king and said. Sir let hem come before me the wise cou^ceilliers. and I will
prove that they say not well ne trewly. And when the wise maistres were comen
Merlyn axed of he^ / if is blood were the encheson for to make the work stand
and endure. All the wise were abashed and could not answer / Merlyn tho said
to the king Sir I shall tell you the^cheson wherefore your work thus failleth
and may not stand / There is under ye montaigne there that ye have begone your
tower a great ponde of water / and in the bothome of the water there ben two
drago^s: that one is white: that other reed / that fyghten to gydre against your
were Do ye dygge so deep till your me^ comen to the ponde: and do yowr men take
away the water all out: and than ye shall se the dragons as I have you told
that to gedre fight against your werk And this is the encheson certes wherefore
y^ foundament failleth The king anon let dygge under till they came^ to that
po^de and let done away all that water. and there they fonden two dragons as
Merlyn had told: which egrely foughten to gydre. The white dragon egrely
assailled the read and laid on him so stro^gely that he might not endure / but
withdrewe him and rested in the same cave. And when he had a while rested / he
went before and assailled the reed dragon angrely and held him so sore that he
might not against him endure / but withdrowe him and rest / And after came ayen^
the white dragon and stro^geli fought with the reed dragon and bote him evil
and hy^ ouercam^ that he fleigh the^s and no more came ayene

Of the sygnyfycacion of the two drago^s that were in the bottom of the ponde /
that foughte^ to gedre Capitulo lxiij
THis king Vortiger and his men that saw this bataill had great meruaille and
prayed Merlyn to tell him what it might betoke^. Sire said merlyn. I shall
tell you / The read dragon that betokens yowr self. and the white betokens
ye folk of Saxone: that first ye took and held in this land that now fyghten
against you: and you have driven and enchased: But ye bretons of your lygnage
ouercame^ hem and droue^ hem away. and sythen at the coming again of the Saxons
they recoured this la^d and held it for ever more: and driven out the bretons
and did with this la^d her will / and destroyed criste^dome through out this
land. ye had first joy wit her comy^g: but now it is turned to you great
damage and sorwe. For the ij. brethren of Consta^ce that was king the which
ye let slay shulle come beforn^ a month passed wit a great power from little
bretaigne: and shull avenge the death of her brother and they shull brenne you
first with sorwe / and after they shul slay a great party of Saxons: and shull
out drive the remanau^t of ye la^d And therefore abide ye here no le^ger to make
castle ne none other work: but anon goo else where / yowr life for to save
/ to god I you bitake. for troth j have said to you of thing that shall befall
And vndersto^deth well that Auryla^bros shall be king: but he shall be enpoyese^d
and lyttel time regne

Of king Aurilambros how he pursued Vortyger and Engist: and how they dydden
Capitulo lxiiij
MErlyn and his mother departed fro the king and turned again to Karmardyne. And
so after tyding came to ye bretons that Aurylambros and Vter his brother were
arrived at Tottenesse with a great host. and the bretons anon assembled he^.
and went and received Aurila^bros and vter wit great nobylesse: and lad hem to
london and crowned there Aurilambros: and made him king and dyden to him homage
/ And he axed where vortyger the king might be fonden for he would ben avenged of
his brothers death / and after he would werre upon paynyms And they told hy^
that vortyger was in whales / and so they ladde him thydderward Vortyger wist
well that the brethren came for to co^quere hy^: and he flew thens into a
castelll yt was kalled Gerneth / that stood upon a hygh^ montaigne and there
held he him / Aurilambros and Vter his brother and her folk had besieged the
castle full long time: for the castle was strong and well arrayed So at the
last they cast therein wild fire and brent hows and men and all her array and
as much as was withy^ ye castle. so that Vortiger was bre^t among all other
/ and so deyed he with moch^ sorwe / Tho was Engyst in kent and reigned there and
herd this tyding and anon fled and would have gone in to Scotland / for to
have had socour. but Aurilambros and his men met with hy^ into northcontre and
yafe him bataille: and Engist and his men hem defended whiles that they might
but he and his folk were disconfyted and slain: And Otta his sone fley to
york / and Aurila^bros him followed egrely. Otta a littel while against him
stode^ but afterward he put him to his mercy / and Aurilambros vnderfenge him
and to him and to his men he yafe the contre of Galewey in Scotland. and there
they dwelled. The king aurila^bros went through out ye land and put away the
name of Engistes land / that Engist after his name had called it before / Tho
let he call it ayen^ great Bretaigne. and let make ayen^ chyrches / howses of
relygion / castelles. cytees and burges and towns: whych^ that the saxons had
destroyed. and came to london / and let make the walls of the cite: which
engist and his folk had cast a down The breto^s led him to the monthe of
Anbrian: where some time was an hows of relygyo^ that tho was destroyed through
paynymes: where of a knight that was called Anbri so^me time was founder of ye
house and therefore the hill was called ye mont of Bria^: and after was called
Ambresbury and shall for evermore

How auryla^bros did redress the land of great Bretaygne that was destroyed
through the saxons. Capitulo lxv
THe king auryla^bros let amend and redress the house of Amlesbury. and thery^
he put mokes. but now there be no^nes. a little from ye place that was called
Salisbury. there tho the saxons kyllyd the breto^s. where engist and he should
have made a love day / in which time there were slain a M ^ lxi. knights
through treson of engist. The king thereof had great pity ^ and thought to make
in mind of hem a monument of a stone that might e^dure to ye worlds end And
of this thing they took her cou^seil what thereof was best for to done / Tho
spoke to the king the bishop of London that was called Terneky^. that he
should inquire after Merlyn. for he cowde best tell how this thing might best
be made. And merly^ after was sought and fonde^: and he came to the king. And
the king told him his will of the monument yt he would have made: Tho answerde
Merlyn to the king and said There ben great stones in jrland and long / upon
the hill of kylia^ that men kalled Geants karoll: and if they were in this
place as they ben^ there. here they should endure ever more. in remembrance of
the knights that here ben entered. By my throuth^ said the king. as hard
stones be in my la^d as in jrland. Soth said merly^ ^ But in all your lands
been not such. For the geants set hem for great good of hem self / for at
eueri time that they were wounded or in any manner hurt* they wesshe^ the
stones with hot water / and than wesshe they hem self there with / and anon
they were hole.

How the Bretons wente^ for to seche the great stones in Irland Capitulo lxvi.
When the Breto^s had herd of this thing / they went and swore among he^ that
they would gone seche the stones and nomme with hem Vter the ky^ges brother to
ben her cheueteyne and xv.M. men / and Merlyn cou^ceylled hem for to gon^ in to
Irla^d. and so they dyde^: And when the king of Irla^d that was called
Gwillomer herd tell that strau^giers were arrived in his land: he assembled a
great power and fought against he^ but he and his folk was disco^fyted / The
breto^s went forth till they came^ to ye monte of Kylian and clemed unto ye
mo^te But wha^ they saugh^ the stones and ye manner how they stode^: they had
great mervaille and said between he^ that no man should remene for no strength^
ne engyne. so hughe they were and so long. but merly^ through his craft and
quey^tise remened he^ and brought he^ in her ships. and came ayen^ in to this
land. And merly^ set the stones there yt the king would have he^. and set he^
in ye same manner that they stode^ in Irla^d And wha^ the king saugh yt it was
made he thanked merly^. and rychely hy^ rewarded at his own will / and that
place is kalled sto^heuge for evermore

How passe^t that was Vortigers sone and ye king Guillomer cam^ into this la^d
/ and how a traitor that was called Coppa e^poisened the king Aurila^bros Ca.
lxvij
ANd men shall understood that passa^t that was vortyger sone lived in ye same
time and came into this land with a great power and arrived in the north
contre: and would ben^ aue^ged of his fadres death Vortyger. And strongely
trusted he upon the company that he had brought with hy^ out of the land of
Germayne / and he had conquered all the north contre unto york And when king
Auryla^bros herd this: he assembled a great host of brytons and went for to
fight with hy^ / And he and his people were disco^fyted / but passent eskaped
thens with some of his folk and fled the^s in to Irland / and came to the king
Guillomer and prayed him of help and socour: The king granted hy^ wit good
will and said. he would help him. upon that covenant that I my self must gone
with you* all my power in to bretaigne and I would me avenge upon the breto^s.
rather than they in to my land came^ and token the stones with stre^th^ that
called is Geants karoll / The king Guillomer let ordeyne his ships and went
to the sea with xv. thousand men and arrived in wales and bego^ne to rob and
moch^ sorwe done: Hit befell so that King Aurilambros lay seek at wy^chestre
and might not help him self So that he sent in his name Vter his brother with
a great power for to help wales / and thydderward he went as moch^ as he
might The king of Irla^d and Passent had herd tell that Auryla^bros was seek:
and to he^ both^ came a sarazen which was called Coppa and said: Sire dwell
ye here all in pees wit your host and I behote you through my queyntyse that I
shall slay the king Auryla^bros that is seek / If ye do so said Passe^t / I shall
you rycheli auau^ce This traitor coppa put upon him an habyt of relygyon / and
let shave him a broad crown. and came to the ky^ges court and said that he
would hele the king of his malady Tho said ye traitor to ye king Sir ben of
good confort for I shall give you such a medicine that ye shall sweet anon
right and luste^ to sleep and have good rest and the traitor yaf hy^ such a
poison that he slept anon right and deyed in his slepy^g And the traitor said
that he would gone owte in to the field till he were awaked and so escaped he away
For no man had to him suspectyon for encheson of his habbyt that he was in
clothed: and also for his broad croune. But wha^ the kings men wisten that he
was deed. they were much sorwefully / and soughte^ fast the traitor / but
they might not find hy^: for coppa turned ayene to ye host fro whe^s that he
was comen

How yt wha^ Aurila^bros was deed: in ye morny^g a stern was seyne with a clear
light: and at the bought of the beme was seyn^ the^ head of an orryble dragon
Cap. lxviij
WHa^ king Aurila^bros was thus deed at winchestre. a morn after that he was
deed / about ye time of prime there was seyne a great sterre and clear / and ye
beme of ye sterre was brighter tha^ the son: and at ye bought of ye bee^:
appeared a drago^s head ^ and out of his mouth came ij. great lights / that
were as bright as any fire bre^ny^g. and yt one beme saw toward france and
straught over ye see thidderward And out of that beem came vij bemes full clear
and long as it were the light of fire / This sterre was seyn^ of many a man.
but none of he^ wist what it betokened. Vter yt was the ky^ges brother that was
i^ walys with his host of breto^s saw that sterre. and ye great light that it
yaf. he wo^dred there of greatly what it might betoke^: and let call Merly^ and
prayed hy^ for to tell what it might betoke^

Of ye betokeny^g of ye sterre Cap. lxix
Merlyn saw ye sterre and beheld hy^ long time and fithenes he quoke and wept
tenderly and said / Allas allas that so noble king and worthy is deed. And j do
you to understand that Aurila^bros your brother is e^poisoned ^ and that j see
well in this sterre. and your self betokens by ye heed of ye dragon that is
seyne at ye bought of ye bee^ that is your self yt shall be king and regne. And
by ye bee^ that stond toward ye Est: is vndersto^de^ that ye shall get a sone
yt shall conquer all France. all the lands that be^ longy^g to ye croune of
france: that shall be a worthier king and of more honor than ever was of his
au^cestres. And by the bee^ that stryght toward Irland: is betokened: that ye
shall gete^ a doughtir that shall be queen of jrland: and the vij bemes
betokened that ye shall have vij sons. and every of he^ shall be a king and
regne wit mochel honor: and abide ye no le^ger here: but goo and give bataill
to your enemies and fight wit he^ boldly for ye shall overcome he^ and have the
victory / Vter thanked hertely Merly^ and took his men and went toward his
enemies / And they foughten to gedre dedely: and so he disco^fyted his ennemies
all and destroyed: and him self quelled Passe^t that was vortigers sone And his
bretons queld Gwillomer yt was king of Irla^d and all his men / And Vter anon^
aftir that bataill took his way toward wy^chestre for to done enburye
Auryla^bros king yt was his brother / But tho was the body brought to sto^he^ge
wit mochel honor that he had don made in remembrance of ye breto^s that there
were slayn^ through treson of Engist that same day that they should have beu^
accorded / and in the same place they beryed auryla^bros the second year of
his regne. wit all the worship that might belo^ge^ to such^ a king: of whose
soul god have mercy

Of Vter pendragon / and where for he was kalled so after ye shall here / and
how he was ouertake^ wit ye great love of jgerne / that was ye earls of
Cornewaill wife C. lxx
AFter the death of Auryla^bros vter his brother was crowned and reigned well and
worthily. and in remembrance of the dragon that he was lyked to: He let make
ij. dragons through cou^seill of his bretons that one to be bore beforne hy^
whe^ne he went in to bataille: and that other to abide at wynchestre in the
bysshoppes church And for that encheson he was called ever and after Vter.
Pe^dagron and Otta that was Engystes sone commended but little Vter that was
made new king and against hy^ began to meve werre and ordained a great company
of his fre^des and of his ky^ne and of Offa his brother: yt had take all the
la^d from hu^ber unto york: but they of york held strongely against he^ / and
would not suffer hem to come in to the town nothir to yield the cite to hem^
And he besieged the town anon right and yafe there to a strong assault / but
they of the Cite he^ kept well and strongly: And wha^ Vter herd thereof / he
came thydder with a great power for to help and reseue the town: and put awey
the siege and yafe a strong bataill. and Otta and his company he^ deffended
as well as they might But at the last they were disco^fyted and ye most part of
he^ queld: and otta and offa were taken and put in to prison at london And Vter
hy^ self dwelled a while at york: and after he went to london. and at the
Ester after suyng he would be crowned and hold a solemn fest / and let
sompne all his earls and barons that they should come to that fest / and all
they that had wyfes should bring hem also to that fest. and they came^ all at
the kings commandment as they were commanded The fest was rychely holden
and all worthily sette^ to mete after that they were^ of estate: so that the
earl Gorloys of Cornewaille and jgerne his wife seten alther next the king. and
the king saw the fairness of that ladi that she had. and was rauisshed of her
beaulte: and often he made to her nyce semblau^t in lokyng and lawghyng so that
at the last the Earl perceived the pryue lokyng and lawghyng and the love
between hem. and aroos up from the table all in wroth^. and took his wife and
called to him his knights and went the^s all in wrath without taky^g leave of
the king / The king anon sent after him that he should come aye^ and go no
the^s in despyte of hy^ and ye earl would not come aye^ in no manner wise.
wherefore the king was full wroth. and in wrath^ him deffied as his dedely
enemy And the earl went thens in to Cornewaylle with his wife in to the castle
of ty^tagell. and the king let ordeyne a great host and came in to Cornewaille
for to destroy the earl if he might: But he had put him in such a castle
that was strong and well arrayed of Tyntagell and would not yield hy^ to the king
The king anon besieged the castle. and there dwelled he xv / days that never
he might speed / and ever thought he upon jgerne. and upon her laid he so much
bone that he nyst what to dou^ So at the last he called to hy^ a knight that
was called Vlfyn / which was pryue with hy^. and told hy^ all his counsel.
and axed of him what was best for to done. Sire said he. does send after
Merlyn for he kan tell you the best cou^seyl of any man living / Merlyn anon
was sent after and came to ye king. and the king told him all his will. Sir
said merly^. I shall done so moch^ through craft that j can yt I shall make you
come this night in to the castle of Tyntagel and ye shall have all your will of
that lady:

How Vter bigate on Igerne yt was the earls wife of Cornewaill king Arthour
Capi. lxxi
MErlyn through craft that he cowde changed the ky^ges figure in to the
likeness of the Earl: and Vlfen garlois his chambirlayne unto the figure of
Iurdan: that was the earls cha^byrlayne / so that each of hem was tra^sfigured
to other likeness: And wha^ Merlyn had so done he said to the king: Sir now
mow ye goo suddenly to the castle of Tyntagel and axe entry there and have
your will: The king took preuely all the host to govern and led to a knight
that he moch^ loved and took his way toward ye castle / and with him vlfyn his
cha^berlayne and Merlyn / and when they came thydder / the portier we^d that it
had been his own lord. and when time cam^ for to go to bed The king went to
bed with Igerne the Earls wife and did wit her all his will. and bygate upon
her a sone that was called Arthur. Upon the morn the noble mighty king took
his leave of the lady and went ayen^ to his host: and in ye same night that the
king lay by jgerne in bed wit the earls wife / the kings knights and men
yauen a strong assault to the castle / and the earl and his men manly he^
deffe^ded: but at the last it befell so that at the same assault the Earl him
self was slain and the castle taken / And the king anon turned aye^ to
Tyntagel and spoused Igerne with mochel honor / and made her queen. And sone
after. the time came that she should be delivered and bear a child a sone.
which was kalled Arthour. and after he gate on her a doughtir which was
kalled Amya. and wha^ she came to age: she wa^ nobely married to a noble Baron
which was kalled Aloth: that was lord of leons / When vter long time had
reigned / there came upon him a great sickness as it were a sorwe And in ye mean
time they that had to keep Otta that was engistes sone and Offa his brother
that tho were in prison: let hem gone out for great yeftes that they he^ yaf.
and went with hem And wha^ the two brethere^ were escaped and came ayen^ in to
her own contre / they ordained hem a great host / and a great power / and
begone to werre upon the king

How King Vter chose Alot to keep the land of Bretaigne whiles that he was
seek. for as much as he might not help hy^ self for his sickness Capitulo
lxxij
ANd for asmoche as king vter was seek and might not help hy^ self / he
ordained Alot sone of eleyper yt tho was chosen to be wardeyne and chiueteyne
of all his folk: and he anon^ and his bretons assembled a great host and yafe
bataille to Otta and to his folk: but Otta at the last was disco^fyted / Hit
befell thus afterward that this Breto^s had indignacyon of Aloth: and would not
to him ben^ attendaunt: wherefore the king was anoyed wonder sore: and let hi^
put in an horse or litter y^ ye host among the folk: and they lad hy^ to
veroloyne that tho was a fair cite there that sey^t Albone was martred / and
after was that cite destroyed with paynims / and thydder they had sent Otta
and offa and her people. and they dwelled into the town and let make fast the
yates and there they held hem / And the king came and besieged he^ and made a
strong assault: but they yt were thery^ manly hem defended. The king let
ordeyne his gonnes and his engynes for to break the walls. and they were so
strong that no thing might hem mysdoo. Otta and his people had great despite
that a king lyggyng in a lyttier had hem besieged / and they toke^ counseyll
among hem for to rise up in the morwe and come owte and give bataille unto
the king / and so they dyden. and in that bataill were both Otta and Offa
slain. and al^e ye other that escaped fled into scotland: and made Colegryne
her chyuetayne. and the Saxons that were alive and escaped fro the bataill
broughten ayen^ a great strength^ and among hem they saide^: that if king
vter were deed they should well conquer the land. and among hem they thoughte^
to enpoisen^ ye king. and ordained men for to done this deed: and yaf he^ of
yeftes great plente for to done this thing: And they ordained hem thidderward
there that the king was dwelly^g. and clothed he^ in pour habites the better
all for to spedde her lyther purpose. but nevertheless for all his falsenesse
and quey^tyse they might never come so nygh^ the king: but so at the last they
aspied that the king dra^ke none other licour but only water of a clear well
/ that there was nyghe besides: and thees falls traitor upon a day preuely
went to the well and put therein poison: so that all the water was enpoysened
/ and anon after as the king had drunk of ye water he began to swelle and
sone after he deyed. and as many as dro^ke^ of that water deyde^ also. And
anon as this falsenesse was aspied. the folk of the town let stop ye well
for evermore And when the king was deed his folk bear him to Stonhe^ge with
great solempnite of bishops of barons yt were there: and enburyed hy^ beside
Aurylambros his brother. and after they turned ayen^ euerycho^ and let sende^
aftyr Arthour his sone: and they made him king of ye la^d with much reverence
aftir his faders death / ye xvij / year of his regne

How Arthour that was sone of Vter was crowned after his faders death / and how
he drofe Colegryne and the Saxons and Cheldryck of almaygne out of this la^d /
C. lxxiij
When Arthur was made king of ye la^d he was but young of age of xv. year / but
he was fair and bold and doubty of body / and to meke folk he was good and
courtoys and large of spe^dyng: and made hy^ well beloved among all men there
it was need / And when he began to regne: he swore that the saxons never
sholden have pees ne rest till that he had driven thay^ owte of his la^d / and
he assembled a great host and fought with Colegrine. whom after the time that
Otta was deed / the saxons mayntened / And this Colegryne was disco^fyted and
fled unto york. and took the town / and there held he hi^ And the king
besieged the town / but he might not speed. for the town was so strong. and
they withynne kept ye town well and orpedly / and in the mean time Colegrine
let the town to Bladulf / and fled hi^ self to Cheldryke that was king of
Almaigne for to have of him socour / and the king assembled a great power and
came and arrived in scotland wit v.C. shippes^ And when arthour wist of this
tydyng that he had not power ne stre^gth^ enough for to fight aye^s Childrike /
he let ben the siege and went to London and sent anon his lre^s to ye king
of littel bretaignn^ that was called Hoell his neveu his sustres sone that he
should come to hi^ wit all the power that he might: and he assembled a great
host and arrived at southm^pto^ Wha^ artur yt wiste: he was glad and went
against hy^ and received hy^ with moch^ honor. so that ye ij. hosts he^
assembled and toke^ her way to Nycol yt Cheldryck had besieged: but not yet
taken: They came^ upon childrik and upon his people er they it wist there that
they were. and he^ egrely assailled The king cheldryk and his meyny defended
he^ ma^ly by her power. But king Arthur and his me^ queld so many saxons that
never er was said such slaughter. and cheldryk and his men that were left a
live fledden away / and Arthour he^ pursued and drofe he^ in to a wode / that
they might no ferthir pass / Cheldryk and his men saw well that they were
brought in to much dysese / and yolde^ hem to arthur in this manner that he
should take her horse and her armures and all that they had. and suffer thay^ to
go a foot in to her ships / and so they should gon^ i^ to her own land and
never come again into this land: And upon assurau^ce of this thy^g they yaue^
hy^ good hostages / and arthur by counsel of his men granted this thy^g and
received the hostages and her upon ye other went to her ships. and when they
were in ye see. her mind changed as the deuell it would. and they returned
her nauye and came ayen^ in to this land and arrived at Tottenesse / and went
out of her ships and took ye la^d and clean robbed it. and slewe^ moch^ people
and token all the armure that they might find. and so they went forth till
they came^ to Bathe. but the men of the town shitte^ fast her yates and would
not suffer he^ come with in the town and they deffended he^ well and orpedly
ayens he^

How Arthour yafe bataill to the saxons when they came^ aye^ and besieged the
town of bathe and hem overcame Cap. lxxiiij
When arthour herd this tydinge / he let ha^ge anon^ the hostages / and left
Hoel of Bretaigne his neveu for to keep the march toward Scotland with half
his people: and hy^ self went to help reskew ye town of bathe. and when he
came thydder he yaf a strong bataill of cheldrik and killyd all most the people
that he had. for no man might him with stond ne endure under the stroke of his
swerd: and there both were slain Colegryne and Bladulf his brother. and
Cheldrik fled the^s and would have gone to his ships But when arthur it
wist. he took x.m. knights to Cador that was earl of Cornewaill for to let
and stop his comy^g / and him self went toward the march of scotland: for
messagiers told hi^ that ye scotts had besieged Hoell of bretaigne there that
he lay seek / and therefore hasted thydder ward. and Cador pursued after
Cheldryk and took hi^ er he might come to his ships / and queld Cheldryke and
all his people: And when Cador had done this voyage: he hasted him ayen^ as
fast as he might toward Artur. and fond him in scotland there that he had
reseued Hoell of bretaigne / but the scotts were al far with in Mou^ref And
there they held hem a while. but Artur hem pursued: and they fled thens in to
limoigne. that were in that co^tre.lx. jles / and great ple^te of briddes and
great plente of egles / that were wont to cry and fight to gedres. and make
great noise wha^ that any folk come to rob that land and werren as much as
they might. and so they dyden. for ye Scotts were great rauennours so that
they token all that they might find in the la^d of Lymoigne without any
spary^g. and there with they charged ayen^ the folk in to Scotland for to went

How King Artur axed of Merlyn the auentures of.vj. the last kings that weren
to regne in England. and how the land should end Capitulo lxxv
SIre said Merlyn. In the year of Incarnacyo^ of jesu criste M.cc.xv. shall
come a lamb owte of Winchestre that shall have a white thonge. and true
lips: and he shall have written in his heart holiness: This la^be shall make
many gods houses. and he shall have pees the most part of all his life. And
he shall make one of the fairest places of the world that in his time shall not
fully be made an end. and in ye e^de of his life a wolf of a strau^g land
shall do him much harm. and sorwe through werre / but at ye end ye la^be shall
be master through help of a read fox that shall come out of the nortwest and
hy^ shall overcome the wulf. and the wolf shall deye in a water^ and aftir that
time the la^be shall live no while that he ne shall deye / His sede tha^ shall be
in strange land: and ye land shall be without gouerneur a litell while

And after his time shall come a dragon melled with mercy and Eke with
wodenesse: that shall have a berd as a goot. that shall give i^ England sadewe:
and shall keep the land from cold and hete: and his own feet shall be set in
wyke and ye other in london. and he shall enbrace inhabitacyons / and he shall
open his mouth toward walys^ and the tremblyng of the hydour of his mouth. His
eres shall strech^ toward many inhabitacions and contreys / and his breath shall
be full sweet in strange land. And in his time shall the ryuers run with blood
and with rain: and he shall make in places of his la^d walls that shulle done
much harm unto his seed after his time. Then^e shall there come a people out of
the northwest during his regne. that shall be lad through out a wikked hare that
ye dragon shall done crown king. which that afterward shall flee over the sea
without coming again for dread of the dragon And in that time the son shall be
as read as blood. as men tha^ shall see through all the world: which that shall
betoken great pestilence / and death of folk through dent of sword. And that
people shall be^ fadreles till the time that the dragon shall deye through an hare
that shall mewe against him werre unto the end of his life. which yt shall not
fully ben ended in his time: This dragon shall be hold in his time for the best
body of all the world: and he shall deye besides the marches of a strange
land. and the land shall dwell fadreles without a good governor: and men shall
weep for his death: from the I Will of scheppey unto the haue^ of Marcyll / Wherefore
Allas shall be the commune song of fadreles folk that shull ouerlyuen in his
land destroyed.

And after this dragon shall come a goot out of kar: the which shall have
horns and a berde of silver. and there shall come out of his nostrell a domp:
that shall betoken hunger and sorwe and great death of the people and much of his
land in the beginning of his regne shall be wasted / This goot shall go to
France and shall opene the flour of his life and of his death / In his time
there shall arise an egle i^ Cornewaille that shall have tethres of gold: that of
pride shall be without pere of the land / and he shall despise lords o^ blood.
and after he shall flee shamefully by a bear at Gauersech / And after shull be
made brigges of men upon the costs of the sea. and stones shull fall fro
Castelles / and many other towns shull be made plain: In his time shall seem
that the bear shall brenne. and a bataill shall be done upon ye arms of ye see /
in a feld ordained as a sheld. and at that bataill shall deye many white hedes /
wherefore this battle shall be called the white bataill: And the foresaid bear
shall done this goot much harm and it shall come out of the southwest and of
his blood. Than shall the goot lose much of his land till at the time that
shendshyp shall him overcome: and than shall he clothe him in a lion skin ^ and
than shall he vailliauntly win that he have lost and more thereto For a people
shall come out of the Northwest. which shall make the goot sore a drad. and
tha^ shall he avenge him of his enemies. through the counseyll of two owls /
which first shull ben^ in paryll for to been un done / But the old owl shall
went a certain time. and thereafter he shall come ayene in to this land. Thise
two owls shall do great harm^ to many on: and so they shall cou^seylle the goot
that he shall arere werre against the foresaid bere^ and at the last the goot and
the owls shall come at Burton up on tre^t / and shull went over / and for
dread the bear shall flee. and a swan with him fro his company to Burton
toward the north / and there they shull ben^ in an hard shour / and than the
swan shall be slain with sorwe / and the bear taken and beheded. alther next
his nest that shall sto^de upon a broken brygge. on who^ the son shall cast
her bemes. and many shall hy^ seek for virtue that fro hi^ shall come / jn the
same shall deye for sorwe and care a people of his la^d: so that many lands
shull ben^ on hy^ the more bolder afterward. and the two owls shulle do moch^
harm to the forsaid flour delyse and shull her led in distress. so yt she
shall pass over into france for to make pees between the goot and the flour
delyse. and there she shall dwell till a time that her seed shall come and seche
her and they shull hem clothe with grace / and they shull seche the two owls
and shull put hem to despytous death. and after shall this goot ben^ brought to
dysese and great anguysshe and in sorwe he shall live all his lyfes time

After this goot shall come out of vyndesore a bore that shall have an head of
white. a lions heart / and a pytous lokyng. his vysage shall be rest to seek
men: his breast shall be stanchyng of therst to he^ that ben^ a therst His word
shall be gospel: his beryng shall be meke as a lamb. In the first year of his
regne he shall have great pain to iustifye hem that ben^ untrue / And in his
time shall his la^d be multiplied with aliens: and this bear through fiersnesse of
heart that he shall have. shall make wolfes become lambs: and he shall be
called through out the world the boor of holiness / fersenesse and nobylesse
and meekness. and he shall done mesurably all that he shall have to done unto
the burgh^ of jerusale^. and he shall whette his teth unto the yates of Paris
and upon four lands Spaigne shall tremble for dread Gascoyne shall sweet In
france he shall put his wynge. His great taille shall rest in England softely.
Almaigne shall quake for dread of hy^ / This boor shall give two ma^telles to ij.
tounes of England. and shall made the river run with blood and with brain /
and he shall made many medewes red. and h^e shall get as much as his
Auncestres dyden. and er that he shall be deed: he shall bear three crowns / and
he shall put a land in great subiectyon. and after it shall be releued. but not
in his time. This boor after that he is deed for his doughtynesse shall be
entered at Coloigne. and his land shall be tha^ fullfylled of all good

After the boor shall come a la^be that shall have feet of leed: an head of
bras. an heart of a loppe: a swynes skyn and an hard / And in his time his la^d
shall be in pees The first year of his regne he shall do make a cite that ye
world shall speak thereof. This lamb shall lose in his time a great part of his
land through an hydous wolf. but he shall recoure it. and give a lord ship to an
Egle of his lands / and this Egle shall well govern it. till the time that
pride shall him ouergone. Allas what sorrow / for he shall deye of his brothers
fuered And after shall the land fall to the forsaid la^be: which that shall
govern the land in pees all his lyfes time and after he shall deye and the
land be full filled of all manner good /

After this la^be shall come a molde warpe kursed of gods mouth: a caytyfe /
a coward an hare / He shall have an Elderly skyne as a got: And vengeance
shall fall upon him for sin. In the first year of his regne he shall have of
all good great plente in his land and toward him also. and in his land he
shall have great preysing / till the time that he shall suffer his people live in
to much pride / without chastisy^g. where for god will be wroth. Than shall
arise up a dragon of the north which that shall be fulfers: and shall mewe
werre against the forsaid molde warpe. and shall give hy^ bataill upon a stone:
This dragon shall gadre ayene in to his company a wolf / that shall com^ out
of the west to begin werre against the forsaid Molde warpe in his side And so
shall the dragon and he bind her taylles to gedre. Than shall come a lion owte
of Irland which also shall fall in company with hem: and than shall tremble
the land that tha^ shall be called England / as an aspen leef And in that time
shulle^ castelles be felled a down upon Thamyse. and it shall seem that she
never shall flothe for all the bodies that shull fall deed theryn: The four
chyef flodes in England shull run in blood: and great dread shull be and
anguysshe that shall arrysen / and there after the molde warpe shall flee. and the
dragon. the Lion and the wolf shull he^ drive away: and the land shall be
without hem / and the molde warpe shall have no manner ne power sauf only a
ship where to that he shall mow flee and went. and after that he shall gon^
to land. when the sea is withdraw And after that he shall give the thridde
part of his land for to have the fourth^ part in pees and rest. and after he
shall live in sorwe all his lyfes time / And in his time the hot bathes shulle^
becomen cold. and after that shall the molde warpe deye aue^toursly. Allas
what sorrow. for he shall be dray^t in a flode of the sea His seed shall become
fadreles in strange la^d. for evermore: And than shall the land be departed in
three parties. that is to say to the wolf / to the dragon. and to the lion.
and so shall it be for evermore And than shall this la^d be kalled the land of
conqueste. and so shulle^ the righful heirs of england end

How Arthour overcame Gwillomere that was king of Irland and how the Scotes
became^ his men Capitulo lxxv
WHa^ Guillomer that was king of Irland had tydy^ge that king arthur was entered
at glastenbury: he ordained a great power of Ires men and came to the sea with
Ires people / and so came they in to scotland over the sea and arrived fast by
there that king Arthour was with his host: and anon as he wiste thereof he
went toward hem / and yafe he^ bataill / and overcame he^ anon right. and
Gwillomer fled wit his men ayen^ in to Irla^d / and wha^ this disconfyture
was done: arthour turned him ayene there yt he was into the place there that he
had left the scotts / and would have he^ all slain / but the bisshoppes
abbotes and other folk of the contre and ladies with ope^hede came before the
king Arthour / and creyd him mercy. and saide^. Gentle king and mighty have
mercy and pity of us. and as your self ben of the right law to hold and
maynte^ criste^dom^. full great dishonor it should be to kylle hem that believe
in almighty god as ye done. and for gods love have mercy and pity of us and
suffer us for to live / for we have had much sorwe and pain / for the Saxons
have many time through our land passed / but that is not ynowe to you. for
often times they have done us sorwe and dysese. For our castelles they have
taken and our bestes slain and eten and much harm they have us done. and if
ye would now us quelle / it were non^ honor to a king to quelle hem that cryen
him mercy: For now ye have us ynowgh^ overcome. and for the love of god suffer
us for to live and have mercy of christian people that byleuen in crist as ye do.
When king Arthour herd this sorwe. he had pity of hem. and yaf hem her life:
and they fill done to his feet and became^ his liegeme^. and he took of he^
homages: and aftyr that / king Arthour turned ayen^ with his host and came to
york. and there abode he during that vyage. And tho yaf he all loegers to
Aloth that had spoused his suster. and other yeftes great ple^te. and tho was
Gawen his cousin but of young age: and to all his other men that him had served
in his work he yaf rich yeftes and he thanked hem much of her good service:

How King arthour spoused Gu^nore that was Gu^nores cosy^ earl of Cornewaille.
and after he co^querede of Gwillomer all Irland Capitulo lxxvij
WHa^ Arthur had brought his land in pees and rest and in good state / and

Gunnor. and made her queen / and was a fair lady and a gentle. that Cador the

her wonder well and derely / And anon as wy^ter was passed / he let assemble a

to co^quere ye la^d. and he tarried not long that he ne passed over in to

not accounted to king arthour that any man wist ne non^ so well preised And

good that no man knew the werst and therefore king arthur made a round table.
that wha^ they should sytten to the mete all shull be alyche her and even lyk
served at the table / that none might make awaunt. that one were hyer tha^
other: and king arthur had at the table Bretons: fre^ssh men / Normans
Flemy^ges Bourgouners Mausers Lotherms: and of all the lands a this half the
