How king arthour came in to france and conquered that land of Froll that was a
Romayne. and him queld Capi. lxxvij
HIt befell that king arthur through counseyll of his barons and lords would
gon^ to conquer all France that tho was cleped Galle through romai^s that
held that land in her power and in her lordship. and the romay^s had take
that la^d to a noble knight and worthy of body that was kalled Frolle and wha^
he wist that arthur came: he ordained an host and a great power and fought wit
the king and he and his folk were discomfyted. and thennes they fled unto
Paris / and entered the town and closed fast the yates. and wha^ arthour wist
that Froll was gone to Paris^ he pursued after and cam^ thydder and hy^
besieged. but the cite was so strong and well arrayed and they that were withyn
defended hem well and manly / King arthour dwelled there more than a month /
and there was so moch^ people in the cite that vytailles faylled: and so great
hunger bicame among hem. that they deyden wonder thykke in the cite for
hunger and camen to Frolle and prayed hy^ to ben^ accorded with king arthur for
to have pees. and they would yield them to him and the town also: Froll saw
that no longer he ne might hold the town against her will. and trust greatly
upon his own strength^ / and sent to king arthour that he should come fight
with him body for body: and so should they depart france bitwene hem two. King
arthour anon granted it: and would not that non^ of his people should undertook
it for him. And upon the morwe they both camen well armed about the cite of
paris in a grene field there that they should fight: and anon they smytten to
gedres so fyersly / and so well they foughte^ in both sides that no man cowde
deem the better of hem. And so it befell that Frolle yaf Arthur such a stroke
that he kneled to the grownde. would he / nolde he: and as Frolle withdrowe his
sword. he wounded king arthour in the forhede that the blood fell a down by
his eye^ on his face. Arthur anon sterte up hertely when he felt him hurt: as
a man that seemed almost wode. and he took Tabourne his good swerd and drew it
upon hygh^. and yafe Frolle such a stroke that therewith he clafe his heed
down to the sholdres: so yt his helm might not be his warrant / and so he
fill anon^ deed in the place. and they of the cite made great sorrow for Frolle
/ nevertheless they anon^ yolde he^ to king arthur and ye town also / and
became^ his men and dyde^ to hy^ homage and feaulte: and he vnderfe^ge he^ and
took of he^ good hostages. And king arthur after that went forth with his host
and conquered Angie^ and Angiers Gascoigne Pehyto / Nauerne / Bourgoigne Barry
Lotherne Tury^ and Puthiers and all the other la^d of France he conquered
holych^ / and when he had all conquered and taken by ho^mages and feaultes he
turned ayen^ to paris / and there he dwelled long time / and ordained pees long
time over all the country and through out all France. And wha^ pees was made
over all through his noble knighthood that he had / and also for his own
worthynesse / and no man was so great a lord that durst meve werre against hy^.
nothir to arise for to make The land of France was all in quyte and pees: and
he dwelled there ix yere^ and did there many great wondres. and reproved many
proud man and lyther tyrant. and he^ chastysed after her deseruyng

How king Arthur auau^ced all his men that had trauailled i^ his service
Capitulo lxxix
ANd afterward it befell thus at Estre^. there that he held a fest at Paris.
rychely he began to auau^ce his knights for her service that they had him

Of the letter that was sent from the cite of Rome for pride to king Arthour
Ca. lxxx.
THe iij. day as king arthur sat at his mete among his kings and among he^
that setten at the fest^ a forne he^ came in xij. eldren men of age richely
arrayed / and courtously salued the king and said. they camen from Rome sent as
messagiers fro the Emperor and took to hy^ a lettre that thus much was to
understood. Greatly us mervaylleth Arthure that thou art ones so hardy with yen
in thy head to make open werre and co^take ayens us of Rome. that owen all the
world to deem. for thou have never yet beforne this time proved ne assayed the
stre^gth^ of ye romans: and therefore thou it shall in a little time. For
Julius Caesar conquered all the la^d of Bretaign^ and took there of truage and
our folk have it long had / and now through thy pride thou witholdest it.
wherefore we command the that thou it yield ayen^. and yet have thou more folly
done: that thou have slain Frolle that was our baron of France all with
wrong / and therefore all the communes of Rome warnen and commau^de the upon
live and lyme that thou in have be at Rome ame^des to make of thy misdeeds that
thou have done / and if yt so be that thou come naught. we shull pass the
hylle of joy with strength / and we shull the seek where ever thou may be
fonden. and thou shall not have a foot of la^d of thy^ own that we ne shall
destroy. and afterward with thy body we shull done our will / Wha^ this lre^
was rad. and all men it herd they were a^noyed all they that were at that
solempnite / And the breto^s would have slain^ the messagiers / but the king
would not suffer hem and said that ye messagiers should have none harm and
mow by reason none deserve. but commanded hem to be worshipfully served. and
after mete he took counsel of his kings Earls and Barons what answer he
might best give ayen^ to the messagiers. And they cou^ceylled him at onys that
he should assemble a great host and power of all the lands of which he had
lordship / and manly avenge hy^ upon the Emperor of the despyte that he had
sent him such a letter / and they swore^ by god and by his names that they
should him purswe and brenne as much as they might. and sayde^ that they nold
never faill king arthour / and rather to be deed / and they let write a lettre
for to send to ye Emperor by the same messagiers in this manner

Of the bold answer that king Arthour send to the Emperor of Rome and to ye
Romai^s Ca. lxxxi
Understands among you of Rome that I am king Arthour of Bretaigne and
freely it hold and shall hold: and at Rome hasteli I will be / not for to give
you truage: but for to axen truage. for Consta^tyne which was Eleynes sone
that was emperor of Rome and of all the honor that there to be longed / And
Maxymian king conquered all France and Almaigne: and passed mounth yoye and
conquered all lu^bardye / and these two were mine auncestres. and that they
helden and had / j shall have through gods will

Of ye reverence that Arthur did to the Emperors messagiers of Rome Capit.
lxxxij

How king Arthour fought wit a Geau^te in spaigne that was called Dynabus /
that queld Eleyne that was king Hoelles cosyn of lyttel Bretaigne Cap^ lxxxiiij
King Arthur had not dwelled in the contre but a littel while that men ne told
him that there was comen a great geau^t in to Spaigne: and had rauisshed ye
fair Eleyne that was cousin to Hoell of bretaigne: and had brought her upon an
hill / that is kalled the mou^te of sey^t bernard and there was no man in that
co^tre so bold ne so hardy that durst with him fight / ner come nere the place
there that the geaunt dwelled / and he was called Dinabus that much sorwe did
in the contre: Wha^ king Arthour herd this tyding: he kalled key and Bedewere
and commanded hem to go preuely and epsy where the geant might be fonden. And
they camen to the riuage there that men should gon^ to ye mount that was all
enclosed about with water: and yet is. and ever shall be / And they saw
bre^ny^g fire upon the hylle / and there was also an other hille nigh that: and
thervpo^ was an other fire bre^ning^ Key and Bedewere camen to the next hille
and fonde^ a widewe ope^hede sitty^g besides a to^be sore wepy^g and great
sorwe made / and often she said Eleyne eleyne. And Key and Bedewere a^ed what
her was and wherefore she made so much sorwe / and who lay in ye to^be / O said
she. What sorwe and misaue^ture fair lords seek ye here / for if the Geant
may you here find: ye worth anon deed / Been stille good wife said they.
Thereof dysmay ye not / but tell us the soth why thou make so moch^ sorwe and
wepy^g: Syres said she: for a damisell yt I norisshed with my breast which me^
called eleyne. yt was nece to hoell king of bretaigne: and here lies ye bodi
in this to^be yt to me was betake^ to norissh^ So there came a deuel a gea^t and
rauisshed her and me also. and lad us both^ a way. and he would have forlain^
that maid yt was so yo^ge and te^dre of age: but she might it not suffer so
great and so hugh^ as ye gea^t was And if he now come as he is woned to do.
certis he will you quelle both^ to. and therefore fast went ye he^nes. and
wherefore said they go ye not he^nes / Certis sires said she. when that Eleyne
was deed / the geant made me to abide to done and hau^te his will. and me must
needs it suffer and god it wot I do it not with my good will / for me lever
were to be deed / than with hy^ to dele. so much pain have I wha^ he me
forlyeth. When key and Bedewere had herd all that this woman had told / they
turned ayen^ and came to king arthour and told him all that they had seyne and
herd. Arthour anon took with he^ Loath / and went preuely by night that none
of his host it wist. and came on the moru^ erly to the Geant and faught wit
hy^ stro^gely / and at the last he slow hy^ and Arthur bad Bedewere to smite
of his heed. and bry^g it to ye host to show hem for a wonder / for it was so
great and so hugh^ wha^ they camen ayen^ to ye host they tolde^ wherefore they
had ben^ owte. and showed to hem the heed and every man was glad and joyefull
of the worthy deed ye king Arthur had done which that was her lord. and Hoell
was full sorwefull for his nece that was so lost / and aft wha^ he had space:
he let make a fair chapelle of our lady over Eleyns tomb

How king Arthour yafe bataille to the Emperour^ in which bataill the Emperor
was slain Capit. lxxxv
ARthour and his people had tydy^g that the emperor had assembled a great power
/ as well of sarazi^s as of paynyms and christian men: where of the nombre was lxxx
M / horse men and footmen. Arthour and his people ordained fast forth in her way
toward ye Emperor and passed norma^dye and France unto Bourgoigne. and would
even have gon^ to the host For men told hy^ that the Emperors host would come
to Lucie. The Emperor and his host in the begy^ny^g of August remeved fro
Rome and came forth ye right way to ward ye host of king Arthur. And his espyes
were comen and sayde^. that if Arthur would: he should find there fast by the
Emperor / but they said that the emperor had so great power with hy^ of kings
of the land and o^ paynyms ynfere and also criste^ people that it nere but
great folly to king Arthur to mete wit hy^. for the Espies told that the
Emperor had v. men or vi. ayens own of hyse / King Arthour was bold and
hardy and for no thing him dismayed and said: Gowe boldly in gods name aye^s
the Romay^s that with hy^ led sarasins and paynyms that no manner trust they have
to god but oneli upon her stre^gth^ Gowe now and sech^ hem sharply in ye name
of Almighty god and slew the paynyms and cryste^ men that been with he^ for to
destroy criste^ men and god shall us help. for we have the right / and
therefore have we trust in god. and do we so that ye enemies that be to
cristendome and to god / mow be deed and destroyed. and that men mow record
the worthynesse of knygthode. Wha^ king Arthour had thus said. they cried all
with an hygh^ voys: God fader almighty wurshipped be thy name withouten end /
ame^. and grant us grace well to done and to destroy our enemies that ben^
against crystendome In the name of the fadre of the sone and of the holy ghost
amen. and god give hy^ never grace ne worship in the world ne mercy of him to
have that this day shall feynte well for to smite and egrely: and so they roden
softely. and ordained his wy^ges well and wisely. The emperor herd tell that
king Arthur and his folk were ready arrayed for to fight wit hy^. and thydder
they came: and he ordained his wy^ges in the best manner that he might / and
more trust upon his strength tha^ in god almighty: and that was sey^ afterward
/ For wha^ ye two hoostes mette^ to gedre: the emperor lost so moch^ of his
folk. and also did king arthur / and so many were slayn^ as well in that one
side as in that other. that it was great pity to se and to wit / jn this
bataill were slain through king Arthur v. ky^ges of payny^s and of other wonder
much people. And king arthures men foughte^ so well / that the Romai^s and
paynyms had no more stre^gthe to withstonde: tha^ xx / shepes aye^s v / wolfes
And it befell that in this battle that was wonder hard and long dury^g in
that own side and in that other / ye Emperor among he^ there was slain. but
no man wist for soth who hy^ slow

How king Arthour let enburie his knights that he had there lost in that
bataill. and how he sent the Emperors body to Rome: that there was slain in
bataille Capitulo lxxxvi.
When the Romay^s wist yt the emperor was deed / they forsook the field and
the payny^s also / And king arthur after he^ chaced till it was night: and so
many of he^ queld that it was wonder to telie. and tho turned king arthour aye^
tho it was night / and thanked god of his victory: and in ye morn he let look
and see all the field for his knights that he had lost that is to say / Burel

he non^ pay^ and if they axed hy^ any other truage / right such truage he would
he^ pay. The king let bear key to kene^ his own castle. and there he was
entered. and Ligier was borne to Boloigne: there he was lord. and Holden was
borne to flaundres and there he was entered: and all the other he let entiere

were deed. And arthour him self soiourned that same year in Bourgoigne wit his
host: and thought the same year folewyng to pass ye mounthe of joy / and

subiectyon / but the wykked tyrant mordred hy^ let as ye shall after here

How mordred the traitor to whom king Arthour took his land to keep and his
castelles. and he held it against him Capitulo lxxxvij
When King Arthour had taken to mordred his Reaulme to keep and was gon^ ayens
the emperor of rome: and was passed the sea / Mordred anon took homages and
feautes of all hem that were in this land. and would have had the land to his
own use. and took castelles about. and let he^ array: and after this
falsenesse he did an other great wrong for ayens the law of criste^dom. He
took his own Emes wife / as a traitor should. and ordained him a great host
against Arthurs comi^g for to hold the land against hy^ with stre^gth^ for
evermore. and to slay king Arthur if he might. and send by see and land: and

come to hy^ owte of Saxoyne that was a worthy duke. and promised to him if that

all ye la^d from beyo^de Humber un to Scotland: and all the land that Engist
had of Vortigers yift / when that he spoused his doughtyr. And Cheldryk came
with great stre^gth^ and power of people / And mordred had assembled also i^ his
half that they had xl.M. of strong knights when they had need

How Arthour enchased mordred the traitor. and how he was slain / and also
king Arthour wounded to death. Capitulo lxxxviij
When this tydynge came to King Arthur there that he was in Burgoyne / He was
full sore anoyed / and took all France to Hoell / for to keep wit halne^del

other / that no man wiste who had the better party But so it befell at the
last that morded was slain and all his folk / and the good cheualrie that

yet the breto^s suppose^ that he lived in an other la^d: and that he shall come
yet and conquer all bretaign^ / but certes this is the proposicye of Merlyn:
He said that his death shall be doubtous: and said soth^ for men there of yet
have doubt. and shulle^ for ever more as men says For men wit not whether
that he lives or is deed. Arthur was borne to Auyone the xxij / year. of his

How king Consta^tyne was werred of Mordredes two sons Capitulo xc /
This Consta^tyne was a noble knight and a worthy of body and ye ij sons that
