Of the ky^ges Adelbright and of Edelf Ca xcj
Affter king Co^sta^tines death there were ij / ky^ges in bretaigne that one was
called Adelbright that was a Danoys and held the co^tre of Northfolk and south
fol: That other hight Edel and was a breto^ and held Nychol Ly^desey and all
ye land unto Hu^bar / Thise ij. ky^ges fast werred to gydre / But after they
were accorded / and loved to gedre as they had be borne of own body. The king
Edel had a sustre that was kalled Orewe^ne and he yafe her through great
fre^dshyp to king Adelbright to wife And he begat on her a daughter that was
kalled Argentyll. and in ye thridde year after came upon him a strong
sickness. that needs he must deye / and he sent to king edelf his brother in
law that he should come and speak with him. and he cam^ to him wit a good will:
Tho prayed the king and coniured also in the name of god* that after when he
were deed / he should take Arge^tyl his doughtyr and the land. and that he kept
her well and norisshe her in his chamber / And wha^ she were of age she should
be married to the stro^giest and worthiest man that he might find: and than he
should yield up her sa^d ayene / Edel it grau^ted^ and by oath confermed his
prayer: And when Adelbryght was deed and entered Edell took the damysell
argentil and norisshed her in his chamber / and she became the fairest creature
that might live / or any man find.

How king Edel married the Damysell to a knave of his kychene Capitulo xcij
THis king Edell that was uncle to the damysel Argentill: bethought how that
he might falsely have ye land from his nece for evermore. and falsely against
his oath thought to deceive the damisell. and to marye her to a knave of his
kyche^ that was kalled Curan. and he bicame ye worthiest and strengist man of
bodi that any man wist in any land that tho lived / and to him he thought her
shenfully have married: for to have had her la^d afterward But he was clean
deceyuyd. For this Cura^ that was Hauelockes sone^ which was king of Kyrkelane
in Denmark. and this Curan conquered his wyfes la^d and slew king Edelf that
was his wifes uncle / and had all her land as in an other place is telled more
openly: and he reigned but three year For the Saxons and Danoys hy^ killed and
that was great harm to all Bretaigne: and the Bretons bare him to stonhenge.
and there they hy^ enburyed with mochel honor

Of king Conam Ca. xciij
AFter this Curan reigned Conam that was his cosyn. which was a wonder proud
knight and reigned / and could have no manner love / but ever he was medely^g
with his people. and took his uncle with werre. and quelled his ij. children The
saxones werred against him often times / but he he^ overcame at the last / and so
he was in pees all his lyfes time: and he reigned xiiij year: And after he deyed
and lies at london /

Of king Cortyfa^d of Gurmo^de that came^ through the payny^s in to bretaigne
Cap. xciiij
AFter this Conam reigned his cosy^ Cortyf that was byhated of all his people:
and of no man he was beloved This Cortyf lost all bretaigne through werre / And
in his time fell that great myschief in bretaigne that criste^dome was
destroyed: and all the Bretons were dryue^ owte / and the land he lost
without any recouery^g: but afterward left ye la^d to the saxons as ye
afterward shall here / For in that time there was a paynym^ yt was called
Gurmo^d that was ye ky^ges sone Dauffrykes of the payny^s folk that had the
reaulme after his fadre / and was king / sauf he bequath and yave it to his
brother. and said that he never should be king / but if he might get and
conquer a reaulme in a strange co^tre / For he was bold and right strong of
bodi* and of hy^ profecyed Merlyn and said that he should be a wolf of the sea.
and he let assemble paynyms without no^bre and let appareill ships and went
by many lands and took homages and feautes of many. and so he went by the sea
/ and conbuered many diverse lands. so that he came in to jrla^d: and
conquered that la^d that oftentimes werryd upon breto^s / and bretons upon hem.
and often wo^ne^: and often losten / and yaue hostages to Breto^s. And so they
sent to Gurmonde there that he was in Irla^d that he should come into Bretaign^
and help he against ye Breto^s: to help hem deliver that land of he^. and they
would him gladly hold for her lord: for he was a paynyme and they were also
paynyms: and ye breto^s were criste^. Well ought he the^ for to help so as they
were of one law / Wha^ gurmo^d herd this prayer: he hasted hy^ as much as he
might / and arrived in Scotland and came in to Northu^berla^d there that the
saxons were dwel^y^g. and they co^fermed the couenau^ts bitwene hem that were
made by oaths and by hostages for to bear hy^ true faith: and hold hy^ for
lord and pay to him truage by year Tho began the saxons and the Affryca^s to
destroy rob and bre^ne towns and destroy all thing in asmoch^ as they
might. and they spared nethir man / woman / ne child. lered ne lewd. that
all they quelled. and cast a down towns castelles and chirches / and so put
they all ye la^d in great destructyon: and all they that might fleen fled
thens as well pore as rich: bisshoppes: abbotes: chanons. and all other great
and small. So^me in to littel Bretaigne: and sum in to Cornewaille. all they
that ships might have.

How king Gurmond drofe the king Cortyfe to Chichestre. and queld the breto^s
and through quey^tise get the town Cap. xcv
COrtife the king fley thens in to Chychestre that tho was a good cite and
well strong / and there held hy^ xx. days. And this Gurmond besieged it. but
the cite was so strong: that he might not get that cite by no manner engyn
that he might done: Tho bethought they upon a great quey^tise for to brenne the
town: they made engy^s with glewe of nets and toke^ pieces of tunder and of
fire: and bound it to the sparwers fete and afterward let hem flee and they
anon right fley and logged he^ in the town there that her nestes were / and
instakkes and in euissing of houses. and the fire began to te^de and brent all
the town / And when the bretons saw that in every side they hyed hem owte and
faught But anon they were slain and disco^fyted. and whiles the bataill dured
the king preuely hyd hy^ and stale away in to walls: and men wist never where
he became: and so was the town of Chichestre taken and destroyed And after
went Gurmond and destroyed Cytees and towns yt never were afterward made again
as it is sey^ yet in many places

How this land was cleped England for the name of Engist. and how many ky^ges
were made after in ye land Capitulo xcvi
When Gurmond had destroyed all the la^d through out. he yafe ye lord to the
Saxos. Anon they took it with a good will. For the saxons long time had
desired it / for as much as they were of Engystes ky^rede that first had all
the land of bretaigne: and tho let hem be kalled Englismen. for encheson of
Engistes name. And the la^d they let kalle it England in her la^gage / and the
folk ben kalled Englisshme^ / for as much as i^ his time it was called
Engistes land: wha^ he had conquered it of Vortyger that had espoused his
daughter: but from the time that brute came first in England. this la^d was
called bretaigne^ and the folk bretons: but sith the time that this Gurmo^d
eftsoon conquered it and yaf it unto the saxons / and they anon right
changed the name as before is said / And when this was don Gurmo^d passed over
in to france and conquered many lands and destroyed all christian people / there
that he came. And ye saxons dwelled in this land and begone fast it to
inhabit at her own will: and they would have made new ky^ges and lords. but
they might never assenten to have only a king for to be to hem entendau^t and
there fore they made many kings in diverse shyres / as it was in Engistes time
/ The first kingdom was kent and that other southsexe: and the thridde
westsexe / and the iiij estsexe / and the v / northumberland. and the vj
estangle^ that is to say northfolk and southfolk. and the vij merchenorth: and
that is the erldom of Nichol: hu^tyngdone. herford: gloucestre / wynchestre.
warrewyk and derby / and so departed ye englissh all england in vij. parties
And after that it befell that the kings werred often time to gedre / and ever
he that was strengest beno^me hi^ that was feblest. and so it was long time
that they and no king crouned among hem. ne no christian man was tho among
hem / ne criste^dome nothir. but were paynyms: Till that saint Gregorye was
pope of rome that had seyn children of the nation of England in ye cite of
Rome. that were wonder fair creatures / and had great will and desire hem to
behold. and axed of the marchauntz whe^nes they were and of what nation. and
me^ told hy^ that they were of england / and englisshe they were called. but
they and all the people of England were payny^s and believed not upon god. Allas
said sey^t Gregory well mow they be called englisshe for they have ye vysages
of Angeles. and therefore well ought they to be criste^. And for this encheson
sey^t Gregory sent sey^t Augustine into England and xl. good men with him that
were of good life and holy men to preche and teache and to convert the Englyssh
people and he^ turn to god. and that was in the vi. year that seint gregory
had been pope that is to say. after the incarnacyo^ of our lord jesu crist: V
Clxxxvij year: as the cronicles tells

How saint Augustyn baptized and converted king Adelbright and how he made ye
bisshoppes of his felawes Capit / xcvij.
When seint augustine first came in to England he arrived in the I Will of Tenet
and so passed he forth and came in to Canterbury: and there soiourned he And
king adelbright of kent that was of the lignage of Engist: vnderfeng seint
Augustine and his felawes with much honor: and he yaf hy^ all that he^ neded:
and ferther more he yaf hy^ a fair place that now is called the abbey of
seint augusty^s. in which place he lies he^ self shrined / This king
adelbright was a good man and with good will herd seint augusti^s p^dicacio^s. and
yafe he^ leave to preche through all his la^d of kent. to torn and co^uerte to
hi^ all the people that he might / and it befell so afterward through gods
grace that in a littell time ye king adelbright he^ self was converted to god
and all his people of his land was baptized And in the mean time while the people
he^ turned to god: seint Augustine came to Rouchestre and there preched he
gods word: The paynyms therefore him skorned and cast on hy^ reight tailles /
so that al his mantell was honged full of reigh tailles / and for more despyte
they cast on him the gutes of reighes and of fysshe wherefore the good man seint
augustyn was sore anoyed and grieved. and prayed to god that all the children
that should be borne afterward i^ that cite of Rouchestre most have tailles /
and when ye king it wist and herd of this ve^geau^ce that was fall through
seins augustyns prayer / He let make an house i^ honor of almighty god wheryn
women should be delivered of her children at the brugges end in which house yet
women of ye cite ben^ delivered of children. Wha^ sey^t Gregory had herd
tell how the englisshmen were turned to god and converted / he sent to seint
augustyn his palione by a bishop that was called Paulyn: and made him prymat
and Erchebisshop of England / and yaf hi^ his power for to make and ordeyne
bisshoppes in the land: and anon as Augustyn had the pallione of the dignite
of the Erchibisshoppe he made ij. bisshoppes of his felaws that came with hy^
fro Rome. that one was called Mellyt / and he dwelled at London. and that other
was called Iustyn that held the dignyte of Rouchestre: and this bishop Mellit
tho went for to preche into Estexe and baptized the king of the contre / that
was kalled Sicwith that was king Adelbrightes cosyn his sustres sone: and
Justin went to preche in southsexe and turned much of the people to god. and
saint augustine went him self prechy^g through out England

How seint augustyn went in to wales there that the Bretons were. and how they
nold not be obedyent to the Erchebisshop of Canterbury Capit. xcviij
WHa^ all england was baptized and turned to god: sey^t augustyn went into that
land there that the Bretons were for to keep he^ fro the englisshme^: that is
to seyne jn to wales. and there he fond monks and abbeyes and vij bisshoppes
For the bretons desired allway the christian people that seint Augustyn had
converted / and said to the bisshoppes that he was a legate of Rome and pmat of
all England. and that they should by all reason to him be obedyent. but for that
he was wit the Englysshemen. they saide^ that they nolde^: but to the
erchibysshop of Carlyon. and said they nold never for no manner thing ben
obedye^t to the Englisshme^ / for ye englisshmen they said ben our aduersaires
and our enemies. and have dryue^ us out of our own contre. and we ben christian
men and ever have ben^: and the englisshmen have ever ben payny^s: but now
late that they ben converted. Seint Augustyn might of he^ none answer have
otherwise. but sayde^ apertely that they nold never hem obey to hy^ ne to the
pope of Rome: And sei^t augustyn turned again to ye king Adelbright that was
king of ke^t and told hy^ that this folk would not be to no man obedye^t: but to
the Erchebisshop of Karlyon. And when the king herd this / he was sore annoyed
and said that he would he^ destroy / and sent to Olfride king of Northumberland
that was his friend: that he should come to him wit all the power that he might:
and that he should mete hy^ at Leicestre and from the^s he would gon^ into wales
and destroy the Erchebisshop of Carlyon. and all them that had refused saint
Augustine

How king Adelbright and the king olfride queld Brecmale that was a king of
Bretons that held the contre of Leicestre Capi. xcix.
HIt befell so that there was a king a Breton. that held the contre of Leicestre
and all the contre about named Brecmale: and this breton herd tell that the
two english kings would mete there at leicestre for to went in to Walys / He
let ordeyne all the power that he had for to fight with thees two ky^ges But
little it avaylled him: for all his folk that he had were slain: and him self
fled and lost his lands for evermore / And these two kings Adelbright and
Olfryd dwelled a while at Leicestre and departed the lands among he^ / and
token homages and feautes of folk of the contre / And there after they wente^ to
ward wales / and they of Wales had herd tell of ye discomfyture that Brecmale
had has at Leicestre. and were wonder ^ore adrad of the two kings: and anon
chose among hem good men and holy of heremytes monks and prestres. and of
other folk great plente / that wenten baarfoot and wollwerd for to have mercy
of the two kings / But the ky^ges were so stern and so wikked that they ^old
never speak with hem: But queld hem all euericho^ Allas what sorrow: For they
ne spared he^ no more than the wolf does the shepes But they smote^ of the hedes
of euerychon / And so they were all martred that to hem camen. that is to
understood. V ho^dred and xl. and afterward the two kings went fro the^s to
Bangore. for to quelle all them that they might there find of ye Bretons: and
when the breto^s that herde^. they assembled and ordained all her power for to
fight wit hem Tho was there a baron in wales that was called Bledrik of
cornewaill. that some time was lord of denoushyre / but ye king adelbright had
driven him to Wales and give him bataille. and at that bataill king Aldelbright
was slain and Eldryf wounded sore / and forsook the field. and the most part
of his people slain and Eldrif fled into Northumberland that was his own land /
And afterward ye people of Leycestre shire made with stre^gthe Cadewan that was
Brecynalis sone king of Leicestre. and he after reigned nobely and with great
honor

How Cadewan King of Leicestre and Elfryd king of Nortu^berland were friends.
and of the debate that afterward was bitwene Edwyn and Cadwaly^ that were both
her sons Capit. C
And after that this bataill was done. the bretons assembled hem and went and
camen unto Leicestre and made Cadwa^ that was Brecinalis sone. king of
Leicestre and of all the contre / and he took homages and feautes of all the
folk of that contre: and after that he assembled a great host and said. he
would gone in to northumberland for to destroy king Elfrid and slay him if he
might / and wha^ he was comen thydder: friends went so bitwene hem and made he^
accorded in this manner that Elfryd should hold all the land from Hu^bar unto
Scotland. Cadewa^ should have all the land a this side Hu^ber unto the south:
and after that they became good friends / all his lyfes during and loved to
gedre as they had be two brethren And this Elfride had a sone that was kalled
Edwyn that had and held all the la^d of Northu^berla^d after his fadres deth^
as his fader had hold all his lyfes time / and Cadewa^ had an other sone that
was called Cadwalyn that held his fadres la^d. as he it held whiles he was a
life. and they loved to gedre as they had be brethren. and the love last
bitwene he^ but only two year: And after began debate bitwen^ he^ through a
lyther enuyous cousin of Cadwalyne yt was called Bryeny: so that they assembled
a great host in both^ parties / and at ye last it befell that Cadwalyn was
discomfited and Edwy^ him pursued and drofe him fro place to place: so at the
last he fley in to Irla^d. And this other destroyed his land / and kast a down
castelles and bre^t his manners / and departed all Cadwalyns land among his
friends: and long time after came Cadwalyn ayen^ from Irland with a strong power:
and in plain bataill quelled Edwyne and all his fre^dshippes. and nameli thaym
that witheld his lands through Edwynes yefte

How king Oswald was queld through king Cadwalyn and Peanda. and how Oswy that
was sei^t Oswaldes brother reigned after him / and queld Peanda Capitulo Cj
When that Edwyne was slain Offris his sone undertook the werre against
Cadwalyn his Eme. so that this offrys deyde during the werre: And after the
death of offrys. tho reigned a gentill christian man that much loved god almighty
/ that had all the land of Northu^berla^d by heritage / that was called Oswold.
and he was king of all that la^d. But for as much as he was friend to Edwyne:
and held a great part of the land of Cadwaly^. the same Cadwaly^ werred upon
hy^ / and drofe hy^ toward Scotland. and when cadwaly^ saw that / he would no
ferther him purswe. but took sum of his folk to Pea^da his brother in law
and prayed him to purswe oswald till that he were take and slain / and
Cadwaly^ turned home ayene / When Oswald herd the tydyng that Cadwalyn turned
hom again. he would no le^ger flee: but abode Pea^da: and yafe him bataille. and
Pea^da was discomfyted and fled: and came ayen^ to Cadwaly^ and said. that he
would never hold any foot of land of hy^: but if it were so that he would aue^ge
him of Oswold / Cadwalyn let assemble a great host for to fight with oswold /
so that he and Peada came unto northu^berla^d and yaue bataill unto Oswold /
and in the same bataille was oswold slain. and his head smite of. and after he
was e^tered at the abbey of Bardeney. in which place god has wrought many a
fair miracle both there and else where. And anon Oswy his brother seized into
his hand all the la^d ^ that was Oswaldes / and the folck of Northumberland
loved him wonder well. and held him for her lord. but he had men of his kyn
worthy enough that would have departed the lo^d. and they werred to gedre ^ and
for as much as they were not strong enough / they came^ to Pea^da and prayed
him of help and socour. and promised him of that lo^d largely upon covenant
that he would him gyde and help and counceill Pea^da herd hyre prayer and so
spoke he with the king Cadwalyn that he should ordeyne a great hoost^ and fast
ordeyn^ him in to northumberland for to fight with Oswy. and Oswy was a meke
man and much loved pees and charity. and prayed Peanda of love and pees. and
proferd him of gold and of silver great plei^te / And this Pea^da was so proud
that he nolde grant him pees for no manner thing. but for all thing he would
wit hy^ fight / so at ye last there was set a day of bataill / and Oswyne had
trust upon god. and Peanda trustyd upon his pride and upon his host that he had
/ And to gedre they smoten egrely / But Peanda anon was discomfited and slain
And this was after ye jncarnacyon of our lord Ihesu crist Vj.C and lv. year:
and this oswyn reigned tho xxviij year. and a king that was called Oswyn that
was Peanda his cosyn werred upon king Oswy and foughten to gedre. but oswy had
the victory: and Oswy^ was discomfyted and slain. and lies at te^nemouth

How king Cadewaldre yt was Cadewaleynes sone reigned aftir his fadre / and was
the last king of Bretons Capitulo Cij
AFter the death of Cadwaley^ reigned his sone Cadwaladre well and nobely And his
mother was the suster of king Peanda. and when he had reigned xij. year. he fell
in to a great sickness: and then^e was there so great discord between ye
lords of the land / that every on weried upon other / and yet in that time
there fell so great derth and scarcite of corn and of other vytailles in this
^^nd. that a man might goo three days or iiij. fro town to town yt he should
not find to bye for gold ne for silver bread wine ne none other vytaille where
with a man might live: But only the people lived by rotes of herbs: for other
living had they none / so much was it failled / about fisshes wild bestes
and all other thy^g. so that yet to this mysauenture there fell so great
mortalite and pestilence among the people by the corrupcyon of the eir. that
the lyuy^g people ne suffysed not to burye ye deed bodies: for they deyde^ so
sode^li both great and small / lord and servant / etyng / going / spekyng. so
that never was herd of more sodeyne death among the people. For he which that
wend to gou^ and to bury the deed body: wit the same deed body was buried.
they yt might flee fledde^ and forsook her lo^des and houses / as well for the
great hunger and scarcite of corn^ and other vitailles / as for ye horrible
mortalite and pestilence in the la^d / and wente^ into other lands for to save
her lives: and left ye la^d all desert and wast. so yt there was not any man to
trauaille and tille ye lo^d ne ere ne sow. so that ye land was bareyne of
corns and all other fruits for defaulte of tiliers. and this mysauenture
dured xj year and moo that no man might ere ne sow.

How Cadwaldre went out of this land in littel bretaigne
CAdwaladre saw the great hunger mortalite and pestilence / and the land all
pour and faylling corns and other vitailles and his folk perisshed / and saw
also the most party of his la^d all wasted and void of people: he appareilled
hem and his folk that were left on live / and passed over in to lyttel
Bretaigne wit a littel nauye unto the king Alayne that he much loved that was
his cosyn and that his fadre had much loved in his time. and as they sailled
in the sea. he made great lame^tacyo^ / and so dyde^ they all that were with
him. and sayde^ Dedisti nos dn^e tan quam oues escarum / and in ge^tibus
dispersisti nos

And than began Cadwaldre to co^pleyne him to his folk pytously and said.
Allas said he to us wrecches and caytyfs For why for owr great sy^nes of the
which we would not amend us / while we had space of repentance / is come^
upon us this mysauenture / which chaceth us out of our own reaulm^ and
propre soil / fro and out of which sometime Romans / scotts Saxons ne Danes
might not exilen us: But what avaylleth it now to us that before time often
fithes have gote^ many other lands / since it is not the will of god that we
abide and dwell in owr own land: God that is werray jugge that all thy^g
knows before they be done or made / he sech^ that we would not cese of owr
sy^nes. and that our enemies ne might not us ne our lignage exylen fro and out
of our reaulme. he would that we amend us of our folyes. and that we seen our
propr^ defaultes / and therefore had he showed to us his wrath and wull chastise
us of our misdeeds / Since that he us does without bataill or strength of our
enemies by great co^panyes wrecchedly to leave owre own reaulme and propre
land. Turn again ye Romans. turn again ye scotts. turn again ye sa^o^s:
turn agayn^ ye fraunsoys. now shows to you bretaygne all desert / the which
your power might never make desert. ne yet yowre power has not now put us in
exill. but only the power of ye king almighty / whom we have often offended by
our folyes which we would not leave unto ye time till that he chastised us by
his dyuy^ power / Among the words and lame^tacion that the king Cadwaladre
made to his folk. they arrived in littell bretaigne and came to ye king Alayne
before said: and the king received him wit joy. and made hi^ to be served
wondre nobely. and there he dwelled long time after The e^glissh people that
were left on live and were escaped the great hunger and mortalite lived in the
best wise that they might: and much people spronge and came of hem. And they
sent into Saxoyn^ where they were borne to her fre^des for men. women. and
children to restore ye cytees with people and other tounes that were all void
of people: and for to trauailie and telle^ the earth / When the Saxons herden
this tyding: they camen in to this land wondre thikke in great company and
logged and herberwed hem self in ye co^tre all about where they wolden: for
they fond no man hem to let ne withstonde / And so they woxen and multiplied
greatly. and used the customs of the contrees where of they were come^ and the
laws and the langages of her own land And they changed the names of cytees
towns castelles and burghes and yaf hem names and called hem as they now be
kalled. and they helden the co^trees. the baronages lordshippes and trees in
manner as the bretons before time had compassed hem And among other companies
that came fro Germayne i^ to this la^d came the noble Queen that was kalled
Sexburga wit men and women without nombre and arrived in the co^tre of
Northumberland: and took the land from Albyone in to Cornewaylle for her and
for her folk / For there was none that might letten hem. For all was desolat
and void of people / but it were a few pour Bretons that were lefthe in
mou^taignes and wodes un till that time. And fro that time forth lost the
bretons this Reaulme for all days: and the Englissh people began to regne. And
departed the land bitwene hem / and they made many kings about by diverse
parties of the lo^d. as here ben^ devised The first of westsex / The second
Merchenrich^ / The thridde Estangle. The fourth^ Kent / The fyfthe southsex.
All thees reigned in this land after that Cadwaladre was passed owte of this
land and dwelled in little Bretaigne wit king Aleyne his cosyn and true
friend And wha^ he had long dwelled there / and had knowing that the mortalite
and pestilence was over passed / and that the lord was replenisshed with
aliene people / he thought to turn ayene in to his own land and prayed king
Aleyne his cosyn of socour and help that he might be restored to his propre
Reaulme and first dignyte / and king Aleyne granted him his prayer wit a good
will. Than did he apparailen hy^ for to take his way and viage into this land:
and prayed god almighty devoutly / that he would make to hy^ the demonstracyon
/ if yt his prayer in to this land were to him plesau^ce or none / for again
the will of god almighty he would no thy^g done Wha^ he had thus devoutly made
his prayer / a voys fro heaven to him said / and bad hy^ leave that journey and
way into England and that he should go to the pope of Rome / for it was so the
will of almighty god: that the Bretons should no more regne in Bretaigne / ne
never recoure the land unto ye time that the prophecye that merlyn had said
before be fullylled: and that should never ben^ / unto ye time were comen that
the relics of his body shull ben^ brought fro Rome and translated in
bretaygne And when the relyques of other saints that have ben^ hyd for the
persecucyon of the paynyme folk. shull be fonde^ and openly showed than shall
they recoure her land ayene / which they have so long time lost through her
great sy^nes Wha^ Cadwaldre had herd this answer / he mervailleth greatly
(...) told it to king Aleyne: Tha^ king Aleyne did sent for the clergy of his
land / and made hem to bring the stories and profecyes that Merlyn and
Sybille had said in her prophecyes. And wha^ he knew that the prophecye that
Festome had prophesied of the regle. and other prophecies accorded to the
dyuyne answer that Cadwaladre had herd / he counseylled him for to leave his
people and his navy / and submit hy^ to ye disposicyo^ of god. and done all
that the a^gele hy^ had commanded. Then^ Cadwaladre called Inor his sone and
Yuory his cosyn that was his sustres sone. and said to he^. take said he my
folck and my nauye that is here all ready and pass in to Wales and be ye lords
of the bretons. that no dishonor come to hem by inter^upcion^ of the paynym^
folk for defaulte of lords. And he hy^ self left his Reaulme of Bretaign^.
and his fo^ck for euermore^ and took hy^ way to Rome to the pope Sergius the
which worshipped hy^ much: and so he was co^fessyd and took penance for his
sins. but he had not long dwelled there but that he deyed y^ xij. kale^d of
may: the year of grace v / Clxxix.

How king Offa was souera^^^ above all the kings of England and how every
king werred upon y^ other Capitu. Cij.
IT befell so that all ye kings in that time that were in ye lo^d. as they of
westsexe Merche^riche / esta^gle of ke^t: and of southsexe and of other costs.
ech^ werred upon other: and he yt was most mighti beno^me ye lo^d of hy^ that
was most feeble But there was a king among he^ that was called Offa* that was
sei^t oswaldes brother^ This offa conquered all the kings of the land / and
reigned above he^ all / and so great was the werre ^ every contre between
kings / that no man might wit how the land went But Abbotes Pryours and men
of relygyon written the lyves and the deeds of kings: and how long every had
reigned / and in whose co^tre and in what manner eueri king deyed. and of
bisshoppes also: and there of made they great books / and let call hem
cronicles. and the good king Alured had y^ book in his ward. and let bring it
at wy^chestre and let yt fast be takked unto a pillar / that me^ might it not
remeve / ne bear it thens / so that every man might it see and thereupon look
For there in ben the lives of all the ky^ges that ever were in England

How the king of Northu^berla^d Osbryght forlay ye wife of Buerne bocard through
strength. and aftyr this Buerne conquered the king with power and strength^.
Capitulo.Ciij.
ANd thus it befell in the same time that there was a king in Northumberland.
that was called Osbright and soiourned in york. And this king went upon a day
into a wode hy^ for to refresshe and disporte: and when he came ayene he went
preueli in to a good man's houses which was called Buerne / and the good man
of that place was gon^ that time to the sea / for often times he was woned
there aspie and awaite thieves and robbours that often times were woned to come
in to ye land to rob brenne and slay / The lady that was this buernes wife
was a wonder fair woman and welcomed the king with mochel honor. and worthily
hy^ served in all thing. When the king had ete^ he took the lady by the hand
and lad her in to a chamber and said: that he would speak wit her a cou^ceil.
and all the folk from the chamber he made avoid / sauf only the ladi and he
But the lady wist not wherefore he it did. till that he had done with her his will
/ And when he had done this deed. he turned ayen^ to york: and the lady he left
there wonder sore wepy^g for the deed that he had done / And wha^ her lord was
comen home and saw her weep and such sorwe make. he axed of her what she had
done and why she made such^ sorwe / Sir said she / quey^tely and falsely the
king Osbright me had done shame and vylayne against my will. and told hy^
truth how ye king had her forlayne wit stre^gth^ where fore she said: she had
lever to deye tha^ live / Fair ^eef be still said he / for against strength^
feblenesse is littell worth. and therefore of me shall thou never the less be
loved: and namely for that thou have told me trewthe / and if almighty god
grant me life: I shall you well avenge / This Buerne was a great man and a
mighty lord and was beloved and had great friends. and let send for ye gretest
lords of the land. and to he^ he made his complaint of ye despyte that the
king to him had done / and said that he would be^ aue^ged how so that ever it
were: and all his friends counceilled and granted hy^ thereto. and they went
to ward york there that the king was And Buerne took his meyne and came to ye
king. and when the king hy^ saw he kalled hy^ curtously Buerne by his name.
and Buerne answerde to him and said. Sir I you deffye: and yield up feautes
homages and lands: and as moch^ as I have hold of you / and so fro this time
foreward I will never of you no thy^g hold And so departed he from the king
without more speech or any abiding. and took leave of his friends. and went to
Denmark. and co^playned to the Gordryne / and told him of the great despyte
that the forsayde king Osbright to him had done of his wife and prayed him of
socour and of help him to avenge. When king Godryne of De^marke and the Danois
had herd the pley^te of this buerne and of the prayer that he had made: they
were wonder glad in heart: for asmoche that they might find cause for to gone in
to England for to werre upon the Englisshmen / and also for to aue^ge Buerne of
the despite that the king had done to his wife: and for asmoch^ as Buerne was
sibbe to the king of De^marke. Anon they let ordeyne a great host of men: and
let prepare ships and asmoche as was need to that viage And when all the
host was ready ye king made his ij brethren cheuytains that were noble
knights and bold. That one was called Hungar. and that other Hubba /

How the Danoys took york and quelled the king Osbright and afterward king
Elle Capitulo C.iiij
When all thing was ready. the two brethren took leave of the king Gordryn: and
went toward ye see for to went in to England as fast as they might speed: Now
is Buerne so well conforted and fast hyed him with ye Danoys / that they ben^
arrived in to northco^tre / and comen through out holdernesse / and destroyed
all ye contre and brent tounes and robbed folk and quelled all that they might
taken / till they camen to york / And when king Osbryght saw hem come he took
his people that he had and came out of the cite: and faught with hem. but no
foyson he had ayens hem: and much was the people that there was slain in both
parties And king Osbright hy^ self there was slayn^. and the cite anon was
take: and the Danois wente^ theryn / and there was also an other king in
Northumberland that Buernes fre^des had chosen / and held him for king. and he
was called Elle: for as moch^ as they would not to king osbright been entendaunt
for the despyte that he had done to Buerne her cosyn. Hit befell thus that the
king Elle was gon^ to wode him for to disporte. and of venyson somdell he had
take. and as he sat in ye wode at mete. to a knight he said / we have well y
sped and moch^ venison taken. And with that word there came in a man and to him
said / jf ye much of venyson have wonnen. an hundred times so moch^ more there
ayens ye have lost For all this contre the danoys have gete^ and take the cite
of york and aye^s you shull it hold. that never ye shull come theryn / and
for soth they have slain the king Osbright. and wha^ king Elle these words
herd. he let assemble all the folk of ye co^tre: And ordained all ye power
that he might haue^ and would have get the town of york wit stre^gthe / but
the danoys camen owte anon and yafe him bataille. and queld the king and the
most party of his men that he had brought with hy^: and the same place there
that they were slain / shall ever be kalled Ellecrost. and that place is
littel from york. And tho abode the Danoys never till they had conquered all
Northumberland / and in that contre they made wardeyns. and went ferther in to
the land and token nothyngam: and there they dwelled all the winter. and dyden
the sorwe that they might And after wha^ somer time cam^ they remeued from
nothyngam and camen in to nychol: and to Ly^desey: and to Hola^d / For no man
might hem withsto^de / so much power and strength^ they had.

How saint Edmond the king was martred Cap. Cv /
And so far had the danois passed from contre un to contre: and ever more
brennyng and robby^g: and destroyed all that they might / till they camen un to
Thetford: and in that contre they founde^ a christian king. that much loved god
and his works. and he was kalled Edmond. And he was king of northfolk and
southfolk This saint Edmond king ordained as much folk as he might and fought
with the Danoys / but he and his folk were discomfyted / and the king him self
driven unto ye castle of Framelyngham And the Danoys him pursued and came^
unto ye same castle: and wha^ king Edmond saw that ye castle might not he^
witstond / he came aye^s he^. with who^ ye Danoys first speke^: and anon^ they
axed of hy^ where king Edmond was now. for soth said he: when I was in the
castle there was the king / and wha^ I went out of the castle he went out also
/ and whethir he shall escape or deye: at gods will must it be Wha^ sey^t
Edmond had ne^pned god. by that they wiste^ well all that it was he him self /
And anon Hubba and Hu^bar toke^ him and said that he should god forsake and
all christian law as many other had don hy^ beforne. And seint Edmond said that
he nold never. but rather he would suffer ye death for gods love and his laws
to keep. Tho took they the king Edmond and bound hi^ unto a tree / and made
her archiers to hy^ shete with his arewes till yt his bodi stikked as full of
arowes as an vrchone is full of prikkes: but for all the pains yt he had he
would never god forsake. and in ye same pain and turment he deyeth: and betoke
his soul to god / and wha^ they sawen that he was deed they smyten of his
head. And in this manner was seint Edmond martred

How Hubba and Hu^gar toke^ the town of Redyng -ca. cvj
WHa^ sey^t Edmond was martred Hu^gar and Hubba went the^s wit all her Danoys
unto Redy^ge: and as they went thidderward: they bre^de towns and Citees: and
quelled all christian people that would not god forsake / and cast a down chyrches
/ and camen to Redy^ge / and took ye town. and there held they hem till yt the
king Edelf of Westsex came thidder with all his power for to take ye town Tho
came^ out ye danois for to give bataill to king Edelf. and at that bataill was
queld an earl of ye danoys that was called Cydrake. Upon the morwe came ye king
Elred and his brother Alured with a strong power and a great host / and the
king Edelf came ayen^ that had foughte^ the day before to that bataill / and
ye Danoys came^ tho out for to fight with hem. and the bataille was wonder
strong. for many a man was there slayn^: and ye danoys that day had ye victory
and the king Eldred and his brother Alured that day were discomfyted But the
fourth^ day afterward ye Danoys and the e^glisshme^ foughte^ to gedre an other
time upon Ekelde^ne: and there was slayn^ a king of De^marke yt was called
Rafy^g. and iiij earls of great power: and that day had ye danoys shame for
they were driven unto Englisfelde. and the xv. day after: the danoys and the
englisshme^ foughte^ an other time at Rafy^g and there were the englisshmen
disco^fyted^ And from thens a Danoys that was called Roynt. went to redy^g with
his host and destroyed all that he might take And king Eldred fought with him.
But he was sore wounded / werfore that he deyed and he had not reigned but v.
year and lies at Wonburne

Of king Alured. and how the Danoys in his time prayed him of mercy that they
must gou^ out of the land Capitulo Cvij
AFter the death of this Eldred reigned his brother alured that Dolfynes was
kalled. Tho wente^ the Danoys and a^^embled hem and went for to seche Alured
that tho was ye new king of Southsex and there they founde^ him at wiltone
with a littel people. and notheles he faught with hem. but at the last he fled
thens from the field and went into westsex. and ordained so much people of his
own reaulme and also of othir^ so till that he had a strong host: so that
the danois had no power ayens him to sto^de. And he came to london with his
host and there were the Danois soiourned / and there would he ^ have foughten
with hem: but ye danoys durst not with him fight / but praird him of pees /
and that they must gon^ ayen^ unto her own contre: and neuermore in to England
for to come again any harm to done. And upon this covenant they should give hy^
to plegge good hostages. and such as ye Englisshmen would axen

How Hubba and Hungar were quelled at Chipenham. and the danoys brought her
king to our king Capitu. Cviij.
ANd the same day that the danoys departed from London so fast they rode^ both^
night and day: and never took rest of going: till that they came^ unto
Excestre. and token to the town. and there they held hem When king Alured
herd the tydi^g. anon^ he let take the hostages: and went from thens to
Excestre with all the power that he had: And when ye danoys herd tell of his
comi^g. they wenten fro thens in to westsexe and camen to Chippenham and there
they dide^ much harm in the contre: they robbed folk and brought hem in
prison / The king Alured hem pursued and came upon hem and fersely hem
assailled / and there were slain both Hubba and Hungar his brother: and Buerne
Bocard / and in this bataill was much folk slain / as well in that one side as
in that other. but the gree of the field lest with the Danoys. For as much as
the king came with littell company. The king hasted him as much as he might
for to wend ayene: And when the Danoys founde^ Hubba his dody deed they
entered it. and made upon it a great logge and let kalle it Hubbes^owe: and so
it is called in to this day / And that place is kalled dene^shire. The barons
somerset wyllstshire and dorset herd tell how that her king was discomfyted^
and ordained all the power that they myghten have: and camen to the king there
he was. and thanked god that they had him fonden a leyue / for they had wend
that the Danoys had him slain / Tho took they a counseill the king and his
Barons that they would gon^ and seche the danoys with hem all for to fyghten:
and so they ridde^ all that night hem all for to seche. and came^ in the morwe
about pryme to Abyngdon. there that the Danoys were: The king tho Alured and
his Barons assembled and there they assailled the danoys egrely. and there yaf
he^ a strong bataill: and the danoys nobely put hem of long time that no man
wist in whethir party yt was the most people slain / But thus it befell as
god would that ye king Alured had the victore with mochel honor / for the
Danoys weren so driven that they ne wist whyther for to torn / and xv. days
the king hem purswed at his will. that glad and feign they were for to speken
of pees and of accord. and token good hostages. and said that they nold never
more up on him werre ne no debate arere. and more over they behyght to the king
Alured that they would gon^ and bring her own king unto him / and that her
king and they all should be baptized: and upon this condycion the noble and
vaylliau^t king Alured granted hem life and lymme / and said to hem that they
should gone her king for to fetch: And at a certain day to comen ayen^ that to
hem was set / And so went they fast forth and camen ayen^ at her day that
was assigned. and all the danoys brought her king with thay^ The king Alured
anon let hem ben^ baptized and her names changed So that the king of the
Danoys was kalled Athelston and xxx of his felawes names were changed also: and
the other were baptized to the right believe and all this was done at Westmynstre

And after that time: the king Alured held with him king Athelstone. and all
his danoys xij days at soioure with mochel solempnyte: and yafe hem great
yeftes after that they were baptized and so they departed.

And when all this was done tho was the good King Alured all at ese and for yt
he had all his enemies ouercomen and that they were turned to the right believe
of almighty god.

How the Danois that were gon^ with Gurmond in to France: camen ayen^ in to
England / And of the death of king alured Capitulo Cix
And thus it befell afterward that the Danoys of northu^berla^d that were
paynyms: came^ with a great stre^gth^ and an huge host of france: that is to
understood. wit he^ that went in to france with Gurmond of Auffryke when he
had conquered England / and it yafe unto the saxons and tho they that came^ fro
france arrived in ke^t and sent in to northumberland that they should come^ to
hem: and when the two hoostes were come^ and assembled. anon^ they went to
destroy the christian people of England fro place to place and dyden moch^ sorwe:
Hit befell thus as the almighty god would an hard chance in Englond^ For the
good king Alured that was woned to abate the Danois: deide in the mean time.
This king Alured had reigned xxx. year: and a good king had ben^. and could well
chastyse his enemies / for he was a good clear: and let make many books. And a
book of Englissh^ of auentures. of kings of batailles / that had been done in
the land / and manj other books of gestes. he let hem write that were of great
wisdom and of good lerny^g / through which book many a man may hi^ amend that
will hem read and upon look: upon whose soul almighty god have mercy / And this
king Alured lies at Wynchestre*

Of king Edward that was king Alured sone Capit. Cx
ANd after this Alured reigned Edward his sone the which was a good man: and a
wise: and was wonder curtois: The danois did much sorwe in the land. and her
power encresced and began for to wexe from day to day For the danoys came^ often
with their companyes in to this land / and wha^ the king saw that he might no
better done: he no^me trewes with hem and granted hem his pees And notheles
the truwes dured not long that the Danois ne begone strongely to werre upon
the Englysshme^. and did hem moch^ sorwe Wherefore king Edward did assemble a
great host for to fight with hem. and tho deyed this king Edward wha^ god
would. This king Edward reigned xxiiij year / and lies at wy^chestre besides
his fadre

Of king Adelston and of Edmonde / and of Eldred and of Edwyne his brother
Capitulo Cxi
After this Edward reigned Adelston his sone: and wha^ he had reigned iiij. year:
he held bataille against the Danoys and drofe king Gaufride that was king of
Danois / and all his host unto the sea. and rested by Scotland and avoyed
strongeli the contre all a year / and after that / they of Cu^berla^d and the
scotts of Westmerland begone to werre upon king Athelston: and he yaf hem so
strong bataille that he quelled so many of hem that no man could tell the
nombre of he^. and after that he ne reigned but three year: and he reigned in all
xxv / yere^ and lies at Malmesbury. And after this adelston reigned his brother
Edmond / for asmoche as king adelston had no sone: and this Edmond was a worthy
knight and a doughty man of body. and a noble knight And i^ the thridde year
after that he was king he went over Hu^bar in which place he fond ij. ky^ges
of Danoys. That one was called Enelaf: and that other Regnaut / and this king
Edmond drofe he^ both^ from the land / and after went and took a great prey in
Cumberland / This Edmond ne reigned but vij. year / and lies at Glastenbury.
and after this edmond reigned Eldrede his brother / that avenged Edward his
fadre of his enemies that hy^ quelled / and after he seysed Northumberland in
to his hand and made the scotts abowe and meke unto his will And the second
year that he had reigned / came Arnalaf gwyra^ that was king of Denmark and
seized all northumberland. and held that lord two year. and after that came
king Eldred and drofe him out of this land: and this king Eldred was a noble
man and a good. of whose goodness sey^t Dunsto^ preched. And this king Eldred
reigned xi. year / and lies at wy^chestre / And after this Eldred Edwyne sone
of Edmond his brother reigned. and was a lyther man toward the god and the
people. for he hated folk of his own land. and loved and honored strange men
and set littel by the holy chirch^. and he took of the holy chyrch^ all the
tresour that he might have that was great shame and vylanie to him self and
peril to his soul and therefore god would not that he should regne no longer
than iiij year. and deyed and lies at Wy^chestre

Of king Edgar that reigned above the kings of Scotland and of Wales / and how
he was begylled through taking of his wife Capitulo Cxij
ANd after this king Edwyne reigned Edgare his brother a man that moch^ loved
god and pees and the holy chyrch^ also / And was a worthy lord bold strong
and mighty. and mayntened right well this land in pees. And this king Edgar was
lord and king above all the kings of Scotland and of Walys / from the time
that Arthour was a gone. and never was sithe^ king of his power. And this noble
king edgar was sey^t edwardes fadre. and wha^ Edgares wife was deed yt was
seint Edwardes mother and e^tered / he herd speak of the fairness of Estrilde
that was orga^us doughtir a baron of dene^shire / that was so fair a woman
that all men speke^ thereof He called on of his knights yt he moch^ loved and
trusted upon and told him Go said he to the noble baron Orgar of Dene^shire and
see if his daughter be so fair as men speken of and if it be sothes: I will
have her to my wife. This knight yt was called Edelwold went forth his way and
came there that the ladi was. and when he saw her so fair he thought to have
her him self to wife. and there of spoke to Orgar her fadre And Orgar was an
old man and had no moo children but only her: and saw that edelwold was a
fair young knight and worthy and rich. and was well with the king. and thought
his daughter should well be married / and well beset upon hy^ and granted hy^ his
daughter if the good lord the king would consent there to. This edelwold came
ayen^ to the king. and told hy^ that she was fair ynowe upon to see. but she
was wonder lothly Tho answered the king and said that he took but littel
charge: Sire said Edelwold tho / She is her fadres heir and I am not rych^ of
lands / and if ye would consent and grant that I must her have / tha^ should
j be rych^ ynowe / In gods name said the king I consent there to. Edelwold
thanked tho moch^ the king and went ayen^ into Dene^shire and spoused ye
damisell in that contre. and dwelled there / And thus it befell upon a time that
he told his counseyll and all this thing unto his wife. how and in what manner
he had begylled his lord ye king that would have had her to wife / and anon as
she it wist she loved hy^ never more afterward as she had done beforne. This
lady conceived by him a sone: and when time was that the child should be borne:
edelwold came to the king and prayed him to have a sone of his at fouston. The
king hy^ granted and let call him Edgar aftir his own name. And when this
was done. he thought yt he was sure ynowe of ye king: that he should not take
his wife: for asmoch^ as his lord was a Ioly man and an amerous

How that the king Edgar wedded the fair Estrylde after the death of Edelwold:
and how yt this Edelwold deyed Capitulo centesimo xiij
THus it befell after that all men in king Edgarys court tho speken and saiden
that this knight Edelwold was rychely auawnced through the marriage of his wife /
and yet they said that he was avau^ced an ho^derfeld more / for he had spoused
the fairest woman that ever was seyne. And the king herd speak somoch^ of her
beauty: he thought that Edelwold / had hy^ deceived and begylled. and thought
preuely i^ his heart that he would gone in to Dene^shire. as if it were for to
hu^te for the heart and for the hynde and other wild bestes. and than he should
se there the lady er he departed the^nes: And this lady was dwelly^g at a manner
besides the forest / there that the king would hunte. and at ye manner he was
herburwed al ye night And wha^ time came the king should soap / he axed after
his Gossyp and after his Godsone: and Edelwold made her to come before the king
/ and notheles if it other had might have been / she should not have comen in
his sight by his will: The lady welcomed the king and swetely him kissed and
he took her by the hand / and tho next by hy^ he set her: and so soped they
to gedre / And tho was a custom and an usage in this land that when a man
drunk unto an other the drynker should sey Wassaill / and that other should
answer drynkehaille / and thus did the king and the lady many times. and also
kyst they ech^ other. And after soap wha^ time was gone to bed. the king
went unto his bed hertely thy^ky^g upon that ladies fairness: and tho was he
ouercomen of her love that him thought that he should deye / but if he had not
his will of her. Upon the morn the king aroos and went into the forest him
there for to disporte with hertes and hyndes and all other wild bestes / and
of the hertes great plente to that ladi he sent. and often he went to solacen
and speken with that ladj whiles he dwelled i^ that co^tre / And after that ye
king remeved the^nes: and thought how he might best deliver Edelwold from his
wife as he had hy^ first deceived / And the king anon after viij. days let
ordeine a parliament at Salesbury of all his baronage counceill to have and for
to ordeyne / how the contree of Northumberland might best ben^ kept that the
Danoys camen not there for to destroy the land / And this Edelwold came also
unto the ky^ges parlame^t. And the king sent hi^ to york for to be keeper of
that co^tre. And thus it befell that men that knew him not slow hy^ by the wey
/ and anon as the king herd that he was deed / he let send after the lady
Estryld: that she should come to the cite of London: and there ben wedded to the
king with great solempnite and worship. and he held a solemn fest. and he
weryd a crown of gold. and the queen weryd also an other And seint Dunston a
morwe came unto the king in to the chamber and fond the king a bed: and the
queen also ynfere And sei^t dunston axed. who she was / The king answerde /
this is the queen Estrilde. And the Erchebisshop seint Dunsto^ said that he did
great wrong and against gods will. to take a woman to wife. whose child he had
take at the foustoun^ And the queen for that word never after loved saint
Dunston / and notheles the good man warned thaim of that folly to let / but his
warny^g availled littell for ye love bitwene hem was so moch^ / The king begat
upon this woman a sone that was kalled Eldred. and tho this child was vi /
year old: the king his fadre deyed. and about ye time he had reigned.xvij. year
/ and lies at Glastenbury

Of saint Edward the martyr how Estrild his Stepmoder let him quelle / for to
make Eldred her own sone king Capitulo Centesimo xiiij
ANd after this edgard reigned edward his sone that he had begote^ on his first
wife that well and nobely governed the land / For he was full of all manner of
goodness and lad full holy life / and above all thing he loved good and the
holy church / And the queen Estrild his stepmoder let him slay for encheso^ to
make her own sone Eldred king and thus was he slain as afterward ye shull
here Hit befell thus on a day that the king Edward went in to a wode for to
play in the south contre besides a town that is kalled Warham. in which
forest was great plente of hertes and of hy^des. And as he had ben^ a while
there him for to pleye. he thought upon his brother Eldred which that was with
his mother the queen. for his place was nigh^ the forest: and he thought for to
gon^ thydder and visit and see his brother / and took with hy^ but a lyttel
meyne. and went hy^ tho toward his stepmoders house: that i^ that time
soiourned in ye castle of Corfe. and as he rode in the thikkenesse of the wode
to aspie his game it befell so that he went amys and lost his meyne that with
him came / and at the last he came owte of the wode / And then^e as he looked
about: he saw there fast besides the manner that his Stepmoder dwelled in. and
thyddderward he went allon^. And anon^ it was told ye Queen. how that Edward
the king was comen allone without any company. and therefore she made yoye
ynowe / and thought in his mind how that she might done that he were slain^ as
preuely as she might And anon preuelich^ she called to her one of his knights
to who^ she had told much of her cou^seill bitwen^ hem: and both they camen to
ye king. and courtously he^ received: and the king told that he was comen her
to visit and also for to speak wit Eldred his brother / The queen many times
him thanked and hy^ prayed that he would there abide wit her all the night / The
king said. that he might not: but ayene he would went unto his his folk if
he might hem find. And when the queen saw that he would not abide: she prayed
hy^ that he would ones drink. and he granted her. and anon^ as the drink came
the queen drank unto the king / and the king took ye cup and set it to his
mouth And in the mean time whiles yt he drank the knight that was with the queen
with a knife smote eue^ the king unto the heart / and there he fill a down
deed of his palfray unto the earth The queen for this deed yaf to the knight
gold and silver great plente and of other richesse ynowe. And the knight anon^
as this was done. he went hy^ over the sea / and so escaped he out of this
land. When this king Edward thus was martred / hit was in ye year of
jncarnacyo^ after our lord Jesus crist / ix C.lxxx year / and he had reigned xij
year and an half. and lies at Glastenbury

Of king Eldred / and how ye king Swyne of Denmark held England. and how
Eldred that was seint edwardes brother was not beloved in his Reaulme / And
therefore he fled into Norma^die Capitulo Centesio^ xv
AFter this king Edward reigned Eldred his brother and saint Dunston crouned him
king: and saint Dunsto^ dyed sone afterward that he had foryeue the queen her
trespace Estrild for e^cheso^ that she was cause of king Edwards death: and
sey^t Dunston had her assoyled and penance her enjoined and she ^yued after a
chaste life and a clean This king Eldred wedded an englissh woman and on her he
begat Edmond Irenside: and an other sone that was called Edwyne: and after
deyed the queen her modre. And in that time came in to england Swyn that was
king of De^marke for to challenge and conquer all that his auncestres had before
that time. and so he conquered and had it all at his a^y^g For the good earl
Cutbert of lyndes^y and all the people of northumberland / and all most all the
great lords of england held with Swyne that was King of Denmark / for as
moch^ as they loved not king Eldred for encheson that his good brother Edward
was slain falsely for encheson of hy^ / and therefore no man set but littel
by him / Wherefore king Swyne had all his will and took all the land and
Eldred the king fled tho into normandy. and so spoke to the duke Rychard
that the duke him yaf his suster emma to wife upon the which he begat two
sons: that one was called alured and that other Edward: And wha^ Swyn had
conquered all the la^d. he reigned nobely / and lived but xv. year. and deyed
and lies at york

How king Eldred came ayene from Norma^dye: and how knoght the Danoys reigned:
and of the werre bitwene him and Edmond Ire^side Capitu / cxvi.
AFter the death of Swyne yt was a danoys Knoght his sone dwelled i^ england and
would have be king / and tho came ayen^ Eldred out of normandye with much
people and with a strong meyne that knoght durst not abide but fley thens into
de^marke. The king Eldred had ayen^ his reaulme and held so great lordship
that he began to destroy all thai^ that had helpen Swyn that was a danoys
against him And afterward came ayen^ this knoght from De^marke with a great
power so that king Eldred durst not with him fight. but fled fro thens in to
london and there held him Tho came Knoght and him besieged so long till king
eldred deyed in ye cite of london / and lies at sey^t Paulus. and he reigned
ix. iere

Of king Knoght cap. cxvij.
AFter the death of this Eldred Knoght that was a danoys began tho for to regne^
but Edmond jrenside that was king eldredis sone by his first wife. ordained a
great host and began to werre upon king knoght: and so he did many times and
often / and the werre was so strong and so hard that wonder it was to wit: And
the queen e^me that dwelled tho at Westmynstre had great dread of her two sons
of ye werre alured and edward lest they should be defoilled and misdone through
this werre / where fore she sent he^ over see in to Norma^dye to ye duke
Rychard her uncle / and there they dwelled in saufte and pees long time: This
edmond jrenside and knoght werred stro^gely to gedre. but at the last they were
accorded in this manner that they should depart the reaulme bitwen^ he^: and so
they dyde^ / and after they became^ good friends and so well loved that they
became^ sworn brethere^: and so well loved to gedre as they had be brethren
geten of o body and of one modery borne

How king Edmond jrenside traitoursly was slayn^ through a traitor. that was
called Edrick of stratton Capit / Cxviij.
ANd after / tho reigned king Edmond Irenside and Knoght the danoys / but thus
it befell afterward that in the same year that they were accorded and so much
loved to gedre: wherefore a false thef traitor had e^uye unto the love that was
between he^ and friendship / whose name was Eldryk of straton^ that was a great
lord and was Edmond jre^sides man and of him held he all the land that he had
/ and notheles he thought to betraie his lord: and make knoght king of the
land. in intent richely to ben^ avau^ced and with hy^ be well beloved. Wherefore
he prayed his lord Edmond jrenside upon a day with him for to eten and to
dwell. and the king courtously him granted. and to him came at his prayer.
and at mete the king was served ryally with diverse metes and drinks. and wha^
night came that he should go to bed. the king took his own meyne and went in
to chamber: and as he looked about: he saw a wonder fair jmage and well made and
in semblant as it were an archier with a bow bent in his hond: and in the bow
a fine arwe / King Edmond went tho nerre to behold it better what it might
ben^ and anon^ the arwe him smote through the bodi and there was the king slowe^
For that Engyn was made to quelle his own lord traitoursly / and wha^ king
Edmond thus was deed and slain^: he had not reigned but x / year. and his people
for him made great sorwe: and his bodi they bear unto Glaste^bury: and there
they hy^ e^tered. And this false traitor Edrik anon went to ye queen that was
king edmondes wife ye wist of her lords death. anon he no^me from her. her two
sons that were fair and young that her lord had upon her got / that own was
called Edward and that other edwyne and lad hem both with hy^ at london. and
took hem to the king knoght y^ he should do wit he^ what his will were. and
told him how que^^tely he had quelled king Edmond for encheson and love of hy^
so that king Knoght all England in his power holy might have. O thou falls
traitor have thou my true brother slayn^ for encheson of me for he was a man
that I most loved in the world / Now by my^ head I shall for thy trauaille you
to reward well as thou have deserved. and anon^ let hy^ take and by^d ho^de
and feet in manner of a traitor / and let cast hi^ in to Thamyse: and in this
manner the false traitor ended his life: The king nomme ye two children and
took he^ to the Abbot of Westmynster / to ward and to keep till he wist what
was best with hem to done

How King Knoght sent king Edmondes sons both in Denmark for to flee / and
how they were saved Capitulo / cxix /
HIt bebell sone afterward that king Knoght had all the land in his hand / and
spoused the queen emme through consent of his Baronage: for she was a fair
woman. yt was Eldredis wife: and the dukes suster of Normandy. and they leued

the queen. what was best for to done wit the sons that were Edmond Ire^sides /
Sir said she they be the right heirs of the la^d and if they lyuen they will
you do much sorwe with werre. and therefore let sent hem in to a strange land

great pity and routh. and would not he^ slay. but led he^ to the king of Hu^gerj
for to noryce / for this walgar was well be known with the king and well

said they were the right heirs of England / and there men would hem destroy /

if they mow lyuen your men they shull becomen. and of you they shull hold all
her land The king of Hungery hem vnderfenge with mochel honor: and let he^
worthily to be kept / And thus it befell afterward that Edwyne the young
brother deyed. and Edward the elder drother lived a fair man and a strong and

and this edward in the chronicles is called among englisshmen Edward the out
law And when he was made knight the kings daughter of Hungery so much hy^

yaf her unto hy^ ^ith good will And Edward her spoused with moch^ honor / The

full glad: This Edward begat upon this lady a sone yt was called Edgar belyng:
and afterward a doughtere that was called Margarete / that afterward was queen
of Scotland. and by the king of Scotland that was called Mancholyn: she had a
daughter that was called maude / that queen was of England through king Henry
that was the first sone of the conqueror that her wedded. and he begat on her
a doughtir yt was called maude. that aft was Empress of Almaigne: and of this
Maude came the king of England that unto this day is kalled Henry the Empresses
sone: and yet had this Edward an other daughter by his wife that was kalled
Cristian and she was a nonne

How king Knoght that was a proud man conquered norwey: and how he became
afterward meke and mild Capitulo C.xx
NOw have ye herd of Edmondes sons with Ire^side that king Knoght we^de that
had been deed as he had commanded walgare before and this knoght had in his
hand all England and Denmark. and after that he went to Norwey that la^d to
conquer / but the king of the land that was called Elaf came with his people
and wend his land well have kept and defended and so there he faught with
him. till at the last he was slain in that bataille / and tho this knoght
no^me all that land in his hand. And when he had conquered Norwey / and taken
feautes and homages there. he came after ayen^ into England and held him self
so great a lord that hy^ thought in all the world his pere no man was. and
became so proud and hauten that it was a great wonder And so it befell upon a
day as he had herd mess at wesmynstre: and would have gone into his palace /
the wawes of ye Thamyse so swyftely against him came^ that all most they
touched his fette. Tho said the king with a proud heart. I commau^de the water to
turn ayen^ or else I shall make you turn. The wawes for his commandment
would not spare But flowed over in hye more and more / The king was so proud of
heart that he would not flee the water: but abode stille in the water. and beat
the water with a small yerde: that he held in his hand. and commanded the
water that it should went no ferther. but al for his commandment the water
would not cese but ever wax more and more an high so that the king was all
vete and stood in ye water. and when he saw that he had abide there to long /
and the water would no thing done his commandment: tho sone he withdrowe hy^
and tho stood he upon a stone and held his hondes an high^ and said this
words in heryng all people This god that makes the sea thus arise an hygh^. he
is king of all kings. and of mightes most: and I am a caytyf and a man dedely
/ and he may never deye^ and all thing does his commandment and to him is
obedient: To ye god I pray that he be my warrant / For I knowelech^ me a
caityf feeble and of no poer. and therefore I will go to Rome without any
lettyng my wykkednesse to punysshe and me to amend For of that god j claim my
land for to hold and of non^ other And anon^ made ready his heir / and him self
to Rome without any lettyng. and by the way did he many alms deeds. and
when he came to Rome also And wha^ he had been there and for his sins done
penance / he came ayen^ into England: and becam^ a good man and an holy: and
left all manner pride and stoutness and lived an holy life all his life
after: and made two abbeys of sey^t Benet. own in England: and that other in
Norwey: for asmoch^ as he loved specyaly seint Benet before all other seintes.
and much he loved also seint Edmond the king and often he yaf great yeftes to
the hows. wherefore it was made rych^: and when he had reigned xx year. he deyed
and lies at wynchestre

Of king Harold that lever had gone i^ foot tha^ ride an horse Capitulo Cxxi
THis Knoght of who^ we have spoke before: had ij. sons by his wife Emme / ye
one was kalled Hardeknoght: and that other Harold: and he was so light of foot
that me^ kalled hy^ communely Harolde harefoot / And this Harlod had no thing
the conditions and manner of king Knoght his fadre. for he set but littel prys

time was never good love bitwen^ him and his brother / for his brother hy^

and lies at westmynstre

Of king Hardeknoght that was haroldes brother Capitulo cxxij
After this Harlot harefoot reigned his brother Hardeknoght a noble knight and
strong and a worthy and much loved cheualrie and all manner goodness / And
when this Hardeknoght had reigned a littel while. he let uncover his brother
Harold and smite of his head that was his brother at westmynster / and let cast
ye head in to a gonge and ye body in to Thamise. and after came fisshers and
took the body with her nets by night: and bear hy^ to sey^t clementes chirch^
and there hy^ beried. And in this manner aue^ged him hardeknoght of his brother
for i^ none other manner he might be avenged / This king Hardeknoght was so
large yeuer of mete and dri^ke that his tables were set every day three times
full with ryall metes and drynkes for his own meyne and for all that camen
unto his court to be rychely served of ryall metes / And this king Hardeknoght
sent after e^me his mother: and made her come ayen^ into england / for she was
driven out of e^glo^d whiles that Harlod harefoot reigned through counsel of
the earl Godewyne that tho was the gretest lord of england next the king. and
most might do what he would through all england through his commau^deme^t: For as
much as he had spoused the daughter of the good king knoght that was a danoys.
which daughter he had by his first wife. And when this queen was driven out of
england and came to ye earl of flau^dres that was kalled Baldwyne his cosyn /
he sonde her there all thing that her needs unto ye time that she went ayen^
in to England that ye king Hardeknoght had sent for her that was her sone and
made her come ayen^ wit mochel honor. This king Hardeknoght wha^ he had reigned
v. year: he deyed and lies at westmy^stre

Of the bilonye that ye danoys dyden to the englysshmen wherefore from that time
after was no Danoys made king of england Capitulo Cxxiiij
AFter the death of this king hardeknoght for as much as he had no thy^g
begoten of his body. the earls and barons assembled and made counceill and
never more after to noma^ that was a Danoys though he were never so great a man
among he^ should never be king of England for ye despite yt ye danoys had done
to Englisshme^. for ever more beforne hand if it were so ye Englisshmen and
danoys hapete^ to mete upon a brygge / ye englisshme^ should not be so hardy to
mean ne stere a foot: but stand still till ye danois were passed forth And more
over if the gentle englisshme^ had not bowyd down her hedes for to do
reverence unto the Danoys they should have been bet and defouled / and such
manner despytes and vilainye dyden the danoys to our englisshme^ / wherefore they
were driven out of the land after the time that king Hardeknoght was deed. for
they had no lord that he^ might maynten

In this manner voyded the Danoys england that never they came ayen^. The earls
and the Barons by her commune assent and counseill senten unto Norma^dye for to
seche the two brethere^ Alured and edward that were dwelly^g with the duke
Rychard that was his eme ^ in intent for to crown alured the elder Brother and
him make king of e^glo^d / and of this thing to make an end The earls and the
barons made her oth^. but the earl Godeweyne of Westsex falsely and traitoursly
thought to slay the two brethere^ anon^ as they should come into england / in
intent for to make his sone Harold king. the which sone he had begote^ upon
his wife that was king knoghtes daughter that was a danoys: and this Godewyne
preuely went him self in to southampto^ for to met there ye two brethere^
wha^ that they should come to lo^d. and thus it befell that the messagiers that
went into Norma^die fond not but oneli Alured yt was ye elder brother for
edward his brother was gon^ to Hungerye for to speak with his cosyn edward the
out law that was edmondes sone with the Irenside: The messagiers told and
said to Alured how the earls and the barons of england sent after hy^ that he
boldly should come in to england and vnderfenge the Reaulme for king
hardeknoght was deed and all the danoys were driven out of the land

How Godewyne the false traitor took Alured upon G^^desdoune when he came fro
Norma^die for to ben^ king of england. and did him be martred in the I Will of
ely. Capit. Cxxiiij
When Alured herd this tydinge^ he thanked god: and went in to a ship wit all
the have that he might and passed ye see / and arrived at sowtha^pton. there
that Godeweyne ye traitor was: And tho this traitor saw that he was come^. he
welcomed him and vnderfeng hy^ with mochel joy. and said that he would led him
to London there that all the barons of England him abode. for to make him king
/ and so they went in her wey toward london. And when they camen upon
Gyldesdoune: tho said ye traitor Godeweyne to alured: take keep about you
both on the lift side and on ye right side and of all ye shul be king ^ of
such^ an hundred more Now for soth said Alured j behote you and if j be king I
shall ordeyn^ and make such^ laws where of god and all folk shall they^ hold well
paid / Now had the traitor commanded all his men that were wit hy^ that
when they were comen upon Gildesdone that they should slay all that were in
Alureds company that came with hy^ from norma^dye. and after that take Alured
and led hy^ in to the I Will of Ely. and there put out both^ his eyes of his
head. and afterward bring him unto the death. And they dyde^ so: for they
quelled all the company that xij. were in nombre of gentil men that were comen
wit Alured from normandye. And after toke^ they Alured and lad hy^ into the I Will
of ely and put his eyes owte of his head: and kutte up his womb and toke^ up
ye chief of his boels / and put a stake in to the ground: and an end of the
boels there to fastened / and with nedles of jren prikked the good child and so
made him go about the stake: till that all his bowelles were drawn all owte /
and so deyed there Alured through treson of the Earl Godewyne: When the lords of
england had herd and wist how Alured that should have ben^ her king was put un
to ye death through the false traitor Godwine. they were all wonder wroth. and
swore among thay^ by god and by his holy names yt he should deye a more werse
death than did Edryk of stratton^ that had betrayed his lord edmond jrenside.
and they would have put hy^ to ye death / but the thef and traitor fley the^nes
into De^marke and there he held him iiij year and more / and lost all his land
in england /

Of seint Edward the confessor that was Aluredes brother how he was king of
england Ca. cxxv /
Ad when this was done all the barons of england senten an other time in to
