this edward in his chyldehode loved almighty god and him drad. and in honest
and clennesse lad his life and hated ye sins as ye death. And wha^ he was
crouned and anointed with a ryall power he foryate not his good manners and
co^dicions that he first used. and foryate not all good customs for no manner
honor: ne for non^ richesse. ne for no manner hygh^nesse But ever more and more
yafe he hy^ to goodness and well loved god and al meekness: and loved god and
the holy chirch^ passing all manner thing: and pour men also / and hem loved
and held as they had ben^ his own brethere^ / and to hem often he yaf great
alms with a good will

Of the first specialte that god showed for seint Edwardes love. by his life
Capit / cxxvi.
It befell on a day as he went from the church of Westmynstre and had herd
mess of saint Johan evangelist / for as much as he loved more specialy seint
Johan evangelist after god and our lady. than he did any other saint: and so
there came to him a pilgrim and prayed him for the love of god and of saint
Johan evangelist some good him for to give / And the king preuely took his
ry^ge of his finger that no man perceived it and yafe it unto the pilgry^ / and
he vnderfenge it and went the^nes This king Edward made all the good laws of
England that yet ben^ most holden: and was so merciable and so full of pity
that noma^ might be more

How the Earl Godewyne came ayen^ into England and had ayene all his land. and
afterward seint Edward wedded his daughter Capitulo Cxxvij /
When the earl Godewyne that was dwelling in de^marke had mochel herd of the
goodness of king edward and that he was full of mercy and of pity. and thought
that he would go ayen^ into England. for to seche and to have grace of him. and
that he might have his la^d again in pees. and arrayed him as moch^ as he might
and put him toward the sea and came into England to London there that the king
was at that time / and all the lords of england and held a parliament /
Godewyne sent to hem that were his friends: and were the most grettest lords
of the land and prayed he^ to be sech^ the kings grace for him. and that he
would his pees and his land grant him His enemies ladden hy^ before the king
to seche grace. And anon as the king hy^ saw: he appelled him of treson. and
of the death of Alured his brother. and these words unto hy^ said. O traitor
Godwyne I yt appelle that thou have betrayed and slayn^ my brother Alured:
Certes sir said Godwyne save your grace and your pees and your lordship j never
hy^ betrayed ne slew him: and therefore I put me in reward of the court / Now
fair lords said the king ye that bien my lieges Earls and Barons of the land
that here ben all assembled. full well ye have herd my^ appelle and the a^swere
also of Godwyne: and therefore j will that ye award and do right The earls and
the barons tho drowe^ hem all to gedre for to done this award by hem self. and
so they speke^ dyuersely among hem For sum said / there was never alience
by homage / serme^t. service / ne by lordshyp between Godwyne and Alured / for
which thing they might him draw and at the last they devised and demed that
he should put him in the kings mercj all to gedres. Tho spoke the earl Leuerich
of Coue^tre a good man to god and to all ye world / and told his reso^ in this
manner: and said / the earl Godewyne is the best frended man of england after
the king and well might it not been gain said / that without cou^ceill of
Godewyne Alured was never put to the death. wherefore I award as touching my part
that hy^ self and his sone / and every of us xij / earls that ben^ his friends
went before the king charged with as much gold and silver as we mow bear
between our hands and pray the king to foryeue his evil will to the earl
Godewyne and receive his homage and his la^d yield ayen^ And all they accorded
unto that award: and came^ in this manner as is above said: every of hem with
gold and silver as much as they might bear bitwene her hands before the king
/ and they sayde^ ye form and the manner of her accord. and of her award. The
king would not hem gayn say / but for as much as they ordained he granted
and confermed. And so was the Earl Godewyne accorded wit the king^ and had
ayene all his land. And afterward he bear hy^ so well and so wisely that the
king loved him wonder moch^ and with hy^ was full pryue And within a littel
time the king loved hy^ somoche that he spoused Edwyne his daughter and made
her queen. And notheles for all that the king had a wife he lived ever more in
chastity and in cle^nesse of body withouthe any flesshli deed doy^g wit his
wife. and the q^ne also in her half lad an holy life ij year and deyed: And
afterward the king lived all his life without any wife. The king yafe the
erledome of Oxenford to Harold that was edwynes sone and made him earl: and so
well they were beloved both fader and he / and so pryue wit the king both the
fadre and the sone: that they might done what thy^g they would by right For
against right he would no thingh done for no manner man: so good and true he was
of conscience. and therefore our lord Ihesu christ great special love to him
showed.

How king Edward saw Swyne king of Denmark drenched in the sea / in the
sacrament as he stood and herd his mass Capitulo Cxxviij
IT befell upon wythso^day as king Edward herd his mass in the great church
of Westmy^ster right at the leuacion of Ihesu cristes body: and as all me^ were
gadred in to the church and came^ nere the auter the sacry^ge for to see: The
king his ho^des lift upon high / and a great laughter took up wherefore all
that about hy^ stood gretely wo^dred. And after mass they axed why the kings
laughter was / Fair lords said he. the king Wine the younger / that was king
of Denmark came into the sea with all his power for to have comen in to
England upon us to have werred / and I saw him and all his folk drenched in
the high^ see. and all this saw I in the eleuacyo^ of Jesus cristes body between
the prestes ho^des / and I had thereof so moch^ joy that I might not my
laughter witholde. And the Earl Leuerich which besides him stod at the
leuacyon / openly saw the form of bread turn into a likeness of a child
yo^ge: and took up his right hand / and first blessed the king / and afterward
the Earl. and the earl anon^ turned him toward ye king to make him see that
holy sight: Tho said the king / Sir earl quod he I see well that ye see.
thanked be god that j have honored my god my sauuour vysibly Ihesu christ in
form of man. whose name be blisshed in all worlds. am^

How the ring that seint Edward had give to a pour pilgry^ for the love of
god and of seint Ioha^ Evangelist. came ayen^ unto king Edward Cap. Cxxix
THis noble man seint edward reigned viij year / and thus it befell upon a time
beforne er he deyed that two me^ of england were gone in to the holy land. and
hadden done her pilgremage and were goy^g ayen^ to her own contre / And as
they went in the wey they met a pilgrim that courtoisly hem sa^ued. and axed

England. Tho axed he who was the king of england. and they answered and said:
the good king edward / Fair fre^des tho said the pylgrim: when that ye come
ayene in to your contre / I pray you that ye will goo unto ye king edward and
often times him great in mine name / and often times thank him of his great

he had herd mess at westmy^ster / for saint johannes love evangelist: and
delyueryd tho the ry^g unto the two pilgrymes: and said j pray you for to gone
and bear this ring / and take it to the king Edward and tell him that I sent
it him. and a full rycher yefte I wol hy^ give For upon the xij day he shall
come to me: and ever more dwell in bliss without end: Sir said the
pylgrimes. what man ben ye and in what place is yowr dwelling. Fair friends
said he: I am Johan the Evangelist: and am dwelling with almighty god: and your
king Edward is my friend / and j love him speciali. for encheson that he has
ever lived in cle^nesse / and is a clean maid And I pray you my message all
for to done as I to you have said. Wha^ seint Johan Evangelist had thus hem
charged suddenly he voyded owte of her sight

The pylgrimes tho thanked almighty god. and went forth in her way. And wha^
they had gon^ two or three miles: they begone to wex weary. and sat a down he^
for to rest. and so they fill a sleep. And wha^ they had slept well. the one of
hem awoke and lift up his head: and looked about and said unto his felawe.
arise up and let us go in our way / What said the one felawe to that other:
where be we now / certes said that other It seems me that this is not the same
co^tre that we laid us in for to rest and sleep For we were from jherusalem
but three miles. They nommen up her hondes and blissed hem and went forth in her
way. and as they went in her way / they saw shepeherdes goy^g with her shep.
that spaken none other langage but Englissh / Leave friends said one of the
pylgrimes. What contre is this. and who is lord thereof / And one of the
shepeherdes a^swered. This is the contre of Ke^t in England / and of the whych^
the good king Edward is lord / The pylgrimes thanked god almyghti and seint
Johan evangelist. and went forth in her way and came to Canterbury / and fro
thens in to London. and there they founden the king Edward. and told him all
fro the beginning unto the end: as much as seint Ioha^ had hem charged: and
of all thi^^ges how they spedde by the way* and took the ryng to ye king
Edward / and he vnderferdeng it and thanked god almighty and seint Johan
evangelist. And tho made he him ready from day to day: for to went owte of his
life when god would for him send

How seint Edward deyed on the xij. day Capitulo Cxxx
ANd after if befell thus in cristesmasse. eve as the holy man Edward was at
gods service matynes for to here of that hygh^ feste he becam^ full seek. and
in the morwe endured with much pain the mass for to here / and after let him
be lad into his chamber: there for to rest him. but in to his halle among his
barons and his knights might he not come hem for to comfort and solace as he
was wonet for to done at that worthy fest. where for all her mirth and comfort
among hem all that were in the hall. was turned into care and sorwe: for
encheson that they dred for to lose her good lord the king: And upon seint
johannes day ewa^gelist tho that came next / ye king vnderfe^ge his ryghtes of
the holy chirch^ / as falls to every christian man. and abode the mercy and the
will of god: and tho he let the two pilgrims before him come and yaf hem rich^
yeftes and betoke hem unto god / And also the abbot of westmynster he let
before hy^ come / and took hy^ that ry^ge in honor of god and sey^t marie and
of seint Ioha^ evangelist: And the abbot took and put it among other relics:
so that it is at westmynstre and ever more shall be: and so lay the king sike
till the xij eue^ / and tho deyed ye good king Edward at westmynstre / and there
he lies: for whose love god has showed many fair miracles. And this was in the
year of Incarnacio^ of our lord Ihesu crist Mlxv year: and after he was
translated and put into the shryne through ye noble martyr seint Thomas of
Canterbury.

How Harolde that was Godewynes sone was made king / and how he escaped fro the
duke of bretaigne Capi. cxxxi
When seint Edward was gone out of this world and was gone to god and worthe^
entered as it aperteigned to such a lord for to be. the barons of the la^d
would have had Edward Helingus sone to Edward the out law that was Edmo^des
Ire^sides sone to be king: for asmoche as he was most kyndest kings blood of
the reaulme / But haroldes sone through the earl Godewine and the strength of
his fader Godewyne / and through other great lords of the Reaulme that were of
his kyn and unto hy^ sybbe seized all England to his hand. and anon let
croune this forsaid Harold king after the enterement of sey^t edward / This
king Harold that was Godewynes sone the second year after that saint Edward
was deed. would have gone in to Flaundres. but he was driven through tempest of
the sea in the co^tre of Pountyfe / and there was he taken and brought to the
duke wiyllyam of Norma^dye. And this Harold wend tho that the duke william
would have ben^ avenged upon him: for encheson that the earl Godewyne which
was Haroldus fadre had let quelle Alured that was seint Edwardes brother. and
pry^cipaly for encheson that ye forsaid alured was queen emmes sone that was
rychardys mother duk of Normandye / that was ayell to ye duk William. And
notheles when ye duk william had Harold in prison and under his power / for as
moch^ as this Harold was a noble knight wise and worthy of body: and that his
fadre were accorded with ye good king Edward. and therefore he would not misdone
him. but all manner things that bitwene he^ were spoken and ordained / Harolde
by his good will swore upon a book and upon the holy say^tes that he should
spouse and wedde duke wylliams daughter after the death of seint Edward: and
that he should besyly done his dever for to keep and save the Reaulme of England
/ to the profit and avauntage of duck wylliam: And wha^ Harold had thus made
his oth^ unto duk william / he let him go and yafe him many rich yeftes / and
he tho went the^nes and came in to e^glo^d: and anon did in this manner wha^
saint Edward was deed. and as a man falsely forswore he let croune hy^ king of
england / and falsely brak the covenant that he had made before with duke william
/ wherefore the duke was with him wonder wroth. and swore that he would upon him
ben^ aue^ged what ever to him might come thereof. And anon^ duk william let
assemble a great host and came in to England for to aue^ge hy^ upon Harold and
to conquer ye la^d if that he might. And in the same year that Harold was
crouned: harolde harestre^ge king of Denmark arrived in to scotland / and
thought to have ben^ king of England. and he came tho in england and and
quelled and robbed and destroyed all that he might till that he came to york
and there he quelled many me^ of armes^ a thousand and an C prestes. Wha^ this
tidy^ge came to the king / he assembled a strong power and went for to fight
wit Harold of De^marke. and wit his own ho^d hy^ quelled. and the Danoys were
disco^fyted: and tho they that were left a live with moch^ sorwe fledde^ the^s
to her ships. and thus king harold of england quelled king harold of De^marke.

How William bastard duke of norma^dye came into england. and quelled king
Harold: Capitulo Cxxxij
And wha^ this bataill was done: Harold became so proud and would no thing pert
with his people of thing that he had gotten. but held it all toward him self /
wherefore the most party of his people were wroth and from hy^ departed. so yt
only with hy^ left no mo but his soudyours / And upon a day as he sat at mete: a
messagier came to hy^ and said that william bastard duke of Norma^dye was
arrived in England with a great host and had taken all the la^d about
Hastynge. and also mined the castle: Wha^ the king had herd this tydinge / he
went thidder wit a little people with all the have that he might / for a littel
people was with him left And when he cam^ thidder he ordained his me^ for to give
bataille to the duke William / but the duk axed him of these iij / things / if
that he would have his daughter to wife as he had made and swore his oath and
behight / or that he would hold the land of hy^ in truage^ or that he would
determine this thing through bataill This Harold was a proud man and a stout.
and trustyd wonder much upon his strength^ and faught with the duke and with
his people but Harold and his men were discomfyted in this bataill: and him self
was there slain. and this bataille was ended at tonbrigge in the second year
of his regne. upon seint Calixtes day / And he lies at Waltha^

Of king william bastard. and how he governed him well and wisely: and of the
werre bitwene him and the king of France Ca. cxxxiij
WHa^ william bastard duke of Normandye had conquered all the land^ upon
Cristmasse day tho next swing / he let croune hi^ king at Westmy^ster: and was
a worthy king. and yaf to Englisshmen largeli lo^des and to his knights. And
afterward he went over the sea and cam^ into Norma^die and there dwelled he a
while. and in the second year of his regne he came ayen^ into England: and
brought wit him Maude his wife / and let croune her queen of England on
withsonday And tho anon after ye king of Scotland that was called Mancoly^
began to strife and werre wit the duke william / and king William ordained hy^
toward Scotland with his men both by land and by the sea for to destroy the
king Mancoly^. but they were accorded: And the king of scotland became his man
and held all his la^d of him And king william received of him his homage and
came ayen^ in to England. And when king william had be king xvij year. maude
the queen deyed. on who^ king william had begoten many fair children / that is
for to seyne Robert Curthuse. Willyam le Rous. Rychard also the which that
deyde / Henry beauclerk. and Maude also the which that was ye earls wife of
Boleynes / and other four doughteres And after his wyfes death began there great
debate bytwen^ hy^ and the king of France Philippe: but at the last they were
accorded And tho dwelled the king of England in the la^d of norma^dye and no
man him werred. and he also upon no man long time / And the king of France
said upon a day in skorne of king Wylliam: that king wylliam had long time
lived in chilhed and long time had rested hy^ / And this word came to the
king of England there that he lay in Norma^dye at Rouen. and for this word was
he evil paid and right wroth toward the king of France: and swore by god
that when he were arise of his gysin he would light a thousand candeles to the
king of France. And anon he let assemble a great host of normandye and also
of Englysshmen / and in the beginning of Heruest he came in to France and
brend all the towns there that he came by through all the co^tre: and robbed and
did all the evil that he might thurghoute all France: and at the last he
bre^de the cite of Ma^dos^ and commanded his people for to bear straw. and as
much as they might to brenne / and hy^ self help thereto all that he might wit
a good will. And there was great hete of the fire which was so great. and of
ye sun yt tho was wonder hoot: that all stuffed hy^ self became and fell in
to a great sickness: And when he saw that he was so strong seek / he
ordained and assygned all norma^dye unto Robert Curthous his sone. and all
england to William the Rous: and bequath to Henry beauclerk all his tresour.
And tho he thus had done: he vnderfenge all the sacraments of the holy church.
and deyde in the xxij year of his regne. and lies at Caan in normandye

Of king Wylliam Rous / that was wyllia^ Bastardes sone that destroyed towns
and houses of Religyon / for to make the new forest. Capitulo Cxxxiiij.
ANd after this William bastard reigned his sone wil^iam the Rows. and this
william was a wonder contraryous man to god and to the holy church: and let
amend and make the town of Cardeys. that the paynyms had destroyed. This king
william destroyed ye holy church: and all his poscessions in what part he
might he^ find And there for there was so great debate between hy^ and the
Erchebysshop of Canterbury Ancelme: for encheson that he vnderna^me him of his
wykkednesse that he destroyed the holy chyrch^ / And for encheson there of: the
king Wylliam to him bare great wrath. and for that cause he exylled him owte of
the land. and the erchebisshop tho went to the court of Rome and there
dwelled he with the ^ope And this King made the new forest and cast and
destroyed xxvi tounes and lxxx houses of religyo^. all for to make his forest
longer and bredder / and became wonder glad and proud of his wode and of his
forest and of the wild bestys yt were thery^ that is was mervaill for to wit.
so that men kalled hy^ keeper of wodes and of pastures: and the le^ger that he
lived the more wikked that he became / both^ to god / and to the holy church
and to all his men And this king let make the great hall at westmynster. so
upon a day of witsonday he held therein his first feste and he looked about and
said. that the halle was to littel by the haluendel. And at the last he became
so co^trarious that all thing that plesed god displesed him / and all thing
that god loved he hated dedely. and so it befell that he dremed and met upon a
night a lyttel er yt he deyed. that he was let blood: and bled a great quantyte
of blood: and a streme of blood lept an hygh^ toward heaven more than an C
vethemen / and the clernesse of the day was turned all in to a derkenesse /
and the firmament also And when he awoke he had great dread / so that he ne
wist what to done / and told his dreme to all the meyny of his counseill / and
said that he had great dread. and supposed that him was some myschaunce to
come. And in the second night before a monk dremed of the household that the
king went into a chyrch^ with much people / and he was so proud that he
despised all the people that was with him. and he took the image of the
crucifixe. and shamefully bote he it wit his teth / and the Crucifixe mekely
suffrid all that he did. but the king as a wode man rent of the arms of the
Crucifixe and cast it under his fete / and defowled it. and threw it all a
broad / And a great flamme of fire came out of the crucifixes mouth: of which
dreme many man had great mervaille / The good man that had dremed this dreme /
had told it to a knight that tho was most pryue with the king of all men: and
this forsayde knight was kalled Hamundes sone / and he told the dreme to the
king / and said that it should betoken other thing tha^ good. Nevertheless when
the king this herd: he laughed and set lyttel thereof: and thought that he
would gone hu^te and pleye in the forest. and his men him counseilled that he
should not that day ne for no manner thing come in ye wode. so that he bode at
home before mete: but anon^ as he had eten: no man might him let that he
nolde gone to ye wode for to have his disporte And so it befell that one of his
knights the which was kalled Walter tyrell / would have shot to an heart and
his arwe glanced upon a braunce and trough misauenture smote the king to the
heart / and so he fell down deed to ye ground without any word speky^g and
so ended he his life / and it was no great wonder for the day that he deyde he
had let to ferme ye erchebisshop rich^ of Canterburj. and xij. abbeyes also.
and ever more did great destructyon to ye holy chirch^ through wrong full taking
and axinges / for no man durst with say yt he would have done. and of his
lythernesse he would never withdraw nothyr to amend his life / and therefore
god would suffer him no le^ger to regne in his wykkednesse / and he had ben^
king xiij year and vj. wekes. and lies at westmynstre

Of king Henry Beauclerke. that was william rous brother / and of the debate
bitwene him and Robbert Curthouse his brother Capitulo centesimo xxxv
ANd wha^ this william rous was deed henri beauclerke his brother was made king

ben^ others heir. and so bitwen^ hem should be no debate ne strife: And when

speak with his brother: And among other things the duke of norma^dye foryafe to

/ And with good love the duke went tho ayen^ in to Norma^dye: And when the ij
year were a gon^ through Enticeme^t of the deuell and of lyther men a great
debate arose bitwen^ the king and the duke / so that the king through counseyll
went over the sea in to Norma^dye And when the king of England was come^ in to
Norma^dye / all ye great lords of normandye turned to the king of england and
held^n ayens the duke her own lord and him forsook and to the king hem yielded
/ and all the good castelles and tounes of norma^dye / and sone after was the
duke taken and lad with the king in to england. and the king let put the duke
in to prison. and this was the ve^geau^ce of god. for when the duke was in the
holy la^d / god yafe him such might and honowr there / wherefore he was chosen
for to ben^ king of Iherusalem. and he would not be it / but forsook it / and
therefore he sent him that shame and despyte for to be put i^ to his brothers
prison.

Tho seysed king Henry all normandye in to his hand and held it all his lyfes
time: And in the same year came the bishop Auncelme from the court of Rome in
to England ayen^ / And the king and he were accorded.

And in the year next coming after. there began a great debate between king
Philip of France: and king Henry of England. Where fore king Henry went in to
Norma^dye: and the werre was right strong between he^ two And tho deyed the
king of France. and Lowys his sone was made king anon after his faders death
and tho went king Henry ayen^ into England and married Maude his daughter to
Henry the Emperor of Almaigne

Of the debate that was bitwene King Lowys of France and king Henry of
England. and how king Henryes two sons were lost in the high see. Capitulo
Cxxxvj
WHenne king Henry had ben^ king xvij year / a great debate arroos between king
Lowys of France and king Henry of England. for encheson that the king had sent
into Norma^dye to his me^ that they should ben^ helpy^g to ye Earl of bloyes.
as mochel as they might in werre against the king of Frau^ce^ and that they were
as ready unto him as they would ben unto her own lord. for e^cheson that the
earl had spoused his sustre dame Maude / for which encheson the king Lowys
king of France did much sorwe to norma^dye: Wherefore the king of England was
wonder wroth. and with great haste went he over the sea wit a great power /
and came into Norma^dye for to defend that land / And the werre between hem
lasted two year / till at the last they two foughten to gedre. and ye king
Lowys was disco^fyted and uneath escaped a way with much pain: and the most part
of his men were taken: and the king did with hem what hem lyked. and sum of
hem let he go freely and sum let he put to the death: But afterward the two
kings were accorded: And when king Henry had holy all the la^d of normandye
and sco^fyted his enemies of France: he turned ayen^ into England with mochel
honowr: and his two sons William and Rychard would come after her fadre / and
went to the sea with a great company of people but er they might come to lord:
the ship come aye^s a Roche and brake all in to pecys. and they were all
drownyd that were theryn / sauf o man that was in ye same ship the which
that eskaped And this was on sey^t Katerynes day / and thees were ye names of
hem that were drownyd / that is to say Wylliam the kings sone Rychard his
brother. the earl of Chestre. Octonell his brother. Geiffrey Rydell / Walter
emucry: Godfrey erchedeken. the kings daughter the Countess of Perses / The
kings Nece the countess of Chestre: and many other / When king Henry and the
other lords were arrived in England and herd thise tidings: they made sorwe
ynowe and all her myrthe and joy was turned into morny^g and sorwe

How Maude the Empress came ayen^ into England: and how she was wedded to
Geyffroy the earl of Angeoy Capitulo Cxxxvij
ANd when that two year were a gone that the earl had dwelled with the king The
earl went tho from the king. and began to werre upon him / and did much harm
in the land of Normandye and took there wit strength^ a strong castle. and
there he dwelled all that year. And tho came to him tydyng that Henry the
emperor of Almaigne. yt which had spoused Maude his daughter was deed. and
that she dwelled no le^ger in almaigne. and ye she would come ayene in to
Normandye to her fadre. And when she was come to hy^ he no^me her tho to him /
and came ayen^ in to englond^ and made the englisshme^ to make oath and feaute
unto the Empress. and the first man that made the oath was William the
Erchebisshop of Canterbury. and that other king David of Scotland / and after
him all the earls and barons of England. Also after the noble man ye earl of
Angoy a worthy knight sent to the king of England that he would grant him for
to have his daughter to spouse Maude the Emperesse. and for encheson that her
fadre wist that he was a noble man / the king granted hy^ and consented
thereto. And tho took he his daughter and ladde her in to Normandye. and came to
the noble knight Earl Gaufryde and he spoused the forsaid Maude with mochel
honor. and the earl begat upon her a sone / that was called Henry the
empresses sone. And after when all this was done / the king Henry dwelled all
that year in Normandye / and after that long time a grevons sickness took
him: where through he deyed.

And this king Henry had reigned xxxv. year / and iiij. months: and after he
deyed as before is said in normandye. and his heart was entered in the great
church of owr lady in Rouen. and his body was brought with mochel honor in to
England: and entered at Redy^g. in the abbey. of the which abbey he was
begynner and foundour

How Stephane king Henry sustres sone: was made king of England Capitulo
Cxxxviij
AFter this king Henry the first. was made king his nepheu his sustres sone
Stephen earl of Boloigne. For anon as he herd the tidy^g of his uncles death:
He passed the sea and came into england / through counsel and strength^ and
help of many great lords in england aye^s her oath. that they had made Maude
the empress: and toke^ the Reaulme and let crown stephen king of the land:
and the Erchebysshop william of Canterburj that first made ye oath of feaute
unto maude the e^presse: set the croune upon king stephenes head and hy^
anointed / and bisshoppe Rogier of Salysbury mayntened the kings party in as
moch^ as he might: The first year that king stephen began to regne he assembled
a great host: and went hy^ toward scotland for to have werre upon ye king of
scotland: but he came aye^s him in pees and in good manner and to him trustyd:
but he made to hi^ none homage for as moch^ as he had made homage unto the
emperesse Maude. And the iiij. year of his regne Maude the Empress came in to
england. And tho began the debate bitwene king Stephen and Maude the empress.
and this Maude went unto the cite of Nichol. and the king her besieged long
time / and might not speed so well the cite was kept and defended / and they
that were with in ye cite queyntely escaped away without any manner harme^ and
tho took the king the cite and dwelled theryn till candellmesse And tho came
the barons that held with the Empress / that is for to say: the earl Randulfe
of Chestre / the earl Robert of Gloucestre: Hugh^ bygot: Robert of morley. and
brought with hem a strong power / and faughte^ with the king: and yafe him a
great bataill / in which bataille king Stephen was taken / and set in prison
in the castle of Bristowe

How Maude the Emperesse went fro Wynchestre unto Oxe^ford / and after she
escaped to wallynford. and what sorwe and disese that she had Capitulo Cxxxix
WHe^ne the king was taken and brought in to ward in the Castle of Bristowe
This Maude the empress anon^ was made lady of England: and all men held her
for lady of the land: but they of Kent held with the king Stephenes wife / and
also William of pree and his reteune help hem and held werre against Maude the
Empress and anon^ after the king of Scotland came to hem with an hugh^ nombre
of people. and tho went they ynfere unto Wynchestre / there that the empress
was and would have taken her / but the Earl of Gloucestre came with his power
and fought with hem. and the emperesse in the mean while that the bataille
dured escaped fro thens and went unto Oxenford and there she held her. and i^
the same bataille was the Earl of Glowcestre discomfyted and taken and wit hy^
also many other great lords. And for his delyuerance so was king Stephen
delivered out of prison. And when he was delivered out of the prison he went
the^s to Oxenford and besieged the Empress: the which that tho was at
Oxe^ford. and the siege endured fro Mychelmasse unto saint andrews ride. and
the empress let tho cloth her all in white lynnen cloth / for encheson that
she would not be known. for in the same time was much snow / and so she
escaped by the thamyse from hem away that were her enemies / And fro the^s she
went to walli^gford / and there she held her: and the king would have besieged
her but he had so much to done with the Earl Randolfe of Chestre. and with
Hugh bigot that strongely werred upon him in every place that he ne wist
whyther for to turn. and the earl of Glowcestre halpe hem with his power

How Gaufryde the Earl of Angeoy yafe up unto Henry ye Empresses sone all
normandye Capitulo Cxl.
ANd after this the king went unto Wylton / and would have made a castle there:

Henry came into England with a strong power and began for to werre upon king
Stephen and took the castle of Malmesbury and did moch^ harm^ / and the king
Stephen had so much werre that he ne wist whither for to went / but at the
last they were accorded / through ye Erchebisshop Theobald and through other
worthy lords of England / upon this condition that they should depart the

half all the land of England And thus they were accorded. and pees cried
through out all england. And wha^ the accord was made bitwene the ij lords.
king Stephen became so sorry for cause he had lost half england and fell in to
a such^ maladye / and deyed in the xix year / viij wekes and v / days of his
regne: all in werre and co^tak / and he lies in the abbey of Feneresham / the
which he let make in the vij year of his regne

Of king Henry the second that was the empresses sone. in whose time seint
Thomas of Canterbury was chau^celer Cap / Cxli
ANd after this king stephen reigned Henry the emperesses sone: and was crouned

his regne: that the duke Henry of Saxone spoused Maude his daughter: and begat

of his regne deide the good earl Robert of gloucestre / the which that had
fownded the abbeye of nonnes Eton / And in that same year ^arike king of
Iherusalem conquered Babiloigne / The xvi. year of his regne he let crown his
sone Henry king at westmy^ster. and him crownyd Rogier Erchebysshop of york in
harmyng of thomas erchebisshop of Canterbury. wherefore the same Rogier was
acursed of the pope

Of King Henry that was sone of king Henrj the Empresses sone: and of the

Capitulo Cxlij
AFter ye coronacyon of king henry / sone of king Henry the Empresses sone went
over in norma^die and there he let marye Eleniore the daughter of the Dolphyne
that was king of Almaigne. And in ye vij year that the Erchebisshop seint
Thomas had ben^ outelawed / the king of France made the king and saint Thomas
accorded / And tho came Thomas the erchebisshop to Canterbury ayene to his own
chyrch^. and this accord was made in the beginning of Aduent: and afterward he
was quelled and martred the v. day of Cristmasse that tho next came: For king
Henry thought upon saint thomas the erchebisshop upon Cristmasse day as he sat
at mete and said thise words: that if he had any good knight with hy^: he had
be many day passed avenged upon ye Erchebisshop Thomas. And anon^ Sir william
breto^. Sir hugh^ morvile. Sir william cracy / and sir Reynout fitz vrse beres
sone i^ e^glissh preuely went unto the sea and came^ into England to the
chyrch^ of canterbury: and him there they martred at sey^t Benettes auter in the
modre church. and that was in the year of Incarnacion of our lord Ihesu crist
M.Clxxij year / And anon after Henry the new king began for to make werre
upon Henry his fadre / and upon his brethere^ also. And so upon a day the king
of France and all the ky^ges sons and the king of Scotland and the gretest
lords of england were arisen against the king henry the fadre. and at the last
as god would he conquered all his enemies. And the king of France and he were
accorded / and tho sent Henry the fadre specialy unto the king of France and
prayed him hertely for his love that he would send to hy^ by lettres the names
of he^ that begonne^ the werre upon him And the king of france sent ayen^ to
him by a letter the names of hem that bego^nen the werre. The first was Johan
his sone. and Rychard his brother / and Henry his sone the new kyng^ Tho was
henry the king wonder wroth and cursed the time that ever he he^ begat / And
while the werre dured Henry his sone deyed sore repe^ty^g his misdede / and
most sorwe made of onj man: for cause of sey^t Thomas death of Canterbury / and
prayed his fadre with much sorwe of heart mercy for his trespass: and his fadre
foryafe it him: and had of him great pity. and after he deyed the xxxvi year of
his regne^ and lies at Redyng

How the christian lost the holy la^d in the forsaid ky^ges time through a falls
christian man that became a sarazene Cap / Cxliij
ANd whiles that king henry the empresses sone lived and reigned the great
bataill was in the holy la^d between the cryste^ men and the sarazenes. but ye
cryste^ me^ were there quelled through great treson of the earl Tyrp^ that would
have had to wife the queen of Iherusalem. that some time was baldewines wife
but she forsook him and took to her lord a knight a worthi man that was kalled
sir Emperches / wherefore the earl tyrpe was wroth and went anon right to ye
Soladyne that was soudan of Babiloigne / and became sarazene and his man* and
forsook his cristendomme and all christian law / and the criste^ men wist not of
this deeds. but wend for to have had great help of hy^ as they were wonet to
have before: and when they came^ in to the bataille / this false criste^ man
turned unto ye sarase^s: and forsook his own nations. and so were ye christian
men there quelled with the sarazens. And thus were the christian men slain and
put to horrible death: and the Cite of Iherusalem destroyed and the holy cross
borne a way^ The king of France let he^ cross for to go into the holy land:
And among hem went Rychard king Henry's sone after the king of France that
took the cross of the erche bishop of tours / but he took not the vyage at
that time / for encheson that he was let by othyr manner ways and needs to be
done. and when king Henry his fadre had reigned xxxv. year and v. months and
iiij days he deyed and lies at fou^tenerard.

Of King Rychard that conquered all the holy land that the christian men had
lost Capitulo Cxliiij
ANd after this king Henry reigned Rychard his sone a strong man and a worthy /
and also a bold. and he was crouned at Westmynster of ye erchebisshop

regne king Rychard him self and Baldewyne the erchebisshop of Canterbury. and
Hubert bishop of Salisbury / and Randulphe earl of Gloucestre. and othyr many
lords of England: went into the holy land: and in that vyage deyde the

that he came in his way unto Cipers / and took cypres with great force / and
sythen king Rychard went forth toward the holy land / and gate there as moch^
as the criste^ men hadden lost before and conquered ye la^d ayen^ through great
might sauf only the holy cross And wha^ king Richard came to the town of
Acres for to get the cite: a great debate arose bitwene him and ye king of
France. so that ye king of france went ayen^ in to france / and was wroth
toward the king Rychard But er king Richard went ayen^ he took ye cite of
acres: And wha^ he had taken it. he dwelled in the cite a while: but to him

england and Normandye also and would croune him king of ye la^d And when king
Rychard herd this tiding / he went ayen^ toward england with all the speed
that he might: But the duke of Ostriche met with him and took him and brought
him to the Emperor of Almaign^ / and the emperor brought him into his prison:
and afterward he was deliured for an hugh^ rau^son^: that is for to say an
hounderd thousand pound. and for which raunsone to be paid each other chalise
of england was molte and made into money: and all the monks of the order of
cisteaulx yaue^ all her books to done hem to selle:

And at the last the pope sent by his auctoryte and enioy^ed to the bisshoppes
of england that if the king would not vnderfonge the Pryour of Canterbury and

that they might pray he would not consent thereto. And wha^ these four

after the a^nuncyacion of owr lady they pronounced the general enterdytyng
through owte all England / so that the chyrch^ doors were shit with keys and
with other fasteny^g and with walls: and when the enterdytyng was pronounced.
than the king began for to wex all out of mesure. and no^me unto his hand:
all the poscessions of the four bisshoppes and of all the clergy through out

her living / wherefore the bisshoppes cursed all hem that put or should meddle
with holy church goods ayens the will of he^ that hem owed / And wha^ the
king would not cese of his malice for no manner thing. the four bisshoppes a
fore said went over see and went to the bishop of Cau^terburj and told him

certay^ persons in his stead. that should done as much as if him self were
there. and wha^ ye bisshoppes herd this: they turned ayen^ into england and
came^ unto Canterbury the tydy^ge came to ye king that the bisshoppes were
come^ ayen^ to canterbury: and hy^ self might not come^ thidder at ye time.
but he sent thidder bisshoppes earls and abbotes for to trete wit he^ that the
king should vnderfo^ge the erchebisshop Stephen and ye pryour. and all ye monks
of canterbury. and that he should never after ye time no thy^g take of ye holy
chyrch^ aye^s ye will of he^ that owed ye goods / and that ye king should make
full ame^des to he^ / of who^ he had any goods taken. and that ye holy chirch^
should have all frau^chises as ferforth as they had in sei^t Edwardes time the
confessor

How king Johan destroyed the order of Cisteaux Capi. cxlix
ANd in the same time the Irysshme^ bego^ne to werre upon king Johan / and king
joha^ ordained hy^ for to went into Irla^d an hugh^ tax through out all
England / that is to say xxxv.M / mark / And sent through all England to the
monks of the order of Cisteaux that they should help him of vi / M. marck of
silver / and they answered and said that they durst nothing do without her
abbot of Cisteaux. Wherefore king johan when he came from Irland he did hem so
moch^ sorwe and care that they nyst where to abide: for he took so moch^
rau^sone of euerj house of hem that the sum of an mounted to ix / M:ccc.
mark. so that they were clean lost and destroyed^ and voided her houses and her
lands / through out all england / and the abbot of Wauerley drad so moch^ his
menace that he forsook all the Abbey and went the^s. and preuely ordained hy^
over see to the house of Cisteaux. Wha^ the tyding came to the pope that the
king had done so moch^ malice. tho was he to the king ward full wroth / and sent
two legatz unto the king. that own was caled Pandolfe and that other dura^t /
that they should warn the king in the popes name that he should cese of his
persecucio^ that he did unto the holy chyrch^ / and amend the wrong and the
trespass that he had done to the Erchebisshop of Canterbury / and to the
pryour and unto the monks of canterbury and to all the clergy of England. and
that he should restore the goods ayen^ that he had taken of hem ayens her will.
and else they should kurse the king by name. and to do this thing and to
conferme: the pope took he^ his lre^s in billis patentz. These two legatz camen
into england and wente^ to the king at Northampto^ there that he held his
parlame^t. and full curtously they him salued and saiden. Sir we ben come fro
the pope of Rome the pees of holy chyrch^ and of ye land to amend / and we
amoneste you first in ye popis half that ye make full restitucio^ of the goods
that ye have rauisshed of the holy church and of the land / and that ye
vnderfenge stephen the Erchebisshop of canterbury in to his dignite* and the
pryour of Canterbury and his monks. and that ye yield ayen^ unto the
erchebisshop all his lands and rentes without any with holdy^g / and yet more
over. that ye such^ restitucio^ him make as holy chirch^ shall hold her
pai^ed. Tho a^swered the king as touching the pryour and his monks of
Canterbury all that ye have said / I will gladly do and all thy^g that ye will
ordeine But as touchy^g the erchebisshop I shall tell you in mine heart as hit
lithe: that the erchebisshop leve his bisshoprich^ / and that the pope tha^ for
hi^ wol pray and than upon adventure me should like some other bisshoprye for to
give him in england / and upon this co^dicyon I wol him receive and vnderfo^ge.
And notheles in england as Erchebysshop if he abide: he shall never have so good
saufconduyt / but he shall be taken. Tho said Pandolfe unto the king / the holy
church never was wonet to discharge an Erchebisshop without cause reasonable /
but ever she had be wonet to chastise pry^ces yt to god and the holy chirch^
were inobediant. What how now quod ye king Manace ye me / Nay said Pandolf.
but ye now openly have told as it stands in your heart: and to you we will
tell what is the popes will. and thus it stand. yt he has you holy
interdited and accursed for the wro^ges that ye have done to the holy chirch^
and to ye clergy. and for asmoch^ as ye dwell and beth in will to abide in
malice and will not come to none ama^dement. ye shall understand that fro
this time afterward / the sentence is upon you yeue^ and holds stead and
strength^. and upon all thay^ that with you have co^muned before this time
whethir they ben^ earls barons or knights. or any other what so ever they
ben^: we hem assoille saufly unto this day and fro this time afterward of what
condition ever that they be: we hem accurse that wit you comen^ and so do we
sentence upon he^ openly and specialy / And we assoill quytly Earls barons
knights and all other manner men of her services homages and feautes that they
should unto you done And this tidinge to co^ferme we give pleyne power to the
bishop of wynchestre / to the bishop of Northewhiche: And the same power we
give in Scotland to the bisshoppes of Rouchestre and of Salisbury: and in
wailis we give ye same power to the bisshoppes of seint david: and of Landalf
and of seint ass. and more over we send through all crystendome that all the
bisshoppes beyond the sea that they shall done accurse all thay^ that helps
you or any cou^ceill yeueth you in any manner need that ye have to done in any
party of the world And we assoille hem aso all by ye auctoryte of the pope.
and command he^ also with you for to werre: as with hy^ that is enemy to all
the holy chirch^: Tho a^swerde the king / what mow ye done me more Tho
answered Pandolfe / We seyne to you in verbo dei / that ye ne none heir that
ye have never after this day may be crowned Tho said the king. by him that is
almighty god. and j had wist of this thy^g er that ye came into mi la^d that ye
had me brought such tiding I should have made you ride all an holy year / Tho
a^swerde Pandolfe full well / wend we at our first comy^g that ye would have
ben^ obedyent to god and to holy chirch. and have fulfilled the popes
commandment / and now we have showed to you and pronounced ye popes will as
we were charged therwyth: and as now ye have said that if ye had wist ye cause
of our coming that ye would have made us ride all an holy year and as well ye
might have said that ye would have take an holy year of respyte by the popes
leave. but for to suffer what death ye cowde ordeyne we shul not spare for to
tell you holy all the popes message and his will that we were charged with

How Pa^dolfe delivered a clerk that had falsed and cou^terfeted the ky^ges
money before the king him self Capi. Cl.
ANd anon tho commanded the king the sherews and and bailifs of Northa^pton /
that were in ye kings p^sence that they should bring forth all ye priso^ners
that they might ben^ done unto the death before Pa^dolf: for encheson the king
wend that they would have gain said her deeds. for cause of death all thing
that he had spoken before Wha^ the priso^ners were come^ before the king The
king commanded some to be hanged and some to ben^ draw: and some to draw out
her eyes out of her head And among all other there was a clerk and had falsed
the kings money / and the king commanded that he should be hanged. and when
pa^dolfe herd this commandment of the king: he stert hy^ up smertly and
anon^ axed a book and ca^dell and would have cursed all he^ that set upon the
clerk any ho^de and pa^dolfe hi^ self went for to seche a cross: and the king
followed him and delivered him the clerk by the ho^de that he should done wit hy^
what that ever he would: and thus was the clerk delivered and went the^s And
pa^dolf and his felawe Durant went fro ye king Johan / and came ayen^ to the
pope of Rome. and told hy^ that king joha^ would not amend but ever abide so
accursed And notheles ye pope granted ye year through out e^glo^d that me^
might sing masses in couenable chirches and make gods body and give it to
sike me^ that pass should out of this world and also that men might christian
children over all And wha^ the pope wist and saw that the king would not be^
under ye rule or governance of holy church for no manner thing / the pope sent
to the king of France in remissyo^ of his sins that he should take with him
all the power that he might and went into England for to destroy king Johan.
When this tyding came to king Ioha^ / tho was he sore annoyed and sore drad
lest that he sho^de lose his Reaulme and him self be done to death / Tho sent he
to ye pope messagiers and said that he would ben^ justified and come to a
maundeme^t in all things: and would make satisfactyon to all manner men after
the popes ordenau^ce / Tho sent the pope ayen^ in to england Pa^dolf. and other
messagiers camen to Canterbury there the king abode And the xiij day of may the
king made an oath for to stand to ye popes ordenance before Pa^dolf the Legate.
i^ all manner things in which he was accused. and that he should make full
restitucion to all men of the holy chyrch^ and of religyon / and of the goods
that he had taken of hem ayens her will: and all ye great lords of england

oath they sayde^ that they would make him hold it by stre^gth^ / Tho put the
king him to the court of rome and to the pope^ and tho yaf up the Reaulme of
England and of Irla^d for him: and also for his heirs for evermore that should
come after him: so that king Johan and his heirs should take two reaulmes of
the popes hand^ and should hold tho two royaumes of ye pope / as to ferme payng
every year unto ye court of rome a thousand mark of silver. and tho took the

and the Reaulme of england into the popes hond Innocent the iij / and put me

king Johan and kept it v days as for seysin taky^g of two reaulmes of england
and of Irland and confermed all manner things by his chartre that follows after

Of the letter obligatorie that king Johan made un to the court of rome wherefore
the petres pe^s been gadred through out all England. Ca Cli
TO all cryste^ people through out all the world dwelling Johan by the grate of
god King of England grety^g to your university and knowing it be: that for
asmoche as we have grieved and offended god and owr mother chyrch^ of rome for
asmoche as we have need to the merci of our lord Ihesu christ And we may
nothing so worthy offer as competant satisfactyon to make to god and to the
holy chirch^. but if it were our own body. as with our reaulmes of England and
of Irland. than by the grace of god we desire to mek us for the love of hi^
that meked hy^ to the death of the cross: through counseil of the noble earls
and barons we offren and freely grant to god and to the apostles saint petre
and seint paul and to our modre chirch^ of rome and to owr holy fadre the pope
jnnocent the thridde: and to all the popes that comes after him all the
reaulme and patronages of chyrches of England and of Irland with her
appertenau^ces for remissyon of our sins. and help and health of our kyn
sowles and of all christian sowles. so that from this time afterward we woll
receive and hold of our modre church of Rome as fee ferme doing feaulte to
our holy fadre the pope Innocent the thridde / and to all the popes that comen
after hi^ in the manner above said And in presence of ye wise man Pandolfe the
popes subdekene we maken liege homage as it were i^ the popes presence / and
before him were / and we shull done all manner things above said. and thereto we
by^ den us and all that comen after us and our heirs for evermore without
any gain seyeng: to the pope and eke the ward of chyrches vacaunt / and in
toke^ of this thing ever for to last we will conferme and ordeyne that our
specialle re^tes of the forsaid reaulme sauy^g sei^t petres pens in all thing
to ye mother church of Rome payeng by year a thousand mark of Silver at ij.
terms of ye year: for all manner customs that we should done for the forsaid
reaulmes. that is to seyne at Mychalmasse and at Estren. that is to seyn^ vij C
marc for england and.ccc. mark for Irland: saving to us and to our heirs or
Justices and our other frau^chises and other realtes that apperteygneth to the
crown. And all these things that before ben^ said we will that it be ferme
and stable withouten end / and to that oblygacyo^ we and our successors and
our heirs i^ this manner be^ bound that if we or any of owre heirs through any
presumpcyo^ fall in any point against any of these things above said. and he
be warned and wull he not amend him: he shall than lose the foresaid reaulme for
evermore: and that this chartre of oblygacyo^ and owr warrant for evermore be
ferme and stable without gayn saying. we shull fro this day afterward be
true to god and the mother church of Rome and to the pope Innocent the
thridde. and to all thay^ that comes after him: and the reaulmes of England
and of Irland we shull maynten^ trewly in all manner points aye^s all manner me^
by owr power through gods help

How the clerks that were outelawed out of England came ayen^ and how king

The erchebisshop took hy^ up tho in his arms and kyssed hy^ courtously

and the friday next aftyr the castle of Farneham. and the monday next aftyr

How in the same time the pope sent into England a legate that was called Swalo:
and of king Ioha^nes death Capit. Clv.
ANd in the same time the ^^pe sent into England a legate yt was kalled Swalo.
and he was pressed cardynall of rome for to maynten^ king Ioha^nes cause ayens ye
barons of England / but the barons has so huge part and help through Lowys ye
kings sone of France / that king Johan wist not whydder for to turn or gone
And so it fell that he would have gon^ to Nycholl and as he went thidderward:
he cam^ by the abbey of swyneshede* and there he abode two days. And as he
sat at ye mete ^ he axed a mo^k of the house how much a lofe was worth that
was sete before him upon the table: and the monk said that the lofe was worth
but an halpeny. O said tho the king here is great chepe of bread. now quod the
king And I may live suc^ a lofe shall be worthy etc. shillyng or half a year be
gon^ And when he said this word moch^ he thought and often he syghed and took
and ete the bread and said. by god the word that I have spoken it shall been
soth: The monk that stood before ye king was for this word full sorry in heart.
and thought rather he would hy^ self suffer pitouse death ^ and rather ordeyne
therefore some manner remedy ^ and anon the monk went to his abbot and was
shryue^ of him and told the abbot all that the king has said and prayed his
abbot for to assoille hy^. for he would give the king such^ a vassaille that
all England should be glad thereof and ioyeful Tho went the monk into a gardeyne
and fond a great tode theryn. and took her up and put her in a cup and
prykked the tode through with a broche many times till that the venime came out
in every sides into ye cup. and tho took he ye cup and filled it with good
all and brought it before the king and knelyng said Sir quod he Vassaille. for
nevyr days of your life ne drunk ye of such^ a cup / Begy^ne monk quod
the king / and the monk dra^ke a great draught / and took the king the cup
and the king also drank a great draught: and set down the cup. The monk
anon right went into ye fermorie and there deyed forthwyth^ / on whose soul god
have mercy. am^ and v. monks sing for his soul specyaly: and shulen whiles
the abbey stand. The king aros up anon full evil at ease / and commanded to
remeue the table. and axed aftyr the monk / and men told hy^ that he was deed
/ for his womb was broken in sunder. When the king herd this / he commanded
to trusse / but all it was for naught. for his belly began so to swelle for the
dry^ke yt he dra^ke that he deyed withy^ two days the morwe aftyr seint Lucas
day / And this king Johan had fair children of his bodi begoten / that is to
seye Henry his sone whych^ was king aftyr his fadre. and Rychard that was Earl
of Cornewaill. and Isabell that was emperesse of Rome / and Elyonore that was
queen of scotland. And this king Ioha^ wha^ he had reigned xvij year.v. months
and v. days / he deide in the castle of newerke. and his body was buried at
wy^chestre

/ and in the beginning he put in the sentence the kings sone of France Lowys
/ and notheles the same Lowys would not spare for to werre for all that / But
went anon and took the castle of Berka^sted and the castle of Herford / and

seye. the earl Randolfe of Chestre. and william Earl marchall: and William the

How Lowys turned ayen^ into France and of the co^firmacyo^ of king Johannes
chartre Capitulo Clvij
WHen Lowys herd this tydyng / he drad sore to be deed and lost / and let

Erchebysshop of Canterbury and through othyr great lords that all the
prysonners on that one half: and that other should be delivered and gon^ quyte
/ And Lowys himself should have for his costages a thousand pound of silver

Profecie of Merlyn the king henry the first expouned^ that was king Johannes
sone Capitulo C.lx
ANd of this Henry profecyed merlyn and said: that a lamb should come out of
Wynchestre in the year of Incarnacion of our lord MCC and xvi / with true
lyppes / and holiness in his heart / and he said soth: for ye good king Henry
was borne in wynchestre / and he spoke good words and sweet: and was an holj
man and of good conscience / And merly^ said. that this Henry should make the
fairest place of all the world. that in his time should not be full ended: and
he said soth: for he made the new work of the abbey of seint petres chyrch^
at westmy^ster that is fairer of sight tha^ any other church that men knowt
through all cristendome: but king Henry deied / er that work was full made: and
that was great harm: And yet said merly^. that this la^be should have pees the
most time of his regne. and he said full soth: for he was never annoyed through
werre ne disesed in no manner wise till a littel before his death And yet said
Merly^ in his prophecye more: that in the regne and end of ye forsaid la^be a
wolf of a strange land should done him great harm through his werre / and
that he should at ye last ben^ master through help of a reed fox that should
come out of the northwest and should him overcome. and that he should drive him
unto the water: and that prophecye full well was know / for withinne a little
time er the king deyed Simond of Mou^fort earl of Leicestre that was borne i^
France began against hy^ stro^geli to werre. through which doy^g many a good
bachylere was shent and deed and disheryted / And when king Henry had the
victory at Euesham / and sir Symond the earl was slayn^ through help and might
of Gilbert of clare earl of Gloucestre that was in keeping and ward of the
forsaid simonde through ordenau^ce of king Henry that went ayen^ to the king
with mochel^ power / wherefore the forsaid simond was shent. and that was great
harm to the communes of england that so good a man was she^t for truth and
deyed in charity. and for the common proffyte of the same folk. and therefore
almighty god for hy^ has sithenes showed many a fair miracle to diverse men
and woman of the sikenesse and disese that they have had for the love of him
And Merlyn also told and said in his profecie that after that time the land
should live no while: and then^ his seed should ben^ in strange land without
pasture And he said sothe For king He^ry^ lived no while after when Simond
mounford was deed that king henry ne deyde anon^ after hy^ / And in the mean
time sir edward his sone that was the best knight of ye world of honor / was
tho in the holy land and get there Acres And in that co^tre he begat on dame
Alienore his wife Johan of Acres / his doughtyr yt aftyrward was countess of
Gloucestre And he made in the holy land such a vyage that all the world spoke
of his knyghthode and every man drad hy^ hygh^ and low thurghoute all
crystendom as the story of him tellyth as aftyrward ye shull here more openly
And from the time that king henry deide till that sir Edward was crowned king.
all the great lords of England were as fadreles children wythowte any socour
that thaym might maynten^ and govern and defend ayens her dedely enemies

Of king Edward that was king Henryes sone Capitulo Clxj
ANd aftyr this king Henry reigned his sone Edward the worthest knight of all
the world of honor for gods grace was in him. for he had the victory of his
enemies: As Soon as he herd of the death of his fadre he came to London wit a
sayre company of prelatz and earls and barons. and all manner men did him moch^
honor For in every place that sir Edward rode in London / the streets were
coured over his h^ede with rych^ clothes of silk. of tapytes and wit rich
covering. and for joy of his comy^g / the noble Burgeys of the cite cast owte
at her wyndowes gold and silver ho^des full in tokenyng of love and of
worshipp / seruyse and reverence. And owte of ye conduyt of chepe ran white
wine and read as stremes does of the watyr. and every man thereof might dry^ke
at her own will and this king Edward was crownyd and annoy^tyd as right heir
of England wit mochel honor And aftyr mass ye king went into his paleys for
to hold a ryall feste among he^ that him did honor And when he was set unto
his mete ye king Al^^e^dre of Scotland came for to done hy^ honor and
reverence wit a quey^tyse. and an hundred knights wit hy^ well horsed and
arrayed. and when they were light a down of her fredes the^ let he^ gon^
whither that they would / and who that might take he^* took at her own will
wytoute any challenge And aftyrward came sir Edmond king Edwardes brother a
curtoys knight and a gentle of reno^me. And the Earl of Cornewaille. and the
Earl of Gloucestre: and aftyr he^ came the Earl of Pa^broke and the earl of
Garenne. and ech^ of hem by he^ self lad in her ho^de an hundred knights
gaylly disgised in her arms And wha^ they were light of her horses they let
hem gone whyther that hem lyked: and who that cowde might he^ take to have hem
stylle without any let: And wha^ all this was done / King Edward did his
diligence and his might for to amend the Reame and redress the wro^ges i^ ye
best manner that he might to the honor of god and holy church / and to
may^tene his honor and to amend the anoyau^ce of the commune people

How ydeyne that was Lewelynes daughter prince of walys: and Aymer that was
therles brother of Mou^ford were taken in the sea Capitulo Clxij
THe first year afterward that king Edward was crownyd: Lewelyne pry^ce of
Walys sent into france to the earl of mou^tford that through cou^ceill of his
friends ye earl should wedde his doughtyr / and the earl tho avysed hy^ upon

arrayed ships for his doughtyr and for sir Aymer and for thayre company that
should goo with her And this Lewely^ did great wrong: for it was covenant that
he should yeve his doughtyr to no manner man without cou^ceill and consent of
king Edward And so it befell that a burgeis of Brystrowe came in the sea with
wine lade / and hem took wit might and power. And anon the burgeis sent hem to
the king / And when Lewelyn herd this tydy^g he was wonder wroth and eke
sorwefull / and began to werre upon king Edward. and did moch^ harm unto the
Englysshmen / and beat a down the kings castelles. and began fast to destroy
king Edwardes lands* And wha^ tydyng came unto king Edward of this thing / he
went unto Walys and so moch^ he did through gods grace and his great power
that he drofe Lewely^ unto moch^ meschief that he fled all manner stre^gthe /
and came and yield him to king Edward. and yaf hy^.l.M marc of silver for to
have pees. and took the damysell and all his heritage / and made an obligacyon
to king Edward / to come to his parliament ij. times of the year. And in the
second year after that king Edward was crownyd he held a general parliament
at westmynster / and there he made ye statutes for defaut of law by common
assent of all his baronage and that Estre next sewy^ge the king sent by his
letter to Lewely^ prince of walys that he should come to his parliament for his
land. and for his holdyng in walls as the strength^ of the letter obligatorye
witnessed. Tho lewelyn had scorn and despite of the kings commandment / and
for pure wrath began ayene for to werre upon king Edward and destroyed his
lands And tho king edward herd this tydyng / he wex wonder wroth unto Lewelyn
/ and in have assembled his people / and went him toward walys and werred so
upon Lewely^ the pry^ce. till that he brought hy^ in much sorwe and disese.
And Lewely^ saw that his defense might not auaille: and cam^ ayene and yield
him to the kings grace and cried him mercy and long time knelyd before ye
kings fete The king had of him pity and commanded hy^ for to arise: and for
his meekness foryafe him his wrath and to him said / that if he tresspaced
against him an other time he would destroy hy^ for ever more. Dauyd that was
Lewelines brother that same time dwelled with the king Edward / and was a fell
man / and a ^otill and e^vyous / and far casty^g: and moch^ treson thought.
and euyrmore held hy^ stylle for to wit and aspye the ky^ges will / and
euemore made good semblan^t and seemed so true that no man might perceive his
falsenesse

How Lewelyne through engyne of David his brother werryd ayene upon king edward.
ca. clxiij
Hjt was not long aftir that time that king Edward ne yafe to Dauyd lewelines
brothyr the lordshyp of Frodesham and made hy^ a knight. and so mochel honor
did he nevyr aftyr to no man of Walys. for encheson of him king edward held
his perlame^t at london. when he had done in walys all that he would / and
changed his money yt tho was full cute and ended: wherefore the common people
pleined he^ wonder sore: so yt the king let enquere of he^ yt such^ trespaces
dide^ and.ccc. were atteynt of such manner falsenesse. wherefore some were
ho^ged and some drawn and aftyrward honged. The king ordained that ye sterly^g
halpeny and ferthing should gon^ through out his la^d. and conmau^ded that no man
fro yt day aftyrward yaf ne feffed house of religyo^ wit land teneme^t wtoute
special leave of ye king: and he that did it should be punyssed at the kings
will and ye yift should be for naught. And it was not long aftir yt Lewely^
prince of walys through ticeme^t of Dauyd his brother and by both^ her consent
they thought to disheryte king edward in as moch^ as they might^ so yt through
he^ both^ ye kings pees was broke^^ and wha^ king edward herd this / anon^ he
sent his barons into Northu^berla^d and to the surreis also yt they should gon^
and take her vyage upon the traitors Lewely^ and Dauyd: and wonder hard was
for to werre tho. For hit is wy^ter in walys when in other co^trees is somer
And lewely^ let ordeyn^ and welaraye with vytailles his castle of Swa^don: and
was theryn with an hugh^ nombre of people / and plente of vytailles so that king
Edward wist not where for to enter / And when the ky^ges men it perceived: and
also the strength of walys / they let come by ye see barges and botes and great
pla^kes as many as they might ordeyne and for to have gon^ to the forsaid
castle of Swandone with men on foot and eke on horse But the walsh men had so
much people. and were so strong that they driven ye Englysshme^ ayen^. so that
there was so moch^ prees of people at the turnyng ayen^ that the charge and the
berthen of hem made the barges and bottes sink. and there was dre^ched full
many a good knight yt is to seye Sir Rogier of Gilford: Sir William of
Ly^desey: that was sir Johannes sone sir Robert and sir Rychard Tanny / and an
hughe no^bre of other. and all was through her own folly. for if they has had
good espies they had not ben^ harmed. Wha^ king Edward herd tell that his
people was so drenched he made sorwe ynowe. but tho came sir Ioha^ of veyssye
from the king of Aragon and brought with him moch^ folk of Bachiloers and of
Gascoynes. and were sowdiours and dwelling with the forsayde sir Johan of
veyssye. and vnderfo^ge of him wages and with him were withholde and noble men
it were for to fight / and brent many towns / and quelled much people of
walsshme^ all that they might taken And they all with might and strength^ made
strong assault to the castle of Swa^don and get the castle / And wha^
Dauyd the pry^ces brother herd this tydynge. he ordained him to flight / and
Lewely^ the pry^ce saw that his brother was slowen and was sore abashed. for
he had no power his werre for to mayntene / and so Iewelyn began for to flee
and wend well for to have eskaped^ But on a morwe sir Rogyer Mortiemer met
with him only with x knights / and set him round about and to him went and
smote of his head and presented him unto the king Edward: and in this manner the
prince of Walys was taken and his head smyten of / and all his heirs
disherited for evermore through right full dome of all the lands of the Reaulme

How Dauyd that was Lewelynes brother pry^ce of walys was put to the death
Capitulo Clxiiij
DAuyd that was the princes brother of walys through pride went for to have
ben^ prince of walys aftyr his brothers death. and upon that sent he aftyr
walsshmen to his parliament at dinbygh^ and folych^ made walys arise ayens the
king. and began to meue werre ayens the and began to meve werre aye^s the king
and did all the sorwe and disese yt he might by his power. When king Edward
herd of this thing he ordained men to purswe upon him. and Dauyd fersely him
defended till that he came to the town of seint morice. and there was david
take as he fled and lad to ye king And the king commanded that he should be
ho^ged and draw and smiten of his head. And quartryd hy^ and send his head to
London. and the four quartyers send to the iiij. towns chief of Walys / for
they should take example and thereof ben^ ware: And aftyrward king Edward let
cry his pees through out all walys / and saised all the land into his hande^
and all the great lords that were left a live came to done feaute and homage
to the king edward as to her ky^de lord / And tho let king edward amend the
laws of walys that were defectife And aftyr he sent to the lords of walys by
his letter pate^t that they should come all to his parliament / And wha^ they
were come^. the king said to hem full curtoisly Lordynges ye be well come and
me behooves your cou^ceil and your help for to went in to Gascoyn^ for to
amend the trespaces yt me was done when I was there. and for to entrete of
pees bytwen^ the king of Aragon and the prince of Morey: And all the kings
liege men Earls and barons conse^ted and granted thereto And tho made him king
Edward ready and went into Gascoyn^ and let amend all the trespaces that him
was done in Gascoyne / and of ye debate that was bytwen^ the king of Aragon and
the prince of Morey / he cesed and made hem accorded. And whylle the good king
Edward and the queen Elianore his wife were i^ gascoyne: the good earl of
cornewaill was made wardeyn^ of england. till that edward came ayene And tho
enquered he of his traitors that co^geted falsenesse ayens him. and ech^ of
hem all vndyrfe^ge her dome aftyr that they had deserved: But in the mean time
whiles that ye good king edward was beyond the sea to done hem for to make
ame^des ^ that ayens him had trespaced. There was a falls thief traitor that
was kalled Rys ap meriedoke and began for to make werre ayens king Edward / and
that was for encheson of sir Spain tiptot wrongfully greved and disesed that
foresaid rys ap Meriedok And when king Edward herd all this he send by his
letter to Ris ap meriedok that he should begy^ne for to make no werre / but that
he should be i^ pees for his love: and when that he came ayene into England: he
would undertake the querell and done amend all that was mysdon^ The forsaid Ris
ap meriedoke despised ye ky^ges commandment / and spared not for to done all
the sorwe that he might to the kings men of England. but anon aftyr, he was
taken and lad to york / and there was he drawn and hanged for his felonye.

Of the redressyng that king Edward made of his justices and of his clerks
that they had done for her falsenesse. and how he drofe the yewes owte of
England for her vsery and mysbeleue Capitulo Clxv
When king Edward h^ad dwelled three year in Gascoyne / will came to him for to
turn ayene into England And tho he was come ayene he fond so many play^tes
made to him of his justices and of his clerks that had done so many wro^ges
and falsenesse that wondyr it was to here. And for which falsenesse Sir thomas
weilond the kings justyce forswore England at the tower of London for
falsenesse that me^ put upon hy^ whereof he was atteynt and proved falls And
anon aftyr when the king had done his will of the justices: tho let he inquire
and aspye how the jews desceyued and begylled his people through her sy^ne of
falsenesse and of vserye / and let ordeyne a pryve parliament among his lords
/ and they ordained among hem that all the jews should void England for
mysbeleue and also for her falls vserye that they dyde^ unto the christian men And
for to speed and to make an end of this thing all the communite of England
yafe unto the king the xv / penny of all her goods menable / And so were^ the
jews dryve^ out of England. And tho went the jews into france and dwelled
there through leave of king Phelyp that tho was king of France.

How king edward was seysed in all the lord of Scotland through consent and
grant of all the lords of scotland Cap / C.lxvi
HIt was not long aftyr: that Alysander king of Scotland was deed. and David
earl of Hunty^gdone that was the kings brother of Scotland axed and claymed
the ky^gdome of Scotland: for encheson that he was rightful heir of the land
of scotland: but many great lords of Scotland sayden nay Wherefore great debate
arose between hem and her friends / for as moch^ that they would not co^sente
to his coronacyon / and in ye mean time ye foresaid david deyde / And so it
befell that the same Dauyd had three doughtyrs. the which that were worthily
married / the first doughtyr was married to Bailloll / the second to Brus / The
thridde to Hasty^ges / And ye forsaid Bailloll and Brus chale^ged the land of
Scotland / and great debate and strife aroos bytwen^ hem for encheson that each
of he^ would have be king And when the lords of scotland saw the debate between
hem / they came to king edward of England and seysed hy^ all ye land of
scotland as her chief lord. And when the king was seized of the lords of
Scoltla^d: the forsaid Bailloll brus Hastynges camen to the kings court and
axed of the king which of hem should be king of Scotland / And king edward yt
was full gentle and true let enquere by the chronicles of scotland and by the
great lords of scotland / which of he^ was of the eldest blood / and it was
found that Bailloll was eldest: and that the king of scotland should hold of
the king of england: and done him feaute and homage. And aftyr as this was
done: bailloll went into scotland. and there was he crownyd king of scotland.
And in the same time was upon the sea strong werre bytwen^ the englisshme^ and
ye Norma^s: but upon a time the normans arrived all at Dover. and there they
martred an holy man that was called thomas of Dover / and aftyrward were the
Norma^s quelled that there escaped of hem not on. And sone aftyr King Edward
should lose ye duchye of Gascoyne through king Phelip of france through falls
castyng of the dousepieres of ye land Wherefore sir Edmond that was king
Edwardes brother yafe up his homage unto ye king of france: And in that time
the clerks of England granted to king edward halfendelle of holy church
goods in helping for to recoure his land ayen^ in Gascoyne and the king sent
thither a noble company of Bacheliers And him self anon^ would have went to
portesmonth. but he was let through one maddoke of walys that had seysed the
castle of Swa^done into his hand / and for that encheson ye king turned ayene
unto Walys at Crystmasse. And for encheson that the noble lords of England
that were sent into Gascoyne had no comfort of her lord of the king. they were
taken of sir Charles of France / that is to say sir joha^ of Britaigne. sir
Robert tipttot sir Rauf Tanny. sir Hugh^ Bardolf / and sir Adam of Cretynges
and yet at the ascencion was Madok take in walys. and an other that was kalled
Morgan^ and they were sent to the tour of London and there they were beheded

How sir Johan Bailloll king of scotland withsaid his homage. and of sir Thomas
turbeluille Capitulo Clxvij
ANd when sir joha^ bailloll king of scotland vndyrstode that king edward was
werred in Gascoyne / to who^ the reaume of scotland was delivered falsely tho
