should abowe to the king of France. and this thing for to bry^ge to an end he
swore. and upon this covenant deeds were made bitwene hem and that he should
have by year a thousand pou^des worth of la^d to bring this thing to an end /
This false traitor tok his leave and went the^nes and came into england unto the
king and said that he was broken out of prison. and that he has put him in
such^ peril for his love / wherefore the king cowde him moch^ tha^k and full
glad was of his coming / and the false thief traitor fro that day aspied all
the doing of the king and also his cou^ceill / for the king loved him well / and
was with him full pryue: but a clerk of England that was in the ky^ges house of
france herd of this treson. and of the falsenesse: and wrote to an other clerk
that was dwelling wit the king of england / all how Thomas turbeluille had done
his false coniectyng / and all the cou^ceill of england was written for to have
sent unto the king of France: and through the forsaid letter that the clerk had
sent fro france: hit was fond upon him / wherefore he was lad to London and
drawn / and honged there for his treson / and his ij. sons that he had put in
france for hostages were tho beheded

Of the conquest of Berewyk Capitulo Clxviij
WHen ye ij / cardinals were went ayen^ into france for to trete of ye pees
at ca^bry / the king sent thidder of his earls and barons that is to saye^ sir
edmond his brother. earl of lancaster and of leycestre / sir henry lacy earl of
nichol. and william Vesy a baron / and of other barons about xiiij: of the
best and wysest of england / And in the sam^ time the king Edward took his
vyage to Scotland: for to werre upon Johan Bailloll king of scotland / and sir
Robert roos of berewik fled fro the Englysshmen and went to the scotts / and
king Edward went him toward berewik and besieged ye town. and tho that were
withy^ man ly hem defended and set a fire and bre^de two of king Edwardys
ships and said in despyte and reprove of him Wend king Edward wit his long
shankes to have get Berewik all our vnthankes gas pykes hy^ When king Edward
herd this scorn anon^ through his myghtynesse he passed over the dikes and
assailled the town and came to the yates and gate and conquered ye town / and
through his gracyous power quelled xxv thousand and vij C scotts. and king
Edward lost no man of reno^me sauf sir Robert of cornewaill / and him quelled a
fleming out of the read halle with a quarrel: as the forsaid Richard did of
his helm. and commanded hem for to yield hem and put hem to ye kings grace.
and the scotts would not / wherefore that halle was bre^t and cast a down: and
all tho that were withyn were brent. and king edward lost no mo men at that
vyage of simple estate / but xxviij englysshmen And the wardeyns of the castle
yafe up the keys wtoute any assaute: And there was taken william Douglas and
sir simo^d Frisell / and the earl Panryk yield hem to the pees. But Ingham of
Humsrenille and Robert the brus that were with the king Edward forsook king
Edward and held with the scotts / and aftyrward they were take and put into
prison. And afterward the king foryaf hem her trespace and delyured hem owte of
prison. And tho let king Edward closen Berewyke with wallys and with dyches And
aftyrward Robert Rous went to Ty^dalle and set nyewebrugge a fire and Exham.
and Lamerstoke: and quelled and robed the folk of the contre. and aftyrward he
went fro thens unto Dunbare: and the first wedenesday of March^ the king sent
the Earl of Garenne sir Hugh^ party: and sir Hugh spencer wit a fair company
for to besiege ye castle But one that was kalled sir Rychard syward a traitor
a falls men ymagined for to begyll the Englysshme^. and sent to the englysshme^
he^ for to deceive and said that he would yield to he^ ye castle. if they would
grant he^ viij days of respite that he might se^d and tell to sir Johan
Bailloll king of scotland how his men ferde that were withyn the castle / and
sent hy^ word if that he nold remeue the siege of the Englysshmen: that they
would yield ye castle to e^glysshme^ The messagier came tho to sir johan
Bailloll king of scotland there that he was with his host and his message told
him: and sir Ioha^ took tho his host and came in the morwe erly to the
castle: and sir rychard siward saw him come that was master of the castle.
and said unto the englysshme^. O god quod he I see now of folk a fair conpanye
well apparayled I will go aye^s him and with he^ to mete and hem assaille / And
sir Hugh^ the spencer saw ye falsenesse of him and the treson: and said to him
O traitor tak and proved yowre falsenesse shall not auaylle you / And Hugh^
the spencer commanded anon^ for to bi^de him. and in all have went to her
enemies and quelled of the scotts xxij.M. for the scotts had that time no man
with he^ of honor / sauf sir Patrik Graham that manly faught and long / and
at the last he was quelled And tho said the e^glyssh men in reprove of the
scotts: the se scater and scotts hold I for sotes of wrences vnwarre erly in
a morny^g in an evil tymyng went ye fro Dunbare

When they that were in the castle saw the scomfyture they yolden the castle

How king Edward of his great grace delyured ayen^ the scotts owte of prison
that were cheuytaynes of the land: and they drowe^ hem to the Frensshmen through
cou^ceyll of William waleys Capitulo Clxix
WHen king Edward had made tho an (...) of the werre and taken the cheuytaines

years / so that englyssh^ merchants and also frenssh^ might saufely gon^ and
come in both sides. The king edward granted it so that he must have his men
owte of pryso^ that were in Gascoyne. and the king of france granted anon^:
and so they were delyvred / And in ye same time the Scotts sent by the bishop

her power / and so they should gon^ into England that la^d for to destroy from
Scotland till that they came to kent / and the scotts trust moch^ upon the
Frensshmen. But of yt thing they had no manner grant. And notheles ye scotts
begone to rob and quelle in Northumberland and did moch^ harm

How william Waleis let slay sir Hugh^ of Cressyngham: and of the bataill of
Fonkyrke Cap clxx
WHen this tyding was come to king Edward that wyllia^ Waleys had orde^^ned
such^ a strong power and that all scotland to him was atte^dau^t and ready to
quelle Englysshmen and to destroy the land / he was sore annoyed: and sent

there he held him in the castle: and the walsshme^ every day he^ escried and
menaced: and did all the despite that they might / so that the englysshmen upon
a time in a morning went out from the castle the mou^tau^ce of x mile. and
passyd over a brygge / And wyllia^ waleys came with a strong power and drofe

they that might take ye brigge askaped / but sir Hugh^ the ky^ges tresorer

And all that he fo^de he set a fire and brend / But the pour people of

For when William waleys fled from ye bataille / that same Friar brya^ him

How the castle of Estreneline was besieged Capi. Clxxij
King Edward came with an huge power to the castle of Estrenelyn and besieged
the castle: but it littell availled. for he might do the Scotts non^ harm:
for the castle was so strong and well kept / and king Edward saw that / and
thought hi^ upon a quey^tyze. and let make anon^ there two peyre of hygh^
galowes before the towr of the castle. and made his oth^ that as many as were

they that were in the castle herd this: they cam^ and yield hem all to the
kings grace and mercy. and the king foryafe hem all his maltalent / and there
were all the great lords of Scotland and swore to king Edward that they should
come to London to every perlament: and should stand to his ordenau^ce

How Troylebaston was first ordained Capitulo / C.lxxiij
THe king edward went the^s to London: and we^de have rest and pees of his
werre wit which werre he was occuped xx. year / that is to seye: In walys In
Gascoyne and in Scotland: And thought how he might recover his tresour that he
has spended about his werre ^ and let inquire through the reaulme of all
mystaky^ges and wrongs done through mysdores in England of all y^ time that he
has ben^ owte o^ his ^eaulme / that men kalled Tro^^ebaston: and ordained there
to ^^^tyces: and in this manner he rec^ured tresour without nombre And his
encheso^ was for he had thought for to have gone into the holy la^d for to werre
upon gods enemies For enche^on that he was crossyd long time before. and
notheles that law yt he had ordained deed much good through all England to hem
that were ^^^^bode: for they that trespaced were well chastyzed and aftyrward
the meker and the bettyr. and the pour co^munes were in rest and in pees. and
that same time king Edward enpryso^ned his own sone Edward for encheson that
walter of Langeto^ bishop of Chestre that was the kings tresorer had made
upon him complaynt. and said that the forsaid Edward through cou^ceill and
procurement of one p^ers of ganastone a squire of Gascoine had broke ye parkes
of the forsaid bishop / and the forsaid piers cou^ceilled and lad the sam^
Edward / and for this cause king Edward exilled his sone out of England for
evyrmore.

Of the death of William waleis the false traitor Cap. Clxxiiij
ANd when this king edward had his enemies overcome jn walys / in gascoyne and

How the Scotts came to king Edward for to amend her trespace that they had

How Robert the brus chale^ged scotland Capit. Clxxvi
ANd aftyr this Robert the Brus earl of Carryk sent by his letter to the earls
and barons of Scotland that they should come to him to scone in the morwe aftyr
the conceptyo^ of our lady for hygh^ needs of the land / and the lords came at
the day assygned And at the same day sir Robert ye brus said. Fair lords full
well ye know that in my person dwells the right of the reaume of Scotland.
and as ye wit well I am right full heyr* seth that sir Johan Bailoll that was
our king us has forsake and left his land: and though it so be that king
Edward of England wit wrong full power has made me to hy^ asse^te ayens my
will if that ye will grant that I be king of Scotland I shall keep you
aye^s king Edward. and ayens all manner men And with that word the abbot of
Skone arose / and before hem all said: that it was reason for to help him: and
the land to keep and defend. and tho said he in presence of hem all that he
would hy^ give a thousand pound for to may^ten^ that la^d: and all the othyr
granted the la^d to him: and with her power him for to help / and defyend
king Edward of England: and said that robert the brus should be king of scotland

How sir Ioha^ of Common gay^sayd the crownyng of sir Robert the Brus Cap.
Clxxvij
LOrdynges said sir Johan of Common thenketh upon the truth^ and the oth^ that
ye made unto king Edward of england. and thouchyng my self j will not break
mine oath for no man And so he went fro that company at that time. wherefore
robert the brus and all that to hy^ consented were wonder wroth and they
menaced sir Ioha^ of Comy^. Tho ordained they an othyr cou^ceill at Do^frys to
the which came the foresaid sir joha^ common / he dwelled but two mile from
donfrys there that he was wo^t for to soiourne and abide

How sir Johan was traitoursly quelled Ca. Clxxviij
When Robert the brus wist that all the great lords of scotland were come to
scone sauf sir Johan common that soiourned tho nygh^ Scone: he sent aftyr hi^
specially yt sir joha^ comy^ should come and speak with hi^ / and upon yt he sent
aftir hi^ joha^ comyns brother and prayed hi^ for to come and speak with him at
ye gray frerys / and that was ye thursday after ca^delmasse: and sir Ioha^
granted hi^ for to went with hy^. And when he had herd mass he took a soppe
and dra^k and afterward he bestrode his palfray and rode his way. and so came
to dofris. and robert ye brus saw hi^ come at a wy^dowe as he was in his
chamber. and made tho joy ynowe. and came aye^s him and co^ied him about ye
neck and made with hy^ good se^bla^t. And wha^ all ye earls and barons of
scotland were p^sent. robert ye brus spoke and said Lords quod he ye wite well
the encheson of this coming / and wherefore it is: if ye will grant that I be
king of scotland as right heir of the land. and all ye lords that were there
said with one voys that he should be crounyd king of scotland and that they
would him help and mayntene ayens all manner men on live / and for him yeve it
if were need. and deye also / The gentle knight tho Johan of Comyne answered
and said / Certes nevyr for me / ner for to have of me as much help as the
value a boutouue / for that oth^ whych^ I have made to the noble king Edward
of England I shall hold whiles my life lastyth / and wit that word he went
fro the company and would have lept upon his palfray And robert the brus
purswyd hi^ with a draw sword and bare him through the body: and sir Johan
comy^ fylle down to the Earth. but when rogyer that was sir Ioha^ comyns
brother saw the falsenesse. he stert to sir Robert the Brus and smote him wit a
knyfe: but the false traitor was armed vndyr so that the stroke might do hi^ no
harm. and so moch^ help cam^ about sir Robert the Brus. so yt rogyer common
was there quelled and all to hew into small pieces And robert ye brus turned
ayen^ there that sir Johan Common the noble baron lay wounded and pyned toward
his death besides the high Auter in the chyrch^ of the gray frerys: and said
unto sir Ioha^ comy^. O traitor thou shall be deed and nevyrmore aftir let
mine avau^ceme^t. and took his sword at the hygh^ auter and smote hy^ on the
head that ye brain fill a down upon the ground / and the blood stert an
hygh^ upon the wallys: and yet unto this day that blood is seen there. that no
watyr may wasshe it away / and so deyed that noble knight in the holy church
And when the traitor Robert the Brus saw that no man tho would let his
coronacion he commanded all them which were of great power to come to his
crounyng to saint Johannes town in Scotland. And so it befell that in owr lady
day of Annu^cyacyo^ the bishop of Glastone and the bishop of saint Andrewe
crowned for her king Robert the brus in seint Johannes town and made him king.
And anon drofe owte all the Englysshme^ out of scotland / and they fled and
came and playned unto king Edward: how robert the Brus had dryue^ hem owte of
the land and disherited hem

How king Edward dubbed at westmy^ster xxiiij. score knights Capitulo / Clxxx
ANd when king edward herd of this meschyef he swore that he would thereof ben^
avenged / and said that all the traitors of scotland should ben^ honged and
drawn / and that they should nevyr ben^ raunsoned And king Edward thought upon
his falsenesse that ye scotts has done: and sent aftyr all the bachelerye of
England that they should come to London at witsontyde. and he dubbed at
westmynster xxiiij score knights. Tho ordained him the noble king Edward for

How Robert the brus was sco^ fyted in bataille^ and how symond Frysell was
slain Ca / clxxxj
THe Friday next before ye assumpcyon of our lady king Edward met Robert the
Brus beside seint Ioha^nes town in scotland and with his company. of whych^
company king Edward quelled vij.M. when Robert ye brus saw this meschief he
began to flee and hyd him that no man might him find But sir simond Frysell
pursued him sore so that he turned ayene and abode bataill / for he was a
worthy knight and a bold of body: and the Englysshmen pursued ever sore in
every side And queld the stead that sir simond Frisell rode upon / and they
took him and lad hy^ unto the host And sir simond began for to flater and speak
fair and said / Lords I shall yeve you iiij mark of silver and mine horse.
mine harneys and all mine armure and become a beggar Tho a^sweryd theanbode of
peuenes that was the kings archier: now god me so help / it is for naught
that thou spekest / for all the gold in england I would the not let gon^
without commandment of king Edward And tho was he lad to king Edward. and
the king would not see him but commanded to lead him a way to have his dome at
london. And on our ladies even natiuite he was honged and drawn. and his heed
smyten of: and honged ayen^ with cheynes of yren upon the galowes / And his
head was set upon london brugge upon a spear: and ayens Crystmasse the body
was bre^d for encheson that the men that kept the body by night they saw so
many deueles raumped with great jren crokes rennyng upon the galowes and
horrybyly turmende the body and many that hem saw anon^ aftyr they deyed for
dread. and some wore^ wode or sore sikkenesse they had and in that bataill was
take the bishop of Glaston^. ye bishop of sey^t Andrews. and the Abbot of
scone all armed with jren as me^ of arms as falls traitors and falls prelates
ayens her oath. and they were brought to the king: and the king sent hem to the
pope of Rome that he should do with he^ what his will were

How Johan Earl of Atheles was take and put to the death Capitulo C.lxxxij

encheson that he claymed kynred of king Edward. And the king nold no le^ger be

How Robert the brus fled from scotla^t to Norwey Ca / clxxxiiij
ANd at that time was robert the Brus moch^ hated among the people of scotland.

How king Edward deyed Capitulo C.lxxxv
WHen king Edward had abated his enemies he turned ayen^ southward. and a
maladye took him at Burgh up sand in the march of scotland: and he wist well
that his death was full nygh^. and kallyd to him sir Henry ye Lacy Earl of
nychol / sir Guy earl of warrewyk^ sir Aymer valaunce Earl of Panbroke. and sir
Robert of Gylford baron / and prayed hem upon the faith that they him owed /
that they should make Edward of Canervan king of England his sone as rathe as
they might / and that they should not suffer Piers of Ganesto^ come ayen^ into
England for to make his sone to use ryotte. and they granted hy^ with good
will. And the king took the sacrament of holy chyrch^ as a good christian man
should. and deyde in very repentance. And when he had be king xxxv. year / he
deyed: and was buried at westmynster with mochel solempnite / upon whose soul
god have mercy. Amen

Of Merlyns prophecyes that were declared of king Edward that was king henryes
sone Capitulo c.lxxxvi
ANd of this king Edward prophesied Merlyn and called hy^ a dragon / the second
king of the vj last kings that should be for to regne in england / and said
that he should be meddled wit mercy / and also with strength^ and sternesse. yt
should keep england for cold and here / and that he should open^ his mouth
toward walys. and that he should set his any foot in wyke. and that he should
close wit walls that should do moch^ harm to his seed / and he said soth: for
ye good king edward was meddled with mercy and with fersenesse / with mercy aye^s
his enemies of walys. and aftyr of Scotland with fersenesse when he put hem to
death for her falsenesse as they had deseruyd it. and well kept he England from
cold and hete. since he kept it from all manner enemies that came upon him to
done him any wrong And well he opened his mouth toward walys / and made it
quake through ye hydour of his mouth when he conquered it through dynt of swerd:
for ye prince Lewelyne and David his brothir Ris: and Morgan were put unto the
death / for their falsenesse and her folly / And he set his o foot into wyke
and conquered Berewyk / at the which conquest were slayn^ xxv / thousand^ and
vij ho^dred owte take hem that were brend in the reed halle And the walls that
he let make / shall be noyous unto his seed as men shall here aftyr se in the
life of sir Edward of Carnaruan his sone. And yet merly^ said that he should
make ryuiers run in blood and with brain and that seemed well i^ his werrys
there that he had the maistrie And yet Merlyn said that there should come a
people owte of the North west during the regne of the forsaid dragon that should
be lad by an ylle greyhownde that should ye dragon crown king that aftyrward
should flee over ye see for dread of the dragon without comi^g ayen^ ^ and that
was proved by sir Johan bailloll. that king edward made to ben^ king of
scotland that falsely arose aye^s him. and aftyr he fled unto his own lands
of france and nevyr come ayen^ into scotland for dread of king edward And yet
said merly^. that people yt should led the foresaid Greyhou^d. should be fadreles
un till a certay^ time / and he said soth. for the people of scotland gretely
were disesed aftyr that sir Johan Bailloll her king fled from scotland And
yet said Merlyn that ye sun should become in his time as read as blood in
tokeny^g of great Mortalite of people. and that was well known when the scotts
were slain / and sith said Merlyn that ye same dragon should noryssh a fox that
should meove great werre against him that should not in his time been endyd* And
that seemed well by Robert ye Brus that king Edward norysshed in his chamber
that sythenes stale away and meouyd great werre aye^s him which werre was not
endyd in his time And aftyrward Merly^ told that this dragon should be hold the
best body of all ye world. and he said soth. for the good king Edward was ye
worthyest knight of all ye world in his time. And yet said merlyn that the
dragon should deye in the march of an othyr land / and that his la^d should be
long without any good keeper. and that me^ should weep for his death from the
I Will of shepey unto the I Will of marchyll / Wherefore allas should be her commune
song among people fadreles in the land / and that prophecy was known ouerall
full well: for the good king Edward deyed at Burgh up sa^des / that is upon the
the march of Scotland. wherefore the Englysshmen were disco^fited and sorowed
in Northumberland: for encheson that king edwardes sone set by the scotts no
force for ye riot of piers of Ganasto^: wherefore allas was ye song thurghout
all england. for defaute of a good wardeyn from the jle of sheppey unto the I Will
of marcyll. the people made much sorwe for king Edwardes death. for they wend
that the good king Edward should have gon^ into the holy land for that was
holli his purpose / upon whose soul god for his high grace have mercy

Of king Edward that was king edwardes sone. Cap. clxxxvij.
ANd aftyr this king edward reigned edward his sone yt was bore in Caernarva^.
and this Edward went into france and spoused Isabell the kings doughtyr of
France the xxv / day of janyuer / at the chyrch^ of our lady at Boloigne / In
the year of owre lord Ihesu Crist a M / ccc / vij and the xx day of Feuerer the
next year that came aftyr he was crowned solemply at westmynster: of the
erchebysshop Robert of wy^chestre: and of the erchebysshop of Canterbury and
there was so great prece of people yt sir Johan Bacwell was deed and murdered /
And anon as the good king edward was deed / Sir edward his sone king of
england sent aftyr Piers of Ganaston^ into Gascoyne: and so moch^ loved he him
that he called him his brother. And anon^ aftyr he yafe him the lordshyp of
Wallyngford. and it was not long aftyr that he ne yafe him the Erledome of
Cornewaille ayens all the lords will of the Reaulme / And tho brought he sir
Walter of Langeton bishop of Chestre into prison into the tower of London with
two knaves allon^ him to serve For the king was wroth with him for cause that
sir Walter made compleynt upon hy^ to his fadre: wherefore he was put into
prison in the time of troyllebastone And the foresaid Piers of Ganaston^ made so
great maistries that he went in to the kings tresorye in the Abbeye of
westmynstre and tok the table of goold with the tresselles of the same / and
many othyr rich iewelles / that some time were the noble and good king
Arthures: and took hem to a merchant that was kalled Aymery of Friscombande.
For he should bear hem over the sea in to Gascoyne / and so he went thens. and
the iewelles came nevyr ayen^ aftyr. wherefore it was great loss unto this la^d
/ And when this Piers was so rychely avau^ced he became so proud and so stout
that it was a wondyr: whereof all the great lords of the Reaulme had hy^ in
despyte for his great bery^g. wherefore sir Henry the lacy Earl of Nycholl and
sir Guy Earl of warrewyke. and them which good king Edward had yeven ye charge
that Piers of Ganaston^ should not come into England for to bri^ge his sone
Edward into Riot And all the lords of England assembled hem at a certain day:
at the freres prechours at London and spoken of the dishonor that king Edward
did unto his Reaume and to his crown. and so they aygred that the forsaid
piers of Ganastone should ben^ exilled out of England for evyrmore and it was
done. for he forswore England / and went into Irland: and the king made him
chiuetayne and governor of the la^d by his conmyssyon / And there this piers
was chyuetayne of all the land: and did there all that him lyked. and had
power what he would / And at that time were the templers exilled through all
crystiente. for encheso^ that men put upon hem that they should done sum thing
ayens the right faith and good believe King Edward loved the foresaid Piers of
Ganastone so much that he might not forlet his company: and so moch^ the king
yafe and behyght to the people of England that the e^illyng of the forsaid Piers
should been revoked at Stawnforde through hem that him had exylled: Wherefore the
foresaid Pyers of Ganaston^ cam^ ayen^ into england And when he was come ayen^
in to this land^ he despised the grettest lords of this la^d. and kalled sir
Robert of Clare earl of Gloucestre bore sone / and the earl of Nichol sir Henry
the Lacy Brostebely: and sir Guy earl of Warrewyk ye blake hounde of Arderne /
and also he called the noble earl and ge^tyll Thomas of Lancaster Chorle: and
many other scorns and shame he^ said. and by many other great lords of
England. wherefore they were towardys him full angry and sore annoyed: and in
the same time deyed the earl of Nychol. but he charged or he was deed Thomas of
Lancaster Earl that was his sone in law that he should mayten^ his querell
ayens the same Piers of Ganaston^ upon his beueson And so it was ordained
through help of the earl of Lancastre and of the earl of warrewyk / that the
foresaid Sir Piers was beheded at Gauesich besides warrewyk ye xix day of Iuyn^.
in ye year of grace a Mccc. and xij / wherefore the king was sore annoyed and
prayed god yt he might se that day to ben^ ave^ged upon the death of the foresaid
Piers / and so it befell aftyrward as ye shall here / Allas the time. for the
forsaid Earl of Lancastre and many other great barons were* put to pitous death
/ and martred for e^cheson of ye forsaid querell. The king was tho at London:
and held a parlame^t: and ordained the laws of sir Symond monfort. wherefore
the earl of Lancastre and the Erlys and all the clergy of england made an oth^
through cou^seill of Robert of wynchestre for to may^ten^ the ordenau^ces for
evyrmore

How Robert ye brus came ayen^ into scotland. and gadred a great power of men

ANd when sir Robert the brus that made him king of scotland that was fled i^to

for he was disco^fyted at Ba^nokesborne / therefore mayde^s made a song thereof
in that co^tre of king Edward of england. And in this manner they songe^ Maidens
of england sare may ye morn for right have ye lost your la^mans at
Ba^nokesborne with heualogh / what wend the king of England to have get
Scotland with rumbylowe

When king Edward was disco^fyted he was wonder sorry: and fast fled wit his
folk that was left on live and went to Berewyke / and there held he him / and

How ye town of Berewyk was take through treson: and how ij. cardinals were
robbed in england:.C. clxxxix
ANd i^ mydle^te^ so^day in ye year of our lord Ihu^ crist Mccc.xvi. Berewyk

had put there for to keep ye same town with many burgeis of the town wherefore ye
children that were put i^ hostage through the burgeis of Berewyk folewed the

maistir lowys of Beaumo^t bishop of Dureha^ / and as they went they were taken

middelto^ was attay^t and take: and ho^ged. and drawn at lo^don^ and his heed
smitten of: and set upon a spear and upon new gate And the iiij quarters
sent to for cites of england And that same time befell many myschefes in
e^glo^d: for the pour people deyde in england for hunger. and so moch^ and so
fast deid that uneath men might he^ bury. for a quartyr of whete was worth xl
shylly^ges. and ij year and an half a q^rter of whete was worth x marc: and
oftetymes the pour people stale children and ete hem. and also all the hou^des
that they might take. and eke horse and cattes / and aftyr there fill a great
moreyne among bestes in diverse co^trees of England dury^g king edwardes life

How the scotts robbed Northumberland Capitulo Cxc
ANd in the same time came the Scotts ayen^ into England and destroyed
Northumberland and bre^d that la^d and robbed it. and quelled men women and
children that lyenth in cradellys / and brent also holy church and destroyed
cristendome and took and bare englysshmennys gooddes as they had ben^ sarazenes
or paynyms. and of the wykkednesse that they dyden / all the world spoke thereof
through all crystendome

How the Scotts would not amend her trespace. and therefore scotland was
enterdyted Capitulo Cxci
AN when pope Johan the xxij / aftyr saint petre herd of the great sorwe and
meschief that ye scotts wrought. he was wonder sorry that cristendome was so
destroyed through ye scotts And namely they destroyed so holy chyrch^ /
wherefore the pope sent a general sentence vndyr his bulls of led unto the
Archibisshop of Caunterbury / and to the erchbisshop of york / that if robert
the brus of scotland would not be justified and make amends unto the king of
england Edward her lord / and make amends of his loss and his harms that
they had done in England: and also to restore the goods that they had taken of
holy church that the sentence should be pronu^ced through all england And when
the scotts herd this they would not let her malice for the ^opes
commandment Wherefore robert brus James douglas and Thomas Raudulph earl of
Moiref^ all tho that with him communed or hem help in word or in deed were
accursed in every chyrch^ through all england eueri day at mass iij times: and
no mass should be song in holy church through out all scotland / but if ye
scotts would make restytucyon of the harms that they had made unto holy
chyrch^: wherefore many a good pressed and holy men therefore were slayn^ through the
reaume of scotland / for encheson that they would sing no mass ayens ye ^opes
commandment and ayens his will: and to done and fullfyll the tyraunts will

How sir Hugh^ the spe^cers sone was made the kings chamberlayne and of ye
bataill o Mytone Capitulo Cxcij
ANd it was not long aftyrward that the king ordained a parliament at york and
there was sir Hugh^ the spe^cers sone made chamburlayne / and in the mean time
while the werre last: the king went ayene into scotland that it was wonder for
to wit. and besieged ye town of Berewyke. but scotts went over the watyr of
solewath that was three mile from the kings host / and pryuely they stelle
away by night and came^ into England and robbed and destroyed all that they
might and spared no manner thing till that they came^ unto york. And when the
Englysshmen that were left at home herd this thy^g / all they that might
trauaille as well monks and prestes and frerys and chanons^ and seculers came
and mete with ye scotts a my^one up Swale: The xij day of octobre Allas what
sorwe. the Englyssh housbondmen that cowde nothing of the werre that there were
quelled and dre^ched in an arm of the sea And her chiviteyns Sir william of
Melton / Erchebisshop of york and the abbot of Selby with her stedes fled and
camen unto york: and that was her own folly that they had that mischau^ce for
they passed the watyr of Swalle: and the scotts set a fire the stakkes of
hey and the smoke thereof was hugh^. that the Englysshmen might not see the
scotts / And when ye Englysmen were gone over the watyr ^ tho camen the
scotts wit her wynge in manner of a shield and came^ toward the englysshmen in
array: and the Englysshme^ fled. for uneath they had any me^ of arms. for the
k^g had hem almost lost at the siege of Berewyk / and the scottish hobylers
went between the brugge and the englysshmen And when the great host hem met^
the englyssh men fled between the hob^^ers and the great host and the
Englysshmen almost were there quelled and he that might wend over ye watyr was
saved / but many were draint. Allas for there was slain many men of relygion
and seculiers and eke prestes and clerk^s. and with moch^ sorwe the
erchebysshop ascapyd. and therefore called ye scotts that bataill the white
bataill

How king Edward did all manner thing that sir Hugh^ the spe^cer would. Cap.
Cxciij
ANd when king Edward herd this tydinge: he remeued his siege from berewyk and
came ayene into England / But sir Hugh^ the spencer the kings sone that was
the ky^ges chambyrlayne kept so ye kings chamber that no man must speak with
the king but he that yaue him a brybe for to done his need / and that over
mesure. And this Hugh^ bear hy^ so stout that all man had of hy^ scorn and
despyte and the king hy^ self would not ben^ gouernyd ne ruled by no manner man
but only by his fadre and by hi^ / and if any knight of England had woddes
manners or lordshyppes that they would coueyt. anon^ the king must yeve it hem.
or else ye man that ought it should be falsely endyted of forest or of felonye:
And through such^ doing they disheryted many a good bachelier and so much land
they geten that it was wondyr^ and when the lords of England saw the great
couetise and the falsenesse of sir Hughe the spencer the fadre and of sir hugh^
the sone / they came^ to the gentle earl of Lancastre and axed him cou^ceyll
of the disese that was in the Reaulme through sir Hugh ye spe^cer the fadre. and
of sir Hugh^ the sone / and in haste by own assente they made a pryue assemble
at shirborne in Elmede / and all they made there an oath for to break and
destrouble the doing bitwene ye king and sir Hugh the spencer and his sone upon
her power / And they went into ye march of walys and destroyed the la^d of ye
forsaid sir hughes

How sir Hugh^ the spencer and his fadre were exilled out of England Capi.
Cxciiij
WHen king edward saw ye great harm and destruc / tio^ that ye barons of
e^glo^d dide^ to sir Hugh^ the spe^cers ^a^de and to his sons in every place
that they camen upon. and the king tho through his cou^ceyl exilled sir Ioha^
Monbray: sir Rogier of Gliford: and sir Goselyne Dauill. and many other lords
that were to he^ co^se^t / Wherefore the barons did tho more harm than they
dide^ before. and when the king saw that the barons would not cese of her
cruelte / the king was sore adrad lest they would destroy him and his reaume
for his mayntenaunce / but if that he asse^ted to hem. And so he sent for hem
by lettres that they should come to london to his perleme^t at a certay^ day as
in his lre^s was contained And they came^ wit three batailles well armed at all
poi^ts and eueri bataill had cote armures of grene cloth / and thereof ye right
q^rt was yelwe with whit bendes. wherefore yt parlame^t was called ye parlame^t of
the whitbende And in ye company was sir Vmfrey de Bohene / earl of Herford and
sir Rogier of Clyfford: sir Johan Monbray / sir Gecelyn dauyl / sir rogier
mortymer uncle of sir rogier mortymer of wygmore: sir Henry of trais sir Johan
Giffard. and sir bartholomewe of badelesmore: that was the kings stiward: that
the king had sent to shirborne in Elmede to the earl of Lancaster and to all
that with him were for to trete of accord that him allied to ye barons. and
with that company / and sir Rogier Da^morie / and sir Hugh^ Dandale: that had
spoused kings neces suster. and sir Gillebert of Clare of Glowcestre that was
queld in scotland as before is said And the two lords had tho ij. parties of
the erldome of gloucestre. and sir Hugh^ the spe^cer the sone had the thridde
part in his wyfes half. the thridde sustyr and the ij. lords went to the
barons with all power ayens sir Hugh^ her brother: in law / And so there came
wit he^ sir Rogier of Clyfford: sir Johan Mo^bray / sir Gosselme dauyll. sir
rogier Mortymer of work sipe / Rogier mortymer of Wygmore his nepheu / sir
Henry trais. sir johan giffard sire Bartholomewe of badelesmore with all her
company / and many other that to hem were consent / All these great Lords
camen to westmynstre to the kings parliament: and so they spoken and did that
both sir Hugh spe^cer the fadre. and sir hugh^ the sone were owtelawed of
England for evermore / And sir Hugh the fadre went to Dover and made moch^
sorwe / and fell down upon the ground by the sea bank acros with his arms
and sore wepi^g said / now fair England and good england to almighty god I the
betake / and thries cust the ground and we^de never to have comen ayen^: and
weeping full sore kursed the time yt euyr he begat sir hugh^ his sone: and said
for him he had lost all Englong / And in presence of he^ that were about him /
he yafe hy^ his curse: and went over the sea to his lands / but sir hugh^ the
sone would not gone out of England. but held him in the sea. and he and his
company robbed two dromondes beside sa^dewych and took and bear away all the
good that was in thaym to ye value of xl.M pound

How the king exilled Earl Thomas of Lancastre and all that held with him /
and how the Mortymer came and yield him to the king and of the lords Cap. Cxcv
IT was not long aftyr yt the king ne made sir hughe spencer the fadre and sir
Hughe the spe^cer the sone come ayene into England aye^s the lords will of the
reaulme: and sone aftyr the king with a strong power came and besieged the
castle of ledes and in the castle was the lady of Badelesmere / for e^cheson
that she would not grant ye castle to queen Isabell king Edwardes wife: but
the pryncipall cause was for encheson yt sir Bartholomewe badelesmere was ayens
the king. and held with ye lords of England: and notheles ye king by help
and socour of men of london. and also of help of southern men the king gate
the castle mangre he^ all that were theryn / and took with him all that he might
find: and when the barons of england herd of this thing. sir Rogier mortymer
and other many lords took the town of brugeforth wit stre^gthe Wherefore the
king was wonder wroth and let outelawe thomas of Lancaster and Vmfrey de
bahoune earl of herford / and all tho that were assentant to the same quarrel /
and the king assembled an huge host. and came against the lords of england.
wherefore the mortymers put he^ to the kings mercy and his grace / and anon^
they were sent to ye tour of London and there kept in prison / and when the
barons herd of this thing they camen to Pounfret / there the earl thomas
soiourned / and told hi^ how that Mortimers both had yield hem to the king and
put hem in his grace

Of the siege of Tykhill Capi. Cxcvi
WHen sir Thomas earl of Lancastre herd this they were wonder wroth. and all
that were of his company. and greatly they were discomfyted. and ordained her
power to gedre / and besieged the castle of Tykhyll. but they that were
withynne. so manly defended hem self that the barons might not get the castle
And when the king herd that his castle was besieged: he swore by god and by
his holy names / that the siege should be remeved / and assembled an hughe
power of people / and went thydderward to reskewe the castle / and his power
encresed from day to day. Whenne the noble and gentyl Earl of Lancastre and the
Earl of Herford. and the barons of her company herd of this thy^g they
assembled all her power and went hem to Burton up Trent and kept the brygge
that the king should not pass over But it befell so on ye / x / day of the
month of march^ In ye year of grace thousand three hundred and xxi / the king
and the spencer sir Aymer Valaunce earl of Penbroke. and sir Johan earl of
Arundell / and her power we^ten over the watyr and discomfited the Earl Thomas
and his company. and they fledden unto the castle of Tutbery: and fro thennes
they wenten to pounfret / and in that vyage deyed sir rogier da^morie in the
Abbey of Tutbery / and in that same time the Earl thomas had a traitor with
hy^ that was kalled Robert of Holand a knight that the earl had brought up of
naught: and had norysshed hy^ in his botelerie / and had yeven him a thousand
mark of land by year And so much he loved him that he might done in the Earls
court all thing that him lyked both among hye and low / and so que^tely yt
thief bare hy^ aye^s his lord / yt he trustyd more upon him tha^ upon any man a
lyve. and the earl had ordained by his lettres for to went into ye Erldome of
Lancastre for to make me^ arise to help him in that vyage^ that is to seye.v.C
/ men of Arms: but the false traitor came no there no manner men for to warn ne
to make arise for to help his lord And wha^ the traitor herd tell that his
lord was disco^fyted at Burtone as a falls thief traitor he stalle away / and
robbed in Rauenesdale his lords men that came fro the scomfyture. and took of
hem horse and harneis / and all that they had: and quelled of hem all that he
might take And tho came and yield hy^ unto the king. When the good Earl Thomas
wist that he was so betrayed he was sore abashed and said to him self O
almighty god quod he how might robert hola^d find in his heart me to betraye:
sithen^es that I have loved hy^ so moch^. o god well may now a man see by him
that no man may deceive an other rather tha^ he that he trust most upon: he
has full evil yield my godnesse and the worship that I to hy^ have done: and
through my ke^denesse have j him avau^ced and made hi^ high^ from low / and he
makes me go from hygh^ unto low. but yet shall he deye in evil death

Of the scomfyture of Burbruge / Capitulo / c.xcvij
THe good earl thomas of Lancastre. Humfrey de Boho^ne Earl of Herford and the
barons that wit hem were. took cou^ceill between hem at friar prechours at
Pou^fret. Tho thought Thomas upon the traitrie of Robert Hola^d: and said in
reprove Allas holand has me betrayed. Ay is in the reed some euel shrede / and
by common assent they should all went to ye castle of Du^sta^burgh. the
which parteyneth to the Erledome of Lancastre. and that they should abide there
till yt the king had foryeue he^ her maletalent. But when the good Earl Thomas
this herd / he answered in this manner and said Lords quod he: If we gon^
toward ye North the Northren men will seyne that we go toward the scotts / and
so we should be hold traitors: for cause of distaunce that is bitwene king
Edward and Robert the brus that made him king of scotland. and therefore I say
as touching my self that I will goo no ferther into the north tha^ to my^ own
castle of Pownfrete. And when sir Rogier clyford herd this he aroos up anon
in wrath and drowe his sword. and swore by almighty god and by his holy names.
but if that he would gone with hem he should be deed: and that he would slay him
there / The noble and gentle earl Thomas of Lancaster was sore a drad and
said: fair sires I will gon^ with you whyder so ever ye me led Tho went they
to gedres into the North and wit he^ they had vij.C men of arms and camen to
Burbrygge: And wha^ sir Andrew of Herkela that was in the north contre through
ordenau^ce of the king for to keep the contre of scotland / herd tell how that
thomas of Lancaster was discomfited and his company at burton upon Trent: he
ordained hy^ a strong power: and sir Symond ward also that was tho sherewe of
york. and came^ and met ye barons at Burbrygge. and anon^ they break the
brigge that was made of tree And when sir Thomas of Lancastre herd that sir
Andrewe of Herkela had brought with him such^ power he was sore adrad: and sent
for sir Andrew of Herkela and with him spoke and said to him in this manner.
Sir Andrewe quod he / ye mow well vndyrsto^de how that our lord the king is
lad and mysgouerned by moch^ falls cou^ceille through sir Hugh the spe^cer the
fadre / and sir Hugh^ his sone / and sir Johan Earl of Arundell. and through
master Robert baldolke a falls pylled clerk that now is in the ky^ges court
dwelly^g / wherefore I pray you that ye would come wit us wit all the power that
ye have ordained and help to destroy the veny^ of England / and the traitors
that been therinne / and we will yeve unto you the best part of v / Erledomes^
that we have and hold / and we will make unto you an oath: that we will never
done thing without yowre cou^ceill and so ye shall be efte as well with us as ever
was Robert of Holand / Tho answered sir Andrew of Herkela / and said. Sir
thomas that would I not done ne consent there to: For no manner thing ye might me
give without ye will and commandment of owr lord the king: for than should
I ben^ hold a traitor for evyrmore. And when the forsaid noble Earl Thomas of
Lancastre saw that he nold not give consent unto him for no manner thing. Sir
Andrewe said he / Will ye now not consent to destroy the veny^ of the Reame
as we be consent / at one word sir Andrew j tell the that or this year be gone
that ye shull ben^ take and hold for a traitor and more tha^ ye hold us now
and in wers death ye shall deye tha^ euyr deyed any knight of england And
understands well that ye deed nevyr thing that sorer shall you repent: and
now goth and does that you good lyketh. and I wull put me unto the mercy and
the grace of god / And so went the false traitor sir Andrewe of herkela i^ his
way as a falls traitor tyrant and as a falls forsworn man for through the noble
Earl of Lancastre / he vnderfeng the arms of cheualerie / and through him he
was made knight. Tho might me^ see^ archyers draw hem in that one side and in
that other and knights also: and fowghten to gedre wonder sore / and also
among other sir Humfrey de boughon earl of herford a worthy knight of ^no^me
through all cristendome stood and faught with his enemies upon the brygge / a
thief a Rybaude skulked under the brigge And fersely with a spear smote the
noble knight into the fowndement. so that his bowelles came^ out there^ allas
the sorwe / for there was slain the flour of solace. and of comfort. and also
of curtesye And sir Rogier of Clyford a noble knight stood euyr and fought and
well and nobely him defended as a worthy baron But at the last he was sore
wownded in his head. and sir willyam of Sullaya^d Sir Rogier of Bernefeled were
slain at that bataille.

When sir Andrewe of Herkela saw that sir Thomas men of lancaster lassed and
slaked anon he and his company camen to the gentle knight sir Thomas of
Lancastre and said / yield the trai / tour yield the. The gentle Earl a^swered
tho and said / Nay lords. traitors be we none and to you will we nevyr us
yield whiles yt owr lyfes lasten. but lever we have to be slain i^ our truth
tha^ yield us to you / And sir Andrew ayene grad upon sir Thomas company
yollyng as a wode wolf / and said: yield you traitors taken yield you / and
with an hygh^ voys said. bethe ware syres that none of you be hardy upon life
and upon lymme. for to misdone Thomas body of Lancastre and with that word the
good Earl Thomas went into the chapel / and said knelyng upon his knees and
turned his visage toward the cross and said. O almighty god to the I me
yield and holy put me into thy mercy And wit that the vyleyns Rybaudes ^ept
about him in every side as tyraunts and wode turmentours and dispoilled him of
his armure. and clothed him in a rob of ray that was of his squyers lyuere:
and forth lad him unto york by water / Tho might men seen much sorwe and care
/ for the ge^tyll knights fledden in every side. and the rybaudes and the
vyleyns egrely hem discryed and grad an high yield you traitors. yield you /
And when they were yolden / they were robbed and bounden as thevys. Allas the
shame / and despyte that the gentill order of knyghthode there had at that
bataylle. and the land tho was wytoute law. for holy chyrch^ tho had no more
reverence tha^ it had been a bordelhows and in that bataille was the fadre
ayens the sone^ and the uncle ayens his nephew: for somoche vnkendenesse was
never seyn before in england. as was that time among folk of one nacyo^ / For
o kynrede had no more pity of that othyr^ than an hungry wolf has of a
sheep. and it was no wonder / For the great lords of England were not all of o
nacyon. but were meddled with other nations / that is for to seyne / sum
Breto^s. so^me Saxons: sum danoys. some Pehites / sum Frenshmen: sum
Normans: sum Spaynardes: sum Romans / sum Henaudes. sum Flemmynges /
and of other diverse nacyo^s / the which nacyons not accorded to the kind
blood of England / And if so great lords had ben^ only wedded to Englyssh
people / than should pees have ben^ and rest among hem without any envye

And at that bataill was sir Rogier Cliford tak / Sir Johan Mo^bray. sir
William tuchet. Sir william fits William. and many other worthy knights there
were taken at that bataille: And sir hughe Dandell the next day after was
taken and put into prison. and should have been done to death / if he had not

anon^ after was sir Bartholomewe of badelesmere taken at stowe park a manner of
the bisshoppes of Lyncolne that was his nephew: and many other barons and
baneretz wherefore was made moch^ sorwe

How Thomas of Lancaster was beheded at Pou^frete: and v. barons honged and
drawn there Capitulo Cxcviij.
ANd now shall I tell you of the noble earl Thomas of Lancastre when he was
taken and brought to york: many of the cite were full glad and upon him cried
with an high voys O sir traitor ye arne welcome / blessed be god for now
shall ye have the reward that long time ye have deserved / and kast upon him
many snow balls and many othyr reproues did they hy^^ but the gentle earl
all suffryd and said nothir oon ne other / and in the same time the king herd
of this same sconfiture and was full glad. and in have came to Pounfret and sir
hughe the spencer and sir Hughe his sone and sir Johan Earl of Arundell / and
sir Edmond of wodestoke the kings brother earl of Kent: and sir Aymer of
valaunce Earl of Panbroke / and master Robert Baldock a falls pyled clerck /
that was pryue and dwelled in the kings court* and all came thither with the
king. And the king entered into the castle: And sir Andrewe of Herkela a falls
tiraunt through the kings commandment took with him the gentle Earl Thomas
to Pounfrete. and there he was prysoned i^ his own castle that he had new
made^ that stood ayens the abbey of king Edward^ And sir hughe the fadre and
his sone cast and thought how and in what manner the good Earl thomas of
Lancastre should be deed without any judgment of his perys / wherefore it was
ordained through the kings justices that the king should put upon him points
of treson And so it befell that he was to ye bar before the kings justices
bare head as a thief in a fair halle withyn his own castle that he made thery^
many fest both to rich and eke to pour. and these were his justices Sir Hugh^
the spe^cer of fadre / Aymer of valaunce earl of Pe^brok. sir edmond of
wodestok earl of Kent: sir Johan of bretaigne earl of Richemond / and sir
Robert of Nalemethorpe justice / and sir robert him acoulped in this manner.
Thomas at the first owr lord the king and this court excludes you of all manner
answer. Thomas our lord ye king put upon you that ye have in his land ride^
wit baner displaied against his pees as a traitor. and with / that word the
gentle earl thoa^s wit an hygh^ vois said. nay lords for soth and by sey^t
Thomas I was never a traitor. the justice said ayen^ the thomas / our lord the
king put upon you that ye have robbed his folk and mordred his people as a
thief. Thomas the king also put upon you that he discomfited you and your people
with his folk in his own reaume. wherefore ye went and fled to ye wode as an
outelawe / and also ye were taken as an outelawe / And thomas as a traitor ye
shul be ho^ged by reso^ but ye king had foryeve you that jews for love of
queen Isabel. and thoa^s reason would also that ye should be ho^ged: but the king
has foryeve you yt for cause of your lygnage But Thomas for asmoche as ye were
take fleyng And as an owtelawe the king will that your head shall be smytten of
/ as ye have well deserved / anon does hy^ owte of presence / and anon bry^g
him to his jugeme^t: When the ge^tyl knight Thomas had herd all these words.
with an high voys he cried sore weeping and said Allas saint Thomas fair fadre
allas shall I be deed thus. Grant me now blyssefull god a^swere but all
avaylled him no thing / for the kursed gascoynes put hy^ hydder and thydder and
on him cried with an hygh^ voys. O god most dreadful well known is now thyn
open traitrye. an evil death shall thou deye as thou have well deservyd / Tho
set they upon his head in scorn an old chappelet all to rent and to torn
that was not worth an halpeny And after they set him upon a leave white
palfrey full vnsemelich and eke all bare and with an old bryddell. and with an
horrible noise they drouen him owte of ye castle toward his death / and cast
upon him many balls of snow. And as the turmentours lad him out of ye
Castle: Tho said he this pytouse words: And his hands held upon high
toward heve^ Now the king of heaven yeve us mercy for the erthely king has us
forsake. and a friar prechour went with him out of the castle: till that he
came to the place that he ended his life: unto who^ he shrofe him all his life:
And the ge^tyl earl held the friar wonder fast by the clothes. and said fair
fadre abide with us till that I be ded / for my flesh quaketh for dread of
death. And soth for to seye / the ge^till Earl set him upon his knees and
turned him toward the Est: but a Rybaulde that was kalled Hygone of Mostone set
hand upon the gentle Earl and said in despyte of him: Sir traitor turn the
toward the scotts thy foul death to vnderfong. and turned him to ward the
north: The noble and gentill earl Thomas answered tho with a mylde voys and
said. now fayrlordes I shall done all your will: and with that word the friar
went fro him sore weeping. and anon a ribaulde went to him and smote of his
head the xi. kal of apryll in the year of grace M / ccc.xxi. Allas that ever
such a ge^tyll blood should ben^ done to death without cause and reason. and
traytoursly was the king cou^ceilled / when he through the false counceill of ye
spe^cers suffered sir thoa^s his uncles sone be put to such a death. and so ben
beheded ayens all manner of reason: and great pity it was also that such a noble
king should ben^ deceived and mysgouerned through the right false counceill of
the false spencers the which he mayntened through los lerie ayens his honor
and eke profit For aftyrward there fill great vengeance in England. for
encheso^ of the forsaid thomas death / When the gentle earl of his life was
passed the pryour and the monks of Pounfrete geten the body of sir Thomas of
the king. and they buried it before the high auter on the right side That same
day that this gentle lord was deed there were honged and draw for the same
quarrel at Pounfret / Sir william tuchet / sir william fitz willya^: Sir
warreyne of ysille: sir Henry of Bradborne / and sir willyam chenie barons all
/ and Johan page squire. And sone aftyr at york were drawn and honged sir
Rogier Cliford / Sir johan of Monbray barons. and sir Gosselm Dauyll knight.
And at Bristowe were draw and honged sir Henry of wymyngton. and sir Henry
Mounfort barons: And at Gloucestre were draw and honged. Sir Johan Giffard.
and sir william of Emelbrugge barons And at London were honged and draw sir
Henry Ties baron And at wynchelsee sir Thomas Colepepir knight. And at
