How king Edward went into Scotland with an hou^dred thousand men of arms and
might not speed Capi. Cxcix
ANd when king Edward of England had brought ye flower of cheualerye unto her
death through counceyl of sir hugh^ spencer the fadre. and sir hughe the sone /
he became as wode as any lyo^ne / And what so ever the spencers wolden have it
was done / And so well ye king loved he^ that they might done wit him all
thing that they would. wherefore the king yafe unto sir hugh^ spencer the fadre
the erledome of wy^chestre: and to sir andrewe of Herkela the erledome of
Cardoill in p^iudice and in harmyng of his croune / And king Edward tho th^^gh
cou^seille of the spe^cers disherited all he^ that had ben^ ayens him in any
querell with thomas of lancaster and many other were disherited also. for
encheso^ yt the spe^cer coueited for to have her lands. and so they had all
that they would desire with wrong and aye^s all reason Tho made the king Robert
of baldok a falls piled clerk chau^celer of england through counceyll of the
foresaid spencers / and he was a falls ribaud^ and a coueytous: And so they
counceylled the king much that the king let taken tho his own ward all the
goods of the lords that wrongfully were put to the death into his own hand /
And as well they token ye goods that were in holy church as the goods that
were without / and let he^ be put into his tresorye in the cite of London. and
thereof let hem be kalled his forfayts / and by her cou^ceill the king wrought
for evyrmore / he disheryted hem that the goods oughten / And through her
counceyll let arere a talliage of all the goods of England / wherefore he was
the richest king that ever was in England aftyr wylliam Bastard of Normandye
that conquered england: And yet through counceyl of hem him seemed that he had
not ynowe / but made yet every town of England find a man of arms upon her
own costages for to gone and werre upon the Scotts that were his enemies
wherefore the king went into scotland wit an houndred thousand men of arms at
witsontyde in the year of owr lord Ihesu crist M.CCC and xxij But the scotts
went and hyd hem in mountains and in wodes / and carried the Englysshmen fro
day to day that the king might for no manner thing hem fy^de in plain field /
wherefore many englysshmen that few vitailles hadden / for hunger they deyden
wonder fast suddenly in going and in coming: and namely tho that had ben^
ayens Thomas of Lancastre and robed his men upon his lands / Whenne king
Edward saw that vitaylles failled him: he was tho wonder sore discomforted for
encheson also that his men deyed / and for that he naught might speed of his
ennemies / so at the last he came ayene into England: And anon after came
James Douglas and also Thomas Randulph with an huge host into England into
Northumberland. and with hem the Englysshmen that were driven owte of england.
and camen and robbed the contre and quelled the people: and also brent the town
that was called Nortallertone and many other towns unto york. And when the
king herd this tidy^ge / he let sompne all manner me^ that myghten trauaille.
and so the englysshmen met the scotts at the abbey of Beigheland the xv. day
after Mychelmasse in the same year above said. and the englysshmen were there
discomfyted. and at that scomfyture was take sir johan of Britaigne earl of
Richemond that held the contre and Erledome of Lancastre. And after he paid
an huge raunsone and was let gone. And after that he went into france: and
came nevyr aftyrwdrd ayene

How sir Andrewe of Herkkela was taken and put unto the death / that was earl of
Cardoille Capitulo ducentesimo
ANd at that time sir Andrewe of Herkela that new was made Earl of cardoille /
for cause that he had taken the good Earl Thomas of Lancaster. he had ordained
through ye ky^ges commandment of England for to bring him all the power yt he
might: for to help him ayens the scotts at ye Abbey of Beigheland / And wha^
the false traitor had gadred all the people that he might / and should have come^
to the king unto the abbey of Beighela^d: the false traitor lad hem by an other
contre through Copela^d and through the erldome of Lancaster and went through the
co^tre and robed and queld folk all that he might / and ferthermore ye falls
traitor had taken a great some of gold and silver of sir James Douglas for to
be ayens the king of England: and to be helpyng and holdyng with the scotts.
through whose treson the king of England was scomfyted at Beiheland er that he
came thydder: wherefore the king toward him was wonder wroth and let pryuely
enquere by the contre about how that it was. and so me^ enquered and aspied
that at the last trewth^ was found and sought / and he atteynt and taken as a
falls traitor as the noble earl Thomas of lancastre him told. er that he were
done unto the death at his taking at burbrygge. and to hy^ said: or that year
were done he should be take and hold a traitor And so it was as the holy man
said. wherefore the king sent pryuely to Sir anthoyn^ of Lucy a knight of the
country of Cardoille that he should take sir Andrewe of Herckela and put hy^
unto the death. and to bring this thy^g unto the end the king sent his
commission so that the same Andrewe was taken at Cardoill / and led unto the
bar in ye manner of an earl worthily arrayed and with a swerd gurt about hy^
and hosed and spored: Tho spoke sir anthoyne in this manner. sir Andrewe quod he
the king put upon the for asmoch^ as thou have been orped in thy deeds: he ded
unto the mochel honor and made the Earl of Cardoill: and thou as traitor unto
thy lord the king laddest his people of this co^tre that should have help hy^ at
the bataill of Beyghela^d. and thou laddest the^ away by the co^tre of Copela^d
and through the erledome of Lancastre wherefore our lord the king was scomfyted
there of the scotts through thy treson and falsenesse and if thou had com^
be times. he had had the maistiry / and all through treson thou dydest it for
the great some of goold and silver that thou vnderfe^g of James douglas a scote
the kings enemy / and our lord ye kings will is that the order of
knyghthode by the which thou vndyrfeng all thin honor and worship upon thy
body be all brought to naught. and thy estate undone yt other knights of low
degree mow after the beware / the which lord has the avaunced hugely i^
diverse contrees in England. and that all mow take example by the her lord
aftyrward trewly for to serve / Tho commanded he a knave anon to have of his
spores on his helys / and aftyr he let break ye sword over his head. the
which the king him yafe to keep and defend his land therewith when he made
hi^ earl of Cardoil / and aftyr he let him unclothe of his furred tabart and of
his hode and of his furred cotes and of his gurdel And when this was done sir
Anthoyne said unto him. Andrewe quod he: now art thou no knight but a knave /
and for thy treson ye king will that thou shall be ho^ged and draw. and thy
boweles taken owte of thy body and brent before the / and thy body quartred and
thyn head smyten of. and sent unto London / and there it shall stand upon
London brugge. and thy four quarters shull be sent to four towns of England
that all other mow be chastysed by the. And as Antoyne said so it was done all
manner thing in the last day of Octobre in the year of grace M.ccc. and xxij
year And the son tho turned i^ to blood. as the people it saw And that dured
fro the morn til it was xi of the clokke of the day.

Of ye miracles yt god wrought for saint Thomas love of Lancaster. wherefore the
king let close the church doors of the Pryowre of pounfret. for yt no man
should come thery^ to the body for to offre^ / Capitulo / CCj.
ANd sone aftyr that the earl Thomas of Lancastre was martred a pressed that
long time had been blind dremed in his slepyng that he should gone unto the
hylle there that the good Earl thomas of Lancastre was done unto the death. and
he should have his sight ayen^ and so he dremed iij nights sewy^g: and ye
priest let tho led him to the same hylle And when he came to that place that
he was martred / on deuoutely he made there his prayers and prayed god and sey^t
Thoa^s that he must have his sight ayene. and when he was in his prayers he
laid his right hand upon the same place that the good man was martred on. and
a drope of dry blood and small sand cleued on his hand and therewith stryked
his eyes and anon through might of god and of sey^t Thomas of Lancaster he had
his sight ayen^: and thanked tho almighty god and seint Thomas / And when this
miracle was known among men. the people came thydder in every side and kneled
and made her prayers at his to^be that is in the pryorie of Pounfrete and
prayed the holy martyr of socour and of help: and god herd her prayer /

Also there was a yo^ge child dre^chyd in a well: in the town of Pounfrete.
and was deed three days and three nights: and men camen and laid the deed
child upon saint Thomas tomb the holy martyr. and the child arose there from
death to life as many a man it saw: and also moch^ people were owte of her mind
and god has he^ sent her mind ayene through virtue of that holy martyr. and
also god has yeuen thereto creples her going / and to crooked her ho^des and her
feet: and to blind also her sight / and to many sike folk her hele of
diverse maladyes / for the love of this good martyr Also there was a rich man
in Coundom in Gascoyne / and such a malady he had / that all his right side
roted and fill a way from him that me^ might se his liver and also his heart.
and so he stanke that uneath men might come nigh him. wherefore his fre^des were
for him wo^dre sorry. but at the last as the almighty god would. they prayed to
saint Thomas of Lancastre that he would pray to almighty god for that
prisoner. and behit to gon^ to Pou^frete for to done her pilgrimage / And in
vysion the next aftyr the martyr seint thomas came unto hy^ and anointed over
all his sike bodj. and therewith ye good man awoke and was all hole / and his
flesh was restored ayen^ that before was roted and fall away: for which
miracle ye good man and his fre^des loved god and sey^t thomas euyr more aftyr.
And this good man came into england and took with hy^ iiij felawes and came to
Pounfrete unto that holy martyr and did her pilgrimage. but ye good man yt was
sike came thither all nakyd sauf his brech^. and when they had done they turned
home ayen^ into her co^tre and told of ye miracle where so ever they came. And
also ij me^ have be helyd there of ye mormall through help of yt holy martyr
though yt evil be holyd i^curable When ye spe^cers herd that god did such
miracles for this holy martyr / and they would beleve it i^ no manner wise. but
said openly yt it was great heresye such^ virtue of hy^ to believe. and wha^ sir
hugh^ the spe^cer the sone saw all this doing: anon^ he sent his messagier
from pou^frete there that he dwelled to king Edward that tho was in Crauene at
Skypto^. for cause that the king should vndon^ that pylgrimage. and as the
ribaude ye messagier went toward the king for to done his message: he came by
the hylle on the which the good martyr was done to death / and in the same
place he made his ordure: and wha^ he had done / he went toward the king. a
strong flix him came upon that er he came to york / and shed all his bowls
at his fondeme^t. And when sir Hugh^ the spencer herd this tydyng some deel he
was a drad. and thought for to undone the pylgrimage if he might by any manner
way / and to the king went and said that they should be in great sklau^dre
through out all cristendome for the death of Thomas of Lancastre if that he
suffered ye people done her pilgrimage at Pou^frete. and so he counceilled the
king that he commanded to closse the church doors of Pou^frete. in the which
chyrch^ ye holy martyr seint thomas was entered / and thus they dyden ayens all
fraunchyses of ye holy chyrch^ / so that fowr year aftyr might no pylgrime come
unto that holy body: and for encheson that the monks suffered men come and
honor that holy body of seint thomas the martyr through counceill of sir Hugh^
spencer the sone: and through cou^ceill also of maistir Robert of baldok the
false pylled clerk that was the kings chau^celer / the king co^sentyd that
they should be set to her wages And let make there wardeins over her own good
long tyme^ and through commandment of the forsaid sir Hugh^ the spencer xiiij
Gascoynes well armed kept the hylle there that ye good man seint thomas was do
(...) unto his death: so that no Pilgryme might come by yt way: Full well wend
he to have be take crystes might and his power / and ye great loos of miracles
that he showed for his martyr sey^t thomas through all crystendome. and that
same time the king made robert of baldolke the pyled clerk falls through prayer
of sir hugh^ the spe^cer the sone chau^celere of England. And in the same time
was ye castle of Walyngford yolden aye^s the king through the prisoners yt were
withinne the castle for sey^t thoa^s quarrel of Lancaster. wherefore the people
of the contre came and toke^ the castle upon the foresaid prysonners. Wherefore
sir johan of Golyngton knight / and sir Edmond of the beche prisonners and a
squire that was kalled Rogier of Walton were take and sent to the king to
Pou^frete / and there they were done in prison / and the forsaid Rogier was
sent unto york and there he was draw and hanged: And anon after sir To / gier
Mortymer of wigmore bra / ke owte of the toure of London in this manner. The
forsaid sir To / gier herd that he should be draw and honged at london / in the
morn after seint Laurence day. and on the day before he held a fair fest in
ye toure of London / and there was sir stephen segraue constable of ye toure
and many great men wit him and when they should soap / the foresaid stephen sent
for all the officiers of the toure / and they came and soped with him And when
they should take her leave of hy^ / a squier that was called stephen that was
full pryue with the forsaid Rogier through his cou^ceil yafe hem all such^
drank that the least of hem all slepe^ two days and ij. nights: and in the
mean time he escaped away by watyr / that is to say by the Tamyse / and went
over the sea and held him in france: wherefore the king was sore annoyed and
tho put the same stephen out of his constablery

How the queen Isabel went into france for to trete of pees bitwene her lord
the king of England and the king of France her brother Capitulo CC.ij
THe king went tho unto london: and there through cou^ceil of sir hugh^ the
spe^cer ye fadre and of his sone: and of maistir Robert baldok a falls pyled
clerk his chaunceler let seize tho all the queen's lo^des into his own hand /
and also all the lands that were sir edwardis his sone / and were so put to
her wages ayens all manner reason / and that was through the falsenesse of the
spe^cers And when the king of France that was queen jsabelles brother herd of
this falsenesse he was sore annoyed aye^s the king of England and his false
counceillers: wherefore he sent a letter unto king Edward under his seal: yt he
should come into france at a certay^ day / for to done his homage / and thereto
he somened hy^. and else he should lose all gascoign^. And so it was ordained
in England through ye king and his cou^ceill that queen Isabel should we^de into
france for to trete of pees bitwene her lord and her brother. And that Oliver
yngha^ should we^de in to Gascoigne and have with hy^ vij.M. men and moo of arms
to ben^ seen shall and wardeyne of gascoign^ and so it was ordained that Queen
Isabell went tho over see / and came into france / and with her went sir aymer
of valau^ce Earl of pe^broke yt was there mordred suddenly in prive sege: but
that was through gods vengeance / for he was one of the justices that
consented to sey^t thomas death of Lancaster: and would never after repe^te hy^
of that wykked deed: And at that time sir Oliver of yngha^ went over into
gascoign^ and did moch^ harm to the king of france: and gate ayen^ that king
edward had lost* and moch^ more thereto

How king Edward sent sir Edward his sone the eldest into france Capi. CC / iij
THe queen Isabel not but a quarter of a yer^ dwelled in France. Sir Edward
her eldest sone ne axed leave for to went into France for to speak with his
modre Isabell the queen. And the king his fadre granted hy^ wit a good will
and said to him Go my fair sone in goodis blissyng and mine. and thenke for to
come ayen^ as hastly as thou might. And he went over see and came into France.
and the king of France his uncle vnderfe^g him with mochel honor. and said
unto him. fair sone ye be welcome. and for cause that your fadre come not for
to do his homage for ye duchye of Guyhe^ne as his au^cestres were went for to
do. I give you yt lordshipp to hold it of me in heritage as all your
auncestres have done tofore you: wherefore he was called duke of Gwyhenne

How the king exilled his queen Isabell and Edward his eldest sone / Capitu.
CCiiij
WHenne king Edward of England herd tell how the king of France had yeuen
the duchye of Gwyhe^ne unto sir Edward his sone without consent and will of
him. and that his sone had vnderfonge the duchye. he became wonder wroth and
sent to his sone by his lettre and to his wife also that they should come ayen^
into England in all the haste that they might: The queen Isabell and sir Edward
her sone were woder sore adrad of the kings menace and of his wrath. and
pryncipaly of the falsenesse of the spencers both^ of ye fadre and of the sone
/ and at his commandment they would not come. wherefore king Edward was sore
annoyed and let make a cry at London / that if queen ysabell and edward her
eldest sone Came not in to England. that they should been holden as enemies to
the Reame of England. and for that they would not obey and come by the kings
commandment into england. they both were exilled the modre and her sone.
When the queen Isabel herd thees tidings she was sore adrad to be she^t
through the false co^getyng of the spe^cers: And went with ye knights that were
exilled out of England for saint Thoa^s cause of Lancaster: that is to seye
sir rogier of wygmore / sir william trussell / sir Johan of cromwell. and many
other good knights. wherefore they toke^ her cou^ceill: and ordained among he^
for to make a marriage between the duke of Gwyhe^ne ye ky^ges sone of England
and the earls daughter of Henaude. yt was a noble knight of name and a doughty
in his time. and if that thy^g might be brought about. tha^ stood they
trouwy^g with the help of god to recover her heritage in England. whereof they
were put out through the false congetty^ges of ye spe^cers.

How king Edward through cou^ceill of the spe^cers sent to the douseperes of
France that they should help that the queen Isabel and her sone sir Edward
weren exilled out of france Capitulo. CCv
When king Edward and the spe^cers herd how queen jsabell and sir Edward her
sone had alied hem to the earl of henaud and to them that were out exilled of
england for encheson of thomas of Lancaster. they were so sorry that they wiste
not what to done / Wherefore sir Hugh^ the spe^cer the sone said unto sir Hugh^
his fadre in this manner wyse^ Fadre accursed be the time and the cou^ceill that
ever ye consented that queen Isabell should gon^ unto france for to trete of
accord between the king of england and her brother the king of France for that
was your counceyll. for at that time for soth your wit failled. For j dread me
sore lest through her and her sone we shull be she^t / but if we take the better
cou^ceill / Now fair Sires understands how mervaillous felonye and falshede
the spe^cers ymagined and cast. for privily they let fylle.v. bales wit silver.
the sum amounted.v. thousend pound / and they sent the barelles over see
preueli by an alyen that was kalled Arnold of spaigne that was a brecour of
london / that he should gon^ to ye douseperes of france. that they should
procure and speak to the king of france that queen Isabell and her sone Edward
were driven and exilled out of France / And among all other things that
they were brought to the death as preuely as they might be / But almighty god
would not so / for when this arnold was in ye hye see he was taken with
zela^ders that met him in the sea and took hy^: and lad hy^ to her lord Earl of
henaude. and moch^ joy was made for yt taking. and at the last this Arnold
preuely stale hy^ self away fro the^s and came to london: And of this taky^g
and of other things the earl of Henaude said to ye queen Isabell Dame makes
you merry and been of good chere. for ye be rycher tha^ ye wend have ben^* and
take ye these.v. barelles full of silver that were sent to the douzeperes of
France. for to quelle you and your sone Edward and the^keth hastily for to
went in england and takes ye with you sir Johan of Henaude my brother. and
v.C. me^ of arms: for many of he^ of france in who^ ye have had great trust
/ had great deinte you for to scorn. and almighty god grant you grace your
ennemies to overcome. The queen Isabell sent tho through Henaud and Flau^dres
for her sowdyours. and ordained her every day for to went into England ayene /
and so she had in her company Sir Edmond of Wodestoke that was Earl of Ke^t
that was sir edwardes brother of England

How king Edward let keep the costs of the sea / and tried out the best men
of werre in England Capitulo CCvi.
WHenne king Edward herd tell that queen Isabell and Edward her sone would
come into England with many aliens and with hem that were out lawed out of
England for her rebelnesse: he was sore adrad to be put a down and lose his
kingdom Wherefore he ordained to keep his castelles in walys as well as in
england with vitailles and her apparaille. and let keep his River and also ye
see costs. whereof the v. ports token to keep hem and also the sea. And at the
feast of decollacyon of saint Johan baptist the citezeins of London sent to the
king to Porchestre an hondert men of arms And he commanded ferthermore by his
lre^s and ordained that every ho^dred men should taken wape^ of england to
triours as well of me^ of arms as of men a foot. and that they should ben^ put
in xx. some / and in an C. some / and commanded that all the men were a ready
wha^ any outehese or cry were made for to purswe and take the alie^s that
came^ into england for to benymme hy^ the land. and for to put him out of his
kingdom. And more over he let cry through his patent lre^s in every place and
in every market of England that the queen Isabell and sir Edward his eldest
sone and the earl of Kent that they were taken and saufli kept without any
manner harm unto hem doing: and all other manner people that came with hem anon
smite of her hedes without any manner rau^sone And what man that might bry^g
sir Rogier heed mortymer of wy^g more should have an C. pound for his
trauaille. And furthermore he ordained by his patent lre^s and commanded to
make a fire upon eueri hye hille besides the rivers / and in low contrees for
to make hye bekenes of tymbre that if it so were that the aliens came unto the
la^d by night / that men should te^de ye bekenes that the contre might be
warned and come and met her enemies: And in ye same time deied Sir rogier
mortimer his uncle in the toure of London.

How the queen Isabel and sir Edward duke of Gwihenne her sone came to land at
Herewych / and how they dyde^. Capitulo CCvij
THe queen Isabell and sir edward her sone duke of guihe^ne: sir Edward of
wodeboke earl of kent and sir joha^ therles brother of henaud and her men drad
not the menace of the king ne of his traitors. for they trust all in goddys
grace. and came^ unto herewich in southfolk the xxiiij day of of Septe^bre: and
in the year of grace.M.ccc.xxvi. And the queen and sir Edward her sone sent
lre^s to ye maire and comminalte of London requyryng he^ that they should ben^
helpi^g in the quarrel and cause that they had bego^ne. that is to seye: to
destroy the traitors of ye reame / But none a^swere was sent again. wherefore
the queen and sir Edward her sone senten an other pate^t letter under her
seals. the tenor of which lettre here followed in this manner Izabell by the
grace of god queen of England / lady of Irla^d. and countess of pountyf. and
we Edward the eldest sone of the king of england / duke of Gwihenne. earl of
chestre and of Pou^tyf: and of Monstroille to the maire and to all the
conminalte of the cite of London sends grety^g for as much as we have before
ye time sent to you by our lettres how we become into this la^d with good array
and in good manner for the honor and profit of holy chirch and of our right
dear lord the king and all the Reame with all our might and power to keep and
maynten^ as we and all the good folk of the foresaid reame are holde^ to done.
And upon that we prayen you that ye would ben^ helpy^g to us in as much as ye
may in this quarrel. that is for the commune profit of all the Reaume. and we
have had none a^swere of ye forsaid lettres ne know not yowr will in that
party / wherefore we sent to you again and pray and charge you that ye bear
you so ayens us that we have no cause to grieve you: but that ye ben^ to us in
helpyng by all the mayes that ye may. For ye may well openly known that we and
all they that ben^ comen with us into this Reame thenken not to done tha^ all
thy^g if it lyked good and shall be for the commune proffyte of all the Reame:
and only to destroy Hugh the spencer our enemy and also enemy to all the
Reame of England. as ye well openly knows. Wherefore we pray you and charge
you in ye says that ye owe to owre lord the king and to us. that if the said
Hugh spe^cer our enemy come withinne your power that ye done him hastily to
ben^ taken and saufly kept* unto ye time till we have ordained of him owr
will: and that ye leave it not* in no manner wise as ye desire honor and
profit of us all and of all the Reame. Understanding well that if ye done
owr prayer and maundement. we shall the more be holden unto you and also ye
shull get for yowr self wurshypp and profit if ye send us hastily answer of
all yowr will. Yeue^ at Baldok the vj. day of Octobre / Which lettre erly in
the daweny^g of the day of saint Denis was taken upon the new cross in sheep
And many copies of the same lre^ were takked upon wyndowes and doors: and upon
other places in ye cite that all men passing by the way might see^ and read /
And in the same time king Edward was at london in the tower at his mete / and a
messagier came into the hasle and said that the queen Isabell was come to land
at Herewych: and had brought in her company sir Johan of Henaud and with him
me^ of arms without nombre: And wit that word Sir Hughe the spe^cer the fadre
spoke and said thus to the king. My most wurshypfull lord and king of England.
Now mow ye make good chere for certey^ly they ben^ all owres The king saw
this word confortable / notheles he was sorefull and pensyf in his heart / And
the king had not yet fulfylleth his mete: there came in the halle an other
messagier and said that the Queen Isabell was arrived at Herewych beside
yepswych in southfolk. Sir hugh the Spencer the fadre spoke and said to the
messauger in this manner / Tell me that ye have seyne / my fair friend is she
come with a stre^ghte: Certys sire soth for to say / she ne had in her
company but vij. ho^dred men of arms and with that word sir Hughe the
spencer the fadre cried with an hygh^ vois and said: Allas allas we been all
betrayed: for certys with so lyttel power she had never come to land: but folk
of this land were to her consent And therefore after the mete they took her
counceill and went toward walys for to arere ye walsshmen ayens queen Isabell
and edward her sone all for to fight / and so they were in purpose euericho^ /

How maistir Waltier stapilton bishop of Excestre that was the kings Tresorer
was beheded at London Capitulo / CCviij
ANd in the same time king Edward was sore adrad / lest men of london would
yield hem unto the queen Isabell and to her sone Edward: wherefore he sent
Maistir Waltier Stapylton his tresorer for to be wardeyne and keeper of the cite
of London with the mayre / And so he came to the Gylldehall of London / And
axed the keys of the yates of the Cite through virtue and strength of his
commyssyon / and would have had the keeping of the cite / But the co^munes
answered and said that they would keep the cite to the honor of king Edward
and of Isabell the queen / and of the duke the kings sone without any more:
The bishop was tho sore a^noyed and swore oath that they all should abye it
anon as king Edward were comen owte of walys / and the communes all anon^ of
the cite token the bisshopp and lad him amydes chepe / and there they smoten of
his head / and set his heed into his right hond. And after they beheded two of
his squyers that held with the bisshopp / And one of he^ was kalled Wyllia^ of
wall / that was the bisshoppes nevew That other was called Johan of pady^gton
/ And also they toke^ a burgys of London that was kalled Ioha^ marchall / that
was sir Hugh^ the spencers Spy the fadre: and smyten of his head also: And i^
that same time that same bishop had in london a fair towr in maky^g in his
closse upon the River of the Tamyse^ that was without temple bare: and him
faylled stone to make thereof an end / wherefore he commanded his men to gon^
to ye church of freres carmes. and there they token stone to make therewith the
tower / and much sand and mortar and old robous that was left / and for the
despyte that the bisshopp had done unto holy chyrch^: he and his two squyers
were buried in that sand / as though they had ben^ hou^des: and there they leyen
xi. wekes till that the queen Isabel sent her lettres / to the communes and
prayed hem that they would suffer and grant that the bishop might be taken
owte of that place and been buried at Excestre at his own church / and so he
and his two squyers were buried at saint Clemens church / wytoute temple bare /
And it was no wonder though ye bishop deyed an evil death / For he was a
coueytous man. and had with hy^ no mercy. and evil cou^ceilled ye king And
sone after was Arnold of Spaigne taken he that was asse^tent to have lad the
v.M. pound of silver i^ v. barelles ferryetes unto the douseperes of france
for to help and have the queen Isabell to her death and Edward her sone also:
And this Arnold was put to death without the cite of London:

How king Edward and sir Hugh^ the spencer and the earl of Arundell were taken
Capitulo CCix
WHen king Edward had sent maistir walter stapilton his tresorer into london
for to keep the cite on them aye^s the queen Isabel his wife and aye^s Edward
her sone Anon hy^ self took with him sir Hugh spencer the sone: and sir Johan

and token her way toward bristowe. and there the king abode a littel term. and

and took no leave of the stiward ne of none in ye kings household And went over
into walys for to arere the walssh men ayens dame Isabell the queen and the
duke her sone and the Earl of kente and sir Johan of Henaude / and they went
and purswed after hem / and her power e^cresed every day / so at the last the

that other side of the same hylle / And the false piled clerk Master Robert
baldock there fast besides hem / and were brought ayen^ into england as
almighty god would. and the king him self was in sauf keeping in the Castle of
Kenilworth. and hy^ kept sir He^ri that was sir Thomas brother of Lancaster.
And sir hugh^ spe^cer the fadre came and put hy^ in the queen's grace and sir
Edward her sone duke of Gwihenne: But sir Hugh^ spe^cer ye sone after the time
yt he was take would ete no manner mete no their dry^ke / for he wist to have
non^ mercy sauf only to be deed: And the queen and her counceyll tho had
ordained that he should have been done to death at london. But he was so feeble
for his moch^ fasting that he was deed almost: And therefore it was ordained
that he should have his judgment at herfort. and at a place of the toure his

Prophecye of Merlyn declared of king edward the sone of king Edward Cap / CCxi
OF this king Edward prophesied Merly^ and said that there should come a goot
out of Care that should have horns of silver / and a berde as with as snow /
and a doppe should come out of his nosethirles that should betoken much harm
hunger / and death of the people: and great loss of his la^d and that in the
begynny^g of his regne should be haunted much lecherye. He said soth. allas ye
time / for king Edward that was king Edwardes sone was borne at canaruan in
Walys / for soth he had horns of silver and a berde as snow. when he was made
prince of walys / so much he yafe hy^ to riote and felonye / And soth said
Merlyn in his prophecye / that there should come out of his nose a doppe for in
his time was great hunger among ye pour people: and strong deth^ among the
rich that deyde in strange land with mochel sorwe. and in werre in Scotland /
and afterward he lost scotland and gascoigne: And whilles that him self was
king. there was much lecherye hau^ted And also merly^ told and said that this
goot should seche ye flour of life and of death. and he said sothe / for he
spoused Isabel the ky^ges daughter of france / And in his time Merly^ said
that there should be made brugges of folk upon dyches of ye see: and that was
well seen at bannokkesborne in scotland wha^ he was disco^fyted there of the
scotts And merly^ told also that stones should fall from castelles and many
towns should be made pley^ / and he said soth^: for wha^ king Edward was
discomfited in Scotland. and came tho southward. ye scotts besieged the
castelles and did hem moch^ harm and brent towns unto the hard erth^. And
afterward Merly^ said that an egle should come out of Cornewaille that should
have fetheres of gold / that of pride should have no piere: and he should despise
lords of blood: and after deye through a bear at Gauersise. and that prophecye
was full well know and fond sothe. For by the egle is understood sir Piers of
Ganastone. that tho was earl of Cornewaille^ that was a wonder proud man that
despised the baronage of england* but afterward he was beheded at gauersichet
through ye earl of Lancaster and through the earl of warrewyk. And merlyn told
that in his time yet should seem yt the bear should bre^ne. and that bataill
should be upon an arm of the sea in a field araied like a shield / where should
deye many white hedes. and he said sothe / for by the brennyng of the bear is
betokened great dread through cutty^g of swerd at that bataill ordained i^ a
field as a shield upon an arm of ye see. is betokened the bata^lle of mytone
For there came^ the scotts in manner of a shield in manner of a wynge and slew
upon swalle men of relygyo^ ^ prestes and seculers wherefore ye scotts kalled
that bataille in despyte of englysshme^ the white bataille: And after Merly^
said that ye foresaid bear should done the goot much harme^ and that should be
upon the southwest also upon his blood and said also that the goot should lose
moch^ dele of his land / till ye time that shame should hy^ overcome. and tha^
he should clothe him wit a lyo^s sky^ne and should wy^ne ayen^ that he had
lost. and much more through people that should come out of the northwest. that
should make hy^ been adrad. and him avenge of his enemies through cou^ceil of ij.
owls that first should be in peril to be undone / And that ij. owls should
wend over ye see into strange la^d / and there they should dwell till a
certey^ time: and after they should come into england ayene And the.ij. owls
should do moch^ harm unto many one / and that they should cownceylle the got
for to meve werre ayens the foresaid bear: and that the goot and the owls
should come unto an arm of the sea at Burton up trent and should we^de over:
and that for dread the bear should flee with a swan in his company unto bury
toward ye north through an unkind owtputter / and that the swan tha^ should be
slain with sorwe: and the bear should be slayn^ full nygh^ his own nest that
should sto^de upon Pou^frete^ upon whom the son shall shede his bemes / and
many folk him shall seche for the mochel virtue / And he said full sothe for
the good Earl thoa^s of Lancaster was borne in ye northwest and cosyn to the
king and sone of his uncle* And by law he made ye king lose much la^d. the
which had purch^ased wylfully^ till at the last the king thereof took shame and
him self filled with cruelte* And after he gate ayene that he had lost and
much more thereto / through folk that he let assemble out of ye northwest that
made him to ben^ adrad and aue^ged hy^ of his barons through cou^ceill of sir
hughe the spe^cer the fadre and of sir Hugh^ the sone that beforne were
outelawed of e^glo^d for her wykkednesse But afterward came ayene into England
sir hugh^ the spencer the fadre out of france / and so moch^ counceilled the

outeputter / And also sir symo^d ward earl of york they came and met with
Thomas of lancaster wit an huge company: and hem there discomfited / and in

a spear in the foundeme^t: And the good earl Thomas was take and lad unto
pounfrete And tho he was beheded beside his own castle: but afterward many

were done to death for saint Thomas quarrel of Lancastre. people of many lands
became the bolder for to meue werre upon the king / for her blood was turned to
many and diverse nacyons.

And afterward Merlyn told and said that the foresaid owls should done much
harm unto the flour of life and of death: And they should bring her unto much
disease / so that she should goo and we^de oueruer the sea into france for to

the harm that they had done to quen^ Isabell his suster. Wherefore through her
ordenau^ce and consent of the spencers the queen Isabell went over see into

and the gentill Earl of Henaude that if they wit her help might destroy and

wherefore the quen^ jsabell and sir Edward her sone and sir edmond of Wodestoke
the kings brother of England and sir Johan of Henaude and sir Rogier mortymer

spytouse death as before is said and her conpanye. and also for the great
falsenesse that they did to the king Edward and to his people: and Merly^ said
also more that the got should be put into great disese and in great anguissh^
and in great sorwe he should led his life / and he said soth: for after the
time that king Edward was take he was put into ward till that ye spe^cers were
put unto the death / And also for encheson yt he nold not come unto his own
parliament at london as he had ordained and assigned him self and to his

king should done Sum of the barons of England came^ and yelde^ up her homages
unto him for hem. and for all the other of the reaume in the day of Conversion
of saint paul / and in the year of his regn^ xx: and they put him out of his
ryalte for evermore: and ever he lived his life afterward in moch^ sorwe and
anguissh^

Of kind Edward the thridde after the conquest Capitulo CCxij
And after this king Edward of Carnarvan reigned sir Edward of wy^desore his

How king Edward went to sta^ hope for to mete the scotts Capitulo CCxiij

said the scripture in despite of englysshmen

Long berde hertles: pey^ted hood wytlees / gay cote graceles / makes england

How the Englysshmen stoped ye Scotts in the park of Stanhope: and how they
turned ayen^ into scotland Capi. CCxiiij
ANd at that time the scotts had assembled all her power and camen into
England and quelled and robbed all that they might take / and also brenten and
destroyed all the north contre through out till that they came^ to the park of
Stanhope in wiredale and there the scotts helden hem i^ a buscheme^t: but when
the king had herd through certain aspies where the scotts were. anon right
wit his host besieged hem withyn the forsaid park so that the scotts wiste
nevyr whereto gon^ out: but only unto her harms / and they abyde^ in the park
xv. days. and vitaylles hem failled in every side: so that they weren greatly
epired of her bodies / And since yt Brute came first into Brytaign^ unto this
time was never seyne so fair an host: what of englysshmen and of aliens and of
men of foot. the which ordained hem for to fight with the scotts through engyn
of sir Henry Earl of Lancastre. and of sir Johan Henaude: yt would have gone
over the water of with for to have fought with the scotts. But sir Rogier
mortimer consented not thereto / for he had preuely taken mede of ye scotts hem
for to help that they might went ayene unto her own contre / and the same
Mortymer cou^ceilled so moch^ thoa^s of Brotherton^ the Earl marchall yt was
king Edwardes uncle. that the forsaid Thomas should not assemble at that time
unto the scotts and he assented / but he wist not the doy^g bitwen^ the
scotts and the forsaid mortymer / and for encheso^ yt he was marchall of
England and to hy^ parteyned ever the vauntwarde he sent hastily to the earl of
Lancastre. and to sir Ioha^ of henaude yt they should not fight upon ye scotts
in prejudice and harmy^g of hy^ and his fee. and if they did that they should
sto^de to her own peril. and the forsaid his bataille. at the rere doos of ye
earl of Lancaster for to have fought with him and with his folk if he had meved
for to fight with the scotts / and in this manner he was deceived and wist
nothing of this treson: and thus was the king pri^cipaly deceived / and when it
was night Mortymer that had wach^ for to keep of the host that night
destourbled ye wach^ that no thy^g must be done / and in the mean while ye
scotts stele by night toward her own contre as fast as they might / and so
was the king falsely betrayed that we^de that all the Traitors of his land
had been brought to an e^de as it was said before. Now here ye lords how
traitoursly the king was deceived and how mervously and boldly ye scotts did
of werre. for James douglas with CC / hundred men of arms ryden thurghowte the
host of king Edward: And in the same night the Scotts skaped from her place
toward her own^ contre as is above said. till that they c^men to the kings
pawillo^ and quelled there many men in her beds and cried some time naward
Naward. And an other time a do^glas a donglas. wherefore the king that was in his
pauillo^ and moch^ other folk were wonder sore affraied / But blysshed be
almighty god the king was not taken: and in great peril was tho the reaume of
England: and that night the moon shone full clear and bright and for all the
kings men the scotts escaped harmeles / and in the morwe when the king wist
that the scotts were ascaped into her contre / he was wonder sorry and full
hertely wept. and yet wist he not who hy^ had done that treson: but that falls
treson was full well y know a good while after as the story tells: The king
edward came again tho to york sorwefull: and his host departed and every man
went into his own contre with full hevy chere and morning semblant. and the
Henaudes took her leave and went unto her own contre: and the king for her
trauaille hugely hem rewarded and for encheson of that vyage y^ king dispe^dyd
much of his tresour and wasted. And in that time were seyne two mones in the
firmament that one was clear and that other was derke as me^ might tho see
thurghoute the world ad a great debate was that same time ayens the pope Johan
the xxij aftyr saint Petre. and the emperor of almaigne tho made hi^ emperor
ayens the popes will that tho held his see at Auymo^ wherefore that e^perour
made his cry at rome and ordained an other pope that hight Nycholas / that was
a friar menour / and that was aye^s ye right of holy chyrch^ wherefore he was
kursed: and the power of that other pope sone was leid and for encheson that
such^ mervailles were seyne Men said that the world was nygh^ at an end

Of the death of king Edward of Carnarvan Cap: ccxv
And now turn we ayene to sir Edward of Carnarvan / that was king sometime of
England. and was put a down^ of his dignite Allas for his tribulacion and sorw
that hy^ befell through falls cou^ceill that he leued and trusted upon to moch^
that afterward were destroyed through her falsenesse as god would. And this
Edward of Carnarvan was in ye castle of Berkley under the keeping of sir morys
of berkeley / and sir Johan of Mautrevers and to he^ he made his co^play^t of
his sorwe and of his disese and oftetymes he axed of his wardeyns what he had
trespaced aye^s dame Isabell his wife and sir Edward his sone that was made
new king that they would naught visit him / Tho a^sweryd one of his wardeyns
/ my worthy lord displese you not that I shall tell you. the encheson is for
it is done hem to understood that if my lady your wif came any thing nigh you
that ye would her strangle and quelle and also that ye would do to my lord your
sone that same. Tho answered he with simple chere: allas allas am I not in
prison / and all at your own will: now god almighty it wot I thought it
nevyr. And now I would that I were deed / so would god that I were. for tha^
were all my sorwe passed

Hit was not long after that the king through counsel of mortimer granted
the ward and keeping of sir Edward his fadre to sir Thomas to journey and to the
foresaid sir Johan Mautrevers through the kings lettre. and put owte holy the
forsaid sir Moryce: of the ward of the king. and they took and lad the king
unto the castle of Corfe / the which castle the foresaid king Edward hated as
any death / and they kept him there saufly till it came unto sei^t mathewes day
in Septembre in the year of grace thousand three hundred xxvij / that the
forsaid sir Rogier Mortymer sent the manner of the death how and in what wise
Edward of carnarva^ should be done to death / And anon as the forsaid Thomas
and Johan had seyne the lettre and commandment / they made king Edward of
carnarvan good chere and good solas as they might. at that soper and no thing
the king wyste of these traitrie And when ye time was for to goo to bed / the
king went unto his bed / and lay and slept fast. and as the king lay and
slept / the traitors falls forsworn ayens her homage and her feaute ^^me^
pryuely into the kings chamber and her company wit he^ / and leyden an hughe
table upon his womb and with men pressede^ and helden fast a down iiij
corners of the table upon his body / wherewith the good man awoke and was wonder
sore adrad to be deed there and slain: and turned his body up sodowne. Tho
token the false traitors and as wode tyrau^ts an horn^ and put it into his
fou^dement as deep as they might / and token a spite of coper bre^nyng and put
it through the horn into his body: and oftetymes rolled therewith his boweles /
and so they quelled her lord that no thy^g was perceived and aftyr he was
entered at gloucestre.

How king Edward spowsed Phelip the Erlis doughtyr of henawde at york Cap.
cc.xvij
ANd aftyr Cristmasse tho next swyng sir Johan of Henaude brought with him
Phelipp his brothers doughtyr that was earl of Henawde his nece into England /
and king Edward spowsed her at york wit mochel honor: and sir Johan of Bothum
bishop of Ely and sir william of Melton Erchebisshop of york songen the mass
that sunday in the even of Conversion of saint Paul. In the year of grace a
M.CCCxxvij / but for encheso^ that the king was but young and tender of age when
he was crouned full many wrongs were done while his fadre lived / for e^cheson
that he trowed ye cou^ceilliers that were falls about him that cou^ceilled him
to done other wise than reason would wherefore great harm was done unto the
reaume and to the king. and all men directed it the hynges deed: and it was not
so almighty god wo^e wherefore it was ordained at the kings crownyng that the
king for his tender age should be governed by xij great lords of England
without which no thing should be done: that is for to seye. The erchebisshop
of Caunterbury* the erchebisshop of york: the bishop of wynchestre and the
bishop of Hereford. The earl of Lancastre The earl Marchall and the earl of
Kent. that were the ky^ges uncles: and the earl of Garenne / Sir Thomas wake:
Sir Henry of percy. Sir Oliver wyngham and ^oha^ of Roos barons / All these
were sworn trewly for to cou^ceill ye king And they should a^swere every year
in the parliament of that / that should be done in the time of that gouernaille /
but that ordenau^ce was sone vndon^ / and that was much loss and harm to all
england for that king and all the lords that should govern hy^ were governed
and ruled aftyr the ky^ges modyr dame Isabell: and by sir Rogier mortimer. and
as they would all thing was done both among high^ and low / and they toke^
unto hem castelles tounes lands and re^tes in great harm and loss to the
croune and of ye kings state out of mesure

How ye pees was made bitwene the Englysshmen and the scotts and also of
iustyfye^g of Troillebastone Capitulo CCxvii
THe king Edward at witsontyde. the second year of his regne through cou^ceill
of his modyr: and of sir Rogier mortimer ordained a parliament at Northampton.
at the which parliament the king through there cou^ceill and non^ other of the
la^d withy^ age granted to been accorded wit the scotts in this manner that
all ye feautes and homages that ye scotts should do unto ye crown of england
foryafe he^ unto the scotts for euyrmore by his chartre ensealed / And
ferthermore an endenture was made of the scotts unto king Edward that was king
He^ryes sone. which e^de^ture they called it Rageman / in the which were
contained all the homages and feautes / First of ye king of Scotland and of all
the prelates Earls and barons of the Reaulme of Scotland with her seals set
there on. and other chartres and remembrau^ces that king Edward and his barons
had of her right i^ ye reame of scotland. it was foryeve hem ayene. holy
church: and also with ye blake cross of scotland. the which the good king
edward conquered in scotland / and brought it out of the abbey of Scone: that
is a full precious Relic* And also ferther more he relesed and foryafe all
the lands that the barons of england had in scotland by old conquest. And
this pees for to be hold and last the scotts were bound unto the king in xxx
/ thousand pownde of silver to be paid withy^ three year / that is to seye every
year x.M. pownde by evyn porcyons / and ferthermore above all this they spoke
bitwen^ the parties above said that David Driton^tier that was robert the brus
is sone the false tiraunt and traitor and falls forswore ayens his oath that
arose ayens his liege lord ye noble king edward and falsely made hy^ king of
scotland that was of age of v / year And so through his kursed cou^seill dauyd
spoused at berewyke dame Ioha^ of ye tour that was king edwardes suster as ye
geest tellyth upon Mary magdalene day In ye year of grace a MCCC. and xxviij to
ye great harm and empeiri^g of all the ky^ges blod whereof yt gentle lady was
come. Allas the time For wonder moch^ was that fair damysel disparged since
that she was married aye^s all the common asse^te of England: and fro the time
that Brute had conquered Albion and nempned the lord aftyr his own name
Britaigne that now is kalled England after the name of Engyst. And so was the
reaume of Scotland holden of the reaulme of england and of the crown by feaute
and by homage: For brute conquered that land and yafe it to Albanak his second
sone: and he kalled the land Albayne aftyr his own name. so that the heirs
that camen after hy^ helde^ of Brute and of his heirs the kings of Bretaigne
by feaute and homage and from that time unto this king edward / ye reame of
scotland was holden of the reame of England by feautes and seruyces above said
/ as the chronicles of England and of scotland beren witness more plenarly And
accursed be ye time that this parliament was ordained at Northampto^ / for
through falls cou^ceyll there was falsely disherited and yet he was withyn age.
and yet when king Edward was put a down of his Royalte of e^glo^d yet men put
hy^ not out of the feautes and seruyces of the reaulme of scotland ne of the
fraunchises disherited him for evermore And notheles the great lords of
england and were aye^s to conferme the pees and the tremes above said. sauf
only queen isabell that was the kings modyr Edward and the bishop of Ely and
lord mortimer. but reason and law would not that a fynall pees should be made
between he^ wytoute the common assent of England

Of the debate that was bitwene quen^ Isabell and sir Henry earl of lancaster
and of Leicestre and of the ridy^g to Beford Capi. CCxvij
When the forsaid david had spoused dame Iohane of the tour in ye town of
Berewyke as before is said / the scotts in despyte of ye englysshme^ called
dame joha^ the countess make pees for ye corwardyse pees that was ordained:
but ye kings person bare the wit and blame with wrong of the maky^g of ye
accord. and all was done through the queen and Rogier mortymer / and it was not
long aftyr that ye queen Isabell ne took into her own hand all ye lordship
of Pou^frete almost / and all the lands that were of value that apperteyned to
the croune of e^glo^d so yt the king had not for to dispe^de but of his uses
and of his escheker / For the quen^ jsabell and mortymer had a great meyn^ of
her retenau^ce. that followed evermore the ky^ges courte^ and went and took at
ye ky^ges pryse for her penny worthes at good sheep. wherefore ye co^tre that they
came^ ynne were full sore adrad and almost destroyed Tho begone the commynalte
of England for to hate Isabell the queen that so moch^ loved her when she came
ayene for to purswe the false traitors the spencers from france. And that same
time the false traitor Robert of Holand that betrayed his lord sir Thoa^s of
Lancastre / was tho delyured owte of prison* and was wonder pryue with the
queen Isabell / and also with Rogier the Mortimer. but that availled him but
littell for he was take at Michelmasse. that tho came next sewyng after / as he
rode toward the queen jsabell to London: and sir Thoa^s wither smote of his
head besides the town of saint Albones: and this sir Thomas dwelled tho wit
sir Henry earl of Lancastre. and he put him in hydyng for dread of the queen
For she loved him wonder moch^ and prayed unto the king for hy^ that the same
thomas must ben^ ex^^^ed out of england. and the noble earl sir Henry of
lancaster had often times herd the common clamor of the englysshmen: of the
diseses that were done in England. and also for diverse wrongs that were done
among the commune people. of the which the king bare the blame with wrong.
for he nas but full young and te^dre of age And thought as a good man for to
done away and slake the sklau^dre of the kings person if that he migh^t in
any manner wise So as the king was thereof nothy^g gylty. wherefore he was in peril
of ^^th and lymme And so he assembled all his retenau^ces and went and spoke
unto the^ of the kings honor and also for to amend his estate: And sir thomas
brotherton earl Marchall. and sir Edmond of wodestoke that were the kings
uncles. and also men of London made her oath him for to may^ten i^ that same
querell And her cause was this / that the king should hold his housold and his
meyny as a king ought for to done and have also his ryalte: and that the queen
Isabell should deliver out of her hand into the kings ho^de all manner
lordshyppes rentes towns and castelles that apperteyned to the crown of
england as other queen's had done before her: and meddle with none other thing /
And also that sir Rogier mortimer should dwell upon his own lands: for the
whych^ lands he had help disherite much people / so that common people were

through whose counceill the ordenau^ce that was made at the kings coronacion was
put a down. that is to seyne that the king for amendment and helping of the
reaume and in honor of hy^ should be gouernyd and ruled by xij the gretest and
wysest lords of all ye reaume: and without hem should nothing be granted ne
done ne said. for the which couenaunts malycyously were put a down fro the
king: wherefore many harms shames and reproues have fall unto the king and his
reaume / and that is vndyrsto^d for asmoche as Edward sometime king of England
was ordained by the asse^t of the comynaulte in plain parliament for to be
vndyr the ward and governance of Henry earl of Lancastre his cosyn for
savacion of his body. he was take owte of the castle of Kenilworth there yt he
was in ward: and through counseill of queen Isabell and of the mortymer
without consent of any parliament they took and lad hy^ there that nevyr after
non^ of his kynred might wit him speak ne see / and after him traitoursly
mordred. for whose death a foul slaundre arose thurghoute all crystendome when it
was done / And also the tresour that sir Edward of carnarvan had left in many
places in england and in Walys were wasted and born^ away withou / te the will
of king edward his sone in destructyon of him and of all his folk Also through
whose cou^seil that the king yafe up the ki^gdome of scotland: for the which
reame the kings au^cestres had full sore y trauailled: and so did many a noble
man for her right and was deliured unto David yt was robert the Brus son^ all

How king Edward went over the sea for to do his homage unto the king of
France for the Duchye of Gwyhenne Capitulo CC / xix
IT was not long after yt the king of France through cou^ceil of his
douseperes ^ent to king Edward of england that he should come to Paris and done
his homage as reason it would for the Duchye of Gwyhenne and so through cou^ceyll
of the lords king Edward went over the sea and at ascencion tide he came unto
Paris the thridde year of his regne for to do his homage unto the king of
France. who vnderfeng his homage: and made of him much joy and wurship / but
wha^ king Edward had made his homage / hastily he was sent fore into England
through the queen Isabell his modre / and anon^ he came ayene into England upon
witsonday / without any taking leave of the king of France. wherefore he was
wonder wroth

How sir Rogier Mortimer bare him prowdely and so hye Capi. CCxx
ANd now shull ye here of sir Rogier Mortymer of wingmore that desired and
coueyted to be at an hygh^ astate. so that the king granted him to be called
Earl of the march^ through out all his lordshyp. And he becam^ so proud and so
hauteyne that he would lose and forsake the name that his auncestres had ever
before. and for that encheson he let hem kalle Earl of the march. and non^ of
the co^munes of England durst call him by none other name for he was called so
through ye kings cry that men should kalle him earl of the march: And the
mortymer bare him tho so hanteyne and so proud that wonder it was for to wit.
and also disgysed hy^ with wondre rich clothes out of all manner reason. both of
shaping and of weryng: whereof the Englysshme^ had great wo^dyr how and in what
manner he might co^tryue or find such^ manner pride: and they said among hem
all conmunely that his pride should not long endure. And the same time sir
Geffrey mortimer the yo^g yt was the mortimers sone let him kalle king of folly
/ and so it befell aftyrward in deed: for he was so full of pride and of
wrecchednesse yt he held a round table in walys to all men that thither would
come. and cou^trefeted the manner and the doy^g of king arthures table but
openly he failled. for the noble king artur was the most worthy lord of
reno^me that was in all the world in his time: and yet came never none such^
aftyr. for all the noble knights in criste^dome of deed of arms a losed
dwelled wit king Arthure. and held hy^ with their lord / and yt was well seen /
for he conquered in bataille a romayne yt was kalled Frolle / and get of hy^
the reame of France and quelled hy^ with his ho^des. and also he faught with a
geau^t that was called Dynabus and quelled him that had rauisshed the fair
Eleyne yt was king Hoeles nece of littel britaigne / and aftirward he quelled
in bataill the emperor of Rome yt was called Lucye / that had assembled aye^s
king Arthur. for to fight with him so moch^ people of Romans. and Phehis / and
of sarasyus that no man cowde he^ nombre. and he disco^fyted hem all: as the
story of hy^ tells / and in that same time common loos sprung in england
through coniecty^g and ordenau^ce of the freres prechours that sir Edward of
Carnarvan that was king edwardes fadre. of whom the geest tells / sayden that
he was a live in the castle of Corfe wh^erfor all ye co^munes all most of
England were in sorwe and in dread whethyr that it were so or not for they
wyste^ not how traitoursly the Mortimer had hi^ done mordred

How Edmond of Wodestoke that was earl of Kent and the kings brother Edward of
Ca^^a^uan / was beheded at wy^chestre Capitulo CCxxi
ANd upon a time it befell so that sir Edmond of wodestoke earl of Kent spoke
unto the pope Johan the xxij. at avyuion^ and said that almighty god had
oftetymes done for Thomas love of Lancaster many great miracles to many men and
women that weren through diverse maladies undone as unto the world / and through
his prayer they were brought unto her health. and so sir Edmond prayed the pope
hertely. that he would grant hi^ grace that the forsaid Thomas might be
translatyd. but the ^ope said nay. that he should not be translated unto the
time that he were bettyr certefyed of the clergy of England. and sent by her
obedience what thing god had done for the love of Thomas of lancaster aftir the
suggestyon that the foresaid Earl of Kent had unto hy^ made. and when this
edmond saw that he might not speed of his purpose. as touching the translacyon
/ he prayed him of his cou^ceill as touching sir Edward of Carnarva^ his
brother^ and said that not long a gone he was king of England. what thing
might best be done as touching his delyurance sith that a commune fame is
through england that he is a life and hole and sauf. When the pope herd him
tell that sir edward was a lyve / he commanded the earl upon his benyson that
he should help with all the power that he might him to be deliured owte of
prison: and save his body in all manner that he might / And for to breng this
thing to an end he assoilled hy^ and his company a pena and culpa and all tho
that help to his deliurance / Tho took Edmond of wodestoke his leave of the
pope and came again into England / and when sir Edmond was comen. sum of the
freres preschours came and said that sir edward his brother yet was a live in
the castle of corf vndyr the keeping of sir thomas gurnay. Tho sped hy^ the
foresaid edmond as fast as he might till yt he came unto ye castle of Corfe:
and spoke so fair wit Johan dauerill that was conestable of the same castle.
and yafe hy^ rich^ yeftes for to have acquytau^ce of hy^ and to know of his
cou^ceill. and thus it befell that the forsaid sir Edmond prayed spicially to
tell hy^ preuely of his lord his brother sir Edward if that he lived or were
deed / and if he were a live he prayed of him ones to have a sight And this sir
Ioha^ Dauerill was an hygh^ herted man and full of courage. and answered
shortly unto sir Edmond* and said. that sir edward his brother was in hele and
under his keeping: and durst show him unto no man. sith yt was defended hy^ in
ye kings half Edward that was Edwardes sone of Carnarva^. and also through
commandment of quen^ Isabell the ky^ges modyr / and of sir rogier the
Mortymer that he should show his body unto no manner man of ye world sauf only
unto thay^ upon peine of life and lymme and to disherityng of his heirs for
evermore. But the false traitor falsely lied. for he was not in his ward. but
he was take thens and lad unto ye castle of Berkelee through Thomas garnay by
conmau^dement of the Mortimer till that he was deed as before is said / but sir
Edmond of Wodestoke wist no thy^g that edward his brother was deed: whereupon he
took a lettre unto the forsaid sir Ioha^ and prayed him hertely that he would
take it unto king edward his brother as to his worthi lord / and he vnderfeng
the lre^ of hy^: and behight hi^ for to do his message wtoute any manner faill
and with that sir Edmond took of him his leave the^s of ye forsaid Johan and went
tho in his own^ co^tre and lorshypp in Kent that he had there* and anon as
this johan wist that sir edmo^ was gon^ into kent his own lordshyp. anon^ he
went in all the have that he might fro the castle of Corfe and came unto sir
rogier the mortimer and took hy^ the lettre yt sir edmond of wodestoke earl of
Kent had take him closed and ensealed with his own seal. and when sir rogier had
vnderfe^g the lettre. he unclosed ye lre^ and saw what was contained theryn
and began it for to read. whereof ye begy^ny^g was this. wurshippes and
reuere^ces wit brothers legau^ce and subiectione Sir knight wurshipfull and
dear brother if it you plese I pray you hertely yt ye be of good confort / for
I shall so ordeyne for you that sone ye shull come out of pryso^ and be
delyured of yt disese yt ye ben in. and your great lorship shall vndrestande
that I have to me co^senty^g almost all the great lords of England wit all her
apparaille that is to say with armure with tresour without nombre / for to
maynten^ and help your quarrel ferforth that ye shull be king ayene as ye were
before: and that they all have sworn^ to me upon a book: as well prelates as
earls and barons / When sir Rogier the mortymer saw and understood ye might and
the strength^ of the letter anon for wrath his heart began to swelle / and evil
heart bare toward sir Edmond that was earl of Kent / and so wit all the haste
that he might he went unto dame Isabell the quen^ that was the ky^ges modre.
and showed her Sir edwardes lre^ and his will and his purpose / and how he had
coniectyd and ordained to put a down king Edward of wy^desore her sone of the
ryalte and of his ki^gdome / Now certes sir rogier quod the queen has sir
Edmond done so / by my fadre soul quod she / I wull be thereof avenged if that
god grant me life / and that in a short time / And anon with that the queen
Isabel went unto king edward her sone there that he was at the parliament at
wy^chestre for to have amended the wrongs and trespaces that were done among
the people in his reaume And tho took she and showed him the lettre that sir
edmond of Wodestoke earl of Ke^t had made and ensealed with his own seal. and
bad upon her benyson that she should be avenged upon him: as upon his dedely
enemy Tho was the queen so wroth toward sir edmond earl of Kent / and cesyd
never to pray unto her sone till that he had sent in all have aftyr him: And
upon that the king sent by his lettres after sir edmond of wodestoke that he
should come and speak with him at wy^chestre all manner thing left / And when sir
edmond saw that the king sent after hy^ with his lettres ensealed / he hasted
hy^ in all that he might till that he came to wynchestre: but tho the queen
wist that Sir edmond was come unto wy^chestre. anon^ she prayed and so fast
went unto king edward her sone that Sir edmond the good Earl was arestyd
anon. and led unto bar before Robert of Henaude that was coroner of the
kings household: and he associated unto hy^ sir Rogier the Mortimer: and tho
speak the forsaid robert and said Sir edmond earl of Kente ye shall understand
that it is to done us to wit. and principaly unto owr liege lord sir edward
king of England that almighty god save and keep that ye be his dedely enemy
and a traitor / and also a common enemy unto the reaume. and that ye have
been about many a day for to make preuy delyuera^ce of sir edward some time
king of England your brother the which was put a down of his rialte by
common assent of all the lords of england / in pesing of owr lord the ky^ges
astate: and also of his reaulme / Tho a^sweryd the good man and said for soth
sir vnderstonderstondeth well that I was never traitor to my king ne to ye
reame. and that I do me on god and on all the world: And ferthermore by the
kings leave I shall it preue and defend as a man owght to do. Tho said Mortimer
/ sir edmond it is so fer forth y know yt it may not well be gaynesaid. and
that in p^sence of all that here ben^ it shall be well prouyd. Now has this false
mortimer the sam^ lettre that sir Edmond had take to sir Johan Daueryll in the
castle of Corff. for to took unto king Edward his brother / that sir edmond
wist not of ne supposed no thing that sir Johan Daueryll had ben^ so falls to
delyure his lre^ in such wise to the Mortimer and thought no manner thing of
that lettre. and said to sir Edmond and showed a letter sealyd and axed him if
he knew that lettre and the seal / This sir Edmond looked thereon and avysed him
long on the printe of the seal. for he might not see the lettre withy^forth
what was thery^ / and wist well that it was his seall. and thought yt it had be
some letter that had bore no great charge: and thought no thing of that other
lettre / and said openly in hery^g of hem all. ye forsooth this is my seall / I
will it not forsake / Loo quod the mortimer. Sires ye heren all what he has
said and that he knowelecheth that this is his lettre and his seal / and now ye
shul here all what is contained theryn / and than this mortimere opened the
lettre that he had folde^ a fore to gedre. and red it opy^li word by word in
heryng of he^ all^ And when the letter was red he sayd^ ^o sires ye have herd
all what is here written. and that he had knowlegyd that this is his letter and
his seal. and may not go there from And than they all cried and yafe dome that
he should be honged and draw / and his heed smyt of in manner of a traitor and
he and his heirs disherited for evermore: and so he was lad forth and put into
prison And when this was done and the quen^ wist that he was dampened by wey of
law. both of life and of lymme / and his heirs disherited for evermore /
through open knowlegyng in pleyne court: wherefore he^ thought that were good that
the forsaid sir edmond were hastly put to death without wityng of ye king / or
else the king lyghtely would foryeue him his death: and tha^ that should turn
he^ to much sorwe so as he was empeched and anon the queen through cou^ceyll
of the mortymer / and without any other cou^ceil sent in have to the baillyfs
of wy^chestre / that they should smite of sir Edmondes head of wodestoke earl of
Kent without any manner abidy^g or respite up pain of life and lymme / and
that he should have none other execucion be cause of tarieng natwithstandyng the
judgment: Tho toke^ the baillifs sir Edmond out of prison / and lad hy^
besides the castle of wynchestre: and there they made a gonge fermer smite of
his head. for none other man durst it done. and so deyed he there. allas the
time: that is to seye / the x. day of octobre / the thridde year of king
edwardes regne. and when the king wist thereof he was wonder sorry / for he louyd
hi^ well / and let entier him at the friar minours at wy^chestre /

Of the death of sir Rogier mortimer earl of the march Capitulo CCxxij
ANd so it befell at that time sir Rogier Mortimer Earl of the march^ was so
proud and so hauteyne that he held no lord of the reame his pere and tho
became he so covetous that he followed dame Isabel the queen's court that was
king Edwardes modyr / and besete his penny worthes wit the officiers of ye
queen's household in the same manner that the ky^ges officiers did. and so he made
his taky^g as touchy^g vitailles. and also of cariages: and all he did for
cause of spe^ces: and for to gadre tresour / and so he did without nombre in all that he might / Tho made he hi^ wo^dre secret with ye quen^ jsabel: and so
moch^ lorship and retinue had that all the great lords of england of hy^ were
adrad. whefore ye king and his cou^ceill toward him were angry and ordained
among he^ to vndon^ him through pure reso^. and law for cause that king edward
that was the kings fadre traytoursly through he^ was mordred / in the castle of
Berkelee as before is said more plenarli in ye CCxvij chapitre of this book /
and some that were of the kings cou^ceill loved ye mortimer / and told him in
pryuete how yt the king and his cou^ceill were about from day to day him for
to she^d and vndon^: wherefore the mortimer was sore a^noyed and a^gry as ye
deuel aye^s he^ that were of the ky^ges counceil: and said yt he would ben^
aue^ged how so ever he took on. yt was not long afterward yt king edward and
dame Phelip his wife and dame jsabel the kings modre / and sir rogier the
Mortimer ne went unto Nothy^gham there for to soiourne / and so it befell that
the quen^ jsabell through cou^ceill of ye mortimer took to her the keys of the
yates of the castle of Nothingha^ so yt no man might come nethyr in ne out by
night: but through the commau^deme^t of the mortimer. neither the king / ne
non^ of his cou^ceill. and at yt time it fell so yt the Mortimer for malice
that he had toward the kings men / and pryncipally ayens hem that had him
accused to the king of ye death of sir Edward his fadre / preuely a cou^ceill
was take bitwen^ quen^ Isabell and the Mortymer. and ye Bishop of Lincoln /
and sir Symo^d of Bereford. and sir Hugh^ of Ttru^piton: and othyr pryue of his
cou^seill. for to vndon^ hem all that had accused the mortymer unto the king of
his fadres death / of treson and of felonye. wherefore all tho that were of the
ky^ges cou^ceill wha^ they wist of the Mortymers castyng / preuely came to king
Edward and seyde^ / that the Mortymer would he^ destroy for cause that they
had accused him of king Edwardes death his fadre. and prayed him that he would
maynten he^ in her right And these were the lords to purswe this quarrel: sir
wyllia^ mou^tagu / Sir Hu^frey de bogun. Sir Willya^ his brother. Sir Rouf of
stafford: Sir Robert of Herford: Sir wyllia^ of Clinton / Sir Ioha^ neuyll of
horueby / and many othyr of her consent: and all these sworn upon a book to
maynten^ the quarrel in as moch^ as they might / and it befell so aftyr that
sir Wylliam Montagu ne none of the ky^ges fre^des must not ben^ herburghed i^
the castle for the Mortimer: but went and token her herburghes in diverse
places in the town of Nothyngham. and tho were they sore adrad / left that
the Mortymer should hem destroy / And in have there came unto king Edward Sir
wylliam Mowntagu there that he was in the castle. and preuely told him that he
ne none of his company should (...) taken the Mortymer wythowte cownceyl and
help of Wyllyam of Eland Conestable of the same castle: Now certes quod the
king I love you well. and therefore I cownceyll you that ye goo unto the foresaid
conestable and command him in my name that he be yowr friend and your help
for to take the mortymer all thy^g left. upon peril of life and lymme: Tho
said willyam Mountagu / sir mi lord grant mercy Tho went the foresaid Mountagu
and came to the conestable of the castle. and told him the kings will And the
Conestable answered and said that the kings will should be done and fulfilled
in as moch^ as he might / and that he would not spare for no manner death. and
so he swore and made his oth^ Tho said the foresaid sir Willya^ mou^tagu to the
Conestable in hery^g of all hem that were helpyng unto the quarrel / Now
certes dear friend: us behooves for to work and do by your cownseyl for to
take the Mortymer. sith that ye be keeper of the castle and have also the keys
in your ward. Sir quod the conestable will ye understood that the yates of the
castle be^ looked with the lokkes that dame jsabell send hydder / And by night
she had the keys thereof / And lies he^ vndyr the bolstyr of ye bed unto the
morwe / and so ye may not comen into the castle by the yates in no manner wise
/ But I know an vowte that streccheth owte of the park under the earth into
the foresaid castle that goth into the weste. whych^ aley dame Isabell the
queen ne none of her men ne the mortimer ne none of his company knows not.
And so j shall led you through that aley that ye shull come into the castle
without aspies of any me^ that been your enemies / And the same night sir
william Mou^tagu and all the lords of his quarrel and the same conestable also
went hem to horse and maden semblant as it were for to we^de out of the
mortymer sight / But anon^ as ye mortimer herd this tyding he wend that they
would have gone over ye see for dread of him: and anon he and his company
toke^ cou^ceyl among hem for to let her passage: and sent letters anon^ to
the ports so that none of the great lords should pass / but if they were
arestyd and take / And among other things william Eland conestable of ye
forsaid castle preuely lad sir wylliam Mou^tagu and his company by the
foresaid wey vndyr the earth. so till they camen into the castle and went up
into the tower there that the Mortimer was in / But sir Hugh^ of Trumpy^gton
hem af^ried hydously and said. A traitors it is all for naught that ye ben
comen into this castle: ye shull deye an evil death euerychone. And anon one
of hem that was in Mowntagu is company up with a mace and smote the same Hugh
upon ye head that the brain breast owte And fell on the grownde. and so was he
deed an evil deth^ Tho took they ye Mortymer as he armed him at the towers
doors when he herd the noise of hem for dread / and wha^ the quen^ Isabell
saw that ye mortymer was taken: she made much sorwe in heart / and the words
unto him said. Now fair syres I pray you that ye done non^ harm unto his
body for he is a worthy knight our welbelouyd friend and our dear cosyn. Tho
went they thennes and camen and brought the Mortimer and presented hy^ unto the
king Edward / and he commanded to bring him in sauf ward: but anon right as
they that were consent unto ye mortymers doing herd tell that he was take:
they went and hyd hem privily and by night went out of ye town each in his
side with heavy heart: and lived upon her lands as well as they might: And so
that same year that ye mortymer was take. he had at his retenue ix / score
knights without squyers and seriau^tes of arms and footme^ / And tho was the
Mortymer lad to london and sir Symo^d of bereford was lad with hy^ / and was
take to ye Conestable of the toure to keep: But afterward was the Mortymers
life examyned at westmy^ster before the king: and before all ye great lords of
England for peril that might fall to the reaume / and to enquere also which
were asse^tyng to sir Edwardes death ye kings fadre. and also through who^ the
scotts askaped from Sta^hope / into scotland without the will of king Edward
/ And also how the chartre Rageman was delyured unto the scotts: whery^ the
homages and feautes of Scotland were contained that the scotts should done
evermore unto the kings of england for the reaume of scotland. wherefore in his
absence he was dampened to be draw and honged for his treson: And this meschyef
came unto hy^ sey^t Andrews even. in the year of Incarnacyon of our lord Ihesu
Crist a.M.CCC. and xxx

How king Edward get ayene unto him gracyously the homages and feautes of
Scotland where of he was put owte through falls counsel of Isabell his modre /
and sir Rogier mortymer yt was new made earl of the march Capit / CCxxiij
NOw ye have herd lords how sir Johan of bailloll in time of pees was chosen
to be king of scotland for encheson that he came of the eldest doughtyr of the
earl david of Ho^ty^gton that was king Alysa^dres brother of Scotland that
deide without heir of his body begoten and how this Johan made feaute and
