he aftyrward withsaid his homage through cou^ceill of ye scotts in the year of
our lord.M.CC.lxxij. and sent unto the pope through a falls suggestion that he
made his oath unto the foresaid king Edward over his astate and his will / of
which oath the pope hi^ assoilled through by his bylles to hy^ sent / and anon
as king edward wist thereof. he ordained anon^ his barons and came unto Berewyke
/ and conquered the town: at which conquest there were slayn^ xxv / M and
vij.C / and ye bailloll that was king of scotland came and yield hy^ unto king
edward: and the king afterward delivered him out of the tower of London / and
all the great lords of Scotland with him that were take at Berewyke and yaf
hem saufco^duit to go into scotland / and the scotts since through her
falsenesse werred upon king Edward. and when sir Johan bailloll king of
scotland saw all this he went and put him over the sea unto Du^pier and lived
there upon his own lo^des as well as he might. till that the scotts would
amend hem of her misdeeds and trespace / and lad with him sir Edward his sone.
wherefore ye scotts in despyte of him called him Ioha^ turnelabard for cause
that he would not offend ne trespace ayens king Edward of England and so he
forsook his reame of Scotland and set thereof but littel prys: and this sir
Johan long time dwelled in France till that he deyed there / And sir Edward
his sone vnderfeng his heritage And did homage unto the king of France for his
lands of Dunpied and so it fell afterward that Edward that was joha^ baillols
sone had with him a squire of England yt was bore in york shyre that was

and full pryue And so this Johan barnaby was at debate with a Frenshman in ye

/ into the castle for to have socour and help of his lord: and anon came

reaume of france which was called Lowys loved moch^ this sir Henry / and he

heritage / And so he yafe moch^ silver unto sowdeours and to aliens for to

this covenant granted her bone as touching him. and tho that weren of the
same quarrel yt which claymed for to have lands or rentes in the reaulme of
Scotland

And these were the names of ye lords that purswede^ this matter that is to
say. sir Edward ye bailloill that challenged the reame of Scotland. sir Henry

to much sorwe and harm For the power of the scotts may every day wex and

and that we may myghtely take the scotts this night and boldly werre upon hem
and let us purswe hem this night. and if they be trauailled through us and they
see our hardynesse. so that other scotts that comen and mete hem and see hem
so trauailled and weary / the sorer wull they be a drad with us for to fight.
and fersly than we shull fight wit he^. and upon hem purswe. so that through the
grace of god almighty all the world shall speak of ye doughtynesse of our
cheualrye. And syres vndersto^deth well that all the company come^ with sir

company sore followed hem and did he^ moch^ sorwe through her assault: so yt
they might not for feeble hem help and for littell people But tho said ye
scotts among hem / what is now befall that so littell a people as the

seems us that he wreccheth by grace / for he is wonder g^cyous in his quarrel:

fers and angrj and went forth. and there they saw people of arms full well

long till thay^ that were in the town^ failled vitailles and also they were so
weary of wakyng that they wisten not what for to done. And ye shul vndyrsto^de
that the scotts that were in ye town of Berewyke through commune cou^ceill and
her assente let cry upon the walls of the toun^ that they might have pees of
the Englysshmen. and thereof they prai den the king of his grace and mercy and
prayed hy^ of trewes for viij days upon this covenant that if they were not
rescued in that side of ye town^ toward scotland of the scotts within viij.
days that they would yield hem unto the king and the town^ also. and to hold
this covenant they profred to the king xij. hostages out of the town of
berewyke. When the hostages were delyured unto the king: anon they of the
town^ sent unto ye scotts and told hem of her sorwe and meschief. And the
scotts camen tho preueli over ye watyr of Twede to the bought of the abbey.
and sir william Dyket that tho was stiward of Skotland and many other that
camen with him put he^ there in great peril at that time of her life: for they
came^ over a brigge that was to broken and ye stones a way. and many of her
company were there drenched. but ye forsaid wyllia^ went over and other of his
company and came by the ships of England and quelled in a barge of hull xvi.
men / And aftyr they went i^to the town of Berewyke by ye watyr side /
wherefore the scotts held tho the town reskued and asked her hostages ayen^
of the king of England. and the king sent word ayen^ that they axed the
hostages with wrong since that they came^ into the town^ of Englo^des side: for
ye covenant was bitwen^ him that the town should be reskued by ye half of
scotland. And anon^ king Edward tho commanded to yield the town^ or he would
hang ye hostages. And the scotts said that ye town was reskued ynowe and
there to they would hold he^. Wha^ king Edward saw yt the scotts break her
covenant that they made / he was wonder wroth. and anon let take sir Thomas
fitz willya^ and sir Alexandre of seto^ wardeyne of Berewyk. the which Thomas
was person of du^bare: and led they^ before all the other hostages for
encheso^ that sir Alixau^dres fadre was keeper of the town And commanded every
day that ij. hostages of the town should be hanged till that were all done
unto the death. but if they would yield the town / and so he should teache hem to
break his couenauntes / And wha^ they of ye town herd thees tydinges / they
became^ wonder sorry and sente^ to the king of england that he would grant he^
other viij days of respite. so that bitwen^ two hou^dred men of arms and xx.
men of arms might be strength^ gon^ bitwene hem to the town of Berewyke hem
for to vytaille that the town^ must be hold for rescued: And if so were that
xxi or xxij or more were slain of the two hou^dred before said that the town
should not be hold for rescued: and this covenant to be holden they sent to
him other xij of ye town^ in hostage: The king of England granted he^ her
prayer / and took the hostages on saint Margaretes even / in the year of grace
a M.ccc. and xxxij. The scotts came fersely in iiij we^ges well araied in arms
for to mete king Edward of england: and edward the king of scotland with her
power / and came fast and sharply ayens eue^so^ge time: and the same time was
flode at Berewyke in the watyr of Twede: that no man might went over on her
horse nor on foot / and the watyr was bytwen^ the two kings and the reaume of
England / and that time abyden ye scotts in that other side / for encheson
that the Englysshmen should have ben^ drownyd or slain

force. And when the Englissh men saw that they lepte^ on her horse and fast
pursued the scotts and all that they abyden they quelled down right. There
might me^ see the doughtynesse of the noble king Edward and of his men how
manly they pursued the scotts / th^at fledden for dread / and there might men
see many a scottissh man cast down^ on the grownde dede^ And her baners
displayed hakked into pecys: and many a good haberione of stelle i^ her blood
bathe. and many a time the scotts were gadred into companies but evermore they
were discomfyted / and so it befell that as god almighty would that the scotts
had that day no more foyson ne might ayens the Englysshmen: than xx. sheep
should have ayens v. wolfes. and so were the scotts discomfyted: and yet the
scotts had well v. men ayens one englysshman / And that bataille was done on

and that were footmen And this victory befell to the Englisshmen on sey^t
margaretes eve In the year of ye Incarnacyon of our lord Ihesu crist MCCCxxxij
And while yt this doing last the englyssh pages took the pilfre of the scotts

sped they yolden to him the town with the castle on the morwe after that the

in the xi. year of his regne and appyred in the firmament a bemed sterre / ye

and wonder great plente of all chafre vitaille and marcha^dyse and there aye^s
ho^ger scarcite meschief and need of money in somoch^ that a quarter of whete
at london was sold for two shillyng. and a good fat ox at a noble: and v. good
peious for a penny: in which year deyed sir johan of Eltha^ earl of Cornewaille
king Edwardes brother and lies at westmynster.

How king edward made a duchye of the Erledome of Cornewaill / and also of vj.
other earls that were new made. and of ye first chalengy^g of the ky^gdome of
France Capit. CC.xxv
IN the year of our lord MCCC and xxxvij: and of king Edward xij / in ye month
of March during the parliament at westmynstre in Lent time king edward made of
the erledome of Cornewaill a Duchye: and let it call the Duchye of Cornewaill
the which duchy he yaf unto edward his first sone with the erledome of
Chestre / And also king edward made at that same time vj. other earls that is
for to seye: sir Henri earl of Lancastres sone earl of leycestre. william of
Boghune Earl of Northampto^ / william of Mon^tagu earl of Salysbury / Hugh^ of

Clyton^ earl of Hu^tyngdone / And in that same year it was ordained in ye same

cloth of gold of silk / velvet or Damask / latin: ba^dekyn ne none such^
other / ne none wild ware ne furre of beyond the sea: but such^ as might
spend an C. pownde of rent a year. but this ordenau^ce and statute was of of
lyttel effect. for it was no thy^g hold In the xiij year of his regne king
Edward went over see into Braban with quen^ Philipp his wife there beryng
child at Andewarpe / there he dwelled more than a year to trete wit the duke of
Braba^ / and each to othre allied for chalengyng of the kingdom of France to
king Edward of England by right and that by inheritance aftyr the death of
Karoll the great king of France brother germayne of queen Isabell king
Edwardes modyr apperteigned. the which was holden and occupied unrightfully by
phelip of Valoys ye Emes sone of king karoll / the which duke and all his in
the forsaid things and in all other thereto belongyng wit all his me^ and
goods. king Edward fond ready unto hy^ and maden and promised bitwene thay^
seurte by good faith and trust / and aftyr that the king hasted him into
england ayen^: and left there the quen^ stille behind him in brakan. Than in
the xiiij year of his regne when all ye lords of his reame and other that
fallen to be at his parliament weren kalled and assembled to gedre in the same
parliament holden at London. after the fest of seint Hilarie: the kings needs
were put forth and promoted as touchy^g the ky^gdome of France. For which
needs to be sped the king axed ye fifthe part of all the mevable goods of
England: and the wulles and the ix shefe of every corn. And ye fordes of every
toun^ / where such^ thing should be taxed and gadred. should answer to the king
thereof: and he had it and held it at his one lust and will / wherefore if I
shall knowlech^ the very trewth^. the ynner love of the people was turned into
hate. and the commune prayers into kursyng for cause that the common people
were so strongely grieved Also the foresaid Phelipp valoys of France had gadred
unto him a great host. and destroyed there in his parties and ky^gdome many of
the kings friends of England with towns and castelles of many other of her
lorshippes. and mani harms shames and despites dyde^ unto the quen^ / wherefore
king Edward when he herd this tidy^ges was strongely meved and therewith an
angered: and se^te diverse lettres over see to ye quen^ and to other that were
his friends glading he^ and certefye^g he^ that he would be there hy^ self in
all the haste that he might. And anon^ aftyr Estre when he had sped of all
thing that him neded / he went over the sea ayen^ / of whose comy^g the quen^
and all his friends were wondre glad and made much joy. And all that were his
enemies and aye^s hy^ helde^ maden as moch^ sorwe. In ye same time the king
through cou^ceyl of his true lieges and cou^ceil of his lords that there were
present with him toke^ the king of Frau^ces name. and took and meddled the
ky^ges arms of France quartred with the arms of England and commanded forth
with his coygne of gold vndyr description and wryty^g of ye name of England and
of France to be made best that might be. that is for to seye. the floryn^ that
was called ye noble prys of vj shillyng viij. pens of sterlinges. and the half
noble of the value of iij. shillynghes / iiij pens. and the ferthyng of value /
xx. pens

How king Edward came to the Sclus and disco^fyted all the power of France in
the haven Capitulo CCxvi
ANd in the next year after that is for to say / ye xv / year of his regne. he
commanded and let write in his chartres writtes and other letters the date of

Vajoys the which long time lay and had gadred to hi^ a full great meyne of
diverse nacyons in the haven of Sclus. and there they fowghten to gedre the

morn / in which bataill were slain xxx.M. men of the kings company of
France and many ships and kogges were taken. and so through gods help he
had there ye victory. and bear the^s a glorious chivalry And in the same year
about sey^t james tide wytout ye yates of sei^t Omers Robert of Autheis with men
of england and flau^dres bitterly faught ayens the duke of Burgoygne and the

there in his need / but his procuratours and messagiers cursedly and full flowly
served hy^ at his need / and hy^ deceived: on whose defaute and laches the king
took trewes bitwen^ him and the king of France. And the king full of woe sorwe
and shame in his heart with drowe him fro the siege and came into Britaigne^ and
there was so great strife for vitaill that he lost manj of his people. And when
he had done there that he cam^ for / he dressed hi^ over see into england ward
/ And as he saylled toward England in ye high^ see / ye most myshappes storms
and te^pestes / thu^dring and lightny^ges fill to hy^ in ye see / the which
was said that it was done and areised through evil spirits made by sorcery and
nygroma^cy of he^ of france. wherefore the kings heart was full of sorwe and
anguyssh weylyng and sighing and said unto our lady in this wise / O blessed
lady sei^t marie. what is the cause that evermore going into france all
things and wethers fallen to me ioyefull and lykyng / and as I would have he^:
but allewey turnyng into england ward / all things fallen unprofitable and
harmefull. Neuyrthelater he skapyng all perilles of the sea as god would came

at Meners. and sent word to the Scotts by his messagiers that he was ready and

wide clothes destitut and desert from all old honest and good usage. And an

men / And the women more nyfely yet passed the men in array and coriouslaker.

pride pa^ adventure afterward brought forth and caused many mysshappes and

How king Edward sailed into Norma^dye and arrived at Hogs with a great host
Ca / cc / xxvij
IN the xxi year of his regn^ king Edward through cou^ceill of all the great
lords of the reame of England called and gadred to gedre in his parliament at
westmy^ster before estre^ ordained hi^ for to pass over ye see ayen^ for to
disese and destrouble the rebels of France: and when his nauye was come to
gedre and made ready / he went with an hugh^ host / ye xij day of Iuyll and
sailled into norma^dye / and arrived at Hogs. And wha^ he had rested him
there vj days for by cause of trauaillyng of the sea / and for to have out
all his men wit all her necessaries out of her ships. he went toward Cadoun^
bre^nyng vastyng and destroyng all the tounes yt he fond in his way And the
xxvi day of Iuyll. at the brigge of Cadony ma^ly and orpedli strengthyd and
defended with norma^s he had there a strong bataille: and a long during through
which a great multitude of people were slayn^ And there were take prisoners. ye
earl of ewe. the lord of ta^kerwille / and an C knights and men of arms and
vj.C footme^ nombred. and ye town and the subarbes unto ye bare walls of all
thing that might be bore and carried out was robbed and despoilled. Afterward
the king passing forth by the co^tre about the country about the broad of xx
mile / he vasted all manner thing that he fo^de / When Phelip of Valoys
perceived all this: all though he were fast by with a strong host he would not
come no nerre. but break all ye brigges beyo^de ye watyr of seyne fro Rone
unto paris wit all ye have yt he might / For soth the noble king edward when he
came to Paris brigge and fond it broken withy^ ij. days: he let make it again
/ and in the morwe after the assumptio^ of our lady. king edward passed over ye
watyr of seyn^ goy^g toward Crescy. and destroyed by the way tounes with the
people dwelly^g theryn. And in the fest of sey^t bartolomewe he passed over ye
water of Sum unhurt with all his host there as never before hand was any manner
way ne passage where ij / M. were slayn^ of he^ that let her passage over:
Therefore ye xxvj day of August king edward in a feeld fast by Cresey hauy^g iij
batailles of Englisshme^ cou^tred and met with Philip of Valoys having wit hy^
iiij batailles. of whych^ the leest passed gretli the no^bre of the englyssh
people / And when thees ij hosts mette^ to gedre / ther^ fill upon hy^ the king
of Beme: the duke of Loreyne / and earls also of Flau^dres Dalunson. bloys /
harecourt. anmarle and nevers. and many other Earls: barons / lords / knights
and men of arms ye no^bre of a M.v.C / xlij. wtoute footmen and othyr men well
armed / yt were nothing rekened And for all this. the vnvnglorious philippe
withdrowe him with the residue of his people wherefore it was said in common
among his own people / nostre beal soy retreyt: That is for to seye. our fair
withdrawith him. Tha^ king Edward and our Englisshme^ thanked god almighty for
such^ a victory / after her great labor taken to hem all thing needful to
her sustynau^ce and saving of her life for dread of her enemies rested hem

came ayen^ for to give bataille and fight wit ye englysshmen. with who^ mette^
and cou^trede^ earls of Warrewyke: northa^pto^ and northfolk wit her company
and slowen two thousand and toke^ many prisoners of the gentills of hem. And
the remanaunt of the same host fled iij mile the^s. and ye thridde day after
the bataill the king went to Caleys ward. destroyng all the country as he rode
thyderward. and wha^ that he was come. yt is for to say the thridde day of
septe^bre: he began to besege the town wit the castle: and continued his siege
fro ye forsaid thridde day of septe^bre unto the thridde day of August the next
year after / And in ye same year during the siege of Caleys: the king of
Skotland wit a full great multitude of scotts came into england to Nevilles
cross about sey^t Lucas day evangelist hopy^g and trustyng to have fonde^ all
the land destytute and void of people. For asmoch^ as the king of England was
beyo^de the sea saufe only prestes and men of holy chyrch^ and wymen and
children and plowghme^: and such^ other laborers / And there they robbede^ and
dyde^ moch^ sorwe. but yet fonde^ they ynow that he^ withstode^ by ye grace of
almighti god. And so a day of bataill was assigned bitwene he^ and certay^
lords and men of holy chyrch^ that were of ye country with other common people
fast by the cite of Duresme at which day through the grace of almighty god the
scotts were ouercomen / and yet were they iij fold so many of he^ as of
Englysshme^. and there was slayn^ all the cheualrie and knighthode of ye reame
of scotland: And there were take as they would have fled the^s David the king
of Scotland him self. the earl of Mentife. sir william Douglas and many other
great men And aftyr that our Englysshme^ when they had rested hem a few days
and had ordained the kepers of the northcontre / they came^ unto London and
broughten wit hem David king of Scotland / and all these other lords that
were taken prisoners / unto the towr of London with all ye have that they
might: And there they left hem in sauf keeping unto the kings coming / and
wenten home aye^ unto her own co^tre: And afterward was the kings rau^sone of
Scotland taxed unto an C / M. mark of silver to be paid in x. year that is for
to seyne every year x / M. mark.

How gy^g Edward besieged Caleys. and how it was wo^ne and yolde^ unto him Cap.
CCxxviij /
IN the xxij year of king edwardes regne he went over the sea in the wy^ter
time / and lay all the winter time at ye siege of Caleys. ye which year the
while the siege lasted Philp ye king of France cast and purposed trechouresly
and with fraud to put away the siege and came ye xxvij day of Iuyll in the
same year with a great host and strong power and neyg^ed unto the siege of
Caleys: the which Phelipp the last day of Iuyll sent to king Edward word that
he would yeve hy^ pleme bataill the iij day next after that about eueso^g time:
if he durst come fro ye siege y abide it: And when king Edward herd that.
without any long tarieng er long avyseme^t he accepted gladly the day and
hour of bataill that Philip had assigned. and when the king of France herd
that the next night aftir he set his te^tes a fire. and remeved and went away
thens cowardly Then^ they yt were in the town and in the castle besieged.
sey^g all this how that they had non^ other help ne socour of the king of
France ne of his men and also that her vitailles withi^ne hem were spended and
vasted. and for defaute of vitailles and of refresshing they eten horse hou^des
cattes and mys for to keep her throuth^ as long as they might. And wha^ they
saw and was fonde^ among he^ at the last that they had no thing among hem for
to ete ne live by ne no socour ne rescuynge of the Fre^sshme^ of that other
side. they wist well yt they must needs deye for defaulte. or else yield the
town. and anon they wenten and token down the baners and the arms of
france on every side that were honged owte / and wenten on the walls of the
town on diverse places as naked as they were borne save only shyrtes and her
breches / and helden her swerdes naked. and the point donward in her hondes and
putte^ roppes and balters about her nekkes and yelde^ up the keys of the
town and of the castle to king Edward of England wit great fere and dread of
heart / And when king Edward saw this as a mercyable king and lord received all
thay^ to grace. and a few of the gretest personers of state and of governance
of the town he sent in to England there to abide her rau^sone^ And the kings
grace suffered all the co^minalte of the town to go whidder they would in pees
/ And without any harm let hem bear wit hem all her things that they might
bear and carry away keeping the town and ye castle to him self: Tha^ through
mediacion of cardinals that were sent fro the pope trews was take there bitwene
france and England for ix / months tha^ next folewy^g. and about Mychelmasse
king edward came ayen^ into England: with a glorious victory. And in the
xxiiij year of his regne / in the eest parties of the world there arose and
began a pestylence and death of sarazens and paynyms that so great a death was
never herd of before / and that wasted away so the people that uneaths the tenth
person was left a live. And in the same year about the southcou^trees and also
in the west cou^tres: there fill so moch^ rain and so great watres that from
Crystmasse unto midsomer there was uneaths day ne night but that it rayned
somewhat / through whych^ watres the pestilence was so enfected and so abundau^t
in all countries and namely about the court of Rome and other places by the sea costs that uneaths there were left lyuy^g folk to bery hem that were deed
honestly / but maden great dyches and pittes that were wonder broad and deep.
and theryn buried hem and maden a renge of deed bodies and casten a littel
earth to hele hem above: and than cast in an other re^ge of deed bodies. and
an other re^ge of earth above hem. And thus weren they buried and none othyr
wise: But if it were ye fewer that were^ great men of estate were buried as
honestely as they might: And after all this in the xxiiij year of king Edwardes
regne. it was hy^ done to wit and understood of a treso^ that was bego^ne at
Caleys and ordained for to seell ye town for a great sum of flory^s unto
king Phelipp of France: through ye falsenesse and ordinance of a knight yt was
kalled sir Geffrey of Cha^^ney that was wonder pryue with king Philip of France
/ And when king Edward h^erde this he took with hy^ the nobles and gentiles lords
and many other worthy and orped men of arms that were there p^sent wit hy^ for
the sole^pnite of that high fest: and well and wisely in all the have that he
might and also as preuely as he might he went over see And that same year the
good king Edward held his Cristmasse at hauery^g: And the morwe after
Neweyeres day the king was in the castle of Caleys with his men of arms that
none of the aliens wist thereof / And that falls conspi^atour and traitor
Geffrey of charney saw that he might not openly have his purpose of the
castle: preuely and stelyngly he came in and held the town with a great
host / and when he wit his men was comen in: he paid the forsaid so^me of
Flory^s as covenant was bitwen^ hem to a Genevey in the town that was keeper
of the castle. and co^sentyng to the same Geffrey in all this falsenesse and
treachery. and bou^de^ the e^glyssh ministres and servants that were in the
castle that they might not help he^ self. ne let hem of her purpose: and
tha^ weny^g that they had be sure ynow: they spake^ all her wykkednesse and
falsenesse opynli an high yt all men might here And now shull ye here how
they were disceyued for they came^ in by a pryue posterne over a little brygge
of tree: and when they were comen in. softely and pryuely ye brygge was drawn
up and kept. that non^ of hem that came^ in might gon^ out. ne no mo come unto
he^. and anon^ our Englysshmen wenten out at pryue holes and wy^dowes / and
over the walls of the town and of the castle / and wente^ and foughten manly
with the frensshmen that were without. and had the better of hem: the which
wh^en they weren occupied by hem self on her side / the king was withy^ the
town hauy^g with him scarcely but xxx me^ of arms / drew owte his swerd /
and with a loud voys cried an hygh^ / a saint Edward / a saint George / And
when the folk herd that / they camen renny^g unto hi^ and yauen there to her
enemies so great assault that there were mo than two hou^dred men of arms and
many other slain and many fledden away: and so by the grace of god almighty ye
victory fill to the Englysshme^: Tha^ the king took with hy^ this Geffrey that
was fynder of this treachery. And also many other frenssh prisoners / and
withy^ a while after he came aye^ into England / And in this same year and in
the year a fore and also in ye year next after was so great pestilau^ce of men
fro the eest into the west. and namely through boches that tho yt siked on this
day deyed on the thridde day / the which me^ that so deyde^ i^ this pestilence
hadden but littell respite of lyggyng: The pope clementz of his goodness and
grace yafe he^ full remissyo^ and foryevenesse of all sins that they were
shriven of / and this pestilence lasted in London fro Michel mass unto august
next folowy^g almost an hole year. And in these days was death wytoute sorowe^
weddy^ges wtoute friendship. wyllfull penance and derth^ wytoute scarcite. and
fleyng without refute or socour: for many fledde^ fro place to place. because
of the pestyle^ce but they were enfecte and might not askape the death After
that the Prophet Isaye says. Who that flees fro' the face of dread / he
shall fall into the dyche. and he that we^deth him owte of the dyche / he
shall be hold and teyde with a gre^ne / but when this pestilence was rested as
god would uneaths the.x / part of ye people was left a life: And in ye same year
began a wonder thing that all that evyr were borne after ye pestilence hadde^
ij. chektethe in her head less than they had a fore

How king edward had a great bataylle wit Spa^yardes upon the sea fast by
wynchelsee Capitulo CC.xxix
ANd in the xxv year of his regne about seint Ioha^nes day in Heruest in the sea fast by wy^chelsee king Edward had a great bataille with men of Spaigne
where that her ships and nauye lay clained to gedyr that either they must
fight or dre^che / and so when all our worthy me^ of arms and the sea costs
fast by wynchelsee and Romeny were gadred to gedre. and our nauye and ships
all ready to the werre: the englisshme^ metten manly and styfly with her enemies
comy^g fersely aye^s he^ And when the spanysh vessels and navy were closed
in all about there me^ might se a strong bataille there were but few that
foughte^ / but that they were spitousely hurt and foul / And after the
bataille there were xxiij ships of the spa^yardes take: And so the englysshme^
had the better. And i^ the next year following of his regne that is to say ye
xxvj year the king through his counceyll let ordeyne and make his new money /
that is to seye the penny the great of value of iiij. pe^s And the half grote
of value of ij pe^s* but it was of lose weighte than the old sterly^g was by
v. shillyng in the pound / And in the vij year of his regne was the great
derthe of vitailles. the which was kalled the dear somer And in the xxviij
year of his regn^ in the parliament holde^ at westmy^ster aftyr Estren sir Henry
earl of lancaster was made duke of Lancastre: and in this same year was so
great drowghte yt fro the month of Iuyll there fill no rain on the earth /
wherefore all fruits seeds and herbs for the most party were lost in
defaute. wherefore there came so great disese of men and bestes and derthe of
vitailles in England. so that this la^d yt ever a fore had be plenteuous had
need that time to seek his vitailles and refreshi^g of other owte yles and
co^trees And in the xix year of king edward it was accorded granted and sworn
bytwen^ the king of France and king Edward of England that he should have again
all his lands and lordshippes that apperteygned to the Duchye of Gwyhe^ne of
old time / the which had ben^ withdraw and wrongfully occupied by diverse
kings of France before hand to have and to hold to the king Edward and to
his heirs and successors for evermore freely pesibeli and in good quete. upon
this covenant that the king of england should leave of and relese all his right
and claim that he had and claymed of the ki^gdome of france / and of ye ritle
that he took thereof / upon which speech and covenant made: it was sent to the
court of Rome on both sides of the kings that ye forsaid couenau^ts should be
enbulled / But god ordained better for the kings wurship of England / For what
through fraud and disceyt of the Frensshmen: and what through letthy^g of the
pope and of the court of Rome the forsaid couenauntz were disquat and left of:
And in the same year the king revoked by his wise and discrete cou^ceill the
staple of wulles out of Flau^dres into England wit all the libertees
frau^chyses and fre customs that longe^ thereto. and ordained in england in
diverse places. that is for to seye at westmy^stre. canterbury Chichestre.
Bristow Lyncolne Hull with all the forsaid things that lo^gen thereto And that
this thing that should thus be done the king swore him self thereto / and prince
Edward his sone with other many great witnesses that there were p^sent: And in
the xxx year of his regne anon^ aftyr wytsonday in the parliament ordained at
Westmynster it was told and certefied to ye king that Phelip that tho held
the kingdom of Frawnce was deed / and that Johan his sone was crowned king /
and yt this joha^ had give karol his sone ye duchy of Gwihenne. of the which
king edward when he wiste thereof / he had great indignacyo^ unto hy^ and was
wonder wroth and stro^gely meved. and therefore before all ye worthy lords that
were assembled there at that parliament / he called edward his sone unto him to
who^ the duchy of Gwihenne by right heritage should long to and yafe it him
there chargy^g and co^mau^dy^g hy^ that he should ordeyne hy^ to defend and
aue^ge him upon his enemies and save and maynten^ his right. and afterward king
Edward him self and his eldest sone edward went to diverse places and seyntes
in England on pilgrimage for to have ye more help and grace of god and of his
seintes. And the ij. kal of Iuyll when all thing was redi to ye viage and
bataill and his retynue and power assembled and his nauye also ready / he took
with hi^ the earl of warrewyk: The earl of southfolk. the earl of Salysbury / and
the earl of Oxu^ford. and a M. me^ of arms and as many archiers / and in the
natyuite of owr lady took her ships at Plymmownth / and begone to sail: And
when he came and was aryued in Gwyhe^ne he was there wurshipfully take and
received of the most no / ble men and lords of that country. And anon after
king edward took with hy^ his two sons: that is for to seye. Sir Leonell Earl
of Vlton / and sir Ioha^ his brother earl of Rychemond / and sir Henri duke of
Lancastre with many earls and lords and men of arms. and ij.M. archiers: and
saylled toward France. and rested him a while at Caleys. and afterward the
king went with his folk a forsaid and wit other Sowdeours of beyond the sea yt
there aboden the kings coming the second day of Noue^bre / and took his
iournay toward king Johan of france there as he trowed to have fonde^ him fast
by Odomaru^ / as his lre^s and covenant made me^cyo^ that he would abide him
there with his host. And when king johan of france herd of the kings coming of
England: he went away with his men and carriage cowardli and shamefully fleyng
and vasty^g all vitailles over all that the englisshmen should not have thereof
And when king Edward herd tell that he fled. he purswed him wit all his host
till Hedene. and tha^ he beholdy^g the vantyng and the scarcite of vitaylles.
and also the cowardyse of the king of france. he turned ayen^ vastyng all the
country. And while all these things were a doing. the scotts preuely and by
night toke^ the town^ of Berewyk sleyng hem that withstode^ hem / and no man
else / but blessed be god the castle nevyrthelater was saved and kepet by
englysshmen that were theryn. Tha^ the king perceived all this and turned ayen^
into England as wroth as he might be: wherefore in parliament at Westmynster was
granted to the king of every sake of wolle / l. shillyng / during the term of
vj. year that he might the might liker fight and defend the reame ayens the
scotts and other mysdores: And so when all things were ready. the king hasted
hy^ to the siege ward

How king Edward was crowned king of Scotland: and how pry^^ce Edward took the
king of france: and sir Philip his yo^ger sone at the bataill of Peyters

ANd in the xxxi. year of (...) regne the xiij. day of (...) the king being in
the castle of Berewyke with a few men. but having there fast by a great host.
the town was yolden to him wtoute any manner defense: or difficulte: Tha^ the

and lords that there were / let crown him king there of the reame of Scotland
And when all things were done and ordained in that co^tre at his lust and

viage was a doing in skotland / sir Edward prince of Walys as man enspyred in
god was in Gwyhenne in the cite of Burdeux tretyng and spekyng of the
chalangyng and of the kings right of England that he had of the reame of
France / and that he would aue^ged be with strong ho^de / and the p^lates peers
and mighti men of that contre consented well to him. Than sir Edward ye prince
with a great host gadred to hy^ the sixte day of Iuyll / and went from
Burdeux going and trauailly^g by many diverse contreyes and he took many
prisoners moo than vj.M / men of arms by the contre as he soiourneid and took
ye town of Remorantyn in Saloigne: And besieged the castle vi. days and at

lord of crown and sir Bursinga^d and many other knights and men of arms moo
tha^ lxxx. And than he went thens by Torene: and fast by chyneney his noble men
that weren with him hadden a strong battle wit the Frensshme^: and an
hou^dred of her men of arms were slain And ye earl of Dau^ce and the Styward
of France were take with an C men of arms. In the which year the xix day of

iiijC^ and xl And in the xxxij / year of king Edwardes regne ye v. day of may

for to sey. the abbot of Cluyne / the earl of Tha^keruille and bursydand that

dei said with dona no^is pace^. in presence of the forsaid me^ that were ordained
to admytte and receive the oaths and of all other yt there might be The same
cha^s leide his right hond on the pa^en with gods body / and his left ho^de
on the missale and seid: we N. swe^e^ on gods bodi and the holy gospelles
that we shull trewly and steadfastly hold toward us the pees and ye accord made
between the two kings and in no manner do the contrary. and there among all his
lords for the more love and stre^gth^ of witness deled and deperted the
relyques of the croune of the criste to ye knights of England / and they
curtosely toke^ her leave. and in the friday next / the same manner oath in
presence of the forsaid knights and of other worthy men prince Edward made at
lovers afterward both kings and her sons and the most noble men of both^
reames wythyn the same year made the same oath. and for to strength all thees
things forsaid. the king of England axked the gretest men of France: and he
had his axing / that is for to seye.vj dukes / viij earls / and xij lords.
that is to say barons and worthy knights / and when ye place and ye time was
assigned. in which both ky^ges wit her counceill should come to gedre all ye
foresaid things bytwen^ hem spoken for to ratefye and make ferme and stable /
The king of England anon^ went toward the sea: and at hou^flette began to
saille leuy^g to his hoostes yt were left behy^de him by cause of his abse^ce
moch^ hevynesse / and at Estre the xix day of May he came into England and went
to his paleys at westmy^ster on sei^t du^stones day. and the iij. day after he
visited Ioha^ king of france that was in ye towr of London and deliured him
freely from all manner pryso^ sauf first they were accorded of iij millio^s of
flory^s for his rau^sone. and the king comforted hy^ and chered hy^ in all
places with all solas and myrthes that lo^gen to a king in his goy^g hom^ward And
the ix. day of Iuyll in the same year the same Johan king of france that before
hand lay here i^ hostage went home again into his own land to trete of the
things and of other that lo^geden and fylle in ye governance of his reame.
and afterward metten and came^ to gedre at caleys both the ij ky^ges with both^
her cou^ceil: about all halewe^ tide: and there were showed the co^dicions and
the points of the pees and of the accord of both sides written / and there
without any withsayng of both^ sides graciously they were accorded. and there
was done and so^ge a sole^pne mass. and after the thridde Agnus dei upon
gods body and also upon the mass book both kings and her sons and the
grettest lords of both reames and of her cou^ceill that there were tha^ p^se^t
and had not swore before the foresaid oath that they had made. and was titled
bitwene hem: they behighten there to keep and all other conuenau^ts that were
between he^ ordained. and in this same year me^nes bestes trees and howsing
with soden tempest and strong lyghteny^g were perisshed: and the deuel appeared
bodily in ma^nys likeness to much people / as they went in diverse places in
the co^tre and spoken to he^

How the great company aroos in France. and the white company in Lu^bardye:
and of many other mervaille Capit / cc.xxxi
King Edward in the xxxvj year of his regne anon^ after Cristmasse in the feste
of co^uersio^ of sei^t Poull held his perleme^t at westmy^ster. in the which
was put forth and showed ye accord and the tretys yt was stablisshed and made
bitwen^ the ij. kings. the which accord plesyd to moch^ people / and therefore
by the ky^ges conmau^deme^t there were gadred and came to gedre in westmy^ster
church the first sunday of Le^t / that is to say the ij. kal of Feurer ye
forsaid Englysshmen and Frensshmen / where was song a mass of the Trinite of
the Erchebisshop of Caunterbury master Symo^d Islepe. And wha^ Agnus dei was
done the king being there wit his sons and also wit the kings sons of france
and other great lords wit candels light and crosses brought forth all that
were called thereto. that were not swore a fore / sworn that same oath that was
written upon gods body / and on the mass book in this wise / we N. and N.
swere^ upon holy gods body and on the gospelles stedvast to hold and keep
toward us the pees and the accord made between the ij. ky^ges and never for to
do the contrary. and when they had thus sworn they token her scrowes that her
oaths were co^prehe^ded into the notaires / and this same year in ye asce^cyo^
eve about mydday was seyn^ ye eclips of the son / and there follows such^ a
drought. that for defaute of reyne there was great barinesse of corn fruit and
hey. and i^ ye same month the vj Kal of Iuyn^ there fill a sa^gweyne rain
almost like blood. at Burgoyne / and a sangwyne cross fro morn unto prime was
seyne and appeired at Boloigne in the air / the which many a man saw and
after it meved and fill in ye midde see. and in the same time in france and in
england and in other many lands as they that were i^ pleyne contrees and
desert bare^ witness / suddenly there apered ij. castelles: of the which went
out ij / hosts of armed me^: and that one host was clothed i^ white / and
that other in blake. and when bataill bitwen^ he^ was holde^ ye white overcame
the blake. and anon^ after the blake took heart unto he^ and overcame the white
and after yt they went again into her castelles. and all ye hosts vanisshed
away. and i^ this same year was a great and an hugh pestilence of people and
namely of m^ / whose wifes as wy^me^ out of governance toke^ hous^o^des as well
stra^giers as other lewd and simple people. ye which foryeteny^g her own
honor and wurship and berthe coupled and married he^ with he^ yt were of low
degree and littel reputacio^ And in this same year deyed He^ri duke of
Lancaster. and also in this ye^e Edward pry^ce of Walys wedded ye countess of
Ke^t. yt was sir Thomas wife of Hola^d the which was deperted some time and
deuroced fro ye earl of Salisbury fro cause of the same knight: and about this
time began and arose a great company of diverse nations gadred to gedre / of
who^ her leders and governors were englissh people / and they were clepid a
people wtoute an head. ye which did moch^ harm in ye party of France / and
not long after there aroos an other company the which in the perties and
co^tres of Lu^bardie did much sorwe. This same year sir Ioha^ of gau^te the
sone of king Edward ye iij. was made duke of Lancaster by reason and cause of
his wife that was the daughter and heir of Henry some time duke of Lancaster.

Of the great wy^de and how prince Edward took ye lordship of Gwihenne of his
fadre and went thither Capit. CCxxxij
ANd in ye xxxvij year of king edward the xv* day of Ianiuer that is to sey on
sei^t Mary's day about eue^song time there aroos and came such^ a wy^de out of
ye south with such^ a fersenesse and strength that it brast and blewe down to
ground high^ houses and strong byldynges towers churches and steples and all
other strong works that stode^ stylle were^ shake / therewith that they ben^
yet and shull be evermore the febeler and weyker while they stand / and this
wind lasted wytoute any cessy^g vij days co^tinnell And anon^ after there
folewed such waters in hey time and in heruest time that all field works
were strongely let and left undone: And in ye same year prince Edward took
the lordship of Gwihe^ne and did to king edward his fadre feaute and homage
therefore: and went over see into Gascoigne with his wife and with his children.

that is for to say* that he should ever after maynteyne the right believe and
feyth of holy church and holy church also with all her mynystres right and
lybertees to defend from all her enemies and euelles: And all that were there

priueleges of holy church encrese and mayntene and amend and all things that
were wrongfully betake^ withdraw and bore away by him or by any other because

And that when he had taken a christian women: he should never come in none other
womannys bed ne none other ma^nys wife to defowle And these forsaid things
trewly for to keep continwe and fullfyll as all his life time was bound by

And tha^ that gracyous prince: prince Edward undertook the cause and the

strongely they fowghten and wrastled to gedre. and the south Egle overcame ye

men's here is walky^g on the earth as it was seen and known of many a men. And

katheryne even three days after lost good without nombre unrecoverable / And
