haille that it vasted and destroyed men bestes howses and trees

Of the bataill of Spaygne besides ye watyr of Nazers / that was between the
prince Edward / and sir Henry bastard of Spaygne^ Capit. CCxxxiij
IN the year of our lord M.CCC / lxvij. and of king Edward xlij. the iij day of
Apryll: there was a strong bataille and a great in a large field kalled
Priazers fast by the watyr of Nazers in Spaygne bitwene sir Edward the prince.
and Henry the Bastard of Spaygne / but the victory fell to prince edward by
the grace of god. And this same pry^ce Edward had with him sir Johan duke of
Lancaster his brother and other worthy men of arms about the nombre of xxx /
M / and the king of Spaigne had on his side men of diverse nacyons: to ye
nombre of an CM. And passing wherefore the sharpness and tersenesse of his
aduersayre with his full boistous and great strength^ maden and driven the
rightful party a bak a great way: but through ye grace of almighty god passing
any mannys strength^ that hugh^ host was distroubled mightfu^^^ by the noble
duke of Lancastre and his host er that the pry^ce edward came nygh him / And
when Henry ye bastard saw that. he turned with his men in so great haste and
strength to flee: that an hugh^ company of hem in the forsaid flode and of the
brigge thereof fyllen down and perisshed / And also there were take the Earl of
Dene. and sir bartram Cleykyn that was chief maker and cause of the werre and
also cheuytayne of the vau^twarde of the bataille / with many other great
lords and knights to the no^bre of two thowsa^d / of who^ two houndred were
of France and many also of Skotland / and there were felled in ye feld on owr
enemies side of lords and knights with other mean people to the nombre of vj.
thousand and moo: and of englyssh men but a few. And after this / the noble
pry^ce edward restored ye same Piers i^to his ky^gdome aye^. The which Piers
afterward through trecherye and falsenesse of the forsaid bastard of Spaigne as
he set at his met was stra^gled and deyde / But after this victory many
noble and hardy men of england in Spaigne through the flixe and other diverse
sickness token her death: And in the same year in the march was seyne stella
Comata bitwene the northcostes and ye west / Whose bemes strecched toward
france / And in ye year next sewy^g of king Edwardes regne xliij in Apryll.
sir Leonell king edwardes sone that was duke of Clarence went toward myleyne
with a chose meyne of the gentiles of england for to wedde Caleys daughter and
have her to wife. by whom he should have half the lordshyp of Myleine: but
after that they were sole^pnely wedded. and about the natiuite of our lady the
same duke of Myleyne deyde / And in the same year the Frensshme^ breken ye pees
and the trewes / Rydy^g on the kings grownde and lorship of England in the
shire and country of Pountife / And token and held castelles and towns. and
bear the Englysshmen on hand falsely and sotely that they were cause of
brekyng of the trewes

And in this same year deyde the duchess of Lancastre. and is buried
wurshipfully in saint Paul's church^

The xliiij year of king Edwardes regne was the great pestilence of men and of
great bestes and by the great falling of watres that fill at that time. There
fill great hynderyng and destroyeng of corn in so much that the next year
after a busshelle of whete was sold for xl. pens^ And in the same year about
the last end of may k^g Edward held tho his parliament at Westmynster. In the
which parliament was tretyd and spoken of the oath and trewes that was broke
between him and the king of France. and how he might upon his wrong be
aue^ged In this same year in the assu^pcyone of owr Lady deyed Quen^ Phelipp of
England a full noble and good woman / and at Westmynster full wurshipfully is
buried and entered. and about mydsomer the noble duke of Lancastre and the
earl of Herford with a great company of knights and men of arms wenten into
france / where they get hem but littell wurshyp and nauye / for there was an
huge oost of Frensshmen upon chalkhull brigge. and an other host also of
englysshme^ fast by the same brygge that long time had leyne there: and many
worthy men and great of the englysshmen ordained and yafe cou^ceill for to
fight and yeve bataille to the Fre^sshme^: But the foresaid lords would nothing
consent thereto ne assent for no manner thing. There anon^ after it happed that
the earl of warrewyk came thidderward for to werre / And wha^ the Frensshme^
herd of his coming. er that he came fully to land. they left her te^tes and
pauillons with all her vitailles. and fledden and went away preuely / And when
the earl was comen to land with his men / he went in all have toward Norma^dye
and destroyed the I Will of Caws: through dynt of swerd and through fire / but allas
in his retournyng to England ward home ayen^ at Caleys / he was take wit
sikenesse of Pestilence and deied / not leuy^g behy^de him aftyr his days so
noble a knight and orped of arms In which time reigned and werred ye orped
knight sir Ioha^ hawkewode that was an Englysshme^ borne hauy^g with him at his
governance that whit company that is a fore nempned^ the which some time
ayens holy church and some time ayens lords werred and ordained great
batailles. and therein that co^tre he did many mervaillous things. And about
ye conversion of saint Paul the king wha^ he had ended and done the enthering
and the axequyes wit great costs and rialtes about the sepulture and berieng
of queen Phelypp his wife: he held his parliament at Westmynster / in which
parliament was axed of the clergy three dismes: that is for to say a great
disme to be paid three year dury^g And the clergy put it of and would not
grant unto Estre next coming / and than they granted well that i^ three year
by certain terms that disme should be paid / and also of ye lay fee was a
iij.xviiies granted to the king to be paid in three years

How sir Robert knolles with other certain lords of the reaume went over the sea into france and of her governance Capitulo CCxxxiiij.
ANd in the xlv. year of king Edward in the begynny^g king Edward wit unwise
counceyll And indiscreet borewed a great sum of gold of the prelatz lords
marchau^ts and other rich men of his reaume seeing yt it should be dispended in
defendy^g of holy church and of his reaume neuerthelater it profyted naught.
wherefore about mydsomer aftir he made a great host of the worthiest men of
his reame among who^ were some lords. that is for to say the lord fitz
water: and the lord graunson and other worthy knights: of which knights the
king ordained sir Robert knolles a proved knight and a well assaied in deed of
arms for to be governor / and that through his cou^ceill and governance all
thing should be governed and dressed. and when they came^ into france as long
as they dwelled and held hem hool to gedre the Fre^sshmen durst not fall upon
he^ And at the last about the beginning of winter for envy and couetyse that
was among he^ and also discord they sondred and parted he^ into diverse
co^panyes unwisely and folely. But sir Robert knolles and his men wente^ and
kepte^ he^ saufwithy^ a castle in britaigne. And when the fre^sshme^ saw that
our men were divided into diverse companies and places not holdyng ne
stre^gthyng he^ to gedres as they ought for to do / fylle^ fersely on our men.
and for the most party toke^ he^ or slowe^ he^: and tho that they took. led
with he^ prisoners. And in the same year Pope Urban came fro Rome to Auion^ for
encheson and cause yt he should accord and make pees bitwen^ the king of France
and the king of England for evermore: but allas or he began his tretes / he
deyed with sikenes the xxi. day of Dece^bre: And was buried as for the time i^
the cathedral church^ of Auion^ fast by the hygh^ auter^ and the next year
after / when he had leyne so / his bones were taken out the erth^ and buried
new in the abbey of sei^t victour fast by Marcill. of which abbeye he was
some time abbot hy^ self And in both^ places yt he was buried in. there be many
great miracles done and wrought through the g^ce of god almighty. and after who^
folewed next and was made pope Gregoire Cardinal Deke^: yt before was called
piers rogier. In the same year the cite of rimoge rebelled and faught aye^s the
pry^ce as other cites in Guyhe^ne did for great taxes costages and rau^sones
that they were put and set to by pry^ce edward / which charges weren
importable and to chargeable. wherefore they turned fro hy^ and fyllen to the
king of France. And when pry^ce Edward saw this: he was sore chafed and
grieved and in turnyng hom^ward ayen^ into England wit sore scarmysshes and
fighty^g and great assautes fought with he^ and took ye forsaid cite and
destroyed it almost to the ground and slow all yt were found in the cite /
and tha^ for diverse sikenesse and maladies that he had / and also for defaute
of money that he not might wythsto^de ne tarry on his enemies: he hyed hy^
ayene into England / with his wife and his meyne / leuyng behind him in
gascoygne the duke of Lancastre and sir Edmond Earl of Cambrygge with other
many worthy and orped men of arms: In the xlvi. year of king Edward at the
ordenau^ce and sendy^g of king Edward the king of Nauerne came to hy^ to
Clary^gdon / to trete with him of certain things touching his werre in
Normandye. where king edward had left certain seges in his stead till he came
home ayene. But king Edward might not speed of that that he asked of him. And
so the king of Nauerne wit great wurship and great yeftes took his leave and
went home again And about the beginning of March wha^ the parliament at
westmy^ster was begone. the king axked of the clergy a subsidy of.l.M.
pownde. the which by a good auyseme^t and by a general co^uocacyon of the
clergy it was granted and ordained that it should be paid and raised of the
lay fee. And in this parliament at the request and askyng of the lords in
haterede of men of holy church the chaunceler and the tresorer that were
bysshoppes / and the clerk of the pryve seall were remeued and put out of
office: and in her stead were seculer men put in And while this parliament
lasted there came sole^pne embassatours sent fro ye pope to trete with the king
of pees and sayden: that the pope desired to fulfill his p^decessours will /
but for all her coming they sped not of her purpose.

Of the besegyng of Rochel* and how the earl of Penbroke and his company was
there take in the haven with Spaynardes. and all his vessels brent Capit /
CCxxxv
THe ix. day of Iuyne king Edward in the xlvij year of his regne held his
parliament at wy^chestre. and it lasted but vij days / to the parliament were
sompned by write of men of holy church iiij bysshoppes / and iiij abbotes
wytoute any mo. This parliament was holden for marchau^ts of London: of Norwych
and of other diverse places for diverse things and points of treson that they
were difamed of. that is for to say that they were rebelle and would rise
ayens the king.

This same year the duke of Lancastre and the earl of Cambryge his brother
came^ owte of Gascoigne into England. and toke^ and wedded to their wifes
petres daughters sometime king of Spaygne / Of which two daughters the duke
had the elder / and the earl the yo^ger: and that same time there were sent two
cardinals fro the pope. that is to say. an Englyssh cardinal and a Cardynall
of Paris to trete of pees between the ij reaumes: the whych^ when they had be^
both long each in his prouy^ces / and in places and in contres fast by tretyng
of the forsaid pees / at the last they took with hem her lre^s of procuracie.
and went again to the court of Rome ward / withowte any effect of her purpose.
In this same year also there was a strong bataill on the sea bytwen^
Englysshme^ and Fle^my^ges and the Englisshmen had the victory and toke^ xxv.
ships charged wit salt. sleyeng and drenchy^g all the men that were theryn /
vnwyty^g hem that they were of that co^tre: And redly moch^ harm had fall
because thereof / ne had pees and accord ye sonner between he^ be made: And in
this same year the Fre^sshme^ besieged the town^ of Rochell: wherefore the earl
of Pe^broke was sent into Gascoigne with a great company of men of arms for
to destroy the siege The whych^ passed the sea and came sauf to the Haven of
Rochell / and when they were there at the haven mouth or that they might enter
/ suddenly came upon he^ a strong nauye of Spaigne / the which overcame tho ye
Englysshmen in moch^ blemysshyng hurtyng and sleyng of many persons / for as
much as the Englysshme^ were not than ready for to fight ne ware of he^. and
in the comi^g upon of the Spaignardes all the Englysshme^ other they were take
or slain. and.x. of hem were wounded to the deth^ and all her ships bre^t /
and there they took ye earl wit an huge tresoure of ye reame of england / and
many other noble men also on mydsomer even the which is sei^t Etheldredes day.
and ledden hem with hem into Spaigne / And of this meschief was no great wonder
for this earl was a full evil liver as on open lechour. and also in a certain
parliament he stood and was aye^s the ryghtes and frau^chyses of holy church^.
And also he counceylled ye king and his cou^ceill that he should axke more of
men of holy church tha^ of other persons of the lay fee / And for that the
king and other of his cou^ceil accepted and toke^ rather evil opynyo^s and
causes aye^s me^ of holy church / than he did for to defend and maynten^ the
right of holy church: it was seen many times after for lake of fortune and
grace / they had not ne bear awey so great victory ne power ayens her enemies
/ as they did a fore. This same year the king with a great host entered the sea
to remeue the sege of Rochell. but ye wy^de was even contrary unto hy^ and
suffered him not long time to go far fro the land. wherefore he abode a certain
time upon the sea costs abydyng after a good wind for hem / and yet came it
not so at ye last he came thens with his men to land ward ayen^ / and anon^ as
he was a land. the wind began to turn and was in an other cost tha^ he was
in a fore

How the duke of Lancaster wit a great host went into Flau^dres. and passed by
Paris through burgoigne / and through all France till he came to Burdeux Cap.
cc.xxxvi.
SOne after in the xlviij year of the regne of king Edward the duke of
Lancaster with a great host went into flau^dres and passed by Paris through
Burgoigne and through all France till he came to Burdeux wytoute any manner
withsto^dy^g of ye fre^shmen / and he did hem but littell harm save he took
and rau^soned many places and tounes and many men and let hem after gon^ freely
/ The same year the king sent certey^ embassatours to the pope prayng him that
he should leave of and meddle not in his court of the kepinges and reseruacyo^s of
benefyces in e^glo^d / and that they that were chose^ to bisshoppes sees and
dignites freely and with full right might joy and have and be confermed to the
same of her metropolytanes and erhebysshoppes as they were wont to be of old
time. Of thees points and of other towchyng ye king and his reame when they
had her a^swere of the pope / the pope enjoined he^ that they should certefye
him ayene by her lre^s of the ky^ges will and of his reame or they determined
ought of the forsaid articles. In the sam^ year deyde Ioha^ the erchebisshop of
york. Ioha^ bishop of Ely / william bishop of wurcestre: jn whose stedes
followed and were made bysshoppes by auctorite of the pope Master alixa^dre
neuill to ye erchebisshoprich^ of york. Thoa^s of Aru^del to ye bisshoprych^ of
Ely. and sir Henry wakefeld to ye bisshopryche of wurchestre / In ye which
time it was ordained in ye perleme^t yt all cathydrall chyrches should joy and
have her electyons hool: and yt the king afterward should not write ayens he^ yt
were chose^. but rather help he^ by his lre^s to her confirmacyon And this
statute was kept and did moch^ profyt and good. And in this parliament was
granted to ye king a disme of ye clergy: and xv of ye lay fee The next year
aftir of king edward ye xlix / the xv / day of Iuyne deyde maistyr william
witlesey erchebysshop of canterbury / wherefore the monks of the same church^
asked and desired a cardinal of England to be erchebisshop / and therefore ye
king was agreued and had me^t and purposed to have exilled ye monks of the
same house / and so they spe^ded moch^ good or they might have ye ky^ges g^ce
aye^ and his love but yet would the king not co^se^t ne grant to her electyo^
of the cardinal / ne ye pope also ne his cardinals / and about the begy^ny^g
of August it was treted and spoken at brugges of certey^ poi^tz and articles
beuy^g bitwene the pope and ye king of England. and this tretis last almoost
ij. year: At the last it was accorded between hem that the pope fro that time
forth should not use ne dele with the reseruacions of benefyces i^ england. and
that the king should not gra^te ne let no bn^fyces by his write. that is called
quare i^pedit. but as touchy^g the electyo^s above said: there was no thy^g
touched ne do: and yt was wyted and put upon certain clerks the which rather
supposed and hoped to be auau^ced and promoted to bisshopriches / which they
desired and coueyted by ye court of Rome rather tha^ by any electyo^s This
sam^ year about ca^delmasse there mete to gedres at Burges many noble and
worthy men of both reames to trete of pees between the two ky^gdomes: And this
tretys lasted two year with great costs and houge expe^ses of both^ parties.
And at the last they went and departed the^s without any accord or effect /
The next year after the l. year of king Edward iiij. non as of May being void
and vacau^t ye Erchebisshopryche of Canterbury Master Symo^d sudbery bishop
of London was made Erchebisshop. and maistir Willya^ Curteney that was bishop
of Herford was than made bishop of London / and the bishop of bangore was
made bisshopp of Herford / And this same time in a certain tretys and speking
of pees: trews was take between France and England fro mydsomer to mydsomer
come ayen^ all an hole year. and about the begynny^g of April the duke of
Brytaigne with many earls barons and other worthy men of england went over see
into Britaigne where they had all their lust desire and purpose / ne had ye
foresaid trews be so sone take. the which let hem much this same time: The
I Will Consta^tyne where that yt castle of seint savor is in that long time was
fowghten and beseged of the Frensshme^ was tha^ yolden to the Frensshmen with
all the apportenau^ces into great harm and hyndryng of the reame of England /
And this same year there were so great and passing hetes that therwyth all a
great pestylence in England and in other diverse parties of the world: that it
destroyed and slow vyolently and stro^ghly both men and woman wytoute no^bre /
This same year deyed sir Edward the lord spencer a worthy knight and a bold.
and in the my^ster of Tewkesbury wurshipfully is buried. and lastyng this
pestilence the pope at the instau^ce and prayer of an Englyssh Cardinal
grawnted to all people that deyde in England that were sorry and repentau^t for
her sins and also shryuen full remyssyon by.ij bulls under leed.vj mo^thes
tha^ next to last. In this same year the Earl of Penbroke was taken and
rawnsoned by Bartra^ cleykyn between Paris and Caleys as he came toward England
upon saint Etheldredes day. the which seint as it was said the same earl
oftetymes had offended. and withyn a while after he deide. and in noue^bre next
after there met at Bryges the duke of Lancastre and the duke of Angeoy wit
many other lords and prelates of both reames for to trete of pees

Of the death of Prince Edward and of the lord Latimer and Dame Alyce peers
through whom and her may^tenours the Reame many a day was mysruled Ca cc.xxxvij
NOt long aftir the lj. year of king Edwardes regne he let ordeyne and hold
at west mynstre the grettest perleme^t that was seen many a year afor^: in ye
which perlement he axed of the co^munalte of the reame as he had done before a
great subsidy to be granted to him for defendyng of him and of his reame. but
the communes a^sweryd that they were so often day by day grieved and charged with
so many tailliages and subsidies that they might no longer suffer non^ such^
charges: and that they knew and wiste well that the king had ynow for sauy^g of
him and of his reame. if the reame were well and truwely gouerned^ but that it
had be so long evil gouernyd by evil offyciers that the reame might nether
be plenteuous of chaffare and marchau^dise ne of richesse: And these things
they profred hem self. if ye king would certeynly to preue and sto^d by / And if
it were fond and preued after that. that the king had need. they would than
gladly every men aftyr his power and state hy^ help and lene / And after this
there were publysshed and showed in ye parliament many pleyntes and defautes of
diverse offyciers of the reame. and namely of the lord Latimer the kings
Chamburleyne both to the king and eke to the reame / And also at the last there
was spoken and treted of Dame Alice peers for the great wrongs and evil
governance that was done by her and by her cou^ceill in the reame: the which
dame Alyce peers the king had hold long time to his lemmen. wherefore it was
the less wonder though through ye freelte of the woma^nys excity^g and stery^g
he consented to her lewdness and evil cou^ceill. ye which dame alice and
also ye lord latymer and other such^ that stered ye king to evil governance
aye^s his profit and ye reames also / all the comminalte axed and desired
that they should be meved and put away: And in her stedes wise men and worthy
that weren true and well assayed and proved and of good governance should be
put in her stedes / So among all other: there was one among the co^munes that
was a wise knight and a true and an eloque^t man whose nam^ was piers de
lamare: and this same Piers was chosen to be speker for the co^munes in the
parliament And for this same piers told and plublisshed the truth and rehearsed
the wrongs aye^s the foresaid dame alyce and other certey^ persons and the
kings cou^ceyll as he was desired by the co^munes And also trusty^g moch^ for
to be supported and may^tened in this matter by help and favor of the pry^ce:
Anon as the pry^ce was deed at ye instau^ce and request of the foresaid dame
Alyce this Piers de lamare was iugged to perpetual prison in the castle of
Nothyngam: in ye which he was two year: and in ye vj. kal of Iuyll lasty^g
that same parliament deyed pry^ce Edward king edwardes first sone that is to sey
on the trinite sunday in the wurship: of whych^ fest he was wo^t every year:
where that ever he were in the world to make and hold the most solempnyte that
he might. whose name and fortune of knighthode / but if it had be of an other
Ectour all men both christian and hethen while he lived and was in good point
wondered moch^ and drad him wonder sore whose body is wurshipfully buried in the
church at Caunterbuey. And in this same year: the men and the Earls tenau^tes
of warrewyk aryse^ malicyously aye^s ye abbot and ye covent of Ensham and her
tenau^tz. and destroyed fiersly ye abbot and ye town and wounded and bet her
me^ and slowe^ of he^ many one / and we^te^ to her manners and places. and did
moch^ harm and breke^ down her parkes and her closes and brente^ and slowe^
her wild bestes and chached he^ brekyng her fisshpondes hedes and let the
water of her po^des stews and ryuers re^ne out and toke^ the fyssh and bear it
with he^ and did he^ all ye harm that they might in so ferforth that forsooth
they had destroyed perpetuely that abbey with all her me^bres and appertenau^ces.
but if the king the so^ner had helped it and take heed thereto. and therefore the
king sent his lre^s to ye Earl of Warrewyk chargy^g hy^ and conn^^u^dy^g that
he should redress and amend tho evil doers and brekers of his pees: and so by
many lords and other fre^des of both^ sides pees and good accord and love was
made bitwen^ hem. and for this hurly^g as it was said / ye king would not be
governed at yt time by his lords yt there were in ye perleme^t. but he took and
made his sone the duke of Lancastre his governor of ye reaum^ / the which
stood so still as governor till ye time yt he deyde. The same year anon^ after
ca^delmasse or ye perleme^t was done ye king asked a subsidy of the clergy
and of ye lay fee / and it was granted him / that is for to say that he should
have of every person of the lay fee both of man and woman that passed xiiij
year age iiij. pens: owtake pour beggars. that were know openly for nedy
pour beggars: and that he should have of every man of holy chyrch^ that was
benefyced or promoted xij pe^s^ and of other that were not promoted iiij. pens
/ owtake the iiij ordes of the freris beggars This same year after michelmasse
Rychard prince Edwardes sone was made pry^ce of Walys / to who^ the king yafe
also the duchy of Cornewaill wit the Erledome of Chestre: And about this time
the Cardinal of England / the iiij. day before Marie magdalene day after mete
suddenly was smyte^ and take wit a palasye and lost his speech. and on marie
madalene day he deyde

Of the death of king Edward and sir joha^ mo^sterworth knight was draw and
honged for his falsenesse Capitulo CCxxxviij
RIght anon after in ye.lij. year of king Edward in ye begy^ny^g of octobre
pope Gregory the xj. brought and remeued his court with hy^ from Auyon^ to
rome: And the xij day of apryl Ioha^ mo^sterworth knight at london was draw
honged and tha^ beheded / and after his body quartred / and sent to iiij. chief
towns of england: and his head set upon london brygge: for this same johan
was full untrue to the king and to ye reame. and full covetous and unstable
for he took oftetymes great sommes of money of the king and his cou^ceil for
men of arms wages that he should have paid he^: and took it to his own use:
and he dredy^g that at the fast he should be she^d and accused for ye same cause
fled puely to ye king of france and was swore to him and became his man. and
behight hy^ a great nauye out of spaygne in to confusion and destroyeng of
England / but rightful god to whom no pryuete is unknown suffered hy^ first to
be she^d and spylt* or that he so traytoursly and falsely his liege lord the
king of England and his people and his reaume. in the whych^ ground the same
Ioha^ was bore / wykkedly through bataill to destroy or bry^g his kursyd
purpose about. In the fest of saint gregory tho next after / king Edward yafe
to Rychard of Burdeux: his heir / that was pry^ce Edwardes sone at wy^desore
the order of knighthode and made him knight / the whych^ king Edward wha^ he
had reigned lj year and more. the xj kal of Iuyne he deyde at shene / and is
buried worshipfully at westmy^stre on whose soul god have mercy^ ame^. And this
king edward was for soth^ of a passy^g goodness and full gracyous among all ye
worthy men of ye world / for he passed and shone by virtue of grace yone to him
fro god above all his predecessors that were noble men and worthy^ and he was
a well and a hardy herted man. for he dread never of no myshapes ne harms ne
evil fortune that might fall a noble werriour and a fortunat for both on lo^d
and on see and in all batailles and assembles with a passy^g glory and joy
he had ever the victory / he was meke and beningne: homel / sobre and soft to
all manner of men / as well to straungiers as to his own subgettes / and to
other that were under his governance he was deuote and holy both^ to god and
to holy church / for he wurshipped / halpe and may^tened holy church and her
ministres with all manner reverence. he was tretable and well auysed in temporal
and wordly needs wise cou^ceyl. and discrete soft and meke. and good to speak
with / in his deeds and manners full gentle / and well taught hauy^g pity of
hem that were in disese. plentous in yeuy^g bn^faytes and almasse. besy and
curiouse i^ byldy^g and full lightly he bare and suffered wro^ges and harms: and
when he was give to any occupacyon. he left all other thing forth: mean time
tendyd and there to semely of body and amene stature hauy^g allwey to hygh^ and
to low a good chere. and there spra^ge and shone somoche grace of him that what
manner man had behold his face or had dremed of him / he hoped that day that
all thing should hap to hy^ ioyefull and lykyng. and he governed gloriousely
his kingdom unto his age / he was large in yevy^g and wise in spe^ces / he was
fulfyld with all honest of good manners and virtues vndyr whom to live it was
as for to reign: wherefore his fame his loose sprange so far that it came
i^to hethenesse and barbary shewy^g and tellyng his worthynesse and ma^hood in
all lands: and that no land under heve^ had brought forth so noble a king so
gentle and so blesshed or might reise such^ an othyr if he were deed.
nevyrthelater lecherye and mevyng of his flesh haunted him in his age.
wherefore the rather as it is to suppose for unmeasurable fullfyllyng of his lust
his life shorted the sonner: and here of take good head like as his deeds
before bear witness for as in his begy^nyng all things were ioyefull and
lykyng to him / and to all people. And in his mydde age he passed all people in
hygh^ joy. wurshipp and blessedness: right so when he drew into age drawy^g
dou^ward through lechery and other sins littell and littel all tho ioyefull
and blesshed things and prosperity decreced and misshaped and infortunat
things and unprofitable harms wit many euelles began for to spra^ge and to
more harm it continued long time after

How that after king Edward the thridde that was bore in wy^desore reigned
Richard of Burdeux: that was prince Edwardes sone of Walys / which prince
Edward was the sone of king Edward Capit. CCxl.
ANd aftir the good king edward the iij. that was bore at wy^desore reigned
Rychard the ij. that was the good sir Edwardes sone pry^ce of Walys. which
king Richard was borne in ye cite of Burdeux in Gascoigne and was crouned at
westmy^ster in the xi. year of his age. and in the second year of his regne
for debate that was between the lord Latimer and sir Rauf feriers knight: yt
weren ayens hawell and shakell squyers: for ye prisoner that was take in the
bataill of Spaygn^ by these ij squyers. and the which the lord Latimer and sir
Rauf feriers would have had / the which prisoner was the Earl of Dene yt they
took in ye bataill of spaygn^. wherefore these two lords camen into the chyrch^
at Westmynstre and fou^den this one Squire heryng his mass beside sey^t
Edwardes shrine / and there they slow hy^. the which was called Hawell / and
shakell was arested and put in the toure of London / and there he was long
time for he would not deliver the earl of Dene his prisoner unto thees two
lords. by sir Aleyn buxhill constable of the tour / And by sir Rauf feriers
one of his aduersairas till the king granted hy^ grace / In the thridde year
of king Richard came the galeys of France into england unto diverse ports
brent and robbed and slow moch^ people of England. that is to say / at
wy^chelsee. Rye. and Hastyng / portesmouthe. Ha^pton. stormore and grauesende /
and dyde^ moch^ harm. and went home ayen^: And in this same year was a
parliament holde^ at westmynster: and at that perleme^t was ordained that every
man / woman and child that were^ at the age of xiiij. year and above:
thurghoute all the reame pore folk and other should pay to the tallage iiij
pens / wherefore came and befell afterward great meschief and much disese to all
the co^minalte of the reame. And in the iiij. year of king rychardes regne the
communes risen up in diverse parties of the reame. and dyde^ moch^ harm / the
which they kalled the hurlyng time and they of Kent and of Estsex made hem in
cheuytaynes to rule and govern ye company of Ke^t and of Estsex / that one
was kalled jake straw and that other was tiler: and they came^ and assembled
he^ upon the blake heth i^ kent on the corpus xp^i day. and after they came^
down in sowthwerk and breke^ up the prison house that is to say the kings
be^che. and the marchalsie and deliured out all the prisoners. And so the same
day they came^ into London / and there they robbede^ the people and slow all
alyents that they might find in the cite and about the cite: and despoilled
all her gooddes and made hauoke / And on ye friday next after that was on the
morn they came^ tha^ to the tour of London / and the king being theryn they
fet out of the tour the erchebisshop of Canterbury / sir Edmond sudbery and
sir Robert haleys hospitaler priour and master of seint Ioha^nes house and a
white friar that was confessor to king Rychard / and brought hem unto the
tower. and there they smyten of her hedes and came ayen^ to London: and slow
moo people me^ of laws. and other worthy men in diverse parties of the cite /
And tha^ they went unto the dukes places of Lancastre beyond sey^t marye
stro^de that was called the sauoy. and there they deuored and destroyed all the
gooddes that they might find there and bare he^ away / and brende^ up the
place And than after they went to saint joha^nes without smythfeld and
destroyed the gooddes there / and brent up that house and went to Westmy^ster
and seint martins grant and made hem gone out of the sei^twarie all that were
withy^. for any manner of gryth And than came unto the temple and to all other
ynnes of men of law. and despoilled he^ and robbed he^ of her goods. and also
tare her books of law. and tha^ they came^ to London and brak up the prison
newgate and drofe out all the prisoners felo^s and other and of both
countours. and all the people that were withyn he^ and destroyed all the books
of both cou^ters / And thus they continued both satyrday and sunday unto the
mo^day next after in her malice and wikkednesse. and than on the monday king
Rychard with his lords that were with hy^ that time and wit the mayre of
London William walworth that was ye time comen with the alderme^ and the communes
of ye cite / and came in southwerke to here and to know the inte^cyon of these
rebels and mysgouerned people: and this Iake straw tha^ made an oye in the
feld that all the people of accord should come nere and here his proclamacyo^ his
cry and his will / And the lords and the mayre and ye alderme^ wit the
co^minalte having indignacio^ of his couetyse and falsenesse and his foul
p^su^pcyon. And anon^ william walworth ye time being mayr drowe out his knyf
and slow Iak straw: and anon^ right there did of smite his head: and set it
upon a spear shafte. and so it was bear through london and set an hygh^ upon
london brigge. Anon^ as thees rysers and mysgouerned me^ were void and clean
vanisshed as it had naught be they / than ye king of his great goodness and by
prayer of his lords made there vj. knights of good and worthy men of the cite
of london that is to say. William walworth that that time was mayre and slow
Iak straw: The second was Nycholas bre^bre. and the thridde johan philiptot:
and the iiij. nycholas Twiford / and the v. Robert lau^des / the vj. Robert
Gayton. And than the king with his lords and his knights returned ayen^ unto
the tour of London / and there he rested him till the people were better seted
and set in rest and pees / and than by process of time as they might get
and take these rebels and rysers they henge hem upon the nex galewes in every
lorshyp thurghoute the reame of england by xl. and by xxx / by x. and by xij /
ever as they might be geten and taken in any parties / And in the v. year of
king Rychardes regne was ye great earth quak* and was generally through out
the world / ye wonesday after witsonday in the year of our lord M.ccc.lxxxxi /
whereof all manner people were sore aghast and dred full long time for dread of
vengeance that our lord showed and did / and in the vj year of the regne of
king Richard sir Henry spencer bishop of Norwiche went with a croiserie over
the sea into ye country of Flau^dres. and there they gate the town of
grauenyng and ye town of broburgh / dunkerk and newport. and there they laded
and fraught.^j. ships with pelage for to have come into England with these
ships and gooddes / And ye bishop of Norwych and his cou^ceil let brenne
thees ships wit all ye pelage in the same haven all into hard ashes: and at
Dunkerke was done a great bataille between the Fle^my^ges and the Englysshme^ /
and at that bataille was slain a great multitude of the Fle^my^ges and an huge
no^bre. and than went the bishop with his retenwe unto ypre / and beseged it a
long time. but it might not be gotten. and so he left that siege / and came
ayen^ into England: for our Englysshme^ were foull destroyed. and many deyed on
the flixe And in this same year came queen Anne into england for to be spoused
unto king Rychard: and her fadre was Emperor of Almaigne and king of Beme. and
with her came the duke of Tassy her uncle / and many other worthy lords and
knights of her co^tre of Beme and of other duche tou^ges to do her reverence
and wurship And sir simo^d Beuerle a worthy knight of the garter. and other
knights and squyers that were^ the kings Embassatours brought hyre in
England. and so forth to London. And the people of the cite that is to seye the
Mayre and ye aldermen and the co^munes ridde^ aye^s her to welcome her. and
every man in good array and every craft with his mynstralsie in the best manner
mete with her on the blakheth in kent. and so brought her unto London through
the cite / and so forth unto westmynstre unto the ky^ges paleys / and there she
was spoused unto king Rychard well and worthily in the abbey of westmynstre. and
there she was crowned quen^ of england And all her friends that camen with her
hadde^ great yeftes and were^ well chered and refresshed as long time as they
abyde^ here. And in this same year was a bataille done in the kings paleys at
westmynstre for certain poy^tes of treson between sir Ioha^ ansley knight
defendant and Carton squier appelau^t. but this sir Ioha^ of a^sley overcame
this Carton and made him to yield him withyn ye lystes and anon^ was this
Carton despoilled of his harneys and drawn out of the lystes / and so forth
to Tiborne: and there he was honged for his falsenesse / And in ye viij year of
the regne of king Rychard sir Edmond of La^gely earl of Ca^brigge the ky^ges
uncle went into portyngale wit a fair meyne me^ of arms and archiers in
stre^gthyng and helpyng of the king of Portyngale ayens the king of Spaygne and
his power: And there the king of Porty^gale had the victory of his enemies
through help and comfort of our Englysshme^ / And when that journey was done
the earl of Ca^brygge came home aye^ with his people into england in haste
blessed be god and his gracyous yifte. am^ And this same year king richard
held his Crystmasse in the march of Eltham. And the same time the king of
Ermonye fled owte of his own land and came into England for to have socour
and help of our king ayens his enemies that had driven hy^ out of his Reame
And so h^e was brought unto the king to Eltha^ there as the king held his
ryall fest of Cristmasse: and there owr king welcomed him and did him moch^
reverence and wurshipp. and commanded all his lords to make hy^ all the chere
that they cowde / And than he besought ye king of grace and of help and of his
comfort in his need And that he might be brought ayene to his kingdom and
lord: for the Turks had devoured and destroyed the most part of his lord:
and for this cause he fled and came thither for socour and help / And the
king then^ having pity and co^passyon of his great meschief and grevous disese
anon he took his counceyll and asked what was best to done And they answered
and said. if it lyked him to give him any good^ it were well y done: and as
towchyng his people to trauaylle so far in to out lands it were a great
jupardie / and so the king yafe hy^ gold and silver and many rychesses yeftes
and iewelles and betaught him to god. and so he passed ayene out of england:
And in this same year king Rychard wit a ryall power went into Skotland for to
werre upon the scotts for the falsenesse and destruction that the Scotts had
done unto the Englysshme^ in the marches. And tha^ the scotts came unto the
king for to entrete wit him and his lords for trewes as for certain years.
And so our king and his cou^ceyll granted he^ trewes certain years unto her
askyng / and our king turned hi^ home ayen^ into England: And when he was come
unto york there he abode and rested him / And there sir Johan hola^d earl of
Ke^tes brother slow the Earls sone of Stafford and his heir with a Dagar in
th^e cite of york. wherefore the king was sore ameued and grieved / and remeued
the^s and came to London. And the mayre with the alder men and the communes
with all the solempnite yt might be done ryden aye^s ye king / and brought him
ryally through the cite and so forth unto westmynster. unto his own paleys: And
in ye ix. year of king Rychardes regne / he held a perlement at westmy^ster
and there he made two dukes and a marqueyes and v. earls / The first yt was made
duke was the kings uncle. sir Edmond of Langlee earl of Cambrigge: and hy^ he
made duke of york / And his other uncle sir Thomas of wodestoke that was earl
of Bukkyngham / him he made duke of Gloucestre And sir Lyonevere that was earl
of Oxu^ford him he made markeys of Dyueleyne. And Henry of Bolyngbroke / the
dukes sone of Lancastre / hy^ he made Earl of Derby / And sir Edward the sone
of york / hi^ he made Earl of Rutcelo^d: Sir Ioha^ Hola^d that was the earls
brother of Kent him he made Earl of Hu^ty^gdo^. Sir thomas monbray earl of
Nothy^gha^ and Earl marchall of England. And sir Mychell de la pole knight. hy^
he made Earl of Sowthfolk and chaunceler of England. And the earl of March at
that same parliament holden at Westmy^ster in plain perlement among all other
lords and co^munes was proclaimed earl of the March heir apperant to the
crown of England after king Rychard / the which earl of the March went over
see into Irland unto his lordshippes and lands: for the Earl of the march is
Earl of Vlster in Irland by right line and heritage / and there at ye castle of
his he lay that time And there came upon him a great multitude in bussheme^tys
of wild Irisshmen hy^ for to take and destroy / and he came owte fersely of
his his castle with his people and ma^ly faught wit hem. and there he was take
and hew all to pieces. and there he deyde / On whose soul god have mercy. Amen
And in the x. year of king Rychardes regne the earl ot Arundell went unto the sea / wit a great Nauye of ships enarmed with me^ of arms and good archiers:
And when they camen into the broad see they met wit the hole flete that camen
wit wine laden from Rochel. the which wine were enemies goodes^ and there our
nauye set upon hem and took hem all and browght hem unto diverse ports and
hauenes of England: and some to london / and there ye might have had a tonne of
rochel wine of the best for xx. shilli^g sterlynges. and so we had great chepe
of wine thurghoute the reaume at that time. thanked be god almighty

How the v. lords arysen at rattecoste brigge Capit. CC.xli
ANd in the Regne of king rychard the xi. year / v. lords aryse^ at rattecort
brigge in the destructyon of rebels that weren that time in all ye reame. The
first of the v. lords was Sir Thomas of Wodestoke the ky^ges uncle and duke of
Gloucestre. And the second was sir Rychard earl of Arundell / and the iij. was
sir Rychard earl of warrewyk. ye iiij was sir Henry boly^gbroke earl of Derby /
the v. was sir thoa^s Mo^bray Earl of nothy^gha^ / And these v. lords saw the
meschyef and mysgouernau^ce and the falsenesse of the ky^ges counceyll /
wherefore they that weren that time chyef of ye kings cou^ceyll fledde^ owte of
this la^d over the sea. that is to say. sir Alisau^dre neuill ye Erthebisshop
of york and sir Robert leveer markeys of Deuelyn and Earl of Ore^ford: and sir
Mychel de la po^le Earl of Sowthfolk and chau^cheler of england: And these iij
lords wente^ over the sea and came never ayen^ for they deyde. And tha^
these.v lords above said maden a perleme^t at westmy^stre: and there they took
sir Robert trefiliam chef justyce. and sir Nycholl bre^bre knight. and
cytezeyne of London / and sir Johan salibury knight of ye kings howshold and
vske / sergeau^t of arms and many mo of other people were^ take and iugged unto
ye death by ye cou^ceyll of these v. lords in her parliament at westmy^stre /
for treso^ that they put upon he^ to be drawn from ye tour of london
thurghoute the cite / and so forth unto Tyburne. and there they should be ho^ged
/ and there her trothetes to be kut. and thus they were served and deyd / And
after that in this same parliament at Westmynstre was sir Symo^d of Beuerlee /
that was a worthy knight of the garter and sir Johan beauchamp knight that was
stiward of the kings howshold / and sir james berners were iuged unto the death
/ and than they were lad on foot to the toure hill / and there were^ her hedes
smyten of / and many other mo by these v. lords In this same perlement and in
the xij year of king rychardys regne he let cry and ordeyne a general Ioustes
that is kalled a turneme^t of lords knights and Squyers: And this joustes and
turneme^t was holde^ at London in smythfeld of all manner of strau^giers of what
lord or country that ever they were: and thydder they were right welcome. and
to hem and to all other was holde^ open household and great festes. and also
great yeftes weren yeuen to all manner of strau^giers And of the kings side
were^ all of suit her cotes her armures sheldes horse trappure and all was white
hertes wit crowns about her nekkes and chains of gold hauy^g thereupon / and
the crown having low before the hertes body. The which heart was the kings
lyuery that he yafe to lords and ladies / knights and squyers / for to know
his household from other people. And in this fest coming to her joustes xxiiij
ladies: lad these xxiiij. lords of gartes with cheynes of gold / and all the
same suit of hertes as is before said from the tour an horsebak through the cite
of London into smythfeld there yt ye ioustes should be hold And this festes and
ioustes was hold general and to all thaym that would come of what land and
nacyon that ever they were / And this was hold during.xxiiij. days of the
kings cost / and thees xxiiij lords to a^swere all manner people that would come
thither: And thither came the Earl of saint Poule of Frawnce and many other
worthy knights / with hy^ of diverse parties full well araied / and out of
Holand and Henaud came ye lord Ostreuau^t / that was the dukes sone of Holand:
and many other worthy knights with him of Holand full well arrayed: And when
this feste and ioustes was ended. the king thanked these strau^giers and yafe
hy^ many great yeftes. And tha^ they token her leave of the king and of other
lords and ladies and we^te^ home ayene into her own co^tre with great love
and moch^ tha^k. And in the xiij year of king Rychardes regne there was a
bataill done in the ky^ges paleys at westmynstre / between a Squire of Nauerne.
that was with king rychard. and an other Squire that was kalled Johan Walsshe:
for points of treson that this Nauerous put upon this walsshma^ But this
Nauerous was overcome and yield him creaunt to his aduersayre And anon^ he was
despoiled of his armure and draw out of the paleys to Tibourne and there he
was honged for his falsenesse And the xiiij year of king Rychardes regne sir
Ioha^ of gau^te duke of lancaster went over the sea into Spaigne for to
challenge his right that he had by his wyfes title unto the croune of spaign^
wit a great host of people / of me^ of arms and archiers / and he had wit him
the duchess his wife and his iij daughters over the sea into spaign^ / And
there they were a great while: And at the last the king of Spaigne began to
trete with the duke of lancaster. and they were accorded to gedre through her
both counceill / in this manner yt the king of spaign^ should wedde the dukes
daughter of lancaster that was the right heir of Spaigne / and he should yeve
unto the duke of lancaster goold and silver that was cast into great wegges and
many other iewelles as many as viij chariettes might carry: and every year
after during the life of the duke of lancaster and of the duchess his wife
x.M. mark of gold of which gold ye adventure and charges they of spaign^ should
aue^ture and bry^g yearly unto bayone to the Dukes assigns by surete made /
Also the duke of lancaster married an other of his daughters unto ye king of
Portingale the same time: and when he had done thus he came home aye^ in
e^glo^d: and the good lady his wife also: But many a worthy man upon the flix
in yt viage deyed And in the xv. year of king rychardes regn^. he held his

sey^t joha^ and ride^ to gedre in the park of wodestoke. and there this worthy

hy^ / wha^ they had co^pled. and thus this good earl made there his end and

Ioha^ walworth and henry va^ner being sherewes of london yt same time a bakers

and would have arested this Romay^. and he brake from he^ and fled unto the

fast the yates and kept the place yt no man might enter: and tha^ moch^ more
people gadred thither. and said that he would have him out: or else they would
bre^ne up the place and all that were withyn / And than came the mayre and
sherewes with other much people and cessed the malice of ye co^munes. and made

And anon^ suddenly the king sent after ye mayre of London and for the two

sey^t Ioha^ Baptist. And tha^ the king kalled to hy^ a knight yt was called sir

hem hu^bely and mekely with all manner obeissau^ce unto him as they ought to
done. And thus they brought the king and the queen to london / And when the
king came as is foresaid to the yate of the brugge of London. there they

of gold and read parted to gedre. and the queen a palfrey all white: and in ye
same array trapped with white and reed / and all the condytes of London ronne^
wit white wine both^ white and read / for all manner people to drink of: And
bitwene saint poweles and the cross in cheep there was made a stage a ryall

and lordshyp and spicyall grace that they might have his good love with ye

pate^tz and his chartre confermed / and the quen^ and other worthy lords and
ladies fell on knees: and besought ye king of g^ce to co^ferme this thy^g: Tha^
ye king took up the queen and granted her all her askyng. and tha^ they
thanked the king and the queen and wente^ home ayen^. And in the xvi. year of
king Rychardes regne / certain lords of Skotla^d came into England to get

and lords certain courses. but not the full challenge that the Scottyssh earl
made / for he was cast both^ horse and man / and two of his rybbes broke wit

a littell time after he was carried hom^ward in a lytier: and at york there he
deyde. And sir Willyam Darell knight Banerer of scotland made an other challenge
with sir Piers courteyne knight and the kings banerer of England of certain

and he saw he might not have ye bettyr / he yafe it over and would no more of
his challenge and turned his horse and rode home to his own^ loggy^g. And one

englissh lords thanked be god hadde^ the field / And in ye xvij year of king
richardes regne deide ye good gracious quen^ Anne yt was wife to king Rychard

brought to london / and so to westmy^stre. and there was she beryed and
