ame^

How king Richard spoused dame Isabel the ky^ges daughter of france in ye
town of Caleys and brought her into England. and let her be crouned quen^ in
ye abbey of seint Peter's of westmy^stre. Ca. cc.xlij
In ye xx. year of king Richardes regne he went hi^ over the sea unto Caleys
with dukes Earls lords and barons and many other worthi squiers with great array
and conmune people of the reame in good array as than appertyned to such^ a
worthi king and prince of his nobley and of his own^ person to done hy^
reverence and obseruau^ce as ouzt to be done unto her liege lord as a mighty
king and emperor i^ his owene to abide and receive there that worthy and
gracyous lady that should ben^ his wife. a young creature of xix year of age
Dame Isabell the ky^ges daughter of France and many other worthy lords of
great name both barons and knights wit moch^ other people that camen unto the
town of Grauenyng / and ij. dukes of France: that one was the duke of
Burgoigne. and that other the duke of Barry: yt would no ferther less tha^ they
had plegges for he^. And tha^ the king Rychard delyured two plegges for hem to
go sauf and come sauf his two worthy uncles the Duke of Gloucestre and the duke
of york And they two wente^ over ye watyr of Graueny^g and abyde^ there as for
plegges unto ye time that the marriage and the feste was done and that thees ij.
dukes of france were come ayen^ unto the greueny^g watyr And than thees two
worty dukes came over the water at Graueny^g and so to Caleys with his
wurshipfull lady dame Isabell yt was the kings daughter of france / and with
her came many a worthi lord and ladi / knights and squyers in the best array
that might be. and there they metten with our meyne at Caleys / ye whych^
welcomed her and her meyne with the best honor and reverence that might be /
and so brought her in the town of caleys. and there she was received wit all
the sole^pnyte and wurship that might be done unto such a lady. and than they
brought her unto the king: and the king took her and welcomed her and all her
fair meyne. and made there all the solempnyte that might be done. And than the
king and his cou^ceill asked of ye Fre^ssh lords whethyr all the couenau^tes
and forewardes wit the compassyon that were ordained and made on both parties
should be trewly kept and hold between hem / And they said ye and there they
sworn and took her charge upon a book and made her oath well and trewely it to
hold in all manner points and couenau^ts withowte contrdaictyo^ or delay in
any manner wise And than was she brought unto seint Nycholas church in caleys.
and there she was worthily wedded with most sole^pnyte that any king or quen^
might be with the erchebisshop and bisshoppes and all mynystres of holy church
/ and than were^ brought home unto the castle and set to mete. And there were
served with all manner of delicasie of all ryall metys and drinks plenteuoisely
to all manner of stra^giers / and all other and no creature warned yt feste: But
all were welcome / For there weren great halles and tents set upon the grene
withowte the castle to receive all manner of people and every office ready to
serve he^ all / And thus this worthy marriage was solempnely done and ends
with all ryalte^ Than these two dukes of France with her people token her leave
of the king / and the queen and wenten ayen^ to Grauenyng water / And there the
Frenssh lords. that is to seye The two dukes and all her mesone were comen
over ye watyr to Greuenyng / and there they metten. and every took leave of
othyr. and so they departed / and owr lords camen again to Caleys / and the
Frenssh lords went over the watyr and so home into France ayene.

And anon^ aftyr the king made him ready with the queen and all his lords and
ladies and all her people with hem and camen over the sea into England. and so
to london. And the mayre and the shereues with all the aldermen and worthy
communes rydde^ ayens hem unto the blake heth in Ket: and there they metten
with ye king and the quen^ / and welcomed hem and that in good array / and every
man in the clothyng of his craft / and her mynystrelles to fore hem. and so
they brought hem unto sei^t georges bar in sowthwerke: and there they took
her leave and the king and the Queen rydden to Kenygton / and than the people of
london turned home ayen^. and in turnyng ayene to London brygge / there was
somoch^ press of people both an horse and on foot / that there were deed on the
brygge xj. persons of men. of women and of children On whose sowles almighty
god have pity and mercy / amen

And than aftyrward the queen was browght unto the tower of London: and there
she was all night. And on the morwe she was brought through the cyre of London
all over. and so forth unto Westmy^stre. and there she was crowned queen of
England: and than she was brought ayene to the ky^ges paleys. and there was
hold and open and a ryalle fest at her coronacyo^ of all manner of people that
thither came: And this was done the sunday next aftyr the feste of saint
Clement: In the xx. year of king Rychardes regne And tha^ the xxv. day of
August next after by evil excitacion and falls cou^ceill and for great wrath
and malice / that the king had of old time unto his uncle ye good duke of
gloucestre. and to the Earl of Arundell and to the Earl of Warrewyke. And anon^
the king by his evil excytacyon and his evil counceyll and malice late in the
eueny^g on the same day above said made him ready with his strength. and rode
into essex unto the town of Chelmesford / and so came to the place suddenly
there where that the good sir Thomas of wodestoke. the ge^till duke of
Glowcestre lay in his place / And than^e the good Duke came to welcome the king
anon^ And the king arested the good duke him self his own body / and so he
was lad down to ye watyr and anon^ put into a ship: and anon^ lad unto Caleys
and browght into the Capyteynes ward to be kept in hold by the kings
commandment of England. And that time ye earl Marchall was Capyteyne of
Caleys: and anon aftyr by the commau^deme^t of the king and by his false
cou^ceill commanded the capitey^ to put hy^ to death. and anon^ certain yomen
that had te good Duke in keeping / took her counceyl how that they would put him
unto the death: and this was her appoy^teme^t that they should come upon hy^ wha^
he were in his bed and a sleep on a fethyr bed / and anon^ they bound him
foot and hand. and charged him to lie still / and when they had done thus /
they toke^ two small towailles and made on hi^ two rid knottes and cast the
towailles about the Dukes nekke / and tha^ they toke^ the feather bed that
lay vndyr him and cast it above him / and tha^ they drowen her towailles each
weyes and some lay upon the fether bed upon him. unto the time that he were
deed. by cause that he should make no noise / and thus they stre^gled this
worthy Duke unto the death / On whose soul god for his hygh^ pity have mercy /
amen

And when the king had arested this worthy duke and his uncle and sent him to
Caleys: he came ayen^ to London in all have wit a wonder great people. and as soon as he was come he sent for the Earl of Aru^dell. and for the good earl of
warrewyk and anon^ as they came: he arestyd he^ him self / And sir Ioha^ Cobha^
and sir Ioha^ cheyne knights he arested he^ him self in ye same manner. till
he made his parliament* And anon^ they were put into hold / but ye earl of
Aru^dell went at large unto the parliament time / for he found sufrysant surete
to abide the lauwe and to a^swere all manner poy^tes that the king and his
con^ceyll would put upon hy^ / and in the xxi year of king Rychardes regne. he
ordained a parlemet at westmynster / the which was kalled the great parliament.
and this parliament was made for to judge this iij worthy lords and other mo.
as he^ list at this time. and for that iuggeme^t the king let make in all have
a long and a large hows of tymbre / the which was kalled an halle and covered
wit tyles over / and it was open all about on both sides. and at the ends /
that all manner of me^ might see thurghout: and there the dome was holden upon
these foresaid lords and iuggement yafe at this foresaid parliament. And for to
come unto this parliament the king sent his wryttes unto every lord baron
knight and squire in every shire throughoute all england that every lord gadre
/ and bring his retenue with him in as short time and in the best array that
they might get in mayntenyng and in strenghty^g of the king ayens he^ that
were his enemies / and that this were done i^ all ha^t and they to come to him
in pain of death. And the king hy^ selue sent into Cheshire unto the cheuitais
of that contre and they gadred and brought a great and an hugh^ multitude of
people both of knights and of squyers and principally of yome^ of Chestreshire
/ the which yome^ and archiers the king took to his own court / and yafe hem
bouge of court and good wages to be kepers of his own body both^ by night and
by day above all other persons / and most loved and bed trust. the which sone
afterward turned ye king to great loss / shame: hyndery^g and his vttyr
undoing and destruction as ye shall here sone aftyr. And yt time came sir Henry
Earl of derby with a great meyne of men of arms and archiers / and the earl of
Ruttela^d came with a strong power of people / both of men of arms and
archiers. And ye Earl of Kent browght a great power of men of arms and
archiers / The earl marchall came in the sam^ manner. The lord Spencer in ye
same manner: The Earl of Northumberland. and sir Henry percy his sone / and sir
Thomas percy his brother / and all these worthy lords broughte^ a fair meyne
and a strong power and each man in his best array And the duke of Lancaster and
te duke of york camen in the same manner with men of arms and archiers
following the king. And sir Wylliam strope tresorer of england came in the same
manner / and thus in this array came^ all the worthy men of this land unto our
king. and all this people came to London in one day / in somoche that every
street and lane in subarbes weren full of hem logged. and x. of xij. mile
about london every wey / And thees people brought the king at westmynstre. and
wenten home ayen^ to her loggynyng: both horse and man. And than on the mo^day
the xvij day of Septe^bre the perlement began at westmynstre / the which was
kalled the great perleme^t. And on the friday nex after the earl of Aru^dell
was brought into the parlemest among all the lords: and that was on saint
Mathews day the apostell and Evangelist / there hewes iugget unto the death in
this halle that was made in ye paleys at Westmynstre: And this was his judgment
that he should gon^ on foot with his hondes bownde behind him. from the place
that he was iuged in. and so forth throughout ye cite of London unto ye toure
hille and there his head to be smyten of. and so it was done in deed in the same
place: And vi. of ye great lords that sat on his iuggement ridde^ wit him
unto the place there he was done unto the death / and so to see that the
execucion were done after her dome and by the kings commandment with hem
wenten on foot of men of arms and archiers a great multitude: of chestre shire
men in strengthyng of the lords that brought this earl unto his death / for
they drad lest the earl should have be rescued and take from hem when they came
into London: Thus he passed forth through the cite unto his death. and there he
took it full pacientely: on whose soul god have mercy. am^ And than came the
freres Austyns and took up the body and the head of this good Earl and bare it
home unto her house. and buried hy^ in her quere: And in the morwe after was sir
rychard earl of warrewyk brought into the perlement there as the earl of
Arundel was iuged. and they yafe the earl of warrewyke the same judgment that
ye forsaid earl had / but ye lords had compassyon of him / be cause he was of
more age and relesed him to perpetual prison. and put him in the I Will of Man.
And tha^ the mo^day next aftyr the lord Cobham of Kent: and sir Johan cheyne
knight weren brought into the parliament into the same halle and there they were
iuged to be hanged and draw. but through the prayer and great instaunce of all
the lords that judgment was foryeve he^ and relesed to perpetual prison And
in this same time was Rychard whittyngdone mayre of London / and Johan
Wodestoke and Wylliam vskem shereues of London. And they ordained at every yate
of london during this same perlement strong wathe of men of arms and archiers
and thurghowte every ward also. And the king made v. dukes / a Duchess / and a
markeys. and four Earls. And the first of he^ was the earl of Derby. and he
was made duke of Hereford / and the second was the earl of Rutteland and he
was made duke of a wemarle: and the thridde was the earl of ke^t and he was
made duke of Furre / and the fourth was the Earl of Huntyngdone and he was
made duke of Excestre. and the v. was the earl of Notyngha^. and he was made
duke of northfolk and the earl of Somersete he was made ye markeys of Dorset.
And the lord spencer was made earl of Glowcestre / and the lord Neuill of Raby
was made earl of westmerland: and sir Thomas percy was made Earl of wurcestre:
And sir william scroppe that was tresorer of England he was made earl of
wylyshire. and sir Johan montagu Earl of Salysbury / And when the king had thus
done he held parliament and ryall fest unto all his lords and to all manner of
people yt thither came And this same year deied sir joha^ of Gau^t the kings
uncle and duke of Lancaster in the bisshoppes ynnem holborn. and was brought
from the^s to sey^t Poules. and there ye king made and held his entreme^t well
and worthily with all his lords in the chyrch^ of sey^t Poules in london and
there he was buried beside dame blau^ce his wife that was daughter and heir to
the good Henry yt was duke of Lancaster / And in the same year there fill a
discencyon and debate between the duke of hereford and the duke of northfolk.
in so moch^ yt they waged bataille and kast down her gloves / and tha^ they
were take up and enseled / and ye bataill joined and the day set and the place
assigned where and wha^ this should be at coue^tre. and thither came the king with
all his lords at yt day: and was set i^ the feld and tha^ thees worthy
lords came^ into the feld clean armed and well arrayed with all / and weren ready
to done her bataill in the place for to fight at vtteraunce. But the king bad
he^ cese and took the quarrel into his hond: And forth wit right there p^sent
exilled the duke of Hereford for the term of x. year: and the duke of
Northfolke for evermore: And sir Thomas Aru^dell erchebisshop of Canterbury
was exilled the sam^ time for ever and deposed out of his see for malice of
the king / And anon^ these iij. worthy lords were^ commanded and defended the
kings reame / and anon^ they gate he^ ships at diverse hauenes and we^te^
over the sea into diverse lo^des ech^ his wey. and the duke of northfolk went
to Venyce and there he deyed: on whose soul god have mercy / ame^ And tha^ king
Rychard made a clerk of his sir Rogier walde^ erchebisshop of Canterbury. And
in the xxij year of king Richardes regne by falls cou^ceill and ymaginacyo^ of
covetous men yt were^ about hy^ were made and ordeyne bla^ke chartres. and
made he^ to be e^seled of all manner rich me^ thurghoute the reame / in so
moch^ that they compelled diverse people to set her seal thereto: and this was
done for great couetyse: wherefore all good hertes of the reaume were^ clean tur
/ ned away from hy^. that was king ever after. And that was an vttyr
destructyo^ and end to hy^ yt was so hygh^ and excellent pry^ce and king / and
through couetyse and falls cou^ceil falseli betrayed: allas for pite that such a
king might not see. and than king Richard set his ky^gdome and his ryall
lord of England to ferme unto iiij persons / the which were these / sir
William stroppe earl of wylteshire and tresorer of England. and sir Ioha^ bussh
and He^ri grieve. and sir Johan bagot knights. which that turned hem to
meschief and deth^ within a littell time as ye after shull find wryte^. And
than king Rychard made great ordenau^ce and went him over the sea into Irland
and many great lords with him with great hosts for to stre^gth^ her king with men
of arms archiers and moch^ great stuff and right good ordenau^ce as lo^geth
to werre / and or he passed the sea. he ordained and made sir Edmond of La^gely
his uncle the duke of york his lieutenau^t of England in his abse^ce with the
governance and cou^ceill of these four knights that hadde^ taken England to
ferme of the king. and than he passed the sea and came into Irla^d. and there
he was well and worthily received. and the rebels that ben^ kalled wild
Irisshme^. Anon^ her cheuitains and her governors and her leders came down
unto the king and yelde^ he^ unto hy^ both body and goods all at his own^
will. and swore to be his liege men: and there to him dyde^ homaae and feaute
and good service: and thus he conquered the most party of Irland in a littel
time / And while yt king Richard was thus in Irla^d sir Henry of Bolynbroke
Earl of Derby that the king had made before duke of Hereford. the which duke
the king had exilled out of this land / and was comen ayen^ into England for
to challenge the Dukedom of Lancastre as for his right and true heritage And
he came down owte of France by land unto caleys: And there mete him sir
Thomas Aru^del that was Erchebisshop of Canterbury yt was exilled out of
England and with him came the Earl of Arundel his sone and heir. the which
was in ward and keeping of sir Ioha^ and sheley knight sum time with the earl
of Hu^tyngdone and with the duke of Excestre. which was in the Castle of
Reigate in southsexe / and there he stale hy^ away and came to Caleys and there
he was kept well and worthily: till these other two lords were come^ unto
Caleys And tha^ this worthy duke and the Erchebisshop of Canterbury Aro^dell
shiped in the haven of Caleys and drowe her course northward and aryued in
york shire at Rauenesporte fast by wydelyngto^. and there he came and entered
the land / and these two lords with him and her meyne And tha^ moch^ people of
the reame that herd of his coming and known where he was anon^ they drew unto
him / welcomed these lords and so coraged he^ in all manner thing and passed
forth into the land and gadred much people

And when king Rychard herd and wist that these two forsaid lords were come
ayene into England / and that they were lo^ded. tha^ the king left his
ordenau^ce in Irla^d and came into England ward in all the have that he might
and came unto the castle of Flynt: and there he abode for to take his
cownceill / what might best be done. but to hy^ came none And than sir Thomas
Percy earl of Wurchestre yt was the kings styward wist and knew this anon he
came into the halle among all the people. and there he brake ye ryall kings
howshold. and anon they were disperkled and every man went his way / and
forsook her master and sovereign lord and left him allone: And thus was king
Rychard brought a down and destroyed and stood allone without comfort or
socour or any good cou^ceyll of any man allas for pite of this ryall king And
anon came tydy^ges that sir Henry of Holy^gbroke was up with a wonder strong
power of people. and that all sherewes of England raised up the shires in
strengthyng of him aye^s the king rychard ^ and thus sone he was come out of
the northco^tre to Brystowe / and there he met with sir willya^ scrope earl
of wildeshire tresorer of England and with sir Johan bussh and sir Henry grene:
and Johan bagot: but he skaped from hem and went over the sea into Irland. and
these iij knights were taken and her hedes smyte^ of. And thus they deyed for
her falls couetyse. and tha^ was king richard take and brought unto the duke:
and anon the Duke put him in fast ward and strong hold / unto his comy^g to
london / and than was there a romer in London and a strong noise that king
Rychard came to westmynstre and the people of London ran thither and would have
done moch^ harm and skate in her woodnesse: but the mayre and the aldermen and
other worthy men seced hem wit fair words / and turned hem home ayene to
London: And there was sir Ioha^ slake deke^ of the kings chapel of
Westmynstre take and brought to London and put in prison in Ludgate. and Bagot
was take i^ Irland and brought to london and put in prison in Newgate there to
be kept and to abide his answer / And son^ after the duke brought king
rychard privily unto London and put him in the tower vndyr sure keeping as a
prisoner. and tha^ came the lords of the reame wit all her cou^ceyll unto the
toure to king rychard and saide^ to hy^ of his misgouernau^ce and extorcio^
that he had done made and ordained to oppress all the commune people and also
all the reame. Wherefore all the common people of his Reame would have hy^
deposed of his kingdom / and so he was deposed at that time in the tower of
London by all his lords cou^ceyll and commune assent of all ye reame. and
there he was put from the toure unto the castle of ledes in ke^t / and there he
was kept a while And than was he lad unto the castle of Pou^frete in the north
co^tre to be kept in prison / and son^ afterward right there he made his end
And than when king rychard was deposed and had resygned his croune and his
ky^gdome and was kept fast in hald than all the lords of the reame with the
co^munes assent and by accord chosen this worthy lord sir Henry of Bolyngbroke
Earl of Derby / duke of Hereford and duke of Lancaster by right line and
heritage / and for his rightful manhood that the people fond in hy^ before all
other they chosen him and made him king of England among hem.

Of sir Henry of Boly^gbroke earl of Derby. that reigned after king Rychard:
which was the fourth^ Henry aftyr the conquest Capitulo CCxliij
aNd after that king rychard the xj. was deposed and put owte of his ky^gdome.
the lords and the co^munes all with own^ assent / and all other worthy of ye
reame chosen sir Henry of Boly^gbroke earl of Derby sone and heir of Johan ye
duke of Lancaster for his worthy ma^hode / that often time had be found i^ hy^.
and in deed p^ued / upon saint Edwardes day ye confessor / he was crowned king
of England at westmy^stre by all the Reames assent next after the deposyng of
king Rychard / tha^ he made henry his eldest sone and heir prince of Walys and
duke of Cornewaill and earl of Chestre. and he made sir Thomas of aru^dell
erchebisshop of Canterbury ayen^ as he was before and sir rogier walden that
king Richard had made erchebysshop of Canterbury he made hy^ bishop of London.
for that time it stood void And he made the earls sone of Arundell that came
with him over the sea from Caleys into England earl of Aru^dell as his fadre
had ben^ and put him in poscessio^ of all his lodes. and there he made feaute
and homage unto his liege lord ye king as all other lords had do^ ^ no tha
anon^ deyed king Richard in ye castle of Pou^frete in ye northcotre for there
he was e^famined unto ye death by his keeper: for he was kept there iiij. or v.
days from mete and dri^ke: and so he made his end i^ this world: yet moch^
people in England and i^ other lands said that he was a live many year after
his death. but whetyr he were a live orde: de forth: they held her falls
opynyons and believe that men had den in much people which c^m^ to great
meschief and foul death: as ye shall here afterward. And when king Henry wiste
and knew verrailly that he was deed / he let sere him in the best manner / and
closed it in a fair cheste with diverse speceries and baumes and closed hem in
a synne^ clothe all saufe his visage. and that was left open that men might
see his person from all other men And so he was brought to london with torche
light bre^nyng unto sey^t Poules. and there he had his mass and his dirige:
wit moch^ reverence and sole^pnite of service. And wha^ all this done: he was
browght from seint poules into the abbeye of westmynstre / and there he had all
his hole service ayen^ / and from westmy^stre he was brought to Langely / and
there he was buried / on whose soul god have mercy ame^ And in the first year
of king He^ryes regne: he held his cristmasse in the castle of wy^desore And
on the xij. even came the duke of a wemarle unto the king and told hi^ that he
and the duke of Surre and the duke of Excestre and the earl of Salysbury and
the earl of Gloucestre: and other mo of her affinite were accorded to make a
mo^myng unto the king on the xij day at night and there they caste^ to slay ye
king in here reuely^g and thus the duke of a wemarle warned the king And than
the king came the same night to London pryuely in all the have that he might to
get hy^ socour and comfort and cou^ceill / and anon these other that would
have done the king to death. fledde^ in all the have that they might for they
knewen well that her cownceyll was bewreyed

And tha^ fled the duke of surre and the earl of Salysburye wit all her meyne
unto the town of Cissestre. and there the people of the town would have arested
hem / and would not stood to her arreste. but stood at defense and fawght manly
But at the last they were overcome and take / and there they smote^ of the
dukes head of Surre. and ye earls heed of Salisbury / and many other moo / and
there they put quartres into sakkes and her hedes on poles borne on high^ and
so they were brought through the cite of London unto London brygge / and there
her hedes were set upon hygh^. and her quartres were^ sent to other good
tounes and cites and set upon trees / At oxe^ford were take Bloute knight and
benet cely knight / and Thomas wynterfell Squire: and these were beheded and
quarterd: and the knights hedes were set on Poles and brought to London and
set on te brygge. and ye quarters sent forth to other good towns: And in the
same year at Prittellwell in a mile in Estsexe there sir Ioha^ holand: the duke
of Excestre was take with the co^munes of the contre: and they brought hy^ from
the mylle unto plasshe. and to the same place that king Rychard had arested sir
Thomas of wodestoke the duke of Glowcestre / And right there in the same place
they smyten of the duke of Excestre his head / and brought it to london upon a
pole. and it was set on london brygge. And in the same year at Brystowe was
take the lord Spencer that king Rychard had made earl of Glowcestre: and the
co^munes of the town^ of Bristowe took him and brought hy^ into the market
place of the town / and there they smyten of his head and sent it unto
London. and there it was set on london brygge And in this same year was sir
Barnard brokeys knight take and arested and put into the tower of london. and
sir Ioha^ shelley knight. and sir Ioha^ maudely^ and sir william Fereby
Chapelayns of king Rychardes / and they were^ arested and put into the toure of
London. and thither came the ky^ges justices and sat upon he^ (...) the toure
of london and there the^ ^ere dampened all four unto the ^^th. and the dome
was yeve unto sir Barnard brokeys that he should gone on foot from the toure
through london unto Tyborne. and there to be honged and after his head smyten of
/ and sir Johan shelley knight / and sir Ioha^ Mawdelyn. and sir william Fereby
persons were draw thurghoute London to Tiborne / and there hanged and her
hedes smyten of and set on London brygge. And in this same year king Henry
the iiij sent queen Isabell home ayen^ into Frawnce. the which was king
Rychardes wedded wife / and yafe her goold and silver ynow: and many other
rich Iewelles and so she was discharged of all her dower and sent owte of
England

And in the second year of the regne of King Henry the fourth: was sir Rogier
of Claryngdone knight: and two of his men and the Pryour of Launde: and.viij.
friar menours. and sum maistres of Dyuinyte and othyr for treson that they
wrought against the king were drawn and hanged at Tyborne all xij persons /
and there began a great disce^sion and debate in the contre of walys bytwen^ the
lord gray Ruthyn^ and owen of Glendere squire of walys / and this owe^ arered a
great nombre of walshme^ and kept all that contre about right strong and
did moch^ harm and destroyed the ky^ges towns and lorshippes thurghoute walys
/ and robbed and slow the kings people both Englyssh and walyssh: and in this
manner he endured a xij. year large And he took ye forsaid lord greyruthyn^
prisoner and kept hy^ fast in hold till he was rau^soned of prisoners of the
march / and kept him long time in hold. and at the last he made hy^ wedde
one of his daughters: and kept him there still wit his wife* and sone after he
deyed. And tha^ the king Henry knowy^g this meschief destruction and treson
that this owen had wrought then^e anon he ordained a strong power of me^ of
arms and of archiers and much other stuff that longed to werre for to abate
and destroy the malice of this false walsshma^ and tha^ the king came unto
walys wit his power for to destroy this owen and other rebels false walssh
men / And anon^ they fledden into the mou^tayns and there might the king done
hem non^ harm in no manner wise for the mou^taignes / and so the king came into
england ayene forlesyng of mo of his people and thus he sped naught there. In
this same year was great scarcyte of whete in England. for a quarter of whete
was at xv shyllyng / And there was marchandyse of England sent in pruys for
whete / and anon^ they had lade and fregzt ships ynowe / and came home in
saufte / blesshed be god of all his yiftes And in the iiij year of king
He^ries reign there was a sterre seyne in the firmament that showed him self
through all the world for diverse tokenes yt should befalle sone after. the
which sterre was named and called by clergy stella Comata / and on seint
Marye magdalene day next folewing in the same year was the bataille of
shrowesbury. and thider came sir Henry Percy the Earls sone of northumberland
with a great multitude of me^ of arms and archiers and yafe a bataille to king
Henry the iiij: through the false counceyll and wykked read of sir Thomas percy
his uncle Earl of wurchestre: and there was sir Henry percy slain. and the
most party of his meyne in the feld. and sir Thomas percy take and kept fast
in hold two days till the king had set rest among his people on both
sides And than sir Thoa^s percy anon was iuged to be deed / draw / ho^ged.
and his head smyten of. for his false treson at shrowesbury. and his head
brought to London and set on london brygge / and the other people that there
were slayn^ on both parties the king let burye: and there was slain on the
kings side in that bataill the earl of stafford and sir walter blou^te in the
kings cote armure under the kings baner and many mo worthy men. on whose soul
god have mercy / Amen. And in the iiij. year of king Henryes regne: came the
Emperor of Co^sta^tynoble with many great lords and knights and much other
people of his co^tre into England to king Henri with hy^ to speak / and to
disporte and to see the good governance and co^dicions of our people and to
know ye co^modytees of England. and our king with all his lords goodly and
wurshipfully hy^ received and welcomed hy^ and all his meyne that came^ wit him
and did hy^ all the reverence and wurship that they could and might And anon^
the king conmau^ded all manner offyciers that he should be served as worthily and
ryally as it lo^ged unto such^ a worthy lord and Emperor on his own cost as
long as the emperor was in e^glo^d and all his men that camen wit hy^ / And
in the same year came dame Jane the duchess of Britaigne in to England / and
londed at fallemouthe in Cornewaill. and from thens she was brought to ye cite
of wy^chestre. and there she was wedded unto king Henry the iiij in the abbey of
sey^t swithynes of wy^chestre with all the sole^nite that might be done and made
/ And sone after^ she was brought from the^s to London: and the mayre and the
alderme^ and the co^munes of ye cite of London rydde^ aye^s her and her
welcomed and brought her through the cite of London to westmy^ster / and there
she was crowned queen of england. And there ye king made a ryall and a sole^pne
feste for her and for all manner of men that thydder would come / And in this
same year dame Blau^che the eldest dowghter of king Henry the iiij was sent
over the sea with the Earl of Somersete her uncle / and with maistir Richard
Clyfford than bishop of wurchestre / and with many other worthi lords
knights and ladies: and worthy squiers as longed to such a worthy kings
daughter / and camen unto Coleyn. And thither came the dukes sone of bar wit a
fair meyne / and received this worthy lady and there ye bishop of wurcestre
wedded and sacred hem to gedre as holy chyrch^ would. And there was made a ryall
feste and a great Iustes in the reverence and wurship of hem and of all people
that thither came. and when this marriage and fest was done. the earl and the
bishop and all her meyne token her leave of ye lord and the lady. and came hom^
ayene into England in saufte: thanked be god* And in the v. year of king
he^ryes regne the lord Thoa^s his sone went over see. and the earl of Kent and
many other lords and knights wit men of arms and archiers a great no^bre to
chastyze the rebels that a forne had done moch^ harm^ to our Englysshme^ and
marchau^ts and to many towns and ports in england on ye see costs And the
lord Thomas the kings sone came into Flau^dres to fore a town: that is
kalled the Skluse among all the ships of diverse nacyo^s that were^ there.
and after there they rydde^ wit her ships ame^nge hem. and wente^ a land /
and sported hem there ij / days / and camen ayene to her ships and token the
broad see / and there they metten with iij. Carikkes of Iene that weren lade
with diverse marchau^dyse and well manned / and there they foughte^ to gedre
long time. but the englysshmen had ye victory. and broughten the Carrykkes
into the ca^bre before wy^chelsee: and there they canted thees goods and one
of this Carrikkes was suddenly there brent And the lords and her people turned
he^ hom^ ayen^ and went no ferther at yt time: And in the same time Serle yoman
of king Rychard Robbes came into England out of scotland. and told to diverse
people that king Rychard was a live in scotland. and so moch^ people believed in
his words: wherefore great part of the people of the reame were^ in great
error. and gru^chyng aye^s the king through informacion of lies and falls lesing
that this Serle had made. For moch^ people trusted and believed in his seeing /
But at the last he was taken in the North co^tre and by law iugged to ben^
draw through every cite and good burgh towns in England: and so he was served
/ and at the last he was brought to london unto the Gildhalle before the
justice. and there he was iuged for to be brought to ye toure of London to
Tyborne / and there honged and than quartred / and his head smyten of and set
on London brygge. and his quartres to be sent to four good tounes of england
and there set up. and thus ends he his false treson and disceyt. And in the
vj / year of king He^ryes regne ye iiij. the Earl of mar of Scotland by
saufconduyt came into england to challenge sir Edmond the Earl of Ke^t of
certain courses of werre on horsebak. and so this challenge was accepted and
granted and the place taken in smytfeld at London: And this earl of mar ye
Scote came proudely into the feld as his challenge asked / and anon^ came in
also the Earl of Kente and rode unto the Scote: and manfully rode to gedre wit
sharp speres diverse courses / But the earl of Kent had the feld and gate him
much wurshyp and thank of all manner of men for his manfull deeds / And in the
vij. year of king He^ryes regne ye iiij. Sir Rychard stroppe Erchebisshop of
york / and the lord Earl Marchall of England gadred unto he^ a strong power
ayens king Henry. And the king hery^g thereof in all have that he might came
with his power Northward and met with he^ at york / And there were thees two
lords take and brought to the king / And anon the iuges were set. and thees
ij. lords brought forth: and there they were dampened unto the death / and both^
her hedes smiten of: and there they made her end / on whose sowles god for his
pity have mercy / amen. And when this was done the king came to London ayene
and there he rested hi^ / Anon^ god for his great goodness wrought and showed
many great miracles for this worthi clerck Erchebisshop of york yt thus was
done unto the death And in ye vij. year of king He^ryes regne / dame Luce the
dukes suster of Mylane came into England. and so at london: and there was she
wedded to sir Edmond Hola^d earl of Ke^t in the priorye of seint Marie ouereis
in southwerk with moch^ sole^pnite and great wurship: the king was there him
self and yafe her at the church^ door: and when they were wedded and mass
done: the king his own person brought and lad this worthi lady into ye
bisshoppes place of wy^chestre: and there was a wonder great fest holde^ to all
manner of people In ye same year sir Robert knolles knight a worthi werrour deied
at his manner in northfolk. and from the^s he was brought to London upon an horse
bare with moch^ torche light: and so was he brought unto ye white freres in
fleetstrete^ and there was done and made for hi^ a sole^pne feste and a ryall
entereme^t / for thay^ that thither would come both^ pore and rich. and there
he lies beryed by dame Constau^ce his wife in the myddel of the body of ye
church: On whose soul god for his pity have mercy Ame^. And thus in this same
year sir Thoa^s ra^pston knight Constable of the toure of London was dreynt at
London brygge as he came from westmy^stre toward the tower in a barge / and
all through lewdenesse And the same year dame Phelip the younger daughter of king
Henry was lad over the sea wit sir Rychard the dukes brother of york and sir
Edmond courteney bishop of Norwych / and many other lords knights and
squiers ladies and gentle women that apperteygned to such a worthy kings
daughter / and camen into De^marke with his lords. And the king received this
worthy lady for his wife and welcomed thees worthy lords and did he^ much
reverence and great wurshypp / and they were brought unto a town^ that was
kalled London in De^marke and there was this worthy lady wedded and sacred to
ye king of Denmark with much sole^pnyte / and there she was crowned queen of
De^marke Norway and Swyte^. and there was made a ryall feste: And when this
feste and marriage was done and ended. these lords and ladies token her leave of
the king and of the queen. and came^ home ayen^ into England in have thanked be
god almighty

And in the viij. year of king Henry's regne there was a man that was kalled
the walssh clerk / and he appeled a knight that was called sir Percheual
sowdone of treson^ and there they were joined to fight unto vtterau^ce withy^ne
listes: and the day and place and time assigned / and lemyted to be done and
ended i^ smythfeld: at the which day the persons came^ into the field / and
foughten sore and mightily to gedres / but at ye last the knight over came the
clerk and made hy^ yield hy^ creaunt of his false empeschement that he said on
hy^. And tha^ was he despoilled of his armure: and draw owte of ye field to
Tiborne: and there was he ho^ged. and ye knight take to grace and was a good
man And in this same year the Earl of Northu^berla^d and the lord Bardolfe came
owte of Scotland / in preiudyce and destructyo^ of king Henry. wherefore they of
the North contre arysen upon he^ and fought with hem and sco^fy^ed he^ and toke^
he^ and smiten of her hedes. and quartred her bodies / and sent the heed of ye
Earl: and quarter of the lord Hardolfe to london: and there they were set
upon the brigge for falls treson yt they had purposed aye^s the king: And in the
ix. year of king Henryes regne. was sir Edmond hola^d earl of Kente made
Admyrall of England for to keep the sea: and he went to the sea with many
ryall ships that weren full well arrayed and empareled and enarmed with many a
good men of arms and archiers and of good defense of werre in the ky^ges name
of England / and so he londed at the last in ye cost of Britaigne in the I Will of
Bryak. with all his people. and he besieged the castle and sauted it / and they
withstode him with great defense and strength. And anon he leyed his
ordenau^ce. and in ye leye^g of a gonne^ came a quarrel and smote the good earl
Edmond in the head / and there he caught dethes wound / but yet they left
naught till yt they had get the castle / and all that were therynne. and
there this good lord deyed / On whose soul god have mercy. amen: And tha^ this
meyne came home ayen^ in to England with the earls body / and was beryed
among his au^cestres right worthily: And in the same year was a great frost
in england. that dured xv. wekes

And in the x. year of the noble king Henry the fowrthe: came the Senechall of
Henaude with othyr meyne to seek Auntres and to get him wurshippes in deeds of
arms both on horsbake and on foot at all manner of points of werre / And the
seneschall chale^ged the earl of Somersete: and the Earl delyured him manfully
of all his chalenges and put his adversary to the wers in all poi^tes and
wanne him there great wurshyp and the gre of the field / And ye next day after
came into the field an other man of arms of ye Senechallis party And aye^s
hy^ came sir Rychard of aru^del knight and the Henaude had the bettyr of him on
foot in one point for he brought hy^ on his knee And the thrydde day came an
other man of arms into the feld: and ayens him came sir joha^ of Cornewaill
knight / and manly and knightly quyte hi^ in all manner poy^tes aye^s his
adversary. and had the better i^ ye field / And on ye iiij. day came an other
man of arms of Henaude into the field: and ayens hy^ came sir Johan cheynys
sone / and manly quyte him ayens his adversary. for he cast horse and man into
the feld / and the king for his ma^hode at that time dubbed him knight And ye
v. day there came an other man of arms of Henaudes party into the feld: and
to hy^ came in sir Johan styward knight. and ma^fully quyte him there in all
manner of poy^tes and had the better / And the vj. day came an other Henaude /
and to hy^ came Willya^ porter squire and ma^fully quyte him. and had the
better in the field / and the king dubbed hi^ knight the same time: And the
vij. day came an other Henaude into the field: and to him came Johan kandysh
squire. and manfully he quyte hy^ on his aduersarye / and had the better in the
field. and there the king dubbed him knight the same day. And on the same day
came an other Henaude and to him came a squire of Gascoygne and proudely and
ma^ly he quite him on his aduersarye and had the better / and anon^ the king
dubbed hi^ knight And on the viij. day came into ye field ij. men of arms of
Henaude / and to hem cam^ ij. soudyours of Caleys that were brethren that were
kalled Burghes^ and well and ma^ly quyte hem on her adversaries / and had the
better in the field and thus ended the chalenges with moch^ wurshippes: And the
king at the reverence of the straungiers made a great feste and yafe hem rich
yiftes^ and they toke^ her leave and went home to her own contre* And in the
xi. year of king Henry's regne the iiij. there was a great bataille done in
smythfelde bitwene two squiers that one was kalled gloucestre that was
appellau^t Arthur was the defendau^t and well and manfully fowghte^ to gedre
long time: and the king for manfullnesse and of his grace took her quarrel
into his hand and made hem to go owte of the field at ones: and so they were
divided of her batailles and the king yafe he^ grace. And the.xij. year of king
Henry's regne the fourth Rys dye a squier of walys yt was a rebel aryser and
supporter to owe^ of gle^dore that did moch^ destruction to the people of Walys
/ was taken and brought to London / and there he came a fore the justices and
was dampened for his treson. than he was leid on an hurdel and so draw forth
unto Tyborne through the cite. and there he was hanged and let down ayene / and
his head smyte^ of and his body quartred and sent to iiij. tounes / and his
head set on London brygge. And in the xiij year of king He^ryes regne tho
deyde sir Ioha^ beauford the earl of somersette that was Captain of Caleys:
and was beried at the abbey of tourehyll: on whose soul god have mercy amen /
And in the same year the lord Thomas king Hen / ries sone wedded the countess
of Somersette. And in this same year came the e^bassotours of france into
England from the duke of Burgoygn^ unto the pry^ce of England king He^ries sone
and heir for help and socour of men of arms and archiers aye^s ye duke of

vmfreuille Earl of kente. and the lord Cobham sir Ioha^ old castle / and many

wellcomed thees Englysshmen / the lords. and all other meyne. and tha^ it was
done him to wit that the duke of Orliaunce was comen to semtclowe fast by Paris
with a great nombre of men of arms and arbalastriers / and thither went our

and would no le^ger abide / And tha^ our Englysshme^ came ayen^ to paris. and

than the king made Thomas his sone duke of Clare^ce and his other sone Johan

beauford Earl of Dorset. and the duke of a Wamarle he made Duke of york / And
than the king ordained his sone sir Thomas duke of Clarence. sir Thomas
beauford. earl of Dorset. and sir Johan Cornewaylle with many other Lords
knights and Squyers / men of arms and archiers to gon^ over ye see into

lords with her retinue shipped at Hampto^ and sailled over into Norma^die and

vij / M. men of arms of Fre^sshme^ / and iij. sergeaunts of arms with hem /
and all were put to flight. and toke^ of he^ vij.C. men of armes^ and CCCC.
horse without thay^ that were slain in the field. And so they rydde^ forth
thurghoute France and toke^ castelles and towns and slowen much people of
fre^sshmen that withstode^ he^ and toke^ many prisoners as they ridde^. and so
they passed forth till they came^ to Burdeux. and there they rested hem a while
and set the contre in pees / and rested till the wyntage were ready to saille^
And tha^ ye duke with his meyne came home into England in saufte: thanked be god
/ And in the same year was the kings coin changed thurghoute england by ye
king and his cou^ceill: that is to seye / ye noble / half / and ferthy^g of
gold. And in ye xiiij. year of king He^ries regne the iiij. he let make galeys
of werre. for he had hoped to have passed the great see / and so forth to
Iherusale^. and there to have ended his life / but god visited hy^ so sone
after wit infirmites and great sikenesse that he might not well endure no while
so ferue^tly / he was take and brought in bed at westmy^stre in a fair
chamber: and as he lay in his bed / he asked his chamberlayne what they kalled
that chamber that he lay ynne. and he a^sweryd and said jherusale^ / And tha^
he said that ye prophecye said that he should make an end and deie in
jherusale^. and tha^ he made hy^ ready unto god and disposed all his will and
sone after he deied and was carried by watyr from westmynster in a barge unto
Feuersha^* and from the^s unto Canterbury by land with much torche light
bre^nyng into the abbey of Crichurche: and there he was entered and buried
beside sey^t Thoa^s of Canterbury shryne / and thus ended the worthy king
Henry about mydle^ten sunday in ye year of our lord a M.cccc.xiij on whose
soul god have mercy. Ame^.

Of king Henry the v. that was king He^ryes sone Capitulo CCxliiij
ANd after the death of king Henry the iiij. reigned king Henry his sone that was
borne at Monmouth in Walys: that was a worthy king and a gracious man and a
great co^querour: and in ye first year of his regne for great love and
goodness he sent to the freres of La^gely there as his fadre had done e^
burye king Richard the second / and let take his body out of the earth ayen^ /
and did bring it to westmy^ster in a ryall chare covered with blak velvet and
baners of diverse arms about / and all ye horse that drowen the chare were
trapped in blake / and bete^ with diverse arms / and many a torche bre^nyng by
all the wey till he came to westmy^stre / and there he let make for hy^ a ryall
and a sole^pne entereme^t. and beryed him by Queen anne his wife as his own
desire was on the ferther side of sei^t Edwardes shryne in ye abbey of seint
Peter's of westmynster: On whose soul god have mercy / ame^ And i^ this same
year were a certain of lollardes taken / and falls heretics that had purposed
through falls treson to have slain our king. and for to have destroyed all the
clergy of ye Reame if they might have had her falls purpose. but our lord god
would not suffer it. for in have our king had wary^g thereof and of all her falls
ordinance: and came suddenly wit his power to seint Ioha^nes wtoute smythfeld /
and anon they toke^ a certain of the lollardes and falls heretics / and
brought he^ unto the kings presence and there told all her falls purpose and
ordinance how they would have done and wrought if they might have reigned and
had her will. and there they told whych^ were her capitay^s and governors And
tha^ the king conmau^ded he^ to be lad to ye toure of London. and tha^ took moo
of he^ both withy^ ye cite / and without. and sent he^ to Newgate and to
both co^trees. and tha^ they were brought in examinacio^ before the clergy
and the kings justices / and there they were co^victed before ye clergy for
her falls heresy and dampened before the justice for her falls treso^. And this
was her judgment that they should be draw from the tower of London unto saint
Gilles feld. and there to be ho^ged and bre^t on the galewes. And also there
was taken sir Rogier acton knight for heresy and eke for treson aye^s ye king
and the Reame. and he came a fore the clergy and he was co^uicted for his
heresy to be bre^d and dampened before the justices to be drawn from the tower
of london through the cite to seint Gilles field and to be honged and bre^t. And
in the second year of king He^ries regne the v. he held a cou^ceill of all the
lords of the Reame at westmy^ster. and there he put hy^ this dema^de and
prayed and besought he^ of her goodness and of her good cou^ceill and good
will to show him as touchy^g the title and the right yt he had to Norma^die /
Gascoygne. and Guihe^ne: the which the king of france wit held wro^gfulli
and vnryghtfully / the which his au^cestres before hy^ had be true title of
co^queste and right heritage: ye whych^ Norma^die Gascoign^ and Guyhe^ne the
good king Edward of wy^desore and his au^cestres before hy^ hadde^ hold all her
life's time And his lords yafe hy^ cou^ceyll to send e^bassatours unto the king
of France and his cou^ceill / and that he should give unto hy^ his right
heritage. that is to say Norma^dye Gascoygne: and Gwyhe^ne: the which his
predecessors hadde^ hold a fore him: or else he would it wy^ne with dynt of
swerd in short time with the help of Almighty god / And than the Dolphyne of
France answered to our embassatours and said i^ this manner / that the king was
over young and to tender of age to make any werre as ayens him. and was not like
to be no good werriour to do and to make such^ a conquest thereupon him and
somewhat in scorn and despyte he sent to him a tonne full of tenys balls.
because he should have so^what for to play with all for hy^ and for his lords
/ and that became hy^ better tha^ to maynten any werre And than anon^ our
lords that weren Embassatours toke^ leave / and came^ into England ayene. and
told the king and his cou^ceil of ye ungoodly answer that they had of the
Dolphyne / and of the present ye which he had sent unto the king And when
the king had herd her words and the answer of the Dolphyn: he was wonder
sore agreued and right evil paid toward ye Fre^sshmen and toward the king and
the Dolphyn. and thought to avenge him upon hem as soon as god would send him
grace and might / and anon^ let make tenys balls for ye dolphy^ in all ye have
yt they might be made / and they were great go^ne stone for the dolphyne to
play with all / And than anon^ the king sent for all his lords and held a great
cou^ceille at westmynstre. and told unto hem the answer that they had of the
dolphyne and of his worthy present that he sent to him and to his lords to
pley with all: and there the king and his lords were^ accorded that they should
be ready i^ arms with her power in ye best array that might be done: and get
me^ of arms and archiers yt might be gotten / and all other stuff that lo^ged
to werre and to be ready with all her retenue to mete at Sowtha^pton be lammasse
next sewy^g without any delay. wherefore ye king ordained his nauye of ships
with all manner of stuff and vitaille yt lo^ged to such^ a werrour of all manner
ordinance in ye haue^ of southampton into the no^bre of CCC / xx. sailles /
And than fill there a great disese and a foul meschyef. for there were three
lords whych^ yt the king trust most moch^ on. and through falls couetise they
had purposed and ymagined the kings death and thought to have slain him and
all his Brotheren or he had take the sea The which were named thus sir Rychard
earl of Ca^brygge brothyr to ye duke of york. The second was the lord scroppe
tresorer of England. and ye thridde was sir Thoa^s gray knight of Northco^tre:
and these lords a fore said for lucre of money had made promise to the
fre^sshmen for have slain king Henry and all his worthy brethren by a falls
train suddenly or they had be ware But al mighty god of his great grace held
his holy ho^de over he and saved he^ from his peryllous meyne and for to have
done this they received of the Frensshmen a million of gold: and that was there
opynly preued. And for this false treson they were all there iuged unto the
deth^ / And this was the iugemet that they should be ladden through Hampton and
without Northgate there to be beheded / And thus they ended her life for her
falls couetyse and treson.

Anon as this was done the king and all his meyne made hem ready and wenten to
ship and toke^ and sailled forth with xv.C. ships and arrived withyn seyne
at kyde cause upon our ladies even in the assumptyon jn Normandye with all his
ordenau^ce and so went hi^ forth to Hareflete: and besieged the town all
about by land and eke by watyr And sent to the capiteyne of the town and
charged him for to deliver the town And the capyteyne said that he none
delyured him and none he would yield to him but bad hy^ done his best. And tha^
our king laid his ordinance unto ye town that is for to say / go^nes Engynes
and trypgetes and shete^ and cast to the walls and eke unto the town / and
kast down both toures and town / and laid he^ unto the grownde / and there
he played at the tenys with his hard go^ne stone / And they that were withyn
the town when they should play their song was well away and allas that ever
such^ tenys balls were made. and cursed all the^ that werre began / and the
time that ever they were borne And on the morwe the king did cry at every Gate
of the town that every man should be ready on the morwe erly to make assaute
unto ye town And willyam Bouchier and Johan grant with xij. other worthy
burgeys came^ to the king and besought him of his ryall pryncehode and power to
withdraw his malice and destructyon that he did unto hem / and besought hi^ of
viij days of respyte and trewes if any reskue might come unto he^ / and else
to yield up the town unto he^ with all her goods. And tha^ the king sent for
the capyteyne and kept the remenau^t still wit him. And the lord Gaucorte that
was Capiteyne of ye town went forth to Rone in all have unto the Dolphyne for
help and socour. But there was non^ ne no man of reskue. for ye dolphy^ would
not abide And thus this Capiteyne came ayene unto the king and yolde up the
town and delivered him the keys: and than he kalled his uncle the Earl of
Dorset: and made hy^ capiteyne of the town^ of Harflete / and delivered him the
keys and bad him gone to put out all the frenssh people both men women and
children and stuffed this town of Harflete with Englysshme^ And than the king
sent in England and did cry in every good town of England that what crafty
man would come thither and inhabyte him there in that town: he should have hows
and howshold to hy^ and to his heirs for ever more And so thither went mani
diverse marchau^ts and crafty men and enhabyted he^ there to stre^gth^ ye town
and were^ welcome: and when the king saw that this town^ was well stufed both
of vitaille and of men This worthy pry^ce took his leave and went to caleys
ward by land. and the frensshmen herd of his comy^g / they thought to stop
him his way that he should not pass that way and in all ye haste that they
might breke^ all the brigges there any passage was for horse and man in so much
that there might no man pass over the rivers nothyr on horse ne on foot / but
if he should be drowned: And therefore our king with all his people went and
sought his way far up to Paris ward. and there was all the ryall power of
France assembled and ready to give hy^ bataille and for to destroy al his
people But almighti god was his gydde and saved him of his enemies power and
purpose thanked be god that saved so his own^ knight And king in his rightful
titell And than our king beholdy^g and seeing the multitude and no^bre of his
enemies to which were in his wey to give him bataill. tha^ the king with a
meke heart and a good spirit left up his hands to almighty god and besought
hy^ of his help and socour: and that day to save his true servant: ad than
owr king gadred all his lords and othyr people about / and bad hem all be of a
good cher^. for they should have a fair day and a gracyous victory and the
better of all her enemies: and praid he^ all to make hem ready unto ye bataill
for he would rather to be deed that day in the field than to be taken of his
enemies: for he would never put the noble Reame of England to Rawnsone for his
person. And the worthy duke of york fell on his knees and besought ye king of
above that he would grant him that day the avauntward in his bataille^ and the
noble king granted him his asky^g and said grant mercy cousin of york and
prayed him to make him redj And tha^ he bad every man to ordeyne a stake of
tree and sharp both^ ends / that the stake might be pight in the earth a
sloppe: that her enemies should not over come he^ on horsebake* For that was her
false purpose. and araied he^ all there for to over ride our meyne suddenly at
the first coming on of he^/ at the first brownt And all night before the
bataylle the fre^shmen maden many great fyres and moch^ revel with howtyng and
showting and pleyde our king and his lords at the dise / and an archier for a
bla^ke of her money / for they wenden all had been heirs. The morn arose /
the day began to spryng: And the king by good auyse let array his bataille and
his wings. and charged every man to keep hem hole to gedres and prayed hem all
to be of good chere. And wha^ they were ready he asked what time of the day it
was. and they said Pryme / than said our king: now is good time. for all
england prayed forvs / and therefore be of good chere and let us go to our
journey. and tha^ he said with an high^ voys In the name of almighty god and of
seint George avau^t baner and seint george this day thine help / And tha^ the
Frensshmen came prykyng dou^e as they would have over ryden all our meyne. but
good and our archiers made hem sone to stomble: for our archiers shet never
arowe amys. but it perisshed and brought to ground man or horse For they shote^
that day for a wager And our stakes made top over terne each on other that
they lay on hepes two spear le^gthe of heyghte. And our king with his meyne and
with his men of arms and archiers that tokked on hem so thikke wit arewes and
leyde on tho stakes and our king with his own hands faught manly. And thus
almighty god and sey^t George brought our enemies to ground and yafe us that
day the victory. and there were slain of Frensshme^ that day in the feld of
Agyncourt moo than^ xi.M. with prisoners: that weren taken / and there were
no^bred that day of Fre^sshme^ in the field moo than six socore thousand: and
of Englysshme^ not vij.M: but god that day fought for us: And after came there
tydinges to our king that there was a new bataille of Frensshme^ ordained ready
to stelle on him and came^ toward him Anon our king let cry that every man
should slay his prisoner that he had take. and anon arrayed his bataylle ayen^
ready to fight with the frensshmen: And when they saw that our me^ killed dou^e
her prisoners: than^e they withdrowe he^ and brake her bataill and all her
array / And thus owr king as a worthy co^querour had that day the victory in
the feld of agyncourt in Pycardie. And tha^ our king returned ayen^ there yt
the bataill was to see what people were deed of englysshme^ and if any were hurt
yt might be helped. and there were deed in the field the duke of Barry. the duke
of Alau^sou^ / the Duke of Borban / the Earl of Nauerne. the chief Conestable
of France. and viij. other Earls: and the erchebisshop of Sau^ce. and of good
barons an hundred and moo. And of worthy knights of great aliau^ce of cotes
armures a thowsa^d and v. ho^dred. And of Englisshme^ was deed yt day the good
duke of york / and the Earl of Southfolk / and of all other of our Englisshme^
there were not deed passing.xxvi. bodies thanked be god / and this bataill was
done on a friday which was Crispynie and Crispynianes day in the month of
Octobre: and anon^ the king conmau^ded to bery hem: and the duke of york to be
carried forth / with him and the earl of southfolk: And there were prisoners the
duke of Orlyau^ce / the duke of Burbone. the earl of Ve^dome: the Earl of Ewe.
the Earl of Richemo^d. and sir Bursigau^t merchant of france / and many other
worthy lords were^ there taken in this bataille of Agy^court / and were
brought unto the town of Caleys: and so over the sea wit the king into
England. and londed at Dover in Kent with all his prisoners in saufte: thanked
be god almighty. and so came to Canterbury and offered at saint Thomas shrine /
And so forth he rode through Ke^te the next way to Eltham. and there he rested
till yt he would come to London. And tha^ the mayre of London and the alderme^
sherews with all the worthy communers and crafts camen to blakhethe well and
worthily arrayed and welcomed owr king with diverse melodies. and thanked
almighty god of his gracious victory that he had showed for him / And so the
king and his prisoners passed forth by hem til he came to saint Thomas wateryng
/ and there met with him all the Relygyous with processio^ and welcomed him.
And so the king came rydyng with his prisoners through the cite of London where
that there was showed many a fair sight at all the conduytes. and at the cross
in chepe as in heavenly array of Angeles archa^geles* patriarchs prophets and
virgins with diverse melodies / sensyng and syngyng to welcome our king. And
all the co^duytes rennyng with wine:

And the king passed forth unto saint Powles. and there met with him.xiiij.
bisshoppes reuessed and mytered with sensers to welcome our king* and songe^
for his high and gracious victory Te deum laudamus. And there the king offered
and took leave and rode to westmy^ster. And tha^ ye mayre took his leave of the
king: and rode home ayen^. And in ye thridde year of king He^ryes regne the v.
came the emperor of Almaygne king of Rome and of Hu^garye into England: and so
to the cite of London And the mayre and the alderma^ wit the sherews and worthy
craftys of London by the kings commandment met with hy^ on the blake hethe
in the best array that they cowde on horsebak. and there they welcomed hy^ and
brought hy^ to london with moch^ honor and great reverence. And at sey^t
Thomas wateryng there met wit hy^ the king with all his lords in good array
and there was a worthy mettyng between the Emperor and the king: and there
they kyssed to gedres and enbrached each other: and tha^ the king took the
Emperor by the hand. and so they came^ rydyng through the cite of London unto
sey^t Powles. and there they offered. and all the bisshoppes stoden reuessed
with sencers in her ho^des sensing. And than^ they toke^ her horse and rydden
unto Westmy^stre^ and there the king logged the emperor in his own paleys /
and there he rested him a great while and all at the kings cost. And sone
after came the duke of Holand into England to come and see there the Emperor:
and to speak wit hy^ / and with king Henry of England. and he was worthily
received and logged in the bisshoppes ynne of Ely: and all at the ky^ges cost.
And when the Emperor had well rested him and seyn the lo^d in diverse parties
and knew the co^modytes than by process of time he took his leave of the king
/ but or he yede he was made knight of the Gartier / and received and wered the
lyuery. and than he thanked the king and all his worthy lords. And the king
and he went over the sea unto Caleys: and abyde^ there long time to have an
a^swere of the Fre^ssh^ king. and at the last it came and plesed hy^ right
naught. and the emperor took his leave of the king. and passed forth in gods
name / and our king came over ayen^ into england in all ye have that he might /
and yt was on saint Lukes eve that he came to Lambythe / And on ye mo^day next
after he came into the parliament at westmynster* and in this same year was a
great derthe of corn in England: but thanked be god it lasted not long. And
in ye fowrthe year of king He^ryes regne the v. he held his parliament at
westmy^ster / in the beginning of ye month of Octobre. and lasted unto the
Puryfycacyo^ of our lady than next after: and there was granted unto the king
to may^ten^ his werre both of spyrytualte and temperalte an hole tax and a
disme / And tha^ anon the king prayed all his lords to make hem ready to
strength^ him in his right: and anon^ he let make a new retenue and charged
all men to be ready at Hampto^ in withson weke than next after without any
delay. and there the king made ye Duke of Bedeford protector and defendour of
his Reame of England in his absence: and charged him to keep his laws and
maynten both spyrytualte and te^peralte.

And when the king had thus done and set all thing in his ky^de on sei^t
Marks day that was that time hokketuys^ay. he took his horse at westmynstre.
and came rydyng to seint Powles. and there he offered and took his leave And so
he rode forth through the cite taking his leave of all manner of people. as well of
pour as of rich^e / prayeng hem all in general to pray for him. And so he
rode forth to Ha^pton and there abode till his retenue were ready: and came^
forth. there was all his nauye of ships with his ordinance gadred and well
stuffed as belonged to such a ryall and noble king with all manner of vytailles
for such a ryall people: as well for horse as for man / as longed to such a
werriour that is for to say armure. go^ues: tripgetes. e^gynes sowes /
bastilles / brigges of lether Scalyng. ladders / malles: spades shouelles.
pykes. paueys / bows and arewes. bow strings. tonnes. chestes: and pypes
full of arewes. as neded to such^ a worthy werrour. that no thing was to seche
when time came / and thither came to him his ships lade with gonnes and
gonnepowdre And when all this was ready and his retenue came / the king and his
lords with all his ryall host went to ship. and token the sea and saylden
into Normandy and londed at Towke upon the Lamasse day than next. and there he
made xlviij. knights at his londyng.

And than the king hery^g of many enemies upon the sea: that is to say.ix.
great Carikkes / hulkes galeyes and ships that weren comen to destroy his

ne take no manner good away from he^ but let thay^ pass in pees upon pain of

But throughout ye grace of god almighty and good governance they rydde^ a fore

And from the^s they went to Vernill in Perch. and anon it was yolde unto

and so he was brought to westmynstre^ and there he was examyned of certain

the clergy for his heresy. and dampened before the justices unto the death: for
treso^ / and so he was lad unto the tower ayen^. and there he was laid on an
hurdel and draw through the cite to saint Giles feld: and there was made a new
pair of galewes: and a strong cheyne and a coler of yren for him / and there
he was honged and bre^t on the Galewes and all for his lewdenesse and his false
opynyons

And in the vj. year of king He^ryes regne the v. he sent his uncle sir Thomas
Beaufort duke of Excestre with a fair meyne of me^ of arms and archers tho for
the cite of Rone. and there displaied he his baner / and sent heraudes unto the
town. and bad hem yield that cite unto owr king her siege lord. And they said
he took he^ none to keep ne non^ he should have there. but if it were right dear
bought and wonne^ with her ho^des / for other answer would they none give but
gonnes / And there the duke took good auysement of the grownde all about / And
anon^ there issued of ye cite a great meyne of me^ of arms both^ on horsebake
and on foot^ and anon^ owr meyne met with he^ and ouertrewe an hepe of hem /
and there were slain and take xxx. persons of right good mennys bodies. and
the remenau^t fled ayen^ into the town / And the duke went unto pou^tlarge
unto the king and told hy^ all how he had speed and how him lyked the grownde.
And anon as he was go / they cast down all her subarbes about the cite unto
the hard grownde / for the king there no refressing should have at his comy^g:

came before Rone / and anon^ he set his siege rownde about that cite / and

fro all times when need were: and than came the earl of warrewyke and had got
Dounfront unto the king Henry of England And anon the king sent the Earl of
warrewyke to Cawdebeke to besiege it / And when he came before the town he

deth^. And anon he leyd his siege And the Captain besought the Earl that he

that there was the best enter / and most pleyne grownde. and therefore the king
assygned the pryour of Kylmayne with his power. and logged him on the Northside

ordinawnce they were full glad: and so they went forth in haste and kept the
grownde and the place that the king had assygned hem And they quitte he^ as
good werriours unto her king. Now will I tell you which were ye chief
Capytayns and governors of ye cite of Rone. Mon sir Gwy Boltlire was chief
capytayne both^ of the cite and of the castle: and mo^ sir Termegan he was

Mo^ sir Anthoyne he was lieutenau^t to mon sir Gwy botyller. Henry cha^tfien he

And grant Iakes a worthy werriour he was capytayne of all men of werre. and
^e was governor outeward both^ on horsebake and a foot of all men of arms /
when they issued out of the cite of all the ports he he^ araied as they should
contre with our meyne: And each of these capitayns lad v.M. men of arms. and
sum moo. and at the first coming of our king there were no^bred by heraudes

wha^ they issued of the cite both on horsebake and on foot: for they came
