two or three thousand of good men's bodies well armed / and manfully contred
wit our Englisshmen / and moch^ people were slain diverse times with go^nes
quarelles and other ordinance / And this siege dured xx. wekes. and eueri they
of the town^ hopped to have be rescued / but there came none / so at the last
they kept so long the town^ yt there deyde many a thousands withy^ the toun^
for defaute of met. of men and wymme^ and of children / for they had ete^ her
horse dogs and cattes that were^ in the town: And often times the me^ of arms
drofe out the pour people out of the gattes of the town^ for spe^dyng of
vitaill And anon^ our Englisshme^ drofe he^ into ye town^ ayen^ So at the last
the captain of the town^ saw the meschief as that they were not rescued and
also the scarcite of vitayll: and that ye people so deyde for defaute of mete
every day many thousands And also saw young children lie and souke her modres
pappes that were^ deed: Than anon^ they sent unto the king besechyng hy^ of
grace and mercy / and brought the keys of the town^ unto the king and
delivered ye town to hy^: and all the soudiours voided the town wit her horse
and harneys. and the co^munes of ye town for to abide still in the town yerly
to pay to him and to his successors for all manner customs and fee fermes and
katherines And tha^ the king entered into ye town^ and rested hy^ in the castle
till the town was set i^ rewle and i^ governance /

How the king of England was made heritier and rege^t of France. and how he
wedded quen^ Katherine Cap. cc.xlv
And anon^ after that Rone was gotten Deep and many other towns in baas
Norma^dye yaf the^ over without stroke or siege wha^ they vndyrstode that the
king had gote^ Rone Also this same year had been a pees made and sworn bitwene
the duke of Burgoygn^ and ye Dolphyne which were sworn upon our lords body
that they should assiste each other against their enemies. and after this
contrayt to this oath: ye Duke Ioha^ of Burgoign^ was slain and pitously
murthred in the presence of the Dolphyn. wherefore the Fre^sshmen were greatly
divided and of very necessyte labouryd to have a traittie with ye king of
England. For the king of England man daily of the^ towns castelles and
fortresses. Also this same year was Queen Jane arested and brought to the
castle of Ledis in Kente. and one friar Raudolfe a doctor of divinity her
confessor which afterward was slain by the keeper of the tower falling at
words and debate. And after the queen Jane was delivered In the.vij. year /
both kings of Frawnce and also of England were accorded: And king Henry was
made heir and renent of France / and wedded dame katheryne the kings
daughter of France at Troyes in Champaigne on Trinite sunday / And this was
made by ye mean of phelyp newly made duke of Burgoigne / which was sworn to
king Henry for taue^ge his fadres death. and was become englyssh. And tha^ the
king with his new wife went to Paris / where he was well and rially received.
and from the^s he with his lords and ye duke of Burgoign^ and many other lords
of frawnce leid siege to diverse towns and castelles that held of the
Dolphins party. and wa^ he^ / but the town of Melun held long. for theryn
were good defendours In the viij. year the king and the queen camen over see
and lo^ded on candelmasse day in the morwe at Dover. And the xiiij day of
Feuerer the king came to London / And the xxj day of the same month the quen^
came: and the xxiiij day of the sam^ she was crowned at westmy^ster. Also the
same year anon^ after Estre the king held a parliament at west mynster / at
which perleme^t it was ordained that ye gold i^ Englyssh coin should be weyed
/ and none received but by weight / and anon^ after at witsontide the king
sailled to Caleys and passed so forth into France / And in March the xxij day
before yt the king came over the duke of Clarence was slain in France / and
diverse lords taken prisoners: as the earl of Hu^tyngdon. the earl of
Somersette with diverse other lords. and all was be cause they would not take
wit hem archers: but thought to have do^ with the Fre^sshmen the^ self
withowte he^. And yet wha^ he was slayn^ the archers came and reskued the body
of the duke / which they would have carried with he^ / god have mercy on his
soul ^ he was a vaillau^t man / and the same year between Cristmas and
ca^delmas the town of Melu^ was yolden to the king In the ix. year on saint
Nycolas day in decembre was borne Henry the kings first begoten sone at
wynde^ore whose godfadres at fo^tston^ was Henry bishop of wy^chestre and Johan
duke of Bedford and the duchess of Hola^d was godmoder: and Henry chicheley
Erchebisshop of Canterbury was godfadre at ye co^fermy^g / And in the x. year
ye cite of Mewes in brye was gote^ which had ben^ long beseged And this same
year the queen shypped at Hampto^ and sailled over to the king into France /
where she was wurshipfully received of the king and also of the king of France
her fadre and of her modre. And thus king Henry wan fast in France and held
great astate and sat at dyuer at grette fest in paris crouned / and ye quen^
also / which had not ben^ see^ to fore / and all people resorted unto his court
/ but as to the king of france he held non^ astate ne rule but was left
almost allon^. Also this year the wether coke was set upon poulus steple at
London. And this year i^ the month of August the king were sike at boys de
vy^ce^t / and when he saw yt he should deye he made his testament and ordained
many things nobly for his soul and devoutly received all the ryghtes of holy
chyrchh^ in so ferforth yt when he was enoy^ted he said ye service with the
priest ^ and at the verse of the psalm miserere meidens that was Benign fac
du^e in bona volu^tate tua syo^ vt edifice^tur mur^^hrlm^. he had tarry there ^
and said thus O good lord thou knouwest that mine intent had ben^ and yet is if
I might live to reedifie the walls of Ihrlm^ / and then^e the priest proceeded
forth / and made an end: And anon^ after the most noble prince and victorious
king flour in his time of criste^ chiualrye who^ all ye world doubtet yaf his
soul into the ho^des of god / and deide and made an end of his naturell life
/ at the said bois de vincent beside Paris / the xxxi. year of his age / on
whose soul have mercy / am^ Then^ was ye body enbawmed and chered and leyd in a
ryall chare. and an image lyk unto hi^ was leide upon ye corpse open with diverse
baners. and horse covered rychely with arms of England and france and also ye
old arms of sey^t Edwardes sey^t Edmond and other / and with great mltitude of
torchis with who^ went the king of Scotland and many other lords. which
acco^panyd ye body till it came unto westmy^st by london in England / and in
every town^ by ye way he had sole^pnely his dirige / On theue^ and mass on ye
morn / and moch^ alms was yeuen to pour people by the way / and the vij.
day of Noue^bre after the corpse was brought through london wit great reverence
and solempnite / to westmy^ster where he now lies. it was wurshipfully buried
/ and after was leyd on his to^be a riall image like to him self of silver and
gylt / which was made at cost of quen^ Katherine. and thus ended and thus was
e^tered and buried ye noble king henry the v. on whose soul and all criste^
sowles god have mercy. amen

Of ye lawde of king Henry ye v. and what he ordeye^d for king rychard and for
hy^ self after his death Cap. cc.xlvi
hEre is to be noted yt this king Henry the fyffte was a noble pry^ce. after he
was king and crowned. how be it to fore in his yongthe he had ben^ wild
recheles and spared no thing of his lusts ne desires but accomplisshed them
aftyr this likynge But as soon as he was crouned enoy^ted and sacred. anon^
sode^li he was changed into a new man: and set all his intent to live
virtuously in may^teny^g of holy chyrch^ destroyng of heretics / kepy^g
justice and defendy^g of his Reame and subgettys / and for asmoch^ as his fadre
had deposed by his labor ye good king richard and pitously made him to deye /
and for thefe^ce done to hi^ against his ligeau^ce. he had sent to Rom^ to be
assoilled thereof. for which offense ye pope our holy fadre enioned hy^ to make
hy^ be prayed fore perpetuelly. and like as he had done to be taken from hi^
his naturel life therefore he should be found iiij tapers to bre^ne perpetuelly
about his body. yt for ye exti^cto^n of his bodily life. his soul may ever be
remembered and live in heaven in spirituel life: and also yt he should every weke
on ye day as it comith about of his death have a sole^pne mass of Requie^ on
the eue^ to fore a dirige with ix leso^s and a dole to pour always on ye day of
xi shi^lli^ges viij pe^s to be delyd penny mele and on^s in the year at his
a^niuersarie his tereme^t to be holde^ in ye most honest wise: and to be deled
yt day xx. pound in pe^s to pour people. and every monk to have xx.
shilly^ges which all these things performed this noble king for his fadre for
king henry ye iiij. for he performed it not dury^g his life. who^ as it is said
god touchyd and was a lepre. or he deyde Also then^ this noble pry^ce let do
kalle all ye abbotys and priours of sey^t benettey order i^ England: and bad
the^ in ye chapter house of westmy^ster for the reformacio^ of the order whery^
he had comynycacyo^. and also of ye bisshoppes and me^ of the spiritualte. in
so ferforth yt they doubted sore to he would have had the teporal tees out of
their ho^des: wherefore by thauys labor and procury^g of the spiritualte
encoraged the king to challenge Norma^die and his right in France. to the^de to
set^e hy^ a work there yt he should not seek occasions to e^tre into such^
matters: and all his life aftyr he labored in ye werrys in co^query^g great
part of ye Reame of france: yt by the a greme^t of the king charles had at the
governance of the reame of france and was proclaimed rege^t and heir of
France And so not wythsta^dyng all this great werre that he had yet he
remembered his soul / and also that he was mortal and must deye: for which he
ordained by his life the place of his sepulture: where he is now buried: and
every day three masses perpetuelly to be songen in a fair chapel over his
sepulture of which the mydylmasse and the first and last mass shall be as is
assigned by him as it apperyth by these versys following Heurici miss quinti

And yet the noble king Henry ye.v. fownded two howses of Relygyo^ vne kalled
Syo^ beside bray^ford of the order of saint Brigitte both of men and women And
on that other side of ye River of Thamyse an hows of monks of Chartrehous. in
which two places he his continuelly prayed for night and day for ever wha^ they
of Syo^ rested they of the Chartrehous done their service And in like wise wha^
they of ye chartrehous rest the other goon / and by the ryngy^g of the bellys
of either place / each knows when they have endyth their service / which be
nobly e^douwed / and doo^ daily there great alms deeds as in ye chartrehows
certain children ben fownde to scole / and at syon certain alms given
daily And yet beside all this. he had found a recluse / which shall be always a
priest to pray for hy^ by ye said chartrehous / which priest is well and
suffycie^tly endowed for him and a servant

Lo here may all princes taken an example by this noble prince that regnyng so
lyttel time not fully.x. year: did so many noble acts as well for his soul to
be perpetuelly remembered and prayed for as i^ his wordly conquestis / and he
bey^g in his most lusty age despised and eschewyd sin and was virtuous and a
great iustiser / in somoch^ that all the pry^ces of cryste^dome drad him / and
also of Hethenes / and had determined in hy^ self if god would have spared him
that he would have werred again the sarazyns: and for to know the aid of other
pnces and all the passa^es in yt journey he sent a knight of Henaude named sir
Hugh^ de lanoye unto Jerusalem / but er he returned he deide at boys du vynce^t
in the xxxvi. year of his age. on whose soul god have mercy /

How king Henry the vi. reigned being a Child not one year of age^ and of the
bataille of vernoil in Perch Cap. cc.xlvij
AFter king Henry the v. reigned Henry his sone: but a child and not fully a
year old / whose regne began ye first day of Septe^bre: the year of owr lord
M.cccc.xxij. This king being in cradel was moch^ doubted and drad by cause of
the great conquest of his fadre. and also the wysedo^ and guydyng of his uncles
ye duke of bedford and ye duke of gloucestre. This year the xxi. day of Octobre
deide Charles king of france and lies buried at sey^t Denis: and tha^ was the
duke of Bedford made regent of frawnce^ and the duke of gloucestre was made
protector and defendour of e^glo^d. and ye first day of march^ afterward was
sir Willya^ taillour priest degrated of his preestde / and on the morn aft he
was brent in smythfeld for heresy. This yer^ sir Iae^s king of scotland married
dame jane the dukes daughter of clare^ce of her first husbo^de the earl of
Somersete at sey^t mary ouereys / also this yer^ the xvij / day of august was
the bataill of vernayll i^ perch bytwen^ the duke of bedford rege^t of France
and the duke of alau^son^ which was a great bataill the duke of bedford had on
his side wit hy^ the earl of salisbury montagu and the lord talbote and all the
power that they could make in norma^dye the garniso^s kept / And also many
capitaines wit moch^ people of the duke of Burgoign^: And on that other side was
the duke of alau^sone the duke of tonro^ yt was therle donglas / ye earl of
boughan with many lords of France and great company of scotts and arminakes:
And then^ the earl do^glas called ye duke of bedford Ioha^ with the leden swerd:
and he sent hy^ word agayn^ yt he should find that day that his swerd was of
steell. and so ye bataille joined on both^ sides and fought long yt there wyste
no man who should have the better a great while but at the last as god would the
victory fill unto the Englyssh partie^ for there were slain the earl donglas.
which a little before was made duke of Turone The Earl of Bowhayne. the earl
of Almarre. the Earl of Townar / the Earl of Vaundore / and the sixthe count
of Nerborne / the which was one of them that slow the noble Duke Johan of
Burgoygn^ knelyng to fore the Dolphyne and many moo unto the nombre of x.M and
moo / There was taken prisoner ye Duke of Alau^son / and many other lords and
gentylls of France / but Scotts yt day were slain down^ right the substance
of them all. In the thridde year of king Henry the vj. the Duke of Glowcestre
married the duchess of Holand: and went over see with her into Henaude for to
take poscessio^ of his wife encheritau^ce / where he was honourabely received
and taken for lord of the land / but sone after he was fay^ to return home
ayen^ and left his wife and his tresowr that he brought with in a town is
called Mounse in Henaude^ ye whych^ promised for to be true / to him.
notwithstanding they delyured the lady to ye duke of Burgoygne which sent her
to Gau^t And from thens she escaped in a man's array and came into zela^d to a
town of his own called zierirce And fro thens she went to a town in hola^d
called the Ghowde / and there she was strong enough. and withstode the said
duke of Burgoygne / And sone after the duke of Glowcestre sent over in to
zeland the lord fytzwater with certain me^ of werre. and archiers for to help
and socour the foresaid duchess of Holand. which lo^ded at a place in zela^d
called Brewers haven / where the lords of the co^tre came down and fowght with
him: and in conclusion he was fayn to withdraw him and his meyne to the sea
again / But yet he slew and hurt diverse lords and moch^ people of that same
co^tre. And so returned he home ayen^ with his meyne and preuailled no thing

Also this same year ye Earl of salysbury. the Earl of southfolk: the lord
Wylby and the lord Scalys wit their retenue leyd siege to the cite of Mowns /
the which cite was yolden to them in a short time* with many other strong
towns and castelles to the nombre of xxxvi. This time all Norma^dye and a
great part of France unto Orlyau^ce was vndyr thobeyssaunce of the king of
England. and all the remenau^t of France was in great tribulacyon and meschief

How there was a great affraye like to have ben^ between the cardinal and the
duke of Glowcestre. and of the coronacyo^ of King Henry the sixthe both in
England and in France Capitulo / CCxlviij.
IN the iiij. year ye same night that the mayre of London Johan Coue^tre had
taken his charge: was a great wacche in London: for affray yt was bitwen^ the
bishop of wy^chestre and the duke of Glowcestre protector etc. For the mayre
with the people of the cite would abide by the duke of Gloucestre as protector of
the Reame. but by labor of lords that went bitwene and in esspeciall by the
labor of the pry^ce of Portingale there was apointement taken that there was no
harm done: and after the battle of Verneill in perch: ye duke of bedford
came over into england And on witsonday this same year at leycestre he dubbed
king Henry knight. And forth with the said king Henry dubbed all these knights
whose name follow. That is to wete Richard duke of york Also the sone and heir
of the duke of Northfolk. The Earl of Oxenford / the Earl of westmerland. the
sone and heir of ye earl of northumberland / The sone and heir of the Earl of
Vrmond: the lord Roos sir James botellier / the lord Natrauas Sir henry gray of
tankeruille Sir william Neuill lord fawconbrygge: sir George neuyll lord
Latymer / the lord wellys / the lord berkely. The sone and heir of the lord
Talbot. sir Rauf gray of werk: sir Robert ver / sir Rychard gray / sir Edmond
Ho^gerford / sir robert Wynkfeld / sir Johan botteller Sir raynold Cobham / Sir
Ioha^ passheley / sir Thomas tunstall. sir Johan chidyoke. sir Rauf Langeford /
sir william Drury* sir william ap thomas / sir Rychard Carbonell / sir rychard
wydeuille Sir Johan sehirdelowe. Sir Nycholl blouket. sir Rauf ratteclyfe: sir

Gillebert beauchamp

Item in the v. year the duke of bedford with the duchess his wife went over
see to Caleys and a littel to fore went over harry bishop of wynchestre. and
on our ladies day annu^ciacyo^ in our lady church at Caleys ye bisshoppe of
wy^chestre when he had song mass was made cardinal ^ and he kne^y^g to fore
the hye altar the Duke of bedford set the hat on his head. And there were
his bulls red as well of his charge as ye reidyssy^g of his benefices
spirituell and te^porel. And this same year was great abundaunce of rain that
the substance of heye and of corn was destroyed / For it rayned all most
every other day / This same year the good Earl of Salisbury / sir Thomas
mou^tagu leyd siege unto Orliau^ce / at which siege he was slain with a gonne
which came out of ye town. on whose soul god have mercy / ame^. for since yt
he was slain Englisshme^ never gate ne preuailled in France but ever after
began to lose littel and littell till all was lost Also this sam^ year a
breto^ murthred a wedowe in her bed wtoute algate which wedowe fownde him
for alms and he bare away all that she had. and after this he took gryth of
ye holy church at seint Georges in sowthwerke. and there took he the cross and
forswore this lo^d. And as he went it happened that he came by the place where
he did this cursed deed in the subarbes of London: and the women of the same
parissh came owte with stones Canell du^ge and slow and made an end of him:
notwithstanding the Constable and many other men bey^g p^sent to keep him. For
there were many women and had no pity

Also this same year the Duke of Northfolk with many ge^tilmen and yoman took
his barge the.viij. day of Nouembre at saint Mary onerays. for to have goo
through London brygge. and through mysguydy^g of the barge it over true on the
pyles. and many men drowned: but the Duke him self wit two or three lepe upon
the pyles. and so were saved with help of me^ that were above the brigge /
which cast down roopes: by whych^ they saved hem self. This same year on
saint Lenardes day king Henry bey^g vij. year of age was crouned at westmynstre
at whose coronacyon were made xxxvi. knights / This year on saint Georges day
he passed over the sea to Caleys toward France. About this time and a fore ye
Reame bey^g in great myserie and tribulacio^: the Dolphyn with his party began
to make werre and get certayn^ places / and made great destructo^n upon
Englisshme^. by ye mean of his capitay^s: that is to wete la here / and poto^
de say^tralles. and especial a maid which they named la pucelle de dieu /
This maid rood like a man and was a vaillau^t capitai^ among the^ / and took
upon her many great enterprises. in so moch^ that they had a beleuee to have
recoured all their losses by her: Notwtsta^dy^g at the last aftyr many great
feats by the help and prowess of sir Ioha^ Luxemburgh / which was a noble
capytayne of the dukes of Burgoign^: and many Englisshme^ pycardes and
Burgoygnous which were of our party before ye town of Co^pyne the xxiij day
of May ye forsaid pucelle was taken. in ye field armed like a man: and many
other capitaynes with her / and were all brought to Roan. and there she was put in
prison: and there she was iuged by ye law to be bre^t. and then^e she said yt
she was with child. whereby she was respited a while: but i^ conclusion it was
fo^de that she was not with child. and then she was brent in Roan^ and the
other Capitayns were put to rawnsone and entreated as men of werre ben^ a
customed etc

This same year about Candelmasse Richard hunder a wollepacker was dampened for
an he^e^ike / and bre^te at the tour hille^ and about midle^te Sir Thoa^s
baggely priest and vicarie of maue^ in in Estsexe beside walden was disgrated
and dampened for an heretic and brent in smythfeld. And also in this same year
whiles the king was in france there were many heretics and lollars yt had
purposed to have made a rising and cast bylles in many places. but blessed be
god almighty the capitayn^ of he^ was taken / whose name was William maundeuille
a weve of Abyngdone and bailey of the same town / which named hy^ self jak
sharpp of wygmoresland in walys / and afterward he was beheded at Aby^gdone in
the witsonweke on the wysday: This same year ye vj. day of Dece^bre king Henry
the vj. was crouned king of France at Paris in ye church of our lady with
great sole^pnite / there being present the cardynall of England / ye duke of
Bedford: and many other lords of France and of England. and after this
coronacyo^ and great feste holde^ at Paris. the king returned from the^s to
Roan / and so toward caleys. And ye ix. day of Feuerer londed at Dover. who^
all the comy^s of Ke^te met at bera^doun bitwene canterbury and dover all in
read hodes and so came forth till he came to the Black hethe where he was met
with ye maire Ioha^ wellys wit all the craftis of London clad all in white / and
so they brought hy^ to London the xxi. day of ye same month This same year was
a restray^t of the wollis of Caleys made by ye soudiours by cause they were not
paid of their wages wherefore the duke of Bedford regent of France being then^
Capitayn came to Caleys the tewysday in the esterweke / And on ye morn after
many soudiours of the town were arested and put i^ ward: And in the same weke
he rood to Terewyne: and by the mean of the bysshopp of terewyne he wedded the
earls daughter of sey^t Poull and came ayen^ to Caleys / And on the xi. day of
juyne on sey^t Bernabes day. there were four soudiours of caleys that were
chyef causers of the restrey^t beheded. that is to wete johan Maddeley. Johan
lundaye Thomas palmer / and Thomas talbot / and an. c.x. banisshed out ye town
that same time and before were banisshed C and xx. soudiours And on mydsomer
eue^ after came the lord regent and his wife to London /

Of ye heresy of Praghe. and of ye cou^celll of aras. where the Duke of
Burgoygn^ became Frenssh Capitulo CC.xlix
About this time pope martyn deyde. And after him Eugenye ye iiij. was pope
This was pesibly chose^ in Rome by the cardinals / and was very and and
indubytate pope / but shorthely after he was put and expulsed owte of Rome i^
such^ wise that he was feign to flee naked In this same time was the cou^ceyl
of basil to which cou^ceyl he was cited to come but he rought not nesette not
thereby / but gate the cite of Rome and abode still pope xvij. year / This year
about witsontyde the heretics of Praghe were destroyed* for at two iourneys
were destroyed of them mo tha^ xxij. thousand. with her capitay^s. that is to
wete procapy^s. saplico and lupus presbiter Also there was taken a Live /
maistir piers clerk an Englysshma^ / and heretic Also this same year was a
great frost and a strong during xi. wekes: for it began on sey^t katherines
eue^ and lasted unto sey^t scolasticais day in feurer. in whych^ time the
vy^tage that came from Burdeur came over shoters hille This year was ye
cou^ceil of Aras and a great traitye bitwen^ the king of England and the king
of France where was assembled many great lords of both parties: at which
cou^ceyl was offered to the king of England many great things by the moyen of a
legate that came fro Rome / whych^ was cardinal of seint cross: whych^ offres
were refused by the cardinal of england and other lords that were there for
the king wherefore ye duke of burgoygne which had ben^ long englyssh sworn /
forsook our party and returned fre^ssh by mean of the said legate and made a
pees with ye fre^sshe king receyuy^g of ye king for reco^pe^sing of his fadres
death ye count of Pontien^ ye lorship of macon with much other as is specyfied
in the said trayttie / and so our e^bassatours came hom^ ayen^ in werse caas
tha^ they went: for they loste^ there ye duke of burgoign^ which had ben^ with
his burgoignons and picardes a singular help in all the conquest of Norma^dye
and of france / This sam^ year was a great battle on ye see bytwen^ the
Ieneweys and the king of Aragon. of which bataill the Ieneweys had ye
victory: for they took ye king of aragon / the king of Nauerne: and the great
master of sey^t james in galise: wit iij.C. knights and squiers. and much
other people. and this was on sey^t Dominikes day. This same year were see^ iij.
sons attones. and anon^ followed the threfold governance in the chirch^ /
that is to wete of Eugenye / and of the cou^ceyll / and of ye neutralite. Also
this sam^ year M.cccc.xxxiiij was a passy^g great wy^de: by which steples
houses and trees were overthrown About this time was in hola^de an holy maid
called Lydwyth. ye which lived only by miracle not etyng any mete. This same
year the duke of Burgoign^ began his order at Lyle of the golden Flies and
ordained certain knights of the order and made statutes / and ordinances
moch^ accordy^g unto the order of the Garter. Also this same year the
Fre^sshmen had enterprysed to have stole^ Caleys in the fissyng time. for many
bootis of France had saufcou^duytis to come to Caleys for to take hery^g And
the soudeours of the town had a custom to come to chyrch^ / and leave their
stauis sta^dyng at the church door: The Fre^sshme^ which were araied like
fysshers had purposed to have taken so their wepen and won the town. but one
of them lay with a comy^ woman ye night to fore and told to her their cou^ceill.
and she on the morn told ye lieutenau^t: which forthwith commanded that
every man should keep his wepe^ in his hand sakry^g time and other: And wha^
they apperceyued this yt they were myspoy^ted. they sailled strayt to deep and
stale and took that town And on newyers eue^ after they toke^ harflete / and
thus the Englisshmen began to loss a littell and a littell in Normandye

How Caleys and Gwyhenes were beseged by the duke of Burgoign^ and how they
were rescued by the duke of Gloucestre Capitulo CC.l
THis year was great noise through England how the duke of Burgoigne would come
and besiege Caleys wherefore the Earl of mortayne wit his armeye yt he had for
to have goo^ with into France was contremau^ded and charged that he should go
to Caleys which was at that time well vitailled and ma^ned. for sir Ioha^
raclife was lyeutenau^t vndyr the king in that town^ And ye baron of duddeley
lieutenau^t of the castle. And the ix. day of juyll the duke of Burgoign^ with
all ye power of Flau^dres and moch^ other people came before caleys and set
his siege about the town and every town of Flau^dres had their tents by he^
self: and this siege endured three wekes. In the mean while the Duke of
Glowcestre being protector of England and went over the sea to Caleys. for to
rescue the town^ or to fight with the duke and his host. if they would have
byden / This time london and every good town of England sent over see to this
rescouse certay^ people well araied of the best and chose^ men for the werre /
And the ij day of August the said duke of Gloucestre arrived at Caleys with all
his army and v. ho^dred ships and moo: and the duke and all his oost that
lay in the siege as soon as they espied the sailles in the sea before they
approached Caleys haue^ suddenly in a morny^g departed fro the siege leuyng
behind the^ moch^ stuff and vitaille and fled into Flau^dres and pycardie
and in like wise did to the siege that lay tofore guynes / where as they of
Gwynes took the great gonnes of brass kalled Dygeon and many other great
gonnes and serpe^tynes: And then^e wha^ the duke of Glowcestre was arrived with
all his oost he went in Flau^dres. and was therinne xj days / and did but
little harm except he burnt two fair vyllages / poperyng and Belle and other
howses which were of no strenghthe. and so he returned home agayn^. Also this
same year the king of Skotland beseged noresburgh with moch^ people. But sir Rauf
gray departed fro the castle and ordained for rescouse. But as soon as the king
vndyrstode his departy^g he suddenly brake his siege and went his way and
leuy^g moch^ ordinance behy^de him. where he gate no wurship This same year
the ij. day of Ianiuer queen katheryne which was the kings mother and wife to
king Henry the fi^^ he deyde. and departed out of this world: and was brought
rially through London / and so to westmynster / and there she lies wurshipfully
buried in our lady chapel / And also this same year the xiiij. day of Ianiuer
fill down the gate with the tower on london brygge toward southwerke. with two
archiers and all that stood thero^. This same year was a great trayttie holden
bitwen^ Grauenyng and Caleys bitwen^ ye king and the duke of burgoigu^.
wherefor the king was the cardinal of England the duke of Northfolk and many
other lords. and for the duke was ye ducesse having full power of her lord as
regent and lady of his lands. where was taken by thaduyse of both parties an
abstine^ce of werre for a certain time in the name of the duchess / and not
of the duke^ because he had goo^ from his oath and liegeaunce that he had made
to king Henry therefore / The king never would write ne apoi^te ne have to do with
hi^ aftir / but al in the duchesses name Also this same year deyed quen^ jane
the ij. day of Iuyll whych^ had been king Henry the fourthis wife. and was
karyed fro bermondsey unto caunterbury: where she lies buried by king Henry
the fourth her howshold. This same year deyed all the lions into the tower of
london: the which had not be seyn many years before out of my^de

How oway^ a squire of Walys that had wedded Queen Katheryne was arested. and
of the scisme of Eugenye and Felix Capitulo CC.li.
IN the xvi. year of king henry deyde Sygismo^de emperor of Almaygne. and
knight of the garter / whose entierement the king kept at saint Powles in
London ryally: where was made a ryall herfe / and the king in his astate clad
in blew was at even at Dirige / and on the morn at mass. etc And after hy^
was elect and chosen Albert Duke of Ostrich^. which had wedded Sigismondis
daughter for to be emperor This was taken and received to be king of Beme and
Hungary / because of his wife that was Sigysmo^dus daughter: whych^ left
after him non^ other heir. This Albert was emperor but one year: for he was
empoysoned^ and so deide he: and sum saide^ yt he deyed of a flixe: but he
was a virtuous man and pyteful so moch^ that all ye people that knew hy^ said^
that ye world was not worthy to have his p^sence / This same year one Owayn a
squier of Walys a man of low birth which had many a day tofore secretly
wedded quen^ katheryne and had by her iij. sons: and a daughter / and he was
taken and commanded to newgate to pryso^ by my lord of gloucestre protector
of the reame / and this year he brake prison by ye mean of a pressed that was his
chappelayne. and after he was taken agay^ by my lord hemond and brought agay^
to newgate / which afterward was delivered at large and one of his sons
afterward was made earl of Richemo^d: and an other earl of Pe^broke. and the
iij. a monk of westmynster / which monk deide son^ after / This same year
also on newyereisday at baynarde castle fill down^ a stak of wode sode^li at
afternone and slow iij. me^ mescieuously and foul hurt other / also at Bedford
on a Shere day were viij. me^ murthred wytoute strok by fally^g a down of a
steirr^ / as they came out of their comy^ halle and many foul hurt. In the
xviij year sir rychard beaucha^p the good Earl of warrewyk deyde at Rowa^ he
being that time lieutena^t of ye king in Norma^die: and from the^s his body was
brought to warrewyk where he lies wurshipfully in a new chapel on ye
southside of ye quire Also this year was a great derthe of corn in all e^glo^d
/ for a busshell of whete was worth xl. pe^s in many places of england. and yet
men might not have ynowgh wherefore stephen Brown yt time maire of London sent
in to Pruse and brought to london certain ships laden with rye / which
eased and did moch^ good to the people. for corn was so skare in England that
i^ some places of england pour people made he^ bread of fern rotes This year
the general cou^ceill of basille deposed pope Eugenie. and they chosen Felix
which was duke of Sauoye. and tha^ began ye scisme which endured unto the
year of our lord Jesus crist M^cccc.xlviij. This felix was a deuote pry^ce and
saw ye sons of his sons. and after lived a holy and devout life and was
chose^ pope by the cou^ceill of basile Eugenie deposed. and so the scisme was
long time. And this Felix had no moch^ obedience by cause of the neutralite.
for the most part and well nygh^ all criste^dome obedied and reputed Eugenye
for very pope: god knows who was ye very pope of them both^ / for both^
occuped during ye life of Eugenye / This sam^ year sir Rychard which was
vicarye of Hermettesworth was degrated of his presthede at Poulys: and bre^te
at tour hill as for an heretyke on sey^t Botulphus day: how well at his death he
deyde a good criste^ man. wherefore after his death moch^ people cam^ to the place
where he had be bre^t* and offered and made a heepe of stones and set up a
cross of tree and held hi^ for a saint till the mayre and sherewes by the
commandment of ye king and of bisshoppes destroyed it: and made there a
doughille: Also this same year the sherews of london fette out of saint
Martins ye grant the seintwarye five persons which afterward were restored
agayn^ to the say^twarie by the ky^ges justices. After Alberte ye iij.
Frederike was chosen emperor / This frederyke Duke of Osterike was long
emperor. and desired to be crowned at Rome by cause of ye scisme / but after
that vnyo^ was had / he was crowned with imperial dy^deme wit great glory and
triu^phe / of pope Nycholas the fowrthe. This was a man pesible quyete and of
singular patience: not hatyng the church / he wedded the king of porty^gales
daughter etc

How the duchess of gloucestre was arested for treson and commyted to
perpetual prison in the ^ie of Man. and of the death of maistir Rogier
Bolyngbroke Capitulo cclij.
IN this year Elianore cobham duchess of Gloucestre was arested for certay^
pointys of treson leyd ayens her where upon she was examined in saint stephens
chapel at Westmynster before the Erchebisshop of Canterbury. and there she
was enyoned to opyn penance for to go through chepe beryng a taper in her hond.
and after to perpetual prison in the I Will of Man vndyr ye kepy^g of sir Thomas
sta^ley: also that sam^ time was arestyd master Thomas southwel a chanon of
westmy^ster maistir joha^ hune a chappelay^ of the said lady / maistir Roger
boly^gbroke a clerk using nygroma^cie: and one margery jurdeman called the
which of eye beside westmynster Thise were arested as for being of cou^ceill
with the said duchess of Glowcestre / and as for maistir Thomas soutwell he
deyde in the tour the night before he should have be reyned on ye morn for so
he said hy^ self that he should deye in his bed / and not by iustise. And in
the xx. year maistir Johan Hune and maistir Rogier boly^gbroke were browght to
the guyldhalle in london: and there before the maire the lords and chief
Justice of England were rayned and dampened both^ to be drawn hanged and
quartred: but maistir Ioha^ hune had his chartre and was pardoned by the king.
but maistir Rogier was drawn to Tiborne: Where he co^fessyd that he never had
trespaced: and in that he deyde fore / not withsta^dyng h^e was hanged beheded
and quartred / on whose soul god have mercy / and Margery jurdemayn was brent
in smythfeld / Also this year was a great affraye in Fletstret by nyghtes time
/ bytwen^ men of court and men of london and diverse men slain and so^me hurt
/ and one herbotell was chief cause of the misgouernau^ce and affraye / Also
this year at ye chesing of the mayre of London the conmunes named Robert
clapton* and Rawlyn holand. Tailor ye aldremen took Robert clapto^ and brought
him at right hand of the mayre as the custom is And then^e certain
tayllours and other hond crafty men cried Nay. not this man. but Rawlyn
holande. wherefore the maire that was padysly se^te to thay^ that so cried to
newgate where they abode a great while and were punisshed: In this sam^ year
were diverse enbassatours sent into Gwyan for a marriage for the king / for the
earls daughter of Armynake. which was concluded / but by the mean of the Earl
of Sutfolk it was let and put a part And after this the said Earl of
suthfolk went over the sea into france: and there he trated the marriage
bytwen^ the king of England and the ky^ges daughter of Secyle and of Iherusale^

And the next year it was conclucluded fully ye marriage* by which marriage the
king should delyuere to her fadre the duchy of Angeoy and the Erledome of
mayne^ which was the keye of Norma^die then^ departed the earl of sutfolk with
his wife and diverse lords and knights in the most ryall astate that might
be out of England with new chares and palfrayes which went through chepe and
so went over ye see and received her and since brought her in the le^te after
to ha^pton where she la^ded and was rially received / and on ca^delmasse eue^
before by a great tempest of thonder and lightny^g at afternone paulus steple
was set a fire on the mids of shafte in the Tymbre / which was quenched by
forse of labor / and spicially by the labor of the morrow mass priest of the
bow in chepe: which was thought impossible sauf only ye grace of god This
year was the earl of staford made and create duke of boly^gham ye earl of
warrewyk duke of warrewyke. the earl of dorset makeys of dorset. and therle of
soutfolk was made marquys of Suffolk

How king Henry wedded Quen^ margarete and of her coronacyon Cap. ducentesimo
lij
IN this year king Henry married at soutwerk que margrete and she came to london
the xviij day of may And by the way all the lords of england received her
wurshipfully in diverse places: and in especial the Duke of gloucestre. and on
ye blake heth the mayre ^ aldremen and all ye crafts in blewe go^nes browdred
wit the deuyse of his craft that they might be thereby known met wit her
with reed hoodes: and brought her to london. where were diverse pagentis and
continuance of diverse histories shewde in diverse places of the cite rially
and costeli And the forsaid quen^ was crouned at westmynster / and there was
joustes three days during withy^ the santuarye to fore the abbeye. This year
the pryour of Kylmyan appeled the earl of Vrmond of treson: which had a day
assygned to them for to fight in smythfeld And the lystes were made and feeld
dressid: but it came to point. The king commanded that they should not fight.
but took the quarellys into his own hond / and this was done at the instau^ce
and labowre of certain^ prechours and doctors of London as maistir gillebert
worthyngton parson of seint Andrews in holborne and other. Also this same year
cam^ a great enbassade into England owte of France for to have concluded a
perpetuell pees but in conclusion it turned unto a triewes of a year: About
this time deyde saint Barnardine a gray friar. which began the new reformacion
of that order in many places / i^ so much yt they yt were reformed been called
obseruau^tes. which obseruau^tes ben^ encrecid greatly in Italye and in
Almaigne: this Bernardyn was canonysed by pope Nicholas the v. In the year
M.cccc.l. Ioha^nes de capestrano was his disciple: which profyted moch^ to the
reformacion of that order / for who^ god showed many a fair miracle: Also here
is to be noted that from this time forthward king henry never profyted ne went
forthward. but fortune began to turn from him on all sides as well in france
Normandye Guyan as in England. Sum men hold opynyone yt king Henry yaf
commyssyo^ plenerly to sir Edward hulle sir Robert roos dene of saint Seuery^s
and other to conclude a marriage for him. with ye Earl of Arminakes suster
which was promised as it was said and concluded: but afterward it was broken:
and he wedded queen Margrete as a fore is said: which was a dear marriage for
the Reame of England: for it is known verily / that for to have her / was
delivered the duchye of Angeoy and the Erledo^me of main* which was the keye
of Norma^die for the Frensshmen tentre / and above this the said marqueys of
suthfolcke axid in play^ perlement a fyftenth and an half for to fecce her
out of France / Lo what marriage was this as to the comparison of that other
marriage of armynyke: for there should have ben^ delivered so many castelles and
tounes in Gwihe^ne: and so moch^ good should have been yeuen with her. yt all
England should have there by enryched / but contrary wise fylle Wherefore every
great prince owght to keep his promise / for because of brekyng of his promise
/ and for marriage of ye Quen^ margret / what loss had the reame of England by
lossyng of Norma^dye and Gwyan by division in the reame the rebelling of
communes against their prince and lords / what division among ye lords. what
murdre and sleyng of them. what feldes fowghten and made in co^clusio^ so many
that many a man has lost his life / and in conclusion the king deposed. and
the quen^ with her sone feign to flee into scotland. and from thens i^nto
France. and so to Loraine that she came first fro. many men deem yt ye breki^g
of ye kings promysse to the suster of therles of Armynak was cause of this
great loss and aduersite

How the good duke of gloucestre Humfrey ye ky^ges uncle was arested at the
parliament of bury and of his death. and how Angeoy in main was delyured
Capitulo CCliij.
IN the year xxv. of king henry was a parliament at bury kalled saint Edmo^des
bury about: which was commanded all the conmunes of the contre to be there
in their most defe^sable array for to awayte upon the hyng. To which
parliament came the duke of Gloucestre hu^frey the kings uncle / which had
ben^ protector of England all the none age of the ky^g^ And anon^ after as he
was in his loggy^ge he was arested by the viscou^te bemond ye conestable of
england accompanied with the duke of Bokyngham and mani other lords: And forth
with all his servants were conmau^ded for to depart from him and xxxij of
the chief of them were also arested and sent to diverse prysons. And anon
after this said areste the for said duke was on the morn deed. on whose soul
god have mercy Amen / But how he deyde and in what manner the certainte is not
to me known / some said he deide for sorwe: sum said he was murthred
bitwen^ two fetherbeddes / other said yt on hot spite was put in at his
fou^deme^t: but how he deyde god knows / to who^ is no thing hid. and then^
wha^ he was so deed he was leid open that all me^ might see hy^. And so both^
lords and knights of the shires with burgeises came and saw hy^ lie deed but
wo^de ne toke^ could they perceive how he deyde. Here may me^ mark what the
world is / this Duke was a noble man and a great clerk and had wurshypfully
ruled this reame to the ky^ges behoue: and never could be found fault to hy^.
but envy of the^ that were governors and had promised ye Duchy of Angeoy and
the erledome of main caused the destructyon of this noble man. for they drad
hy^ that he would have enpesshed that that delyuera^ce / and after they sent
his body to seint Albo^s with certey^ lights for to be buried And so sir geruays
of clifton had tha^ ye charge to conueye ye corpse: and so it was buried at
seint Albo^s in ye abbey: and v. persons of his household were sent to London:
and there were rained and iugged to be drawn ho^ged and quartred / of whom the
names were sir Rogier cha^burlayne knight / on middelto^ a squier Herbard a
squier* Arthur a squier and Richard nedha^ / which v. persons were drawn
from the tour of London. through chepe unto Tiborne / and there ho^ged and late
down^ quyke. and then^ strypt for to have ben^ beheded and quartred / And then^
ye ^^arquys of sutfolke showed there for the the ky^ges perdon vndyr his great
seall / and lo they were perdoned of the remenau^t of the execucyo^ / and had
their lives And so they were brought again to London. and aftyr freely
deliured / Thus began ye troble in ye Reame of England: for ye death of this
noble duke of Gloucestre / All the co^munes of ye Reame began for to murmr
for it. and were not co^^ent. after that pope Eugenye was deed / Nycholas ye
fifthe was elect pope. This nycholas was chosen for Eugenye yet ha^gyng the
cisme not withsta^dyng he gate ye obedia^ce of all cryste^ reames / for after
he was elect and sacred pope: certain lords of france and of England were
sent into sauoye to pope Felix: for to entrete him to cesse of the papocie /
and by the spiciall labor of ye bishop of Norwych^: and the lord of sey^t
Ioha^nes. he cessed the second year aft that pope Nycholas was sacred / And ye
said Felix was made legate of france and cardinal of sauoye / and resigned ye
hole papocie to Nycholas. and after lived an holy life. and deide an holy man.
and as it is said almighty god showed miracles for hy^ / This was the xxiij
scisme bytwen^ Eugenye and felix. and dured xvj year / ye cause was this: the
general counceill of Basille deposed Eugenye / which was only pope and
indubitate / for asmoch^ as he observed not and kept the decrees and statutes
of ye cou^ceill of Co^stau^ce as it is a fore said: nethir he rought not to
give obedience to that general cou^ceill in no manner wise / whereof arose a
great alteracyo^ among writars of this matters pro et contra / which can not
accord unto this day. One party says. that the cou^ceyll is above the pope:
that other party said: nay. but the pope is above the cownceyll. God blessid
above all things give and grant his pees in holy church spouse of Crist.
amen This Nycholas was of Iene comen of low birth a doctor of divinity an
attyf man: he reedified many places that were broken and ruynous: and did do
make a great wall about the palace and made the wall new about Rome for
dread of the turks. And ye people wo^dred of the eresing and resingyng of Felix
to hi^ considered that he was a man of so humble burth^ / and that other was of
affynyte to all the most part of christian pry^ces. where of there was a verse
publyssed in this manner Lux fulsit mundo ces sit Felix Nycholao

How sir Franceys araganoys took Fogiers in normandye / and of the loss of
Constantinoble by the turk Capi. CCliiij.
IN the year of king Henry xxvij / bey^g trewes bitwene france and England a
knight of ye Englyssh party. named Fogiers against the trewes made / of which
taky^g began moch^ sorwe and loss / For this was the occasion by which the
Fre^sshmen ga^e all norma^dye etc. About this time the cite of Constantinoble
which was Imperial cite in all greece was taken by ye Turks ^nfidels which
was betrayed as so^me hold opinion: and the Emperor taken and slain. And
that riall chyrch^ of sa^cta sophia robbed and despoil^led: and the relyques
and images and the rode drawn about the street. which was done in despyte of
christian feyth And sone after all criste^ faith in Greece perisshed and cessid /
There were many christian me^ slain and innumerable sold and put in captivity by
the taking of this towne^ where through ye turk is gretely enhaunsed in pryde^
and it is a great loss unto all cristendomme

In the year xxviij. was a great parliament holden at Westmy^ster. And from
thens by the commandment of the king it was adiourned to the Blake freris at
London / And after Cristmas to westmynster again: And this same year Robert of
cane a man of the west co^tre wit a few ships took a great floote of ships
coming out of the baye lade^ with salt: which ships were of pruis
Flau^dres. hola^d and zeland: and brought hem to Hampto^. wherefore ye
marcha^dys of England being in Flaundres were arested in Brugges Ippre and
other places. and might not be delivered ne their dettys descharged till they
had made apoynteme^t for to pay for thame^des and hurtes of the ships which
was paid by the merchants and goods being in Da^ske were also arested and
made great ame^des: This same year the fre^sshme^ in a morning took by a train
ye town of pount larche: and theryn ye lord faconbrygge was take prisoner. And
after that i^ dece^bre Roan was taken and lost. being theri^ the duke of
Somersette. Edmond the earl of shrewsbury: which by apoy^tement left plegges
and lost all Norma^die and came home. And during the said perleme^t the duke
of Sutfolk was arested and sent into the toure. and there he was a moneth^ and
after the king did do fecche him out. for which cause all the communes of
England were in a great Rumor. what for the delyuerau^ce of Angeoy and mayn /
and after losing of all Norma^dye^ and in espicial for the deth^ of the good
duke of Gloucestre. In so moch^ yt in some places men gadred to gedres and made
hem capitaynes as bleweberd and other: which were afterward resisted and taken
and had justyce and deide. And then^ the said perlement was adiourned to
leycestre / and thither the king brought with him the duke of Suthfolk / and when
the conmune house understood yt he was out of the toure / came^ thither and they
desired to have execucyon on them that were cause of the delyuera^ce of
Norma^die. and had be^ cause of the death of the duke of Glowcestre. and had
sold Gascoygne and Gwyan. of which they named to be gylty the duke of sutfolk
as chief. the lord say. the bishop of salysbury: Daniell and many moo And for
to pease the commons the duke of suthfolke was exylled out of England v. year:
and so during the parliament / he went into Northfolke / and there took he his
shyppyng for to goo owte of the reame of England into france And this year as
he saylled on the sea a shipp of werre kalled the Nycholas of tour met with
ship and found hy^ therynne / who^ they took out and brought him into their
ship tofore the maistir and capytayns. and there he was examined and at
last iugged to the death / And so they put hy^ in a Cabon and his chapelayne for
to shryue him. and that done they browght hy^ into Doner rode and there set
hi^ into the boot and there smoten of his head and brought the body a lord
upon the sondes and set the head thereby. And this was done ye first day of
May: Lo what auaylled him now all his delyuerance of Normandy etc. And here
ye may here how he was rewarded for ye death of ye duke of Gloucestre / Thus
began sorrow upon sorrow and death / for death: etc

How this year was thinsurrexion in Kente of the co^munes of whom Iake kade an
Irissh man was capytayne Ca cc.lv
THis year of owre lord Mcccc.l. was the great grace of Iubilee at Rome: where
was great pardon. in so much that from all places in cristendome great
multitude of people resorted thither: This year was a great assemble and gadryng
to gedre of the co^muns of Ke^te in great no^bre and made an insurrexio^ and
rebelled ayens the king and his laws / and ordained hy^ a capitay^ called
Johan kade an Irisshman / which named him self mortymer cosy^ to the duke of
york And this capitay^ held these men to gedre: and made ordenau^ces among
the^ and browght he^ to blakeheth: where he made a bill of peticions to the
king and his cou^ceyll / and showed what injuries and opp^ssyo^s the pour
co^my^s suffered / and all vndyr color for to come to his above and he had a
great multitude of people And ye xvij day of Iuyn^ the king with mani lords
capitayns and men of werre went toward hy^ to the blakeheth And when the
capitay^ of ke^te understood the comy^g of ye king with so great puissau^ce
withdrewe hy^ wit his people to seuenoke a littel village: and the xxviij day of
Iuyn^ he being withdrawe^ and goon / ye king came wit his army set in order
and enbatailled to the blakheth And by aduis of his cownceyll sent sir v^nfrey
stafford knight and Willya^ stafford squier two valyau^t capitay^s with certay^
people to fight with ye capitay^ and to take hy^ and bring him and his accessaries
to the king. which went to seuenoke and there ye capitay^s met with he^ and
fought against hem and in co^clusio^ slew the^ both^. and as many as abode and
would not yield hy^ ner flee. dury^g this skarmussh fill a great variau^ce
among the lords men and comy^ people being on ye blakeheth against their
lords and capytayns sayng play^ly that they would go to the capitay^ of Kente
to assiste and help hi^^ but if they might have execucyo^ on ye traitors
being about the king whereto ye king said nay / And they said plainly that the
lord say tresorer of Englo^d^ the bishop of salisbury the baron of duddely /
the abbot of Gloucetua: daniel and treuillia^ and many mo were traitors and
worthy to be ded herfor / for to plese the lords meine and also some of ye
ky^ges house the lord say was arested and sent to the tour of london / and
then^e the king hery^g tidinges of the death and ouerthrowy^g of the staffordes
witdrewe hy^ to london. and fro the^s to kylly^gworth: for ye king ne the
lords durst not trust their own howshold meyne etc Then^ after yt the
captain had the victory upon these staffordes anon^ he took sir Vmfreys
salade and his briga^tins smite^ full of gylt nailles and also his gylt spores
and araied hy^ like a lord and a capitay^ and resorted wit all his meyne and
also moo than he had to the blakheth agay^: to who^ came the erchebisshop of
canterbury and the duke of boky^gha^ to ye blakheth and spoke with him / and as
it was said they fownde hy^ witty in his talking and request. and so they
departed / and the thridde day of Iuyll he came and entered into london wit all
his people / and there did make cries in the ky^ges name and in his name: that
no man should rob ne take no man's good but if he paid for it. and came
ridyng through ye cite in great pride and smote his sweerd upon london stone in
ca^wykestrete / And he bey^g in the cite sent to ye tower for to have the lord
say. and so they fete hy^ and brought hi^ to the Guyld hall before the maire
and the aldreme^ where he was examined and he said he would and owght to ben^
iuged by his peers: and the co^munes of ke^te took him by force from the mayre
and officiers yt kept him and took him to a priest for to shriue him / and er
he might half ben^ shryue^. they brought hy^ to the Standard in chepe / and
there smote of his head / on whose soul almighty god have pity and mercy / ame^
And thus deyde ye lord say tresorer of England / After this they set his head
on a spear and bare it about in ye cite. And the sam^ day about the mile end
crowemer was beheded. And the day before afternone the capytaine wit certain
of his meyne went to Phelipp malpas house and robbed him and took a way moch^
good And fro the^s he went to sey^t Margrete patyns to one gherstys house and
robbed hy^ and took away much good also. at whych^ robby^g diverse me^ of
London of their neighbors were and took part with the^ / for this robbyng the
peples hertes fill from him. and every thrysty man was a ferd for to be served
in like wise / for there was many a man in london that awayted and would feign
have see^ a common robbery which almighty god forbede / for it is to suppose
if he had not robbed: he might have goon fer er he had be withstonde / For the
king and all the lords of ye Reame of England were departed. except ye lord
Scales that kept ye tower of London. and the fifte day of Iuyll he did done
smite of a ma^nys head i^ soutwerke / and the night aft ye maire of london the
aldreme^ and the conmunes of ye cite concluded to drive away ye capitay^ and
his host / and sent to the lord scales to the tour. and to Matthew gogh a
capitay^ of Norma^die that they would yt night assaille the capitay^ wit the^ of
Ke^te. and so they did / and came^ to london brygge in southwerke er ye
capytay^ had any knowledge thereof / and there they fought with the^ that kept ye
brygge and ye ke^tisshmen went to harnoys and cam^ to the brygge and shot and
fowght wit he^ and gate the brygge and made the^ of London to flee and slow
many of he^ / and this endured all the night to and fro till ix. of the clock
on ye morn / and at last they bre^te the draw brugge where many of the^ of
London were drowned. in which night Sutto^ an alderman was slain Rogier
heysant and matthew gohe: and many other / And after this the chau^celer of
England sent to the capitay^ a pardone general for hi^. and an other for all
his meyne: and then^ they deperted from southwerke eueri man hom^ to his hows /
and when they were all deperted and goon. there were proclamacio^s made in Ke^te
soutsex and i^ other places that what man cowde take the capitay^ quyke or deed
should have a M. mark. and after this. one Alysawnder Iden squier of Kente took
hy^ in gardy^ in southsex: and in the taking the capytayn Johan cade was
slain^. and after beheded and his heed set on london brygge: And anon^ after
then^e the king came into ke^te and did his justices sit at caunterbury / and
enquered who were accessarees and chyef cause of this insurrexio^ / And there
were viij. me^ iugged to death in one day. and in other places moo / and fro
the^s the king went into soutsex and into the westcontre / where a little
before was slain the bishop of Salysbury / and this same yer^ were so many
iugged to death that xxiij hedes stood on london brigge attones

Of the field that ye duke of york took at brentheth in Kente. And of the

IN the year xxx. The duke of york came out of the march of Walys wit the
Earl of denenshire and the lord Cobham and great puissaunce for reformacio^ of
certay^ jniuries and wrongs / and also to have justyce on certain lords being
about ye king and took a feld at brentheth beside derthford in kente / whych^
was a strong feld / For which cause the king with all the lords of ye lord
went unto the blakeheth with a great and strong multitude of people armed and
ordained for the werre in the best wise And wha^ they had musteried on the
blakeheth / Certain lords were sent to hy^ for to trete and make apoy^teme^t
with hy^. which were the bishop of ely. and the bishop of wynchestre: and the
earls of salisbury and of warrewyke And they concluded that the duke of
somersette should be had to ward and to a^swere to such^ articles as the duke
of york should put on hy^ and tha^ the duke of york should break his feld and
come to the king / which was promised by the king: And so the king commanded
that the duke of Somersette should be had in ward. and then^ the duke of york
brake up his feld and came to the king: and when he was come contrary to ye
promise a fore made / the duke of somersete was p^sent in the field awayty^g
and chief about the king / and made the duke of york ride to fore as a
prisoner through london and aft they would have put hi^ in hold But a noise arose
that the earl of march his sone was comy^g wit x.M. men to london ward: whereof
the king and his cou^ceille fered / And then^ they concluded that the Duke of
york should depart at his will / About this time began great deuysion in
sornisse bitwen^ the great maistir and ye knights of the duche order / which
were lords of yt co^tre^ For the co^munes and tounes rebelled against the
lords / and made so great werre that at the last they kalled the king of Pole
to be their lord. the which king came and was wurshipfully received and laid
siege to the castle of Marienburgh which was the chief castle and stre^gest
of all the land and wan it / and drofe owte the maistir of Danske and of all
other places of that land / And also they that had been lords many years /
lost all their lorshyppes and poscessions

And the year of the Incarnacyo^ of owre. lord M.cccc.liij. on saint Edwardes
day the queen Margrete was delivered of a fair prince which was named Edward /
That same day Johan Norman was chosen for to been mayre of london: And the day

the crafts: where a fore time the mayre / aldremen. and all the crafts roode
a horsebake whych^ was never used after / For syn that time they have goon ever
by water in barges

Ye have well understood tofore how that contrary to the promy-of the king
and also the conclusions taken between the king and the noble duke of york at
brentheth: the Duke of Somersete went not to ward: but abode about the king
and had great rewle. And anon after he was made capytayn of the town of
Caleys and rewled the king and his reame as he would: wherefore ye great lords
of the Reame and also the communes were not plesyd / for which cause the Duke
of york: ye Earls of Warrewyk and of Salisbury wit many knights and squyers
and moch^ people came for to remeue ye said Duke of Somersette and other fro the
king / and the king heryng of their comy^g thought by his cou^ceyll for to have
goon westward. and not for to mete with he^. and had with he^ the duke of
Somersette. the duke of Bokyngha^. the earl of Stafford the Earl of
Northumberland / lord Clyfford and many other. And what time that the duke of
york / and his felawshyp understood yt the king was departed with these said

sey^t Albo^s the xxiij. day of May and there met with ye king To who^ the
king sent certay^ lords and desired he^ to keep the pees and departed. but in
conclusion whiles they treated on that one side: the Earl of warrewyk wit the
march^ men and other entrid the town on that other. and fowght aye^s ye king
and his party And so began the bataille and fyghty^g / which endured a good
while: but in conclusion the Duke of york obtained and had ye victory of that
journey In which bataill was slayn^ the duke of somersete / the Earl of
Northumberland. the lord clifford and many knights and squyers and many moo
hurt / and on the morn after they brought the king in great astate to London:
which was logged in the bisshoppes paleys of London. And anon^ after was a
great parliament holde^: in which parliament the duke of york was made
protector of England. and the Earl of warrewyk capitay^ of Caleys and the earl
of Salisbury chau^celer of England: and all such^ persons as had the rewle to
fore about the king were set a part and might not rewle as they did to fore.
In this same year deyed pope Nycholas ye fifte and after hy^ was calixte ye
iij. This Calixte was a Catalane and an old man wha^ he was chosen and
co^tynuelly seek: wherefore yt he might not parforme his zele and desire that he
had against the turk conceived. and the cause of lettyng thereof. was his age
and sekenes. This Calixte institued and ordained ye feste of the

because of ye great victory that they of Hu^gary had against the turks. yt
same day he was chosen pope in ye year of our lord M.cccc.lv / and deied the
yer^ M.cccc.lviij / that sam^ day that he ordained the feste of the
tra^sfiguracyon to be hallowed: In this sam^ year fill affraye in London ayens
the Lumbardes. The cause began that a yongeman took a dogger from a lu^bard and
brake it / wherefore the yongman on the morn was se^te fore to come before the
maire and aldreme^ / and therefore the offense he was committed to ward / And
then^e the mayre deperted from the guyldhall for to goo home to his diner. but
in the chepe the yo^gme^ of the mercerye for the most part pre^tises held ye
mayre and sherews still in chepe: and would not suffer hy^ to deperte unto the
time that their felawe which was commyted to ward were delivered / and so by
force they rescued their felaw from prison and that dou^ the mayre and shereues
deperted. and the prisoner delivered which if he had be put to prison had be
in ieoperdye of his life and began a rumor in the cite against the Lu^bardes /
and the same eueny^g the hand crafty people of the town arose and run to the
lu^bardes howses and despoylled and robbed diverse of he^: wherefore the mayre
and aldremen came with the honest people of the town and drofe the^ thens and
sent some of the^ that had stolen to newgate / and the yo^gman yt was rescued
by his felawes saw this great rumor afraye and robery ensiwed of his first
me^y^g to ye lumbard: deperted and went to westmy^ster to saintuarie / or
else it had costed hy^ his life for anon after came down an oeyr determyne
for to do justice on all the^ that so rebelle^ in the cite ayens the lu^bardes
on which sat wit the maire that time willya^ marowe th^e duke of boky^gham
and many other lords / for to see excecucyon dou^ but the comyns of the cite

for to have ronge^ the comy^ belle which is named bow belle: but they were
let by sad men which cam^ to the knowlech^ of the duke of bokyngha^ and
other lords and inco^tine^t they aroos for they durst no le^ger abide / for

How the lord Egremo^d was taken by therle of Salisburyes sons. and of the
robbyng of sandwhych. Capitu. CClvij
THis year were taken iiij. great fisshes bitwen^ Eerethe and London that one
was kalled mors marine. the second aswerd fisshe. and ye other tweyne were
wales. In this same year for certain affraye done in ye northco^tre bitwen^
the lord Egremo^d and ye earl of salisbury sons. the said lord Egremo^d who^
they had taken was co^da^pned in a great some of money to the said Earl of
salisbury and therefore co^mysed to pryso^ in newgate in london. where wha^ he had
be a certay^ space he brak the pryso^ and iij. prisoners with hy^ and escaped and
went his way / Also this year the earl of warrewyk and his wife went to caleys
wit a fair felawshyp and took poscession of his office. About this time was a
great reformacion of many monasteries of religion in diverse parties of the
world which were reformed after ye first institucion and continued in many
places. Also about this time the craft of enpry^ty^g was first fo^de in
Magu^te in Almaygne / which craft is mltiplied through ye world in many places:
and books ben^ had great chepe and in great nombre by cause of ye same craft
This sam^ year was a great bataill in the marches bitwen^ hu^gerie and turkye /
at a place kalled septedrawe: where innumerable turks were slayn^. more by
miracle than by man's ho^de For only the hand of god smote the^: sey^t joha^
of capestrane was there p^sent and provoked ye christian people being then^ aferd
afterward to pursiewe ye turks / where infinite multitude were slayn^ and
destroyed: the turks said yt a great no^bre of armed me^ followed the^ yt they
were aferd to turn agayn^. they were holy angelis. This same year the
prisoners of newgate in london brake their prysons and went upon ye leedes and
fought aye^s the^ of the cite. and kept the gate a long while / but at the
last the toun^ gate the prison on the^. and tha^ they were put in feteris and
yro^s and were sore punisshed in ensample of other. In this year also was a
great Erthequake in Napels. i^ somoch^ yt there perissed xl.M. people yt sa^ke
there i^to ye earth Ite^ in the year xxxvi. seint Osmo^d some time bishop of
salisbury was canonised at Rome by pope calixte. and ye xvj day of Iuylle he
was translated at salisbury by ye erchebisshop of Canterbury and many other
bisshoppes: And aft in August sir Piers de brezey Seneshall of Norma^die with the
capitay^ of Deep. and many other Capytay^s and men of werre went to the sea
wit a great nauye and came into the downs by night: and on ye morn erly
before day they lo^ded and came to sandwych both^ by la^d and by watyr and took
the to^ne and ryfled and despoilled it / and tok^ many prisoners. and left the
town all bare / which was a rich place and much good theryn and lad with hem
many rich prisoners. In this same yer^ in many places of france Almaigne /
flau^dres / hola^d: and zela^d children gadred the^ by great co^panyes / for to
go on pilgrimage to saint Mycheles mount in Normandy / which came fro fer
co^tres. whereof the people mervailled: and many supposed that some wyked spirit
meved the^ to so do* but it e^dured not long. because of the long way and
also for lake of vitayll as they went. In this year Raynold pecok bisshopp of
chichestre was founde^ an heretic. and the iij. day of Dece^bre was abiured
at la^bhyte in the presence of ye erchebisshop of caunterbury and many
bisshoppes and doctors and lords te^perall and his books bre^t at poulis
cross. ye have herd tofore how certay^ lords were slain at seint Albons.
wherefore was allway a grucche and wrath had by theires of the^ that were so
slain ayens the duke of york the Earls of warrewyke and of Salisbury /
wherefore the king by thauys of his cou^ceill sent for the^ to london: to
whych^ place the duke of york came the xxvi. day of Ianiuer wit iiij.C. men

came the earl of salisbury wit v.C. me^ / and was logged in therber his own
place / And then^e came the duke of Excestre and of Somersete wit viij.C. men
and lay without temple bare: and the earl of Northu^berla^d. the lord
Egremo^d: the lord Clifford wit xv.C. men and logged without town^. and the
mayre that time Geffray boleyne kept great wacche wit the co^mu^s of ye cite:
and rode about the cite by holborne and fleet street wit a v.M / me^ well
armed and araied for to keep ye pees / And the xiiij. day of feuerer the Earl

How the ky^ges howshold made affraye against the earl of warrewyke / and of the
journey at the bloreheth Capi. cc.lxviij
ALso this same year as the earl of warrewyk was at cou^ceill at Westmynster.
all the kings household meyne gadred them to gedre for to have slain the said
Earl / but by the help of god and his fre^dys: he recoured his barge and
escaped their evil enterprise. how well the cooques cam^ renny^g out wit
spittes and pestels ayens him. And the same day he rode toward Warrewyke / and
sone after he gate him a commission and went over see to Caleys. Sone after
this the earl of Salisbury coming to London was enco^trid at bloreheth with the
lord awdely and moch^ other people ordained for to have distressyd hy^. but he
hauy^g knowleche that he should be mete was accompanied wit his ij. sons: Sir
Thomas and sir Ioha^ neuyll and a great felawship of good men: and so they mete
and fought to gedres / where therle of salisbury wan the field. and the lord
Awdely was slain^ and many gentillmen of chesshire and moch^ people hurt. and
therles.ij. sons were hurt / and going homward afterward they were taken and
lad to Chestre by ye queen's meyne / After Calixte Pius was pope: and was chose^
this year M.cccc.lviij / And he was called tofore Eneas an eloquent man and a
poet laureate^ he was enbassatour of the Emperor before time and he wrote in
the connceill of Basille a noble traittye for the auctorite of the same also he
canonised saint katherine of senys This pope ordained great indulge^ces and
pardon to them that would go werre against the turk And wrote an epistle to the
great Turk exortyng him to become christian: and in the end he ordained a
passage against the Turk at Ankone / to which much people drew out of all
parties of criste^dome: of which people he se^te many home ayen^ / because they
suffysed not. and anon^ aftir he deide at the said place of Ankone the year of
our lord M.cccc.lxiiij the xiiij. day of August

How Andrewe Trollop and the sowdyours of Caleys forsook the duke of york and
their maistir therle of warrewyke. in the westco^tre Capit. CC.lix
THe duke of york the Earls of warrewyk and of Salisbury saw ye governance
of the Reame stand most by the queen and her cou^ceill and how the great
princes of the land were not called to counceill / but set a part / and not
only so. but that hit was said through the reame that the said lords should be
destroyed utterly as it openly was showed at Bloreheth by them that would have
slain the Earl of Salisbury: Then^ they for sauacio^ of their lives and also
for the co^myn well of ye ream^ thought for to remedy thise things assembled
the^ to gedyr with moch^ people / and tok a field in the westco^tre / to which ye
earl of warrewyke came from taleys with many of the hold soudiours. as a^drew
trollop and other: i^ whose wisdom as for the werre he moch^ trusted. And wha^
they were thus asse^bled^ and made their field: The king sent out his
co^missio^s and preuy sealys unto all the lords of his reame to come and
awayte on hy^ in their most defensable wise. and so every men came in such^
wise yt the king was stronger and had moch^ more people tha^ the duke of york
and the Earls of warrewyk and salisbury: for it is here to be noted that eueri
lord (...) so deceived took a counsel shortly in ye same night and deperted
from the field leuy^g behynd* the^ the most part of their people to keep the
feld till on the morn. Then^e the duke of york with his second sone deperted
through walys toward Irla^d / leuyng his oldest sone the earl of the march with
the Earls of warrewyk and Salisbury / which to geder with three or iiij. persons
rood strayt into Dene^shire: and there by hulpe and aid of denham a squire
which gate for the^ a shipp. which cost CC / xx. noblis. and with the same ship
sailled fro the^s into Garnesey. and there refresshyd the^. and from the^s
sailled to Caleys / where they (...) in to the castle by the (...) ^er they
(...) of it. And the (...) in wa^ (...) bey^g wy^ (...) in the field: not (...)
of this ^ode^ departy^g on the morn fond non^ (...) of the said lords / where
for he sent our in all haste men to follow and purswe after to take he^ / but
they met not wit the^ as god would / and then^e the king went to ludlowe and
despoilled the castle and the town. and sent the duches of york wit her
children to my ladi of boky^gha^ her suster. where she was kept long after /
and fortwith the king ordained the duke of somersette capytay^ of caleys and
these other lords so departed as a fore is said were proclaimed rebellis and
great traitors / Then^e the duke of somersette took to hy^ all ye sowdiours
that deperted from the field and made him ready in all have to go to caleys and
took possession of his office. and wha^ he came he fownde therle of warrewyk
therein as capitayn and therles of march and salisbury also. and then^e he
lo^ded by scales and went to Gwysnes. and there he was received / and it

their fre will. for the shipme^ owght more favor to ye earl of warrewyke tha^
to the duke somersete jn which ships were taken diverse men as Ienyn
finkhill. Johan felaw kailles / and purser / which were beheded son^ aft in
caleys / and aft this daily came men over see to thise lords to Caleys and
began to wexe stre^ger. and they borrowed much good of the staple. and on yt
other side the duke of somersette being in Gwysnes gate people to hi^ which
came out and scarmusshed wit the^ of caleys and they of caleys with he^. which
endured many days / During thus this same scarmusshy^g much people daily came
over unto these lords / Then^e on a time by thauys of counseill / the lords
at caleys sent over maistir de^ha^ with a great felawship to sa^dwhich: and took
the town and therein the lord Rivers and the lord Scaleys his sone: and took
many ships i^ the haven / and browght he^ all to Caleys. with which ships
many maro^ners of their fre will came to Caleys to serve ye Earl of warrewyke^
and after this the earl of warrewyke by thauys of the lords took all his
ships and ma^ned the^ well and sailled him self into Irla^d for to speak with
the duke of york. and to take his auys how they should enter into england
agayn^. and when he had ben^ there and done his eraudes he returned agayn^

he came in the westcontre upon the sea* the duke of Excestre admyrall of
England bey^g in the grace of d^e^ accompanied wit many ships of werre met
with therle of warrewyke and his flete. but they fought not. for the substance
of the people bey^g with the duke of Excestre ou^^ better will and more favor to
therle of warrewyk tha^ to him and they deperted and came to caleys in saufte
blessed be god. Tha^ ye ky^ges cou^ceill sey^g yt these lords had gote^ ye
ships from sa^dwhich and taken the lord Rivers and his sone. ordained a
