Denham and many other to go to sandwhich^: and so they did and assailled the
town by water and by lo^d and gate it and brought mou^tfort their capitay^
over see to Ryseba^ke and there they smote of his head / and daily men came
over to them out of all parties of England

How the Earls of March: of warrewyke* and of salisbury entered into England.
And of the field of Northampto^. where diverse lords were slain Capitulo
CClxi.
And after this ye said Earls of March / warrewyke and of salisbury came over
to to Dover with much people and there lo^ded: to who^ all the country drew and
came to london armed: and for to late the lords of the kings cou^ceyl know
their trouth^ and also their intent assembled the^ and told the^ that they
intended no harm to the kings person sauf yt they would put fro hy^ such
persons as were about hy^: and so they deperted from London with a great
puyssau^ce toward northampto^: where the king was acco^panyed wit many lords
and had made a strong field without ye town and there both perties mete and
was fowghte^ a great bataille. in which battle were slain ye duke of
Boky^gha^. the earl of shrowesburi: the vico^te beaumo^d. the lord egremo^d^
and many knights and squiers and oth^ir also. and the king hy^ self taken in
the feld and afterward brought to london. and anon^ afterward was a perleme^t
at westmi^ster dury^g which parliament the duke of york came out of Irla^d with
the earl of Rutela^d ridy^g with a great felawship into the paleys at westmy^ster
and took ye kings paleys and came into perlement chamber and there took the
ky^ges place and claimed ye croune as his propre enheritau^ce and right and
cast forth in writing his title: and also yt he was rightful heyr. wherefore
was much to do. but in conclusion it was appointed and concluded yt king Henry
should regne and be king duri^g his natural life for asmoch^ as he had be^ so
long king and was pocessyd. and after his deth^ the duke of york should be king
and his heirs ky^ges after hy^ / and forthwith should be proclaimed heir
apperau^t. and should also be protector of England dury^g ye ky^ges life. with
many other things ordained in ye sam^ parliament. and if king henry duri^g his
life went from this apoy^teme^t or any article concluded in the said
perlement. he should be deposed and the duke should take ye crown^ and be king.
all which things were enacted by the auctorite of the said perleme^t: at
which parliament the co^munes of the reame bey^g assembled in the common house
comony^g and treatyng upon the title of ye said duke of york suddenly fill down^
the croune which henge then^e in the mids of the said house. which is the
fraytour of the abbey of westmy^ster: which was taken for a prodige or toke^
that the regne of king Henry was ended / and also the croune which stood on
the highest toure of ye steple in the castle of Dover fylle down this same
year

How the noble duke of york was slayn^ and of the field of wakelfeld / and of
the second journey at sey^t Albo^s by the queen and prince / Ca. cclxij
THen^e for asmoch^ as the queen with the prince was in the north and absented
her from the king and would not obey such^ things as was concluded i^ the
perleme^t: it wss ordained that the duke of york as protector should goo
northward / for to bring in the quen^ and subdue such as would not obey wit
who^ went the earl of salisburj. sir Thoa^s neuyll his sone. with much people /
and at wakefeld in Cristmas weke they were all overthrown and slain by the
lords of the queen's pertie that is to wete. the duke of york was slayn^* the
earl of Rutla^d. sir Thomas neuill. and many moo / the earl of salisbuey was
taken a live and other / as joha^ harow of London capitay^ of ye footme^ / and
ha^son of hule which were brought to pou^frete. and there after beheded and
their hedes se^te to york and set upon the yates / and thus was that noble
pry^ce slain^ the duke of york / on whose soul and all criste^ sowles god have
mercy. And this time therle of march being in shrewesbury hering the death of
his fadre desired assistence and aid of the town for taue^ge his fadres death
And from the^s went to walys ^ where at ca^delmasse after he had a bataylle at
Mortimes cross against therles of pe^broke. and of wilshire. where therle of
March had the victory Then^ ye quen^ with the lords of the north after they
had distressed and slain ye duke of york and his felawship came southward with a
great multitude and puissau^ce of people for to come to the king and defete
such^ co^clusio^s as had ben^ taken before by ye perlement aye^s whose comy^g ye
duke of nortfolk therle of warrewyk with much people and ordinance went unto
sey^t Albo^s and lad king henry with he^ and there enco^tred to gedre jn such^
wise yt ye duke of northfolk and the earl of warrewyke with other of their
party fled and lost that journey where king Henry was taken and went with
the queen and prince his sone* which tho had gotten that field: Then the
quen^ and her party bey^g at their above / sent anon^ to london. whych^ was
on asshwednesday the first day of Lent for vytaylle. which the mayre
ordained by thauys of the aldreme^ yt certain cartres laden with vitaill should
be sent to sey^t Albons to the^. and wha^ the cartres camen to crepelgate /
the co^munes of the cite that kept that gate took the vitailles from the
cartres and would not suffer it to pass: Then^ were there certain aldreme^ and
co^munes appoi^ted to go to Barnet for to speak with the queen's cou^ceil for to
entrete that the Northeryn me^ should be se^te home into their country ayen^:
for the cite of London dredde sore to be robbed and despoilled if they had come
/ And thus dury^g this traittie tidings came that ye earl of warrewyke had
met with the earl of march on Cotteswold coming out of walys with a great
meyne of walsshme^ and that they both^ were comy^g to London ward / Anon as
these tidings were known the trayttye was broken. for the king. queen: prince
/ and all other lords were wit them departed from saint Albo^s northward wit
all their people. yet or they departed from the^s / they beheded the lord
bonuille. and sir Thomas kriell which were taken in the journey done on
shrotewisday / then the duchess of york being at London and hery^g of ye
loss of the field at saint Albio^s sent over see her ij. yo^ge sons George
and rychard which went to Vtrecht and Phelipp malpas a rich merchant of
London / Thoa^s vagha^ squire: maistir willya^ hatteclyf. and many other fery^g
of the comy^g of the queen to London took a ship of Andwarp for to have goo^
into zela^d / and on that other cost were taken of one colu^pne a Fre^sshma^ a
shipp of werre. and he took he^ prisoners and brought he^ into france. where
they paid great good for their rau^sone. and there was much good and richesse
in that shipp.

Of the deposicyon of king Henry the sixthe / and how king Edward ye fourth
took poscession / and of the bataille on Palmesonday. and how he was crowned
Capi. CC*lxiij
Then when the earl of the March and the Earl of warrewyck had met to
gedre on cotiswold / inco^tine^t they concluded to goon to London / and sent
word anon^ to the mayre and to the cite that they should come / anon the cite
was glad of their comy^g hopyng to be relieved by them: and so they came to
London / And when they were comen and had spoken wit the lords and estates
then^e bey^g there / concluded for asmoch^ as king Henry was goon with the^
northward yt he had forfaited his croune and ought for to be deposed according
unto the acts maad and passed in the last parliament / and so by thaduyse of
the lords spirituell and temporell then^e bey^g at london the Earl of the
march Edward by ye g^ce of god oldest sone of Richard duke of york as
rightful heir. and next enheriteur to his fadre ye iiij day of March ye year
of our lord M.cccc.lix ^oke poscessio^ of the reame of England at westmy^stre
in the great halle: and after in the church of the abbey: and offered as king
beryng the septre riall. to who^ all the lords both spirituell and te^porell
did homage and obeisaunce as to their soueray^ liege and lawefull lord and
king. and forthwith it was proclaimed through the cite. king Edward the fourth^
of that name And anon^ after the king rode in his riall astate northward with all
his lords for to subdue his subgettes yt time bey^g in the north. and taue^ge
his fadres death And on palmeso^day after he had a great bataill in the
northcontre at a place kalled towton not far fro york. where wit the help of
god he gate the field and had the victory. where were slain of his
adversaries xxx.M men and moo as it was said by me^ that were there / jn which
battle was slain the earl of Northumberland: the lord clifford sir Ioha^
neuill / the earl of Westmerla^dis brother^ Andrew trollop and many other
knights and squiers / Then king henry yt had be king being wit the quen^ and
prince at york hering the loss of yt field and so moch^ people slain and
overthrown / anon^ forthwith departed all three with the duke of somersete. the
lord roos and other toward scotland / and the next day king Edward wit all his
army e^tred into york and was there proclaimed king and obeyed as he owght to
be. and the mayre and aldreme^ and co^myns sworn^ to be his liegeme^. and when
he had tarried a while in the north and yt all the co^tre there had turned to
hy^. he returned southward leuy^g the earl of warrewyke in tho parties for to
keep and govern that co^tre. and about midsomer aft the year of our lord
M.cccc.lx. and the first year of his regne he was crouned at westmy^ster and
enoy^ted king of england having the hole poscessio^ of all the hole reame who^
I pray god save and keep se^de hi^ and acco^plissement of the remenau^t of his
rightful enheritau^ce beyo^de the sea and that he may regne in the^ to the
plesir of almighty god health of his soul honor and wurshipp in this present
life and well and prouffyt of all his subgets: and that there then^ may be a
very fynall pees in all christian reames / that the infidels and miserau^ts may
be withsta^de^ and destroyed / and our faith enchaunced which i^ thise days
is sore minusshed by the puissaunce of the turks and hethe^ men and that after
this present and short life we may come^ to the everlasting life in the bliss
of heaven / Amen

Here ben endyd the Chronicles of the Reame of England with their
apperteignaunces. Enpre^tyd In the Duchye of Braband. in the town of Andewarpe
In the year of owr lord.M.cccc.xciij. By maistir Gerard de leew. a man of great
wysedom in all manner of ku^nyng: whych^ now is come from life unto the death /
which is great harm for many a pour man. On whose soul god almighty for his
hygh^ grace hau^ mercy AMEN
